Abyss | Description | Abysses are interactable objects in instances which spawns cracks and pits that spawn monsters. They can spawn from Act 6 onwards. This encounter is considered Extra Content and has a baseline greater than 8% chance to appear in any map area.
Abyss | Description | Abyss monsters can also be found in Abyssal Depths biomes in Delve.
Abyss | Overview | Abysses start spawning in acts Act 6 and onwards and in maps. Abysses are marked on the minimap with a green icon.
Abyss | Overview | Upon walking over an Abyss, a crack will form on the ground, and a small number of monsters will spawn out of it. The crack will expand as you follow it. The crack will eventually spawn a pit, which spawns many more monsters, including rare monsters. If the player takes too long to follow the crack into a pit or kill most of the enemies that spawn from the pit, it will close up. Otherwise, it will create another crack that leads to a different pit. An Abyss will create between one and four pits. Since the cracks can't cross themselves or each other, the Abyss may end prematurely if it works itself into a corner.
Abyss | Overview | Clearing the enemies out of the last pit will spawn an Abyssal Trove, which can be opened for loot. In addition to generic loot, an Abyssal Trove will always contain at least one Abyss jewel , possibly more. Sometimes, a Stygian Spire monster will spawn in place of the Abyssal Trove, dropping a Stygian Vise in addition to all the items you would normally receive from the Abyssal Trove.
Abyss | Overview | In zone levels 78 and up, instead of an Abyssal Trove or Stygian Spire, Abysses with four pits may open an entrance to the Abyssal Depths , containing an encounter with an Abyssal Lich.
Abyss | Rewards | Abyss jewels have the same functions as regular jewels , but with some differences. They offer different types of bonuses from regular jewels and most mods have tiers that depend on item level. They can be socketed in the jewel slots of the passive skill tree , but also in items with an abyssal socket , such as a Stygian Vise and unique Abyss items.
Abyss | Rewards | Stygian Vise is a belt with an abyssal socket as an implicit, allowing it to equip abyss jewels. Stygian Vises drop from Stygian Spires and Abyssal Liches.
Abyss | Rewards | Abyssal Depths is a side zone that can spawn in Abysses in zone levels 78 and up. It contains Abyss monsters, as well as a boss encounter with a Abyssal Lich , which can drop abyss themed unique items.
Abyss | Unique items | The armour pieces drop from Kurgal, the Blackblooded also have Abyssal Socket, but the boss encounter is not part of Abyss content that found in map

Accuracy | Description | Accuracy is a property of attack hits. Together with the target's evasion , it is used to calculate an attack's chance to hit. Spells do not benefit from accuracy, as they cannot be evaded.
Accuracy | Description | Accuracy can be gained from various sources, such as equipment , buffs , passives , and skills. Player characters inherently gain 2 base accuracy per level , and 2 base accuracy for each point of dexterity.
Accuracy | Mechanics | Accuracy is compared against the target's evasion to determine whether an attack hits or misses according to: [1] [2]
Accuracy | Mechanics | Uncapped Chance to Hit = 1.25 ∗ Attacker's Accuracy Attacker's Accuracy + ( Defender's Evasion ∗ 1 5 ) 0.9 \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\text{Uncapped Chance to Hit}}={1.25*{\text{Attacker's Accuracy}} \over {\text{Attacker's Accuracy}}+({\text{Defender's Evasion}}*{\frac {1}{5}})^{0.9}}
Accuracy | Mechanics | Chance to Hit = min ( max ( Uncapped Chance to Hit ,.05 ) , 1 ) \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\text{Chance to Hit}}=\min \left(\max \left({\text{Uncapped Chance to Hit}},.05\right),1\right)
Accuracy | Mechanics | Chance to hit can not be lower than 5%. It can be a maximum of 100%; there is no purpose in trying to exceed 100%.
Accuracy | Mechanics | Area of effect hits from attacks use accuracy in the same way as non-aoe hits; they can be evaded even when monsters are visibly inside an AoE.
Accuracy | Mechanics | In addition to its role in hitting, accuracy is checked a second time when attack hits attempt to deal a critical strike. Failing this accuracy check will cause a hit with sufficient critical strike chance to become a regular hit. This does not affect critical strikes by spells. [3]
Accuracy | Mechanics | Stats that scale from accuracy, such as Obscurantis or Oskarm , reference the accuracy of the skill, not the accuracy of a specific hit. This means conditional accuracy stats do not affect them (e.g. against Marked Enemy, against Unique Enemies, at Close Range ).
Accuracy | Mechanics | Base monster evasion rating depends on monster level. The below formula ignores bonuses from monster type or modifiers.
Accuracy | Mechanics | Evasion = ( 50 + 16 ∗ Level ) ∗ 1.0212 Level \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\text{Evasion}}=(50+16*{\text{Level}})*1.0212^{\text{Level}}
Accuracy | Mechanics | Minions ' attack hits inherently always hit. Minions do still have an accuracy rating, but is only used for conditional stats (e.g. Animate Guardian with Oskarm ) and otherwise has no functional effects.

Action speed | Description | Action speed is a stat that determines how fast or slow a character performs actions, such as running, swinging a weapon, casting a spell, or recoiling from being stunned.
Action speed | Description | The total modifier to the player character's action speed can be viewed on the Character screen under the Defence tab.
Action speed | Mechanics | A character's action speed determines the relative rate at which its animations play, thereby affecting the overall speed that their actions are performed. [1] [2] All of the character's actions that have an animated component are affected by their action speed. [3] This includes moving, attacking and casting (including channelling), throwing traps and mines, shouting warcries, summoning totems, and recovering from stuns.
Action speed | Mechanics | Modifiers to action speed have a multiplicative effect on a character in conjunction with stats that affect the speed of specific actions, such as movement speed , attack speed , cast speed and stun recovery. [1] Action speed does not directly modify such stats. [3] This distinction is relevant for game mechanics that care about any discrete modifiers to those stats. For example, the brand activation frequency of Arcanist Brand is affected by modifiers to the character's cast speed; whereas it is not affected by modifiers to the character's action speed. [2]
Action speed | Mechanics | Some monsters - mainly endgame and league bosses - have the hidden modifier CannotBeSlowedBelowValueBosses , preventing their action speed from dropping below 50%.
Action speed | Action cap | Because the game engine limits players to starting 1 action per server frame, or 30 actions per second, it is possible to reach a point at which speed stats are no longer useful. This is not a typical issue outside extreme cases. This only limits new actions: repeating animations do not count toward the limit, and channelling is unaffected by it entirely. [4]

Ailment duration | Mechanics | All ailments have a fixed base duration , except for Freeze which scales with the ailment threshold of the hit. These durations can be modified, but are not considered skill effects and therefore cannot be modified by skill effect duration modifiers.
Ailment duration | Mechanics | Viper Strike and Puncture are unique in that they have overrides for the default poison and bleed duration respectively with a skill effect, allowing poisons applied by Viper Strike and bleeds applied by Puncture to be modified by skill effect duration modifiers.
Ailment duration | Dealing damage faster | Modifiers that cause ailments to deal Damage #% faster causes the ailment to deal the same amount of total damage over a shorter duration. Multiple sources of "faster" damage application stack additively with each other, and are then applied as a single total, which is multiplicative with all other modifiers. [1] Calculating the effective duration can be done through the following formula:
Ailment duration | Dealing damage faster | For example, an Ignite with a duration of 6 seconds with 30% faster Ignites has a modified duration of 4.6 seconds and will deal 30% more damage per second over that duration, resulting in the same total amount of damage dealt.
Ailment duration | Dealing damage faster | Dealing damage faster does not improve DPS if the damage over time is already at the damage over time cap.
Ailment duration | Ailment reflection | Modifiers that reduce ailment duration on the player will not reduce the duration of reflected ailments since they are already calculated when applying on the enemy. It will simply be copied from the original inflicted ailment duration [2] instead of being recalculated.

Area | Description | Area serves as generic term to describe any separately loaded zone in the game. Areas have various attributes and rule sets attributed them depending on the type of the area. Using the rules of the specific area the game creates a randomized time-limited instance of an area which can be played by the character.
Area | Mechanics | Areas are separately loaded zones in the game with a specific set of attributes and rules. Those attributes can be thought of as a plan on how to create a specific zone.
Area | Mechanics | An area may have multiple layouts defined that are used to create the randomized instances. The layouts dictate specific features of an instance, so that for example the waypoint and quest objectives are always located in roughly the same positions. As an example, on the Ledge there will always be three stones next to the waypoint showing which of the two directions leads to the Climb.
Area | Mechanics | The individual pieces used to create a map zone are often referred to as a tileset. These individual pieces (such as walls, doorways, rivers etc) are designed by hand and are non-randomized themselves, however they are put together semi-randomly to form a coherent zone according to the layout. This allows a high level of variation in each instance while using the same building blocks ("tiles").
Area | Mechanics | Once the tiles have been generated, the instance will be filled with objects according to the area rules. Specific flags on the area will also change area behaviour - a town does not permit use of skills , a map will scale enemies depending on the map tier, etc. Similar to items maps use a hidden tag system that sets certain attribute that govern which modifiers, monsters and other objects can be placed inside the instance and their likelihood. In addition, each area has a default level associated with it which is used both to determine what monsters , Extra Content , modifiers and such are allowed, but also sets the level of any object within the area.
Area | Mechanics | For example, a level 60 area will also contain level 60 strongboxes and monsters. The level may be overridden, for example by delving deeper , using a Voidstone or other modifiers.
Area | Mechanics | Map rules also include settings such as the spawn chance for league-related objects or masters. Generally this is streamlined to a specific number for most areas, but may be fine-tuned in specific areas to balance around the size of the area. Small areas may have less space to spawn certain league related content. Some areas may also have them disabled entirely (such as towns or Vaal side areas ).
Area | Mechanics | Areas can be connected to each other allowing characters to pass from one area to another. Most of the story areas throughout the Acts are connected in some fashion to each other which can be seen on the world map. Areas also have a parent area which is used to determine where the character respawns after death. Usually this is the most recent town area.
Area | Instances | An instance is a specific, randomly generated zone using the rules defined by the area. It holds the current state of the zone, so whenever an item is dropped or a monster is killed that will be saved within the instance.
Area | Instances | The game automatically creates an instance when a player tries to join an area with the region based on the player's realm choice. If there is an existing instance already created by the player or a party member, then it will be joined instead.
Area | Instances | Instances with no players in them continue to exist for a limited time (about 8-15 minutes in instances created in acts, but much longer for instances created from the map device). The instance is destroyed after the time elapses, along with the items and monsters inside it.
Area | Instances | When entering an area in Acts, holding Control key displays existing instances of the area, and allows the player to create a new instance. The latter can be used to "reset" an area and start it again with a new layout, set of monsters, etc.
Area | Instances | Most instances can hold up to six players at once, with the exception of towns which can hold many more.

Area of effect | Description | Area of effect (often referred to as AoE ) refers to mechanics (such as skills, auras, and monster abilities) that apply to an area of the ground (rather than targeting a particular character, monster, etc.).
Area of effect | Description | Many AoE mechanics deal damage, but AoE mechanics can have other effects. For example, auras produce positive effects on allies within the area, while curses like Temporal Chains produce negative effects on enemies.
Area of effect | Description | While AoE mechanics can affect multiple characters or monsters within the area, not all mechanics that can affect multiple characters or monsters are AoE mechanics. For example, Ice Spear targets a single monster rather than an area, so it is not an AoE skill, even though it creates piercing projectiles that can hit other nearby monsters as well.
Area of effect | Usage | The term "area of effect" or "AoE" is used in several different ways:
Area of effect | Examples | The simplest examples of AoE mechanics are skills like Shock Nova , Ice Nova and Sweep , which create circular areas of effect. Other AoE skills like Cleave and Ground Slam create cone-shaped areas of effect, while others like Flame Surge or Glacial Cascade have more complicated areas of effect.
Area of effect | How modifiers to AoE sizes work | Support gems and other mechanics can increase or decrease the size of an area of effect, almost always by a percentage, e.g. 30% increased Area of Effect. These percentages refer to the total amount of ground covered by the area of effect, not to the area of effect's radius, diameter, or other dimensions. For example, a 100% increased Area of Effect modifier applied to Shock Nova 's circular area of effect will double the area of ground covered by the circle. The mathematics of that mean that the circle's radius and diameter will increase by around 40%.
Area of effect | How modifiers to AoE sizes work | If multiple percentage-based modifiers apply to the same area of effect, they add together. For example, if 40% increased Area of Effect , 20% increased Area of Effect , and 30% decreased Area of Effect modifiers all apply to the same area of effect, the area of effect's size will increase by 30% (40+20-30).
Area of effect | How modifiers to AoE sizes work | A few mechanics apply a specific increase (usually expressed as an integer) to a dimension of the area of effect. For example, the skill gem level bonus for Caustic Arrow specifically grants a +(0-6) to radius increase to the Caustic Arrow area of effect. These specific types of modifiers always apply before percentage-based modifiers are applied to the total area of effect. [ confirmation needed ] This means that dimension-specific modifiers tend to have a greater impact on the area of effect's final size.
Area of effect | Calculations | Distances are displayed in metres, however all calculations are done using internal units equal to 0.1m. Any calculation that would produce a result that is not a multiple of 0.1m will be rounded down.
Area of effect | Calculations | We can calculate the increased area of effect ( A o E % \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}AoE\% ) required to increase a certain base radius r b \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}r_{b} to a desired increased radius r i \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}r_{i} using the formula for area of a circle:
Area of effect | Calculations | π r i 2 = 100 + A o E % 100 × π r b 2 \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}\pi r_{i}^{2}={\frac {100+AoE\%}{100}}\times \pi r_{b}^{2}
Area of effect | Calculations | Cancelling out π \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}\pi and dividing both sides by r b 2 \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}r_{b}^{2} we get
Area of effect | Calculations | r i 2 r b 2 = ( r i r b ) 2 = 100 + A o E % 100 \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\frac {r_{i}^{2}}{r_{b}^{2}}}=({\frac {r_{i}}{r_{b}}})^{2}={\frac {100+AoE\%}{100}}
Area of effect | Calculations | Taking the square root of both sides shows that the proportion of the increased radius to the base radius is equal to the square root of the multiplier to area.
Area of effect | Calculations | r i r b = 100 + A o E % 100 \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\frac {r_{i}}{r_{b}}}={\sqrt {\frac {100+AoE\%}{100}}}
Area of effect | Calculations | This suggests that an area's radius can be increased from 28 to 30 with 15% increased area of effect:
Area of effect | Calculations | ( 30 28 ) 2 ≈ 1.148 < 100 + 15 100 \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}({\frac {30}{28}})^{2}\approx 1.148<{\frac {100+15}{100}}
Area of effect | Calculations | However , the square root of increased AoE is truncated to two decimal places before multiplying the radius, thus 15% increased AoE only results in a radius of
Area of effect | Calculations | 28 × 100 + 15 % 100 = 28 × 1.07238 ≈ 28 × 1.07 = 29.96 \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}28\times {\sqrt {\frac {100+15\%}{100}}}=28\times 1.07238\approx 28\times 1.07=29.96
Area of effect | Calculations | Similarly, 1.16 ≈ 1.077 \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\sqrt {1.16}}\approx 1.077 is also truncated to 1.07, thus the breakpoint to increase a radius of 28 to 30 is 17% increased AoE. [1]
Area of effect | Mechanics with both AoE and non-AoE aspects | Some mechanics' effects may have both AoE and non-AoE aspects. Modifiers that apply to "area of effect" will only apply to the AoE aspect of these mechanics.
Armour | Description | Armour is a form of defence that mitigates incoming physical damage from hits. Armour can implicitly appear on equipment , much like evasion , energy shield , and ward. Armour rating can be increased by wearing equipment , taking certain passive skills , using skills (e.g. Determination and Molten Shell ), and drinking flasks (e.g. Granite Flask and Basalt Flask ).
Armour | Mechanics | Armour grants physical damage reduction against hits , with the exact amount of damage reduction depending on the relative magnitude of the character's armour value and the physical damage of the hit. If the armour value is significantly larger than the damage, most of that damage is prevented. If the armour value is similar to or less than the incoming damage, only a small percentage of that damage will be prevented. For some numeric examples of how damage reduction changes based on armour, see the rule of thumb section later on this page.
Armour | Mechanics | As a result armour is more effective against many smaller hits than fewer larger hits, even if both scenarios represent the same total damage in the same amount of time. For a character with extreme investment in armour, what is considered a 'smaller hit' (receiving 75% damage reduction) can be 5000 damage or more. A character with only a minor investment in armour will encounter the limiting case where the damage reduction is very low (less than 5%) and the maximum damage that armour can prevent per hit is only one fifth of the armour value.
Armour | Mechanics | Armour never mitigates damage over time , as armour only applies to hits. Bleed is an ailment that deals physical damage over time that is based on the initial physical damage of an attack or spell; armour will reduce the initial hit but not the damage over time. However, both the initial hit and the damage over time can be mitigated with sources of #% additional Physical Damage Reduction , such as endurance charges or the suffix of Numbing of Numbing Suffix (3-4)% additional Physical Damage Reduction found on some body armours that require strength to equip. Physical damage reduction is capped at 90%. [1] The statsheet physical damage reduction combines Armour and Physical Damage Reduction values, making it unreliable for calculating effective damage reduction.
Armour | Mechanics | Normally, armour will only grant damage reduction against physical hits, not elemental or chaos damage. However, with the Transcendence keystone or other items (e.g Doryani's Prototype ) or passives (e.g. Juggernaut ), armour can apply to non-physical hits. In cases where armour mitigates multiple types of damage, it does so separately for each type it mitigates. If you make armour apply to lightning damage as well as physical damage, then take a hit containing both physical and lightning damage, then armour will calculate Physical Damage Reduction based on comparing the physical damage to armour, and apply that only to the physical damage, and will calculate Lightning Damage Reduction based on comparing the lightning damage to armour, and apply that only to the lightning damage. [2]
Armour | Mechanics | In the order of damage mitigation , damage reduction from armour is calculated after damage shifts and resistances (if applicable), but before modifiers to damage taken and spell suppression. [3] [4]
Armour | Rule of thumb | When the damage of a hit significantly exceeds Armour, it will never prevent more damage than its value divided by 5 (e.g. 1000 armour will never prevent more than 200 damage at its minimum percentage prevention).
Armour | Armour on monsters | Monsters also have armour values. The general amount of armour on monsters will increase as monster level increases, with monster types like stone golems and zombies having relatively high amounts of armour compared to hellions or sea witches. Boss monsters similarly increase in armour rating throughout the campaign. For example, Malachai, The Nightmare has 783 armour, while early map bosses such as Piety the Empyrean can have around 7000 armour depending on map level. Endgame bosses such as The Elder or Sirus, Awakener of Worlds have over 20000 and 32000 armour respectively. [ confirmation needed ]
Armour | Formulas | The amount of physical damage reduction is a function of armour rating and the physical damage taken.
Armour | Formulas | This is the base formula all other formulas are based upon. It is used to calculate the #% additional Physical Damage Reduction when Hit factor, i.e. the percentage by which the physical damage is mitigated.
Armour | Formulas | D R ( A , D r a w ) = A A + 5 ∗ D r a w \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}DR(A,D_{raw})={A \over A+5*D_{raw}}
Armour | Formulas | where A is the defender's armour rating and D raw is the raw physical damage.
Armour | Formulas | To calculate the armour rating you need to mitigate a given amount of Physical Damage at specific ratio, you can use this formula:
Armour | Formulas | A ( D r a w , D R ) = D R ∗ 5 ∗ D r a w 1 − D R \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}A(D_{raw},DR)={DR*5*D_{raw} \over 1-DR}
Armour | Formulas | You can also calculate the raw physical damage that would have resulted for a given Physical Damage Reduction and Armour rating:
Armour | Formulas | D r a w ( A , D R ) = A 5 ∗ D R − A 5 \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}D_{raw}(A,DR)={A \over 5*DR}-{A \over 5}
Armour | Formulas | To calculate the net physical damage i.e. the damage after damage reduction, the following formula can be used:
Armour | Formulas | D n e t ( A , D r a w ) = 5 ∗ D r a w 2 A + 5 ∗ D r a w \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}D_{net}(A,D_{raw})={5*{D_{raw}}^{2} \over A+5*D_{raw}}
Armour | Formulas | Another way of looking at it is in terms of absolute physical damage reduction:
Armour | Formulas | D R a b s ( A , D r a w ) = A ∗ D r a w A + 5 ∗ D r a w \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}DR_{abs}(A,D_{raw})={A*{D_{raw}} \over A+5*D_{raw}}
Armour | Formulas | D F ( A , D r a w ) = A 5 ∗ D r a w + 1 \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}DF(A,D_{raw})={A \over 5*D_{raw}}+1

Aspect | Description | Aspect skills are granted by items. The skills reserve mana to provide various buffs in a similar way to heralds. Aspect skills are considered spells.
Aspect | Description | Only one aspect skill can be active at a time and they have a base mana reservation of 25%.

Attack speed | Description | Attack speed is a property of attack skills. In combination with action speed , it determines the speed with which attack animations can be performed.
Attack speed | Mechanics | Most attack skills receive their base attack time from the equipped weapon. Base attack time while unarmed is 0.83s, while shield skills such as Shield Crush receive a base attack time from their gem instead. Attack time is used to calculate the number of attacks per second, the typical measure of attack speed displayed on weapons and the character sheet. [1]
Attack speed | Mechanics | Attack speed modifiers can increase or decrease a skill's attacks per second. These modifiers only affect attacks. Other types of skills have their own speed stats, such as #% increased Cast speed or #% increased Warcry speed. Similar to other animations, the practical duration of attacks is also affected multiplicatively by action speed modifiers like Chill and Tailwind.
Attack speed | Mechanics | Triggered attacks are instant, though they still have an attack time for the purpose of stats like #% chance to deal Double Damage with Attacks if Attack Time is longer than 1 second.
Attack speed | Characters | All characters have the following attack speed modifiers in their base stats.

Avoidance | Description | Avoidance is a keyword used to describe several different chance-based forms of mitigation against hits , certain types of damage , or debuffs or other mechanics.
Avoidance | Mechanics | Avoidance can be categorized into three major categories: hit avoidance, damage avoidance, and mechanic avoidance.
Avoidance | Hit avoidance | Hit avoidance currently is primarily against projectiles, typically worded as #% chance to avoid Projectiles , which prevents a hit /collision from a projectile, causing it to pass through the target as if it were evaded or dodged.
Avoidance | Hit avoidance | Hit avoidance prevents the hit entirely and will not trigger any on-hit/when-hit effects or projectile behaviours or reduce remaining projectile behaviour counts (e.g. pierce ).
Avoidance | Hit avoidance | While worded similarly, Avoid Projectiles that have Chained does not appear to be a conditional 100% chance to avoid projectiles: it does not prevent the collision.
Avoidance | Damage avoidance | Damage avoidance, typically worded as #% chance to Avoid X Damage from Hits , is a form of damage mitigation against hits that reduces the damage of certain damage types to 0. It is considered preventing damage for stats like Untiring or Divine Shield. Avoiding all damage from hits does not prevent or undo the hit; on-hit/when-hit effects will still occur for both the attacker and defender. [1] Avoidance should not be confused with evasion , dodge , block , or immunity to damage. [2]
Avoidance | Damage avoidance | The chance to avoid damage from hits is hard capped at 75%. [3]
Avoidance | Damage avoidance | Resolve Avoidance , a mechanic found exclusively in the Forbidden Sanctum , functions similarly to damage avoidance; it does not prevent the hit, but will prevent all Resolve loss from the hit.
Avoidance | Mechanic avoidance | Mechanic avoidance is the most commonly found type of avoidance that applies to different types of debuffs or mechanical effects. Mechanic avoidance is most often used in the context of ailment avoidance. Stacking 100%+ chance to avoid X ailment is functionally identical to having the stat Cannot be X-ed , although the inverse is not true for stats such as the one found on Stormshroud. This form of ailment defence is distinct from ailment immunity in that achieving 100% ailment avoidance will not remove any existing stacks of that ailment. [4] Ailment avoidance is absolute and will prevent the avoided ailment from being inflicted, even if the attacker has a 100% chance to inflict or "always" inflicts ailments - these chances are multiplicative against each other. Avoided ailments are not counted as inflicted by the attacker.
Avoidance | Mechanic avoidance | 100% ailment avoidance against non-damaging ailments also prevents the corresponding type of ground effect from affecting the target ( Chilled Ground , Shocked Ground , Scorched Ground, Brittle Ground, and Sapped Ground). This does not affect Burning Ground and Desecrated Ground as they are not considered ignite or poison respectively.
Avoidance | Mechanic avoidance | Other forms of mechanic avoidance include chance to avoid Blind , Impale , knockback , or stun. These follow the same rules as ailment avoidance. (The stun-specific #% chance to Ignore Stuns stat is effectively avoidance, as it ignores stun for all purposes, though it is not additive with #% chance to Avoid being Stunned.)
Avoidance | Pantheon | Several Gods provide chances to avoid varying types of damage and/or effects.
Avoidance | Helmets | No results found
Avoidance | Monsters | Magic monsters have a 50% chance to avoid fleeing.

Banner | Description | Banner skills are a sub-class of skills that can be manually activated to consume all Valour and place down a banner that provides an aura. The effect and radius of the Banner aura scales with the amount of Valour consumed. Valour is typically gained from melee combat.
Banner | Mechanics | Activating a Banner skill will place down that Banner in your current position, granting an aura to allies around it. Moving out the Banner's radius or activating the skill again will remove the Banner.
Banner | Mechanics | A player is not inherently limited to 1 Banner. While the use of multiple Banners is usually prevented by While you have no placed Banner, you can gain Valour , this may be circumvented with Having a placed Banner does not prevent you gaining Valour on e.g. Perfidy or Worthy Causes.
Banner | Mechanics | Similar to Plague Bearer , Banners cannot be triggered except by Automation. Automation will place a Banner if at least 1 Valour is available, then end the placement once off cooldown.
Banner | Valour | Valour is a counter that increases under certain conditions while you have a Banner skill which augments the power of those skills. Valour is a counter on the character and is shared between all skills that care about Valour. [1] Valour normally cannot be gained while a Banner is placed.
Banner | Valour | By default, players gain 1 Valour on melee kill, or on melee hit against Rare or Unique enemies, no more than once every 0.5 seconds, up to a maximum of 50.

Beastcrafting | Description | Beastcrafting is a method of crafting by sacrificing beasts to the blood altar in the Menagerie. Each beastcrafting recipe requires four beasts to be sacrificed, with most of them requiring one or two specific Red Beast, and the rest any Rare Beast. The four chosen beasts are released into the arena surrounding the blood altar and must be killed to complete the recipe. If the player dies during the attempt, the recipe fails and the beasts are lost.
Beastcrafting | Description | If an item is created, the resulting item level is equal to the level of the main beast sacrificed. Recipes that create unique items cannot generate drop-restricted items. The recipes that either "Add a Prefix, Remove a Random Suffix" or "Add a Suffix, Remove a Random Prefix" use the beast's level to determine the modifiers it can add, ignoring the item's actual item level. Other recipes that add modifiers use the item's item level as usual.

Blight (game content) | Description | Blights are tower defence -like encounters that can spawn from Fungal Growths in any map area (as well as The Sewers and The Imperial Gardens in the campaign ), which will always be accompanied by Sister Cassia. This encounter is considered Extra Content and has a baseline greater than 8% chance to appear in any non-unique map area.
Blight (game content) | Description | Blight encounters are also found in Blighted maps , which are a modified version of existing maps, which contains no regular monsters and instead contains a single Blight encounter. Blights in Blighted maps are far larger, spawn a significantly increased amount of enemies and bosses, and provide a greater quantity and variety of rewards. Players can trade Blighted maps. Atlas passives that affect Blight encounters in maps do not affect Blighted maps. There is also a pinnacle version of Blighted maps called Blight-ravaged maps.
Blight (game content) | Mechanics | Once players interact with the Fungal Growth, Cassia will place a purification pump on the growth, causing it to spawn roots in random directions. At the end of each root is a portal that spawns enemies that slowly move towards the core, only stopping to attack units in its way. The Blight can spawn up to 8 roots, increasing with zone level. Players will be given a short preparation time before the Blight starts spawning monsters. Players can skip this by pressing a button that appears on the bottom right during this preparation period.
Blight (game content) | Mechanics | Some roots will spawn after a delay, and sometimes a root will have multiplied monster density (indicated by a multiplier) or contains a Blight boss (indicated by an icon on top). An icon corresponding to a tower can appear over each root, indicating which tower it is resistant to. Along the paths of the roots, players can construct a tower in specified areas. Towers cost resources to build or upgrade, which are given at the start and also acquired from killing blighted enemies. In a party , a tower belongs to the player who built or last upgraded it, using that player's ring anointments. [1]
Blight (game content) | Mechanics | When an enemy reaches the core, it will lower the pump's durability by a fixed amount and despawn. The pump has 10 durability in maps (20 in Blighted maps or with the Sturdy Construction Atlas Notable), and the amount of durability lowered is based on the monster's rarity (1 for normal, 2 for magic, 5 for rare, 10 for unique). When the pump's durability reaches 0, the Blight encounter fails and monsters will stop spawning.
Blight (game content) | Mechanics | Once all enemies from each portal/lane are defeated, reward chests will spawn at the location of each portal. These chests remain once spawned even if the pump is destroyed and the Blight encounter is failed. Blight encounters will have at least one lane that contains a Blight reward ( Oils or Blighted map ). Oil rewards chests have a baseline ~15% chance to drop a Blighted Map. Additionally, natural loot from killed monsters will drop at the pump's location. (Kills by towers are unaffected by any player's increases to item quantity or rarity.)
Blight (game content) | Mechanics | A maximum of one Blight can spawn per zone naturally; this maximum is shared between the random chance to spawn a Blight, and guaranteed Blight from Blight Scarabs , implicit map mods, enchantments, and the map device craft. [2]
Blight (game content) | Mechanics | The Scarab cannot be used in combination with the map device craft.
Blight (game content) | Mechanics | Characters must complete least one map Blight encounter in a new league to complete Cassia's quest before she will anoint items. This also applies to the Blight Stash Tab.
Blight (game content) | Strategy | The most important thing to do in a Blight encounter is to keep the blighted enemies stalled. If you leave a lane unprotected, you'll have to scramble to defend the pump on your own, which takes away time for you to put down towers. Prioritise building stalling towers (Chilling, Seismic, Summoning) over damage towers (Fireball, Shock Nova) first and have them covered by Empowering Towers whenever possible. An empowered Tier 3 Seismic and/or Chilling tower is usually enough to hold down a lane. Tier 4 stalling towers are not that much better at defending than their Tier 3 counterparts, but a Tier 4 Glacial Cage can buy some time when built near the pump. If the Blight encounter has delayed lanes, try to wait for them to spawn to see if you can get a good tower placement in a chokepoint. Be sure to account for enemy tower resistances, especially seismic resistance.
Blight (game content) | Strategy | Damaging towers are more valuable in Blighted maps than small Blight encounters. Meteor Towers synergise well with stalling towers and are very effective at clearing enemies once you have your defences established. Other damage towers aren't as damaging, but are effective in the right positions. They are significantly better as Tier 4 towers than Tier 3.
Blight (game content) | Strategy | When farming Blight, especially in "juiced" maps, avoid running maps with modifiers that give monsters too much movement speed or slow/stun resistance like Monsters cannot be Stunned and Monsters' Action Speed cannot be modified to below Base Value , which limit your ability to stall and requires high damage by the player to compensate. Enemies may also spawn with random mods which allow them to ignore stun or freeze effects.
Blight (game content) | Strategy | For ring anointments, Your Chilling Towers freeze enemies for 0.2 seconds while they are affected by chilling beams (Opalescent/Silver) is often considered to be one of the best in the game. Other generally good or budget ring anointments include:
Blight (game content) | Strategy | Due to the way off-screen entities behave, it is advised to not move too far away from the Ichor Pump nor build towers too far away from it, as it can possibly cause enemies to leak, even if they would normally be stun-locked.
Blight (game content) | Blight pump rewards | Completing or failing a Blight encounter will cause items that would have dropped from defeated Blighted monsters to drop from the pump in a loot explosion.
Blight (game content) | Blight pump rewards | Additionally, completing a Blight encounter in a Blighted map or Blight-ravaged map has a chance to drop an exclusive anointable Blight unique. The drop rates of these uniques are not affected by item quantity.
Blight (game content) | Blight chests | Completing a blighted map or a blight encounter on a regular map will grant many of the following:
Blight (game content) | Ruthless mode | Reward chests from Blight encounters in Ruthless mode lack reward icons, and drop generic items, oils , or Blighted maps.
Blight (game content) | Related Atlas passive skills | Atlas passives do not affect blighted maps and blight-ravaged maps.
Blight tower | Description | Blight towers can be constructed during Blight encounters. There are several different types of towers, each with different effects and upgrades.
Blight tower | Tower types | Some enemies can either resist or be immune to a certain tower types.
Blight tower | Tower upgrades | Options
Blight tower | Tower upgrades | All 6 tower types begin at tier 1. They remain the same kind of tower for tier 2 and 3 tier upgrades. Upgraded versions of the same tower do more damage, hit more often, have more range and have less cooldown time. There are 2 tier 4 options available. This means there are 18 total options of towers to choose from.
Blight tower | Tower upgrades | Cost
Blight tower | Tower upgrades | Tower cost per upgrade from tier 1 to 4 is 100, 150, 300, 500.
Blight tower | Tower upgrades | Total cost of each tier tower from tier 1 to 4 is 100, 250, 550, 1050.
Blight tower | Tower Range | All towers will only work within a limited radius of the character. For example:
Blight tower | Anointments | Tower effects can be modified by anointments on rings. For the entire list with oil requirements see List of ring anointments. All anointments can be used twice with 2 different rings to double their effects when possible. In a party , a tower belongs to the player that created or most recently upgraded it, using only that player's anointments.
Blocking | Description | Blocking is a layer of defense that will entirely prevent damage from an enemy hit unless modified by some outside effect like Glancing Blows. The chance to block is a random roll made for each hit. [1] Characters and most enemies have 0% base block chance; enemies with a shield typically have some chance to block.
Blocking | Mechanics | Blocking a hit prevents all damage and harmful on-hit effects such as status ailments. Only hits can be blocked; it does nothing against damage over time. Block typically mitigates attack damage and spell damage , though secondary damage can be blocked if it originates from a spell or attack skill. No block chance stat exists against direct secondary damage, such as self-damage or non-skill explosions. [2]
Blocking | Mechanics | Blocking has no cooldown and can occur as long as the defender has block chance, [3] including during other actions, while frozen , and while recovering from stun or a previous block. It does not require wielding a shield or a specific weapon type.
Blocking | Chance to block | The chance to block is a random roll made per hit; it is not entropy-based like evasion. Block has the following base stats
Blocking | Chance to block | Shields and most staves / warstaves typically contribute a significant amount of attack block depending on the base type and implicit modifiers. Dual wielding also innately grants +20% chance to Block Attack Damage Additional block chance can be obtained from items, passive skills , and Tempest Shield.
Blocking | Chance to block | Maximum block chance (for either attacks or spells) is 75% by default. This cap can be modified, up to a hard cap of 90%.
Blocking | Hit effects | The general rule is that blocking prevents the attacker's on hit effects from stats, excluding things skills actively do when they hit. But blocking will not prevent the defender's when hit effects, because preventing those could make blocking a negative thing for the defender. [4]
Blocking | Hit effects | Certain stats, such as "Gain 1 Endurance Charge every second if you've been hit recently", were originally classified as an enemy's hit effects and thus were prevented by blocked hits. [4] This interaction was fixed in patch 3.11.1c.
Blocking | Hit effects | Effects that occur on a successful hit (e.g. Frenzy 's Frenzy Charge generation) will still occur if blocked, as the hit was not prevented. However, skill effects based on damage such as Puncture 's bleed are prevented. [5] Blocked hits also prevent trigger effects from activating, such as Cast On Critical Strike Support.
Blocking | Hit effects | when you Block effects occur before damage is taken (when block doesn't prevent all damage). [6]
Blocking | Reflected damage | Reflected damage can be blocked; [7] however blocking reflected damage will not trigger on-block effects.
Blocking | Block duration | Because block rolls after other mitigation, the game has already calculated stun by the time a hit is blocked. If a blocked hit would have caused a stun, the blocking animation is played. [8] If it would not have caused a stun, then you get a "free" block with no animation.
Blocking | Block duration | Faster Block and Stun Recovery and Increased Block Recovery modifiers reduce the length of the blocking animation.
Blocking | Block duration | The following formula is the complete calculation for the duration of the blocking animation (in milliseconds). If you cannot be stunned, the block animation will never play.
Blocking | Block duration | Block Duration = 350 1 + Block and Stun Recovery + Block Recovery \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\begin{aligned}{\text{Block Duration}}&={{350} \over {1+{\text{Block and Stun Recovery}}+{\text{Block Recovery}}}}\end{aligned}}
Blocking | Block duration | The block animation is affected by an object's action speed ; reductions such as frozen and chilled will cause block recovery to take more time.
Blocking | Pantheon | Soul of the Brine King Major Pantheon power provides the unique modifier You cannot be Stunned if you've been Stunned or Blocked a Stunning Hit in the past 2 seconds.
Blocking | Pantheon | The Soul of the Brine King can be upgraded to grant an additional #% increased Stun and Block Recovery.
Blocking | Taking damage from blocked hits | The You take #% of Damage from Blocked Hits stat causes block's usual 100% damage prevention to be reduced in efficacy, causing the defender to take damage despite blocking the hit. By default, you take 0% of the damage from blocked hits. If this stat exceeds 100%, the defender will take more damage than would have been taken if the hit was not blocked. [9]
Blocking | Taking damage from blocked hits | Other than this, the mechanics of block are unchanged. A blocked hit still cannot apply on-hit effects, such as ailments or curses. This modifier does not affect the chance to play the block animation based on the amount of damage taken.
Blocking | Taking damage from blocked hits | Glancing Blows causes players to take 65% of damage from blocked hits, although it also doubles block chance.
Blocking | Taking damage from blocked hits | Other items with this stat include:
Blocking | Taking damage from blocked hits | Monsters that have innate chance to block (e.g. holding a shield) typically have this stat as an innate modifier.

Blood Stance and Sand Stance | Description | Blood Stance and Sand Stance are stance statuses provided by Blood and Sand and Flesh and Stone. The buff/debuff from the stance depends on which aforementioned skill is used. These skills can be activated again to switch between Blood Stance and Sand Stance. Certain attack skills behave differently based on which stance you are using.
Blood Stance and Sand Stance | Mechanics | Stance setting is shared between all skills that grant Blood or Sand Stance. Toggling one will toggle the other.
Blood Stance and Sand Stance | Mechanics | Skills and passives which interact with Blood and Sand Stance will use Blood Stance by default if you are not actively in either stance (e.g. if you do not have either of the toggle gems equipped).

Brand | Description | Brands are a type of skill which create persistent spells that can be attached to an enemy and periodically trigger additional spell effects, usually dealing damage.
Brand | Mechanics | Casting a brand skill places a brand on the ground where your cursor is located.
Brand | Mechanics | While active and detached, whenever an enemy is within attachment range, the brand will attempt to attach to that enemy, and stay attached until that enemy dies or the brand expires.
Brand | Mechanics | When an enemy dies while a brand is attached, the brand will return to its original position (wherever it appeared when it was first cast) or recalled position.
Brand | Mechanics | You can place 3 brands and have 1 brand attached to an enemy by default. Runebinder allows you to attach an additional brand to an enemy, significantly increasing your damage dealt.
Brand | Mechanics | When a brand is created past the brand limit, a brand will be replaced. Unattached brands are replaced before attached brands.
Brand | Mechanics | Brands are skill effects, not separate objects, meaning various mechanics including leech and reflected damage will apply to the caster.
Brand | Mechanics | Proxies like traps may create their own brands, and deal their own damage with them, but they are limited by the same placement and attachment limits as the player [1]. They may be Brand Recall ed normally. [2]
Brand | Attached/Detached Time | Brands have both a detached and an attached duration. The detached duration only expires while the brand is detached, and the attached duration only expires while it's attached. These durations are not refreshed on attaching or detaching, and the brand ceases to exist when either duration expires. [3] Both are affected by modifiers to skill effect duration, such as More Duration Support. [4]
Brand | Activation frequency | Attached brands will trigger their effects at regular intervals based on your brand activation frequency.
Brand | Activation frequency | Spell Echo Support does not increase activation frequency, but will cause two brands to be placed per cast and decrease the casting time to summon/place brands.
Brand | Activation frequency | Action speed only affects brand placement speed, not brand activation frequency. [5] This means that brands are not affected by any action speed modifiers, including but not limited to: Tailwind , Winterweave , The Flow Untethered , Temporal Chains , Chill , and Freeze.
Brand | Brand attachment range | Brands will attach to enemies that are within 30 units of themselves, by default [6]. This value scales in a linear manner, meaning 40% increased brand attachment range would increase your maximum brand attachment range from 30 units to 42 units [7].
Brand | Brand attachment range | Brand attachment range is only affected by modifiers that explicitly state they apply to brands. Area of effect modifiers do not affect your brand attachment range.

Breach | Description | Breach content involves otherworldly monsters who have stabilized their interdimensional rift to Wraeclast and have begun constructing hives throughout the land, first introduced in Keepers league. It is the sequel of the original Breach mechanic from Breach league.
Breach | Overview | Breaches can be encountered starting from The Mud Flats in Act 6. Players can find Ailith, First of the Keepers near the entrance in The Coast , and will provide an introduction to the mechanic.
Breach | Overview | Breaches are split into two types: Unstable Breaches and Breach Hives. A Breach encounter will feature either one of these encounters, but never both. In maps, a Hive Fortress has a chance to spawn over Breach Hives. In maps, the chance to encounter a Breach Hive/Unstable Breach/Hive Fortress is approximately 40%/45%/15% respectively [1] [ confirmation needed because of as of 3.28 ]
Breach | Overview | All Breach encounters grant an amount of Hiveblood and a chance for one or more wombgifts to drop on successful completion.
Breach | Unstable Breach | Unstable Breaches appear as a massive Breach Hand. Touching it will open an Unstable Breach, expanding outwards for a duration while Breach monsters will spawn in. Breach monsters are unable to leave the circle. A progress bar will appear with two bars: one that increases based on killing Hiveborn monsters, and one that gradually increases over time. The goal is to fill the bar from killing Hiveborn before the timer catches up, collapsing the Breach encounter prematurely.
Breach | Unstable Breach | Defeating enough Breach monsters to fill up the bar will cause the timer to accelerate to max, then stabilizes the Breach, stopping the timer and Breach expansion. When this occurs, several Rare Hiveborn monsters (and sometimes in maps, Vruun, Marshal of Xesht ) near the location of the Breach Hand that must be defeated to successfully collapse the Stabilized Breach. Note that players are intentionally not expected to be able to stabilize Unstable Breaches during the earlier parts of the campaign.
Breach | Unstable Breach | After the Breach collapses, whether it was stabilized or not, loot will drop in a spiral near the character 's current location.
Breach | Unstable Breach | Vruun also always drops a rare Breach ring base type, and sometimes a Hivebrain Gland.
Breach | Breach Hive | Breach Hives appear as a large breach circle containing Breach monsters and semi-organic structures within them. Before beginning the encounter, players can destroy the Breach walls by approaching them or by hitting them. There are also several Flammable Burrows scattered within the Breach Hive, indicated as purple dots on the mini-map. Approaching them will create a large explosion that clears all walls within its radius and cause other nearby flammable burrows within range to explode as well. At the center of the Hive at the core (marked by a Breach hand on the minimap) is a button that will summon Ailith, which begins the encounter where the player must defend her against waves of monsters while she prepares a ritual to destroy the Hive.
Breach | Breach Hive | Once the encounter begins, walking near the hive walls or attacking them will no longer destroy them. The Hiveborn will spawn from rifts that can reach Ailith, indicated by the red dots on the minimap. As you progress through the waves, more of the hive walls may get destroyed. Destroying more of the structure before summoning Ailith will allow more monsters to approach and attack Ailith. Each wave progresses when you kill enough Hiveborn, with every new wave causing a pulse to release from the statue and spawning new enemies and potentially destroying more walls. Hive encounter consist of 5 to 8 waves of enemies.
Breach | Breach Hive | Ailith has a health bar with 20 segments somewhat similar to Blight ; being hit by Hiveborn monsters' skills causes Ailith to take damage to this health bar, and fully depleting the bar before completing the final wave will fail the encounter. Damage is roughly based on the enemy rarity and the strength of the attack, and Ailith has a brief period of invulnerability between taking damage with the duration proportional to the amount of damage taken. While Ailith is channelling, the player can use the nearby purple flames by interact with their icons to gain various helpful effects:
Breach | Breach Hive | Hiveborn monsters will generally prioritize attacking characters over Ailith, with an aggro range of approximately a screen wide.
Breach | Breach Hive | After completing a Hive encounter, loot will drop in a spiral at the statue's location. If the encounter is failed, all the loot from killed monsters will drop, but no Hiveblood or Wombgifts will be awarded.
Breach | Hive Fortress | In any tier of map , a Breach Hive may be replaced with a Hive Fortress , a side area containing more Hiveborn monsters. Hive Fortresses belong to the same instance as the main map. The area contains several "Grasping Coffer" chests that can sometimes contain wombgifts and Foulborn unique items.
Breach | Hive Fortress | In the center of the Hive Fortress, a more difficult version of a Hive encounter can be found. These encounters have 24 waves. During the encounter, additional purple flames (skills and buffs) will spawn once every few waves. Up to 6 purple flames can be held on reserve at a time, so it is recommended to use them liberally.
Breach | Hive Fortress | In addition to purple flame skills found in regular Hive encounters, there is one special skill available at the start:
Breach | Hive Fortress | After completing the Hive encounter, the Breach hand will start pulsing, doing damage across the whole area in intervals. The player must escape from the Hive Fortress successfully in order to collect their rewards. Hands will emerge from the walls to block off several paths and corridors; these appear in the minimap within a wide radius as a small grey hand icon. There is typically only one route to the outer ring of the arena which then leads directly to the exit, and it is possible to start planning the initial route of escape during the waves.
Breach | Hive Fortress | Escaping successfully will grant a significant amount of Hiveblood and drop several wombgifts and sometimes Foulborn unique items or a Hivebrain Gland.
Breach | Hive Fortress | Dying after starting the waves or while escaping will prevent re-entry and will drop rewards earned so far, but no Hiveblood or wombgifts.
Breach | Strategies | Breach rush strategy : as Hiveblood is not affected by IIQ or monsters killed, it can be reliably farmed using a memory thread map provided by Eagon ; instead of killing the map boss and completing the map, the player can rush to and complete the Breach encounter, then exit the map and re-open the same map. The Area is Cursed penalty does not impact Hiveblood acquisition, so this method can be used to have an infinite supply of maps to run without any investment into map sustain. However, wombgifts and other item drops will be negatively impacted by the drop penalty.
Breach (original) | Description | The original version of Breach was a portal that could appear in areas which, when touched, created an interdimensional rift that allows Breach monsters to spill into Wraeclast. It was introduced as part of the Breach league , and received a "sequel" in the Keepers temporary league which reworked it significantly before being fully replaced in version 3.28.0.
Breach (original) | Overview | Breaches will randomly spawn in an area in an inactive state. They're easily identified by the hand-like construct within a purple circle and purple swirls can be seen within the vicinity. Walking into the hand will activate the breach. Breaches can also be spawned using Vaal Breach , but enemies in these breaches do not give experience or drop items.
Breach (original) | Overview | Active breaches will expand their circle outwards and spawn a mix of breach monsters within the circle; the faster the monsters are killed the faster the circle expands. After a while, the expansion of the breach will slow down until it eventually retracts quickly and closes.
Breach (original) | Overview | Breaches stay open for a minimum of 30 seconds, increasing to a maximum of 60 based on how quickly breach monsters are killed. Normal monsters killed while in the breach do not increase the active time.
Breach (original) | Overview | Monsters moving outside of the active radius will despawn after a short delay. During this time, however, it is still possible to attack and be attacked by the monsters before they're removed. It is also possible for monsters inside the breach to hit the character while they are outside it.
Breach (original) | Overview | Breach monsters have increased item rarity and quantity, but have a reduced chance to spawn beyond demons and only rare breach monsters are able to drop maps. In addition there is a chance to obtain breach-specific unique items and splinters from these monsters as well as breach-exclusive Breach Rings.
Breach (original) | Overview | Occasionally, a Breachlord can spawn from a Breach. They will drop a number of Splinters when the breach collapses based on how much damage was dealt to them or the maximum of ten when defeated.
Breach (original) | Overview | Breaches also contain "Clasped Hands", a breach-specific type of chest that opens when a player walks near them. They come in two varieties, "Clasped Hand" or "<Breachlord>'s Clasped Hand". These chests can drop additional splinters and only appear when the breach expands to them. It is possible to see Breachlord specific Clasped Hands before opening the breach itself as a shimmering transparent object.
Breach (original) | Overview | There are fives types of breaches each associated with a damage type, which will affect accordingly
Breach (original) | Breach frequency | Breaches have a baseline greater than 8% chance to occur in maps by default. Xoph, Esh, and Tul Breaches are significantly more common than Uul-Netol or Chayula.
Breach (original) | Breach items | There are two types of currency and one other item class associated with breaches; each is specific to a breach type for a total of 15 currency items.
Breach (original) | Splinters | Splinters are dropped by Breach monsters or Clasped Hands within breaches. 100 Splinters of the same type can be combined into a Breachstone. Splinters obtained during a Breach encounter will drop at the end of the encounter in a single stack.
Breach (original) | Splinters | There is currently an issue with the currency tab; if you remove a stack of 100 splinters they will not upgrade to a Breachstone. In order to fix it, remove a single splinter and put it back on the stack.
Breach (original) | Breachstones | Breachstones are obtained from combining Splinters. They can be put into a map device in order to enter the associated domain of a Breachlord.
Breach (original) | Breachstones | The domain of a Breachlord is a unique area that contains one single large expanding breach and the domain's unique boss at the end. The breach is only active for a limited time that can be extended by killing breach monsters. When the boss area is reached the timer will stop; which allows for fighting the boss at any pace or picking up items that were left behind. Letting the timer run out before the breach fully expands will permanently collapse it for that instance.
Breach (original) | Blessings | Blessings are occasionally dropped by Breachlords in their base Breachstones. They can not be obtained outside of the Breachlord's domain, and are not guaranteed to drop.
Breach (original) | Blessings | Blessing can be used to upgrade Breachstones into their Flawless variants.
Breach (original) | Strategy | Since the breaches can spawn a very large number of monsters that hit hard is advisable to be cautious when opening breaches; death can come quickly and without warning.
Breach (original) | Strategy | Characters that have high survivability, high mobility, high damage output as well as good area clearing ability are best at effectively clearing breaches.
Breach (original) | Strategy | Strategies (not all may be suitable for your build):
Breach (original) | Trivia | Breach and Beyond have been confirmed to share an alternate dimension. [1]
Buff | Description | A buff is an effect that can modify an entity's statistics, and can be identified by a green border around its icon. [1] Buffs with primarily detrimental effects are debuffs and have a red border. [2]
Buff | Identifying a buff | Each buff affecting the player will display an icon with a green border in the top-left of the screen. [1] [2] This is one way to determine whether or not an effect is a buff - if it does not show an icon, it is not a buff that is attached to the player.
Buff | Identifying a buff | Charges and flask effects are not considered buffs.
Buff | The functioning of buffs | A buff adds statistics and modifiers to the creature it is attached to. Although a buff may increase the damage of a affected creature, a buff itself cannot deliver hits or take any action. A buff may include degeneration or damage over time effects. For example, if a monster is attacked by a player using the Wrath aura, the monster is not "hit" by the aura, or the buff, it is the player that hits the monster:
Buff | Buff duration | All buffs have a duration , which can be infinite (as in the case of auras ). This duration is affected by Buff Duration modifiers, and may be affected by Skill Effect Duration modifiers if the buff is considered a skill effect.
Buff | Buff duration | The passive skills which increase buff and debuff duration apply not to buffs on you but to buffs (including debuffs) you create, either on yourself or other entities. This includes all the above as well as such things as the debuffs placed on cursed monsters.
Buff | Buff duration | Buff expiration - Being cursed with Temporal Chains and having the Shaper's Presence buff can make Other effects on Cursed enemies expire % slower. These 2 mods are additive with one another and capped at 75%.
Buff | Buff effect | The effect of a buff can also be increased or reduced. Modifiers that increases Buff Effect increase the bonuses from buffs that affect yourself, that includes both positive and negative bonuses. Therefore one has to be careful when amplifying two-sided buffs.
Buff | Buff effect | Currently, the only source of #% increased Effect of Buffs on you comes from Ichimonji. This will for example increase:
Buff | Debuffs | A debuff is an effect that primarily grants a detrimental effect to the debuffed creature and can be identified by having a specific red border around the icon. For instance the damage over time from Bleeding or Poison are considered debuffs. [3]
Buff | Debuffs | Debuffs on enemies are not generally exposed to the player, though many have audible or visual effects. Non-damaging ailments in particular (other than freeze ) display their icon and effect under an affected enemy's life bar.
Buff | Related Effects | The legacy Unique Jewel Mantra of Flames has the unique mods Adds (3-5) to (8-12) Fire Attack Damage per Buff on You and Adds (2-3) to (5-8) Fire Spell Damage per Buff on You.

Burning | Description | Burning refers to any fire damage over time effect. Burning damage is a synonym for fire damage over time; all burning damage is fire damage over time, and vice versa.
Burning | Mechanics | There are several sources of burning, for example:
Burning | Mechanics | Different sources of burning damage stack cumulatively, but multiple applications from the same source do not. For example, two Spell Totem Support linked with Righteous Fire will not double the burn damage, however a Spell Totem Support linked with Righteous Fire together with a Searing Bond totem will stack with each other. Stacking rules for buffs , debuffs or other effects are defined in terms of that specific buff , debuff or effect interacting with other applications of the same effect, not with other ones that are similar. [1]
Burning | Mechanics | All burning effects will remain present on the target until they have run their course, but for each source, only the one with the highest damage per second will cause damage at any given moment. Humanoids, Monkeys and Snakes will flee while burning. [2]
Burning | Mechanics | As a damage over time effect, burning damage itself is not a hit and cannot benefit from effects that require a hit, such as Fire Penetration Support (but not reduced elemental resistances), added damage, leech , and so forth.
Burning | Mechanics | Burning damage can be increased by the Burning Damage Support support gem, and the following types of modifiers:
Burning | Mechanics | It is important to note that Burning and Ignite are not directly synonymous. Ignite is an elemental ailment which deals fire damage over time and is applied from hits with fire damage. All fire DoT effects are burning damage, but not all of them are ignite. This is a key point when considering buffs and supports such as Elemental Focus Support , which prohibits any elemental status ailment with the linked skill. However since burning damage itself is not an ailment, this support can be used to increase the damage of burning damage for skills that deal burns without igniting, such as Scorching Ray , Righteous Fire , and Searing Bond.
Burning | Related items | Certain unique items interact with burning. Effects specific to Ignite are listed in that page.
Cast speed | Description | Cast speed is a keyword and refers to the speed of using skills which are spells and is calculated as uses per second. Casting a spell consists of cast time and other time mechanics and spell effect. Cast speed is calculated as 1 second/cast time of spell.
Cast speed | Description | Cast speed can be found throughout the game, on passive skills , equipment , skill gems , monster affixes , map affixes, and so on.
Cast speed | Description | The base cast time is derived from the spell being used, it is the length of time required to cast a spell. Cast speed is a derived stat which is equal to 1 divided by Cast Time. Therefore if the cast speed is increased, the cast time is reduced. For example, if a player is using a skill with a base cast time of 0.8 seconds, and the player has a total of 50% increased Cast Speed , then the modified cast time can be calculated as follows: 1 / 0.8 = 1.25 casts per second base cast speed 1.25 ∗ ( 1 + 0.5 ) = 1.88 casts per second modified cast speed 1 / 1.88 = 0.53 seconds modified cast time \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\begin{aligned}1/0.8&=1.25{\text{ casts per second }}&{\text{base cast speed}}\\1.25*(1+0.5)&=1.88{\text{ casts per second }}&{\text{modified cast speed}}\\1/1.88&=0.53{\text{ seconds }}&{\text{modified cast time}}\end{aligned}}
Cast speed | Description | Frenzy charges increase cast speed by 4% per charge.

Chain | Description | Chaining is a behaviour of projectiles and chaining skills that causes them to bounce off their initial target and seek out another nearby enemy.
Chain | Mechanics | Chaining is primarily a way for projectiles to continue after colliding with an enemy, targeting a different enemy. Projectiles (that collide) are implicitly capable of chaining. Rain-type skills (e.g. Rain of Arrows ) and non-colliding projectiles (e.g. Explosive Concoction ) cannot chain. Skills capable of non-standard chaining or "bouncing" such as Arc , Rolling Magma , or Poisonous Concoction of Bouncing indicate this with the Chaining gem tag. [1] The number of times a projectile or chaining skill can chain is equal to the sum of all Skills Chain +# times modifiers.
Chain | Mechanics | As a projectile behaviour, chain is fourth in priority, preceded by split , pierce , and fork , and followed by return. Because only one projectile behaviour can occur per collision, a projectile will not chain if the projectile is also able to split, pierce, or fork.
Chain | Mechanics | Chaining does not allow shotgunning : enemies that were already hit by a skill use firing simultaneous projectiles cannot be hit again by chaining projectiles from that skill use (by any projectile in that set). Chain will prioritize targets that the projectile can still collide with. If no targets are eligible, the projectile will target a nearby enemy but pass through without colliding or dealing damage, and is not considered hitting that enemy. [2]
Chain | Mechanics | Additionally, if a projectile has remaining chains when hitting a target but no targets exist that it can chain to (as opposed to previously chained-to ineligible targets), that target is considered the final target. Even with Projectiles have #% chance to be able to Chain when colliding with terrain , projectiles will never inherently attempt to chain to terrain.
Chain | Mechanics | Most types of chaining require a target within range to occur. This range depends on the skill. Regular projectiles such as arrows have a chaining range of approximately 6 metres. Non-projectile skills typically have less: the chaining range of Exsanguinate appears to be around 5 metres, while the chaining range of Arc is 3.5 metres.
Chain | Mechanics | Similar to other projectile behaviours, on-collision effects such as Ice Shot and Kinetic Blast 's area damage effects will occur when a projectile chains. Effects that require a projectile to collide with a final target (or terrain), such as Fireball 's explosion or snares from Ensnaring Arrow , will not.

Channelling skill | Description | Channelling is a skill behaviour that allows a single use to last until the player releases its button, instead of finishing in one attack or cast time. [1]
Channelling skill | Mechanics | Channelling is one continuous attack or cast with a variable length, not repeatedly attacking or casting. This means:
Channelling skill | Mechanics | Channelling skills 'tick' based on the skill's attack or cast time, modified by attack or cast speed modifiers, as well as the user's action speed. The effect of each 'tick' depends on the skill: it could deal damage, apply a debuff, gain stages for a specific purpose, or even do nothing. It's possible for effects to occur every nth channelling tick rather than each time, or for no effect to occur until the channel ends entirely.
Channelling skill | Mechanics | Channelling can end in various ways:
Channelling skill | Mechanics | Instant skills such as Frostblink do not interrupt channelling.
Channelling skill | Mechanics | Costs are paid when beginning to channel, as well as on each channelling 'tick'. [4] Cooldowns on channelling skills begin when the channel is released. [5]
Channelling skill | Mechanics | Channelling skills cannot be exerted [6] , triggered [7] , repeated [8] , or be supported by Unleash Support. They can be used by some proxies , such as totems and mirages.

Character | Description | A character is a player-controlled persona in the game with a unique name in the game world.
Character | Character creation | After logging into Path of Exile a character can be created through the character creation screen.
Character | Character creation | A character can be created in different leagues and with additional difficulty options. The game recommends starting in the current challenge league for the most active economy.
Character | Character creation | Once the league has been chosen, a character class can be selected. The classes differ by starting location on the passive skill tree , the quest rewards they're given, by their base attributes and their general appearance and voice. They also each have different possible Ascendancy classes.
Character | Character creation | Players can freely choose their character's name; however, it cannot be assigned to any currently existing characters, and it is not possible to use non-ascii letters or numbers in the name. The only special character allowed is the underscore. If an account has remained inactive for over a year their character names will become available for other players to use when creating a new character. [1] Names of your existing characters can be changed from the official website here ; players can store up to 20 uses and accumulate two additional uses each week. [2]
Character | Character creation | By default only 24 characters can be created. After that existing characters have to be deleted in order to create new a one; however this limit can be extended by purchasing additional character slots from the Path of Exile Shop. Up to 255 characters can be created by purchasing Extra Character Slots. [3]
Character | Shared Stats | The stats found in the subsections can be found on every character, regardless of the character class.
Character | Character level | The character level is used for a variety of purposes, most importantly character level will be a limiting factor for equipment.
Character | Character level | The character level can be increased though gaining experience which is obtained by slaying monsters.
Character | Character level | Once a certain threshold is reached, the character will level up gaining one passive skill point and the following bonuses:
Character size | Description | Character size is a rare stat that alters the visual size of an actor's character model. This is a purely cosmetic function, and does not affect the character's collision radius or area of effect. [1]
Character size | Description | The increased character size of golem skills does not affect the player character, rather, it affects the golem's character itself.
Character size | Description | Increased character size is capped at 100%.
Chest | Description | Chests are interactable objects found throughout various areas that can be opened, broken, or activated to drop random or specific items.
Chest | Description | Chests generally drop items at the same level as the area level, and are affected by modifiers to area item quantity. [1] They are not affected by player quantity. [2]
Chest | Generic environmental containers | Generic environment containers are generated as part of specific tilesets. They may generate in random and in multiples. They generally have more generic and less desirable rewards.
Chest | Specific environment containers | These containers are found in specific, more deterministic places and generally have more specific and desirable rewards. They are rarely generated in multiples.
Chest | Relic chests | Relic Vaults are found in special Reliquary zones accessed via Reliquary Key items; contains foil uniques.
Chest | Relic chests | Singular Reliquary chests are found in Valdo's Puzzle Box maps after completing the map; contains foil unique.
Chest | Strongbox | For the mechanic, see Strongbox.
Chest | Incursion | Chests found in Temple of Atzoatl.
Chest | Delve | Chests found in Azurite mine.
Chest | Heist | Chests related to Heist.
Chest | Heist | The following small chests are specific to one or two Heist tilesets. They will drop random loot of a specific type such as weapons, armour, currency, essences and jewellery.
