Contraband | Description | Items dropped from Heist are marked Contraband , and Contraband is dropped if you die or leave a Heist in any way other than an Extraction Point. (In this in-game help text, Contraband means the loot, not the contraband indicator of the item.) Contraband items cannot be identified, equipped, crafted, used, or applied to other items.
Contraband | Description | Player cannot carry Contraband out of Heist by logging out or dying and re-spawn in town or checkpoint. By doing so, the loot would be dropped on the ground instead. Player can remove the contraband indicator from the item by exiting the wing either from the entry point or at an extraction point. Afterward, the item is considered a normal item.
Contraband | Description | To safely remove valuable Contraband found in Heists with less risk of being swarmed by enemies, players can simply return to the entrance crossroads and re-enter the wing, provided that the alarm has not gone off and/or the Curio Display was broken. When lockdown is active, dying means permanently losing all carried Contraband as the portal will be closed.
Corpse | Description | Most creatures leave corpses on the ground when killed. Totems , shattered monsters, and enemies destroyed by certain effects cannot leave corpses.
Corpse | Mechanics | Various mechanics interact with corpses. For example:
Corpse | Mechanics | Any mechanic that actively removes an existing corpse counts as consuming it. [3] This does not include removing corpses by spawning more than a skill's maximum. Removing corpses can be useful to prevent certain on-death effects, or enemy interactions with corpses, such as Necromancer monsters, strongboxes with the Putrifying Putrifying Prefix Detonates nearby corpses Chest plays warning sound (Hidden) prefix, or the "Explodes Corpses" monster modifier.
Corpse | Mechanics | Corpses can be targeted by holding the A key by default (PC), but only if the player has a skill that can target corpses.
Corpse | Mechanics | The amount of maximum life of the corpse scales with the area's level, capped at level 83 (same as tier 16 maps). Player-spawned corpses are not affected by the map's modifiers.
Corpse | Spectral Corpse | If a player has access to the regular Raise Spectre skill and has at least 1 monster saved in the spectre bank , using Desecrate or Corpse Walk has a 15% chance to spawn as a Spectral Corpse instead of a random area monster corpse (or 100% in hideouts ). The corpses can only be interacted with through minion skills, and cannot be otherwise detonated or consumed. Spectral Corpses have a visual effect applied to them to help differentiate them from other corpses.
Corpse | Spectral Corpse | Corpse items also create a Spectral Corpse on use.

Cost | Description | A cost is a property of skills. To use or trigger a skill, its cost must be paid. Most skills have a mana cost by default, though costs of life , energy shield , or rage are also possible. Reservations are not costs. [1] Soul requirements for Vaal skills are not costs. [2]
Cost | Mechanics | All skills have costs, even if those costs are zero. [3] Similar to other stats, costs may be modified by flat additions and subtractions, as well as by multipliers like increased, reduced, less, and more. Support gems are the most common cost multiplier; each support gem modifies a cost multiplicatively.
Cost | Mechanics | Upfront costs are all costs that are not paid per second. This distinction is necessary because some effects cannot apply to per-second costs found on Link skills. Channelling skills pay an upfront cost each channelling tick. [4]
Cost | Mechanics | Costs are paid, which typically causes resources to be spent. Losing resources through other means, such as sacrificing with Dark Pact , losing due to Apep's Rage , or spending for Arcane Cloak 's skill effect, is not considered paying a cost.
Cost | Mechanics | Totems (and other proxies ) make skills they use cost nothing. [5]
Cost | Base costs | Modifiers to base costs apply before both support gem multipliers and global modifiers to cost of skills.
Cost | Added costs | The following modifiers apply after support gem multipliers but before global modifiers to cost of skills:
Cost | Total costs | Modifiers to the total cost apply after other cost modifiers, but before effects that set costs to a specific value (like 0 with Lavianga's Spirit ). [7]
Cost | Skill costs | Note: this list does not include the following skills with alternative costs:
Crafting | Description | Crafting is a core mechanic of Path of Exile involving using currency or other techniques to modify the stats and properties of items. Almost all items interact with crafting mechanics in some way.
Crafting | Upgrading rarity | "Upgrading" refers to changing an item's rarity.
Crafting | Upgrading rarity | Some crafting methods are altered while you have certain Omens in your inventory:
Crafting | Reforging modifiers | "Reforging" refers to randomly rerolling all of an item's modifiers.

Crafting | Augmenting and removing modifiers | "Augment" refers to adding a single explicit modifier to an item. Magic items have a default modifier limit of 2 (1 prefix/1 suffix), while rare items have a default modifier limit of 6 (3 prefix/3 suffix). Rare jewels have a limit of 4 (2 prefix/2 suffix), and certain Experimented base type jewellery have different modifier limits.

Critical strike | Description | A critical strike is a type of hit that multiplies its damage by its critical strike multiplier. Critical strikes inherently gain 100% chance to ignite , freeze , and shock.
Critical strike | Mechanics | When a skill is used or triggers , it performs a critical strike roll. This roll ranges from 0 to 99.99, and determines the critical strike chance a hit must exceed to critically strike. [1]
Critical strike | Mechanics | While hits from the same skill will usually have the same critical strike chance, resulting in all-or-nothing behaviour, conditional modifiers such as Assassin's Mark or Brittle can cause critical strike chance to vary between enemies.
Critical strike | Critical strike chance | A hit's chance to crit is determined by calculating the following:
Critical strike | Critical strike chance | CriticalStrikeChance = ( BaseCriticalStrikeChance + AdditionalCriticalStrikeChance ) ∗ ( 1 + IncreasedCriticalStrikeChance ) ∗ ( 1 + MoreCriticalStrikeChance ) \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\text{CriticalStrikeChance}}=({{\text{BaseCriticalStrikeChance}}+{\text{AdditionalCriticalStrikeChance}})*(1+{\text{IncreasedCriticalStrikeChance}})*(1+{\text{MoreCriticalStrikeChance}})}
Critical strike | Critical strike chance | Base critical strike chance is the default crit value of a skill before any additional crit chance modifiers.
Critical strike | Critical strike chance | Additional critical strike chance is an addition to base crit before other modifiers apply. Concoction skills receive additional crit chance from their gem. Other sources include Brittle , Assassin's Mark , Increased Critical Strikes Support , Rigwald's Curse , and Seething Fury.
Critical strike | Critical strike chance | After base and additional are added together, multipliers such as increased and more apply. For example, if the player is using a weapon with 5% chance to crit, and has +1% to Critical Strike Chance and 50% increased Critical Strike Chance , hits will have 9% chance to crit.
Critical strike | Critical strike chance | Effects which prevent critical strikes (ex. Resolute Technique ) will take priority over effects that causes you to always deal critical strikes (ex. Diamond Shrine ).
Critical strike | Critical strike multiplier | Critical strikes cause hits to deal "extra damage" compared to a non-critical strike, the magnitude of which is determined by critical strike multiplier (i.e. crit multi). Player characters have a base crit multi value of 150%, while monsters have a base crit multi value of 130%, or 50% and 30% "extra damage" respectively. [2]
Critical strike | Reduced extra damage from critical strikes | Take #% reduced Extra Damage from Critical Strikes modifiers multiplicatively reduce the Critical Strike Multiplier exceeding the baseline damage (100%). [3] [4] Similar numerical modifiers stack additively and are capped at 100% reduced extra damage from critical strikes, which is equivalent to Take no Extra Damage from Critical Strikes. For example, a character with 30% reduced extra damage from critical strikes against a monster will be calculated as follows:
Critical strike | Ailments | Critical strikes inherently have always Ignite , always Freeze , and always Shock. [6] These ailments can still be discarded if they do not reach the minimum ailment threshold.
Critical strike | Ailments | Damaging ailments ( bleeding , poison , and ignite ) from critical strikes do not scale with crit multi by default, but inherently have +50% to Damage over Time Multiplier, additive with other sources of Damage over Time Multiplier stats. [7] Allocating Perfect Agony allows critical strike multiplier to scale the Damage over Time Multiplier value. [8]
Critical strike | Ailments | Minions and monsters both have an inherent +30% to Damage over Time Multiplier for Ailments from Critical Strikes , which is in line with, but also distinct from their default 130% Critical Strike Multiplier. [9]
Critical strike | Weapon critical strike potential | An exhaustive list of weapon base Critical Strike Chances. Weapons may have a higher base Critical Strike Chance with the proper Item affix. The second column for min/max values includes increases by local implicit modifiers on the weapon.
Critical strike | Skill critical strike potential | An exhaustive list of the base critical strike chances for spells and other skills with damage components that are not based on a weapon's critical strike chance.
Critical strike | Local critical strike chance | Items that have increases to their local critical strike chance.
Critical strike | Global critical strike chance | Items that have global critical strike chance or other interactions with global critical strike chance.
Critical strike | Critical strike multiplier | Items that have global critical strike multiplier or other interactions with global critical strike multiplier.
Critical strike | Other | Items with miscellaneous interactions with critical strikes.
Culling strike | Description | Culling Strike (also known as culling or cull ) is a property that causes hits to kill enemies left with 10% of maximum life or less. [1] [2]
Culling strike | Mechanics | Culling strike is an on-hit effect that kills the target if its current life is 10% or less of its maximum life after receiving damage. A culling strike occurs even if the the hit deals no damage or had its damage fully mitigated (Ex. "Avoid damage from hits"), but not if the hit itself was avoided (e.g. evasion or dodge ). Culling strike only cares about the target's life percentage and ignores energy shield and guard skills. A hit cannot cull if the damage of the hit kills the target.
Culling strike | Mechanics | Enemies can be culled regardless of their rarity , including bosses. However, it does not affect some enemies that have a scripted death, such as Uber Elder in its final phase, beasts during Bestiary encounters, or Catarina, Master of Undeath.
Culling strike | Mechanics | As culling is a property of hits, damage over time cannot cull. [3]
Culling strike | Mechanics | Culling strike is not considered damage, and will never provide overkill damage for mechanics such as Herald of Ash.
Culling strike | Mechanics | Certain similar effects also kill enemies at different life thresholds, such as Headsman (aka " Slayer cull"", 20%) and The Eternal Struggle (15%). These effects can proc effects that occur on culling strikes such as Goblinedge. However, it cannot proc the quality effect of Culling Strike Support if it does not meet the 10% threshold. It is possible for multiple thresholds of cull simultaneously if the hit reduces the target's life to below each threshold. For example, a hit that takes a target from 30% life to 8% life will simultaneously proc Headsman and Culling Strike Support 's quality effect.
Culling strike | Mods | Item modifiers
Damage effectiveness | Description | Damage effectiveness is a property of skills that modifies the base and added flat damage of hits , primarily to prevent skills from benefiting disproportionately from flat damage. Low values of effectiveness are characteristic of skills that have high multipliers in other aspects of their damage application, such as a rapid hit rate or large damage modifiers.
Damage effectiveness | Mechanics | Damage effectiveness exists for both base damage and added damage. It does not directly affect Gain #% of X damage as extra Y damage , which is a type of conversion.
Damage effectiveness | Base damage | Base damage is generally gained from a weapon by attacks , and from the skill gem by spells. Attack skills will display their base damage effectiveness at the top of their skill gem as Attack Damage: #% of Base. Spells have a base damage effectiveness of 100%, which is not displayed. [1]
Damage effectiveness | Added damage | Added damage is all flat damage that isn't base damage. It can be gained from a wide variety of sources, from gems and equipment to buffs and debuffs , and even mechanics like projectiles passing through a Flame Wall. If damage is added , it is modified by added damage effectiveness regardless of the source, including active skills that add damage to their own hits, like Fire Trap 's added Fire Damage against Burning Enemies. [2] Similar to base damage effectiveness, if a skill lists no added damage effectiveness, it is 100%. [3]
Damage effectiveness | Added damage | Added damage effectiveness for attacks is usually similar to their base damage effectiveness, though they are not necessarily identical.
Damage reduction | Description | Damage reduction is a specific defensive stat most commonly granted by armour against physical hit damage.
Damage reduction | Mechanics | 'Damage reduction' is a specific type of mitigation , primarily gained from armour against hits. Sources of additional damage reduction such as #% additional Physical Damage Reduction are additive with the amount calculated from armour (if any). Damage reduction can mitigate damage over time , though it can only be gained from armour against hits. Despite the generic name, it is unrelated to mechanics like resistances or modifiers to damage taken such as #% reduced Damage taken. [1]
Damage reduction | Mechanics | Damage reduction has a default maximum of 90% [2] and a minimum of 0%. [3] This applies after other modifiers: for example, if armour calculates 100% physical damage reduction against a certain hit, it will be capped to 90%. If the player is also debuffed for -15% by e.g. Penitent Mask 's Crushed , the final reduction will be 85%, not 75%.
Damage reduction | Physical damage reduction | Physical damage reduction is the most common form of damage reduction. It is the only type of damage reduction granted by armour by default. Additional physical damage reduction can be found on e.g. strength -aligned armour equipment and Endurance Charges.
Damage reduction | Physical damage reduction | Physical damage reduction can be lowered through effects such as Poacher's Mark or Crushed. There exists various modifiers that grant hits a chance to ignore physical damage reduction.
Damage reduction | Other damage types | Damage reduction of other damage types can be obtained through certain items or stats, such as Eternal Damnation , Unbreakable , Transcendence , Doryani's Prototype , or The Fourth Vow. Endurance charges also grant additional elemental damage reduction.

Damage reduction | Passive skills | The following passive skills affect damage reduction.
Damage taken | Description | Damage taken refers to the amount of damage taken after all mitigations have taken place. [1] It is a synonym of 'damage dealt', but from a defending standpoint.
Damage taken | Mechanics | Modifiers to 'damage taken' (except damage taken as ) apply to the value calculated after mitigation by resistances and armour. [2] [3] See also receiving damage.
Damage taken | Related skill gems | Skill gems that specifies damage taken.
Damage taken as | Description | Damage taken as , also known as damage shift , is a mechanic that allows damage from one damage type to be taken as another damage type. Most of these modifiers specify they only apply to hits; a few rarer sources also apply to damage over time. Damage shift is not conversion.
Damage taken as | Mechanics | On the receiving side, damage may be taken as a different type. [1] This is done before any mitigation. It is important to note that this is not damage conversion. [2] The shifted portion of the damage does not retain its original damage type , meaning that it will not get mitigated twice; only the final damage type applies. For example, if some of the incoming damage is shifted from physical damage to fire damage, the fire damage would not be mitigated by armour.
Damage taken as | Mechanics | Damage taken as is calculated simultaneously, this means that the incoming damage can be shifted to any other type of damage. For example The Rat Cage has #% of Fire Damage from Hits taken as Physical Damage , this modifier wouldn't have worked if it was a converted to -process. [3]
Damage taken as | Mechanics | Since damage taken as does all calculations simultaneously, this also means that the initial damage cannot be shifted between damage types more than once , preventing a loop. [4]
Damage taken as | Mechanics | This mechanic is useful against elemental penetration, especially against many boss attacks like Atziri's Flameblast (10% Fire penetration) or The Shaper's projectiles and bullet hell (25% Cold penetration), because for example if you have 50% Cold damage taken as Fire, then with a 1000 Cold hit and 75/75/75 res you would only take 500 * (1 - 0.75) + 500 * (1 - 0.75 + 0.25) = 375 damage instead of 1000 * (1 - 0.75 + 0.25) = 500 damage. If you manage to take 100% of the penetrated element as another element then you can completely nullify the effect of penetration (in the above example, a 1000 Cold hit would be taken as a 1000 Fire hit and mitigated with 75% Fire resist, resulting in 250 final damage taken).
Damage taken as | Mechanics | A word of caution: players should avoid having over 100% of a specific damage type taken as other damage types. As all of these stats apply simultaneously, exceeding 100% will cause the player to take more base damage than was originally taken. [5] [6]
Damage taken as | Interaction with reflect | Because "damage taken as" occurs before modifications to damage taken, stats such as #% reduced Reflected Physical Damage taken only apply to reflected damage taken as physical. A build that fully reduces reflected physical damage will still take reflected damage if physical damage is taken as elemental damage or chaos damage. (This does not apply to Cannot take Reflected Physical/Elemental Damage , which functions both before and after damage shifts, preventing this interaction.)
Damage taken as | Ailments and damage over time | Taking damage as cold or lightning damage will allow the portion of damage taken as those elements to chill you, or shock / freeze / sap / brittle you if you have a chance to have those ailments applied to you (e.g. via critical strike or hexes ).
Damage taken as | Ailments and damage over time | Damaging ailments, on the other hand, are based on the damage dealt, not damage taken [7] ; for example, when you have #% of Physical Damage from Hits taken as Fire Damage and physical damage is dealt to you, the taken fire damage never ignites you even if you have +100% chance to be Ignited. Theoretically, the physical damage could ignite you, but ignite does not consider physical base damage by default. [8] However, it is possible for the Physical Damage to Ignite you with modifiers such as Mokou's Embrace 's All Damage from Hits can Ignite you.
Damage taken as | Ailments and damage over time | On the other hand, taking 100% of Fire Damage from Hits as Physical Damage (e.g. The Rat Cage ) will allow the full Fire Damage to Ignite you, even if you only take Physical Damage from the hit itself.
Damage taken as | Ailments and damage over time | Bleeding can only be applied by physical attack damage. Secondary damage will never apply bleeding.
Damage taken as | Ailments and damage over time | A rarer version of this modifier that applies to non-hits (damage over time) (e.g. Cloak of Flame ) will also apply to damaging ailments. For example, if you take a Physical hit that applies Bleeding , you will take 40% of the Physical hit as Fire, be applied with a bleed based on 100% of the base Physical Damage, and take 60% of the Bleed DOT as Physical damage over time and 40% as Fire damage over time. The Fire damage over time is still considered Bleeding damage.

Delirium | Description | Delirium is a zone-wide effect that spawns new enemies and empowers existing ones. The Delirium Mirror version of the encounter is considered Extra Content and has a baseline greater than 8% chance to appear in any non-unique map area. Delirium orbs can also be applied to a map to add a baseline level of deliriousness and rewards; they can also be found with layers of Delirium on them (known as Delirium maps).
Delirium | Encounter rate | Delirium Mirrors can appear starting from Act 5 onwards at a rate of >8%. They stop appearing for characters at level 72 and higher for areas with level lower than 65 [1].
Delirium | Encounter rate | In maps , Delirium Mirrors have a baseline greater than 8% chance to appear in a zone. Delirium maps cannot normally drop but can be obtained from sources of Delirium rewards or with the Pathological notable atlas passive.
Delirium | Delirium Mirror | Randomly while players are completing the acts or running Maps , a Mirror of Delirium will spawn. They will always spawn within a close distance from the zone entrance. Once a player passes through it, it spawns a gray fog that spreads outwards throughout the map, beginning the Delirium encounter.
Delirium | Encounter | New enemies and hazards can spawn within the fog and existing enemies can receive a Delirium modifier , making them stronger or giving them new attacks. All enemies in the fog are Delirious, giving them increased damage and damage reduction.
Delirium | Encounter | In a Delirium mirror encounter, the further out you are in the fog, the stronger the deliriousness effect. In delirium maps, the deliriousness percentage remains constant.
Delirium | Encounter | Enemies killed in the fog in maps can drop Cluster Jewels and Simulacrum Splinters.
Delirium | Encounter | As you kill enemies inside the fog, a reward bar on the bottom left will start filling up. For Delirium mirror encounters, filling the bar completely will increase the counter, and cause you to gain the indicated reward type after the Delirium encounter ends. Additionally, when the first bar reaches level 3, a second reward bar will appear at level 1; at level 5, a third reward bar appears, and so on every 2 reward level.
Delirium | Encounter | Delirious maps do not grant additional reward bars at certain levels. All reward bars increase in level simultaneously instead and drop the indicated rewards each time you reach a new reward level instead of all at once after the encounter ends.
Delirium | Encounter | The Unending Nightmare keystone prevents Delirium mirror encounters from dissipating and also prevents them from being ended manually. Rewards are dropped on reaching a new reward level like Delirious maps, but will still grant an additional reward bar every 2 levels.
Delirium | Scaling | Higher percentages of Delirium increase both monster damage and monster damage reduction. Through empirical testing and official reference points at 100% Deliriousness, it was possible to obtain the following scaling estimates [2].
Delirium | Scaling | Additionally, it is speculated that it provides an overall more multiplier to monster item quantity and rarity [5] [ better source needed ]. However, there are several caveats to this that are being investigated by the Prohibited Library. Monsters from strongboxes [6] , as well as possibly other monsters that are not immediately spawned on entering an area, do not appear to be affected by this multiplier.
Delirium | Timer | Delirium mirror encounters only last a short period of time. After a certain period of time, the fog will stop spreading and start to dissipate outwards in a donut shape. If you step out of the fog for more than 5 seconds, the Delirium encounter will end. Delirium monsters disappear when they are outside the fog and native monsters will have their Delirium modifiers removed. The encounter can also be prematurely ended by pressing a button on the bottom right (which can be key bound). Certain actions will pause or extend the time before the fog stops spreading. The fog also stops moving while there are no players in the instance.

Delirium | Timer | The following will extend the fog timer:
Delirium | Timer | The Unending Nightmare Atlas keystone passive prevents the fog from dissipating. It also prevents you from manually ending the Delirium encounter.
Delirium | Strange Voice | Starting from The Torched Courts (Act 5) , a voice starts talking to the player whenever you touch a Mirror of Delirium. He has unique lines in Act zones.
Delirium | Delirious map modifier | Map items can be affected by a special modifier that covers the entire map in fog permanently, known commonly as Delirious maps. The mechanics are similar to the Delirium mirror encounter that can randomly occur in a map, with the following exceptions:
Delirium | Delirious map modifier | This modifier has five levels of strength, expressed as a percentage -- 20%, 40%, 60%, 80%, or 100%. The higher the percentage, the tougher the monsters and the greater the rewards. Enemies at very high Delirious percentages are extremely difficult, with even normal rarity enemies becoming comparable to high-tier map bosses.
Delirium | Delirious map modifier | Map items can drop with this modifier present at any of the five levels of strength. Delirium orbs can be used on map items. An orb adds 20% delirium to a map item that does not already have the delirious modifier, or increases the map's existing delirium strength by one level (20%).
Delirium | Unique bosses | Omniphobia (in any tier map) and Kosis (in T11+ maps) each have a chance to appear equal to the deliriousness percentage. Allocating Delusions of Persecution and its preceding small passive skills increases the chance to spawn these bosses by 156%, guaranteeing boss encounters in maps with at least 40% deliriousness.
Delirium | Other drops | Simulacrum Splinter , cluster jewels and Delirium orbs are obtained from Delirium encounters.

Difficulty | Description | Path of Exile had three difficulties prior to The Fall of Oriath expansion: Normal, Cruel, and Merciless. Currently there's a single storyline playthrough, without players having to replay the same acts multiple times.
Difficulty | Description | After completing Act 4 for the first time, players restarted the game in Act 1 at the Cruel difficulty, as long as they met the level requirement. After completing Act 4 on Cruel, the same process repeated for Merciless.
Difficulty | Description | Each difficulty level contained the same zones , monsters and quests. The difference in difficulty came from the zones being generated at a different level and hence monsters and items within them also being that level. The only structural differences was that The Twilight Strand does not have a waypoint in Normal difficulty, and The Eternal Laboratory is only a separate area with a map device on Merciless difficulty.
Difficulty | Description | Elemental and chaos resistance penalties and experience loss on death were solely tied on the difficulty the player was on. Switching difficulties modified these penalties.
Difficulty | Description | Difficulties also modified the required amount of Souls for vaal skill gems and the kills needed to enter rampage tiers.
Difficulty | Description | In addition to the experience loss, death in the Hardcore league moves the character from that league and into the Standard league. It's important to note that characters that die in a hardcore challenge league are also moved to Standard, NOT to the respective softcore challenge league.
Difficulty | Description | Upon going to the next difficulty characters did not lose access to the zones of previous difficulties, and could travel back to them from any waypoint.
Difficulty | Bandit rewards | The Deal with the Bandits quest gave different rewards for each difficulty.
Difficulty | Achievements | 6 achievements were modified with the removal of difficulty levels.
Distance | Description | Distance in Path of Exile is measured in metres.
Distance | Description | The base range of a melee weapon is displayed as a numeric value in its infobox with the label "Weapon Range". Additionally, modifiers to melee strike range are described as numeric values. Other than these, distances are not typically made known to the player through the game's user interface as explicit numeric values. In the few cases where a distance value is given, such as Elemental Proliferation Support , that value is a measure of the radius of an area of effect.
Distance | Mechanics | All game entities are squares, defined by a radius (the squares are circles defined by using manhattan distance. [1] Entities that are several screens away from a character are "asleep" and take no actions. Entities that are outside this sleep range of the player's character do not exist on the player's game client (but may still be awake if in range of a different player). The exception to this is other player characters, who are always awake. If another player fires a projectile while outside your sleep range, it may not be able to create the projectile on your client.
Distance | "Nearby" | The word "nearby" is used in the descriptions of many skill effects, passive bonuses, and item modifiers. "Nearby" is not a keyword ; it merely indicates that an effect applies in a circular area, usually with its radius extending from the character or source of the effect. [2] [3] In some cases, such as the poison spreading effect granted by Bino's Kitchen Knife , the radius extends from an enemy that the character interacts with. Nearby as a term is unrelated to whether or not an area can be modified by area of effect modifiers.
Distance | "Nearby" | In descriptions where "nearby" is used, the actual radius of the area of effect is not given. The radius may be small and just beyond melee weapon range, or large as to cover most of the screen, or anything in between. This is a common source of confusion for players who assume that "nearby" is a keyword that means a specific measurement, similar to how the keyword " recently " always means "within the last four seconds". [4] [5] [6] [7]
Distance | "Nearby" | Effects that search for entities in an area (either 'nearby' or 'in your presence') do not find non-blocking objects [8] or untargetable/invulnerable bosses during their scripted phases. [9]
Distance | "In your presence" | Modifiers and stats that take effect when certain types of monsters are "in your presence" such as eldritch implicit modifiers or Loyalty tattoos have a fixed distance of 8 metres.
Distance | Collation of known distances | The following table is an attempt to document most distances through empirical testing and datamined values.
Dodge | Description | Dodge is a layer of defence that provides a chance to prevent hits.
Dodge | Mechanics | Whether a character dodges a hit is determined by their chance to dodge, which is capped at 75%. Dodge is rolled randomly each time the character would be hit. On a successful dodge, the character does not take the hit. For this reason, dodge is handled before block and avoidance , both of which provide a chance to mitigate the damage of hits rather than preventing them outright. Dodge is not affected by the enemy's accuracy.
Dodge | Sources of dodge | The only source of dodge is the Acrobatics keystone, which provides a chance to dodge spell hits from spell suppression modifiers.
Double damage | Description | Double damage is an effect that causes a hit to deal double its damage. Double damage does not stack with and is overridden by triple damage.

Double dipping | Description | Double dipping was an unofficial name for a game mechanic when the same damage modifier applies twice to a single damage source. This mechanic primarily applied to damage over time ailments , prior to its rework in Version 3.0.0.
Double dipping | Description | Previously, ailments dealt damage based on the final hit after damage modifiers, which meant if a damage modifier applies to both the hit and the ailment, then the ailment will gain increased damage on top of the damage increase of the initial hit.
Double dipping | Mechanics | These are the conditions for double dipping to occur:
Double dipping | Mechanics | Then the interaction can be explained as follows:
Double dipping | Mechanics | As a result the modifier has been applied twice to the second modifier. It's worth to note that the second time it applied it multiplied itself.
Double dipping | Examples | (IGNITE VALUE IS OUTDATED: 1.2 -> 2.25)
Double dipping | Ignite | Let's use Fireball for this example. It is a fire based spell so both #% increased Elemental Damage and #% increased Spell Damage can scale it. Since the skill deals fire damage it is possible to ignite enemies, dealing 20% of the initial hit as fire damage over time. This is a different damage source compared to the initial Fireball projectile so it's possible for double dipping to occur if the right stat is used.
Double dipping | Ignite | Assume that the character uses a level 20 Fireball and has 100% increased Elemental Damage that affects the skill gem.
Double dipping | Ignite | In this case the 100% increased Elemental Damage was applied twice because it can apply to different damage sources.
Double dipping | Ignite | Assume that the character uses a level 20 Fireball and has 100% increased Spell Damage that affects the skill gem.
Double dipping | Ignite | In this case the 100% increased Spell Damage didn't apply twice because ignite damage, which is a damage over time, does not scale off spell damage.
Dual wielding | Description | Dual wielding refers to using a one-handed weapon in both hands.
Dual wielding | Mechanics | Dual wielding grants player characters these inherent bonuses:
Dual wielding | Mechanics | Additional bonuses for dual wielding can be obtained from other sources, primarily passive skills. Weapons do not have to be of the same type to receive dual wielding bonuses. There are no penalties of any kind to attacks with the player's off-hand weapon.
Dual wielding | Mechanics | The majority of attack skills will alternate between equipped weapons per skill use, swinging first with the main hand and then with the off-hand weapon. The resulting attack time is the average of the two hands' attack times (which is not the same as averaging the attack speeds). [1] Some skills (e.g. Cleave , Dual Strike ) attack with both weapons simultaneously, in which case the skill directly averages the attack time of the two hands (except Dual Strike of Ambidexterity ). Skills that use both weapons simultaneously typically calculate damage per weapon and then combine their damage (except Viper Strike , which hits separately).
Dual wielding | Mechanics | Skills must be compatible with with both equipped weapons to be usable. For example, Reave cannot be used with a dagger and a sceptre.
Dual wielding | Mechanics | When dual-wielding weapons with different range, the range used is dependent on the skill. [2]
Dual wielding | Mechanics | It is possible to dual-wield two wands ; it is not possible to dual-wield a wand and a melee weapon. If a player was able to somehow equip a wand and a melee weapon simultaneously, the wand would be disabled.
Dual wielding | Mechanics | Unarmed attacks normally count as using the main hand, even if the offhand is empty. The skill animations may appear to alternate hands; this is purely visual and does not affect skill calculations. The Counts as Dual Wielding stat found on Hollow Palm Technique causes unarmed attacks to alternate between hands, however. [3]

Duration | Description | Duration is a keyword that refers to the attribute of certain effects that continue over time, and specify how long the effect remains.
Duration | Skill effect duration | Duration most commonly refers to Skill Effect Duration , a stat and modifier which can increase or reduce the duration of effects of many skills and secondary effects from support gems. Note that not all timed effects from skills are considered skill effects.
Duration | Skill effect duration | Vaal Skills have mechanic known as Soul Gain Prevention , which essentially acts similar to a cooldown. For any Vaal skills with a duration tag, modifiers to skill effect duration also modify the Soul Gain Prevention time.
Duration | Ailment duration | All ailments have a fixed base duration , except for Freeze which scales with the ailment threshold of the hit. These durations can be modified, but are not considered skill effects and therefore cannot be modified by skill effect duration modifiers.
Duration | Ailment duration | Viper Strike and Puncture are unique in that they have overrides for the default poison and bleed duration respectively with a skill effect, allowing poisons applied by Viper Strike and bleeds applied by Puncture to be modified by skill effect duration modifiers.
Duration | Stun duration | Stuns last for a period of time depending on the relative amount and type of damage of a hit as well as Stun Duration modifiers, stun threshold, and stun recovery.
Duration | Trap duration | Traps remain armed for a limited duration, after which they expire. Most traps are triggered automatically when they expire, regardless of whether there are any enemies nearby. Trap duration does not affect the duration of skill effects of the skills used by traps and vice versa.
Duration | Mine duration | Mines remain active for a limited duration, after which they expire. If a mine is not detonated before it expires, it is destroyed without triggering. Mine duration does not affect the duration of skill effects of the skills used by mines and vice versa.
Duration | Totem duration | Totems from skills (not the monster type) remain active for a limited duration, after which they die. Totem duration does not affect the duration of skill effects of the skills used by totems and vice versa.
Duration | Buff duration | Certain buffs with a duration cannot be modified by skill duration effect even if they are obtained from a skill. However, some of these buffs can be modified by other means. Some examples include:
Duration | Buff duration | Buff/debuff expiration rate indirectly affects buff/debuff duration, causing the total duration to complete at an increased or decreased rate. The numerical duration of the effect is unchanged. [1]
Duration | Buff duration | Flasks last for a fixed period of time when used or triggered. Utility flasks can have their durations modified by adding quality or using an Enkindling Orb. Additionally, various modifiers can affect flask duration. While most effects from flasks last for the duration of the flask effect, certain modifiers (e.g. magic flask suffixes that grant immunity to certain ailments or effects if removed from the character or the Onslaught from Rotgut ) have effect durations independent of flask duration.
Duration | Buff duration | Charges last for a set duration, and all stacks of a given Charge are lost upon the duration hitting zero. Various items and passive skills can modify charge duration.
Duration | Cooldown | Cooldown is the lockout time between skill uses with a cooldown , and can only be modified by Cooldown Recovery Rate modifiers.
Duration | Mechanics | The duration of a skill effect can be altered with modifiers such as #% increased/reduced [effect] Duration where all increased/reduced modifiers are summed together and #% more/less [effect] Duration where the product of all more/less modifiers are calculated.
Duration | Mechanics | The total duration value can be calculated as the sum of any added duration, multiplied by the sum of all increases and reductions to duration, multiplied by all more and less duration modifiers.
Duration | Mechanics | duration t o t a l = ∑ i = 1 a added duration i × ( 1 + ∑ j = 1 b increased duration j − ∑ k = 1 c reduced duration k ) × ∏ l = 1 d ( 1 + more duration l ) × ∏ m = 1 e ( 1 − less duration m ) \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\begin{aligned}{\text{duration}}_{total}=&\sum _{i=1}^{a}{\text{added duration}}_{i}\times \\&\left(1+\sum _{j=1}^{b}{\text{increased duration}}_{j}-\sum _{k=1}^{c}{\text{reduced duration}}_{k}\right)\times \\&\prod _{l=1}^{d}(1+{\text{more duration}}_{l})\times \prod _{m=1}^{e}(1-{\text{less duration}}_{m})\end{aligned}}
Duration | Linger | Linger is a keyword that refers to buffs and debuffs that can constantly affect a character , ally , or enemy , and can also persist for a duration once they are no longer constantly affected.
Duration | Cluster Jewel Passives | No results found for the given query.
Effect | Description | Active and temporary effects can be placed on characters. strengthening or weakening the character considerably. They are shown on the top left corner with a short description when hovered over.
Effect | Types of effects | Effects can both be negative or positive depending on if it was an enemy, the character or an ally that inflicted it. They're often inflicted by auras , curses , when within ground effects or when the character is hit by special skills. Many of them are active for a short duration , some of them can also stack leading to even stronger effects.
Effect | Buffs | Buffs have a green border and are shown in one row at the upper left corner. These can originate from skill gems, passive skills and unique items.
Effect | Buffs | Minions and totems also generate icons. They always precede the temporary effects and are separated by a bar.
Effect | Debuffs | Debuffs have a red border and are shown in separate row below Buffs / positive effects. These can originate from skill gems, passive skills and unique items.
Effect | Flask Effects | All the utility flasks and all the affixes on them can create gold bordered temporary effects. Futhermore certain uniques like Doryani's Invitation grant additional temporary effects while other flasks effects are active. Some unique flasks also grant additional effects like Divination Distillate. Flask effects overwrite each other the only exception is which shows the implicit mod of an Quicksilver Flask with a of Adrenaline suffix, both count as different effects.
Effect | Charges | The first number show the duration left, after which the charges expire. The number below is the quantity of those charges.
Effect | Skills | Certain skills display a icon indicating the current state of some mechanic. The first shows Reave and the second a shrine , which is considered a skill as well. They have the same border colour as charges. There's been no need to distinguish the two thus far. [1]
Effect | Minions & Totems | Shows a list of minions. The number indicates the number of minions of those kind, if there is only one a red life bar is shown instead. For more information, see the Minion and Totem articles.
Eldritch altar | Description | When you slay monsters in maps that are influenced by The Searing Exarch and The Eater of Worlds , an altar may appear at their corpses. These Altars can be used to further control the risk and reward of these maps. [1]
Eldritch altar | Mechanics | Eldritch altars have a chance to appear when killing Exarch-influenced or Eater-influenced monster packs. Influenced monster pack size does appear to affect the average number of altars encountered.
Eldritch altar | Mechanics | Each altar presents a choice between two options, each with an Upside modifier and a Downside modifier. The options are chosen at random between two of three modifier categories: "Map Boss (Boss)", "Eldritch Minions (Monster)", and "Player (Player)" effects.
Eldritch altar | Mechanics | Eldritch Altar effects persist throughout the remainder of the map and cannot be removed. It is possible to read these modifiers by hovering over the altar icon that appears on the lower right side of the screen after interacting with at least one Eldritch Altar.
Eldritch altar | Mechanics | Using an Eldritch Altar will also spawn a pack of Eldritch Minions at its location.
Eldritch altar | Mechanics | Eldritch Altar effects can be modified through the Atlas keystones Wrath of the Cosmos or Eldritch Gaze , making the modifiers more rewarding but also significantly more deadly.
Elemental proliferation | Description | Elemental proliferation is a modifier that causes elemental ailments on an enemy to also affect nearby enemies.
Elemental proliferation | Mechanics | Proliferation adds a radius to debuffs that normally don't have a radius, which causes them to apply in an aura -like area around the affected enemy. [1] Proliferating an ailment does not inflict new ailments; it causes other enemies to be affected by the ailment that already exists. [2] An enemy with a proliferated ailment will not proliferate that ailment themselves, similar to how an aura that affects an ally doesn't also spread from that ally. [3]
Elemental proliferation | Mechanics | Because elemental ailments aren't removed when enemies are killed, proliferation can continue from corpses until the ailment's duration expires, provided the corpse is not destroyed or consumed. If a player's ailment is reflected , like with The Fulcrum , that ailment can proliferate from the player to nearby enemies. Ailments from self-damage cannot proliferate, as they are not affected by offensive modifiers.
Elemental proliferation | Mechanics | The area of proliferation is affected by modifiers to area of effect. [4] Proliferation does not cause damaging ailments to scale with modifiers to area damage.
Elemental proliferation | Mechanics | Additional effects built into an ailment such as Enemies Ignited by you have. will also be spread by proliferation. Proliferation does not , however, count as inflicting the ailment for stats like when you Ignite , for each time you have Shocked Recently , or Cover Enemies in Ash for 5 seconds when you Ignite them.
Elemental proliferation | Mechanics | Proliferation has no interaction with ailments from ground effects or chilling areas.
Elemental proliferation | Mechanics | On-kill effects like Berek's Respite , Abberath's Hooves , Master Toxicist or Bino's Kitchen Knife are not proliferation. [5] These inflict new ailments, with their own rules to determine magnitude and duration. They also do not have a modifiable area.
Energy shield | Description | Energy shield is a form of defence that acts as an additional hit point pool on top of life. Along with armour and evasion , energy shield is one of the three defence types that can implicitly appear on equipment. Unlike life, energy shield will recharge naturally after the character has not taken any damage for 2 seconds.
Energy shield | Description | Every class starts with no energy shield, and gains 2% increased maximum energy shield every 10 intelligence.
Energy shield | Mechanics | When a player gains any amount of maximum energy shield from a maximum of 0 ES, energy shield will begin recharging immediately. If maximum energy shield increases or decreases to a non-zero value, the current ES value changes to the same relative percentage of maximum energy shield. [1]
Energy shield | Damage mitigation | If the character has any energy shield remaining when damage is taken, even damage from Labyrinth traps, that damage is inflicted on energy shield first. Physical damage reductions and elemental resistances applies to damage before it is deducted from energy shield. Damage is only applied to life or mana once all energy shield is depleted. The exception to this is chaos damage , which bypasses energy shield.
Energy shield | Recharge | Recharge is active until it is interrupted by damage to energy shield, or damage to the status energy shield protects—normally life, or mana with Eldritch Battery [2]. It is not interrupted by reaching full energy shield or by loss from non-damage sources or skill costs. [3]
Energy shield | Recharge | Energy shield will start recharging if the character does not take any damage for a certain period of time. By default, this time is 2 seconds. It can be reduced with #% faster start of Energy Shield Recharge modifiers from passive skills and equipment.
Energy shield | Recharge | Let r be the sum of #% faster start of Energy Shield Recharge modifiers (as a percentage). The delay period in seconds is given by:
Energy shield | Recharge | Delay Period = 200 100 + r \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\text{Delay Period}}={200 \over 100+r}
Energy shield | Recharge | For example, having 100% faster start of Energy Shield Recharge results in a delay period of 1 second.
Energy shield | Recharge | Energy shield recharge rate modifies recovery from recharge and is by default:
Energy shield | Recharge | This recharge rate can be increased with #% increased Energy Shield Recharge Rate modifiers.
Energy shield | Recharge | With Eternal Youth , recharge rate is 33.33% of life instead.
Energy shield | Stun prevention | While the character has any energy shield remaining, the character has a 50% chance to ignore being stunned. This bonus is not additive with other stun avoidance modifiers from passive skills and equipment; the chance to ignore stun granted by energy shield is rolled separately. [4] This avoidance does not require damage to reach energy shield; it will work even when all damage is taken by an Aegis or Ward first, or bypasses energy shield due to Divine Flesh. It is disabled by Eldritch Battery [5] even when damage can still be taken by energy shield through Mind Over Matter.
Energy shield | #% increased Energy Shield | Unique items that increase or decrease the global energy shield rating by a percentage.
Energy shield | +# to maximum Energy Shield | Unique items that grant a flat bonus to the global energy shield rating.
Energy shield | #% increased Energy Shield Recharge Rate | Unique items that grant #% increased Energy Shield Recharge Rate.
Energy shield | #% faster start of Energy Shield Recharge | Unique items that grant faster start of Energy Shield Recharge.

Evasion | Description | Evasion is the first layer of defence that affects a character 's chance to evade incoming attacks. Evasion is opposed by the attacker's accuracy. Evasion is one of the four core defences that can appear locally on equipment , along with armour , energy shield and ward.
Evasion | Description | All classes start with 15 base evasion rating. Gaining a level does not implicitly grant an increase to evasion. [1].
Evasion | Description | Dexterity grant a bonus to evasion. Every 5 points of dexterity grants 1% increased Evasion Rating. Values of dexterity that are not multiples of 5 will be rounded up to the nearest multiple of 5 (e.g. 141 dexterity will be rounded to 145).
Evasion | Mechanics | Evasion prevents hits by attack skills. Spells cannot be evaded. The chance to evade an attack is based on the defender's evasion rating, though the actual chance to be hit by an attack also depends on the attacker's accuracy. Because chance to hit cannot be lower than 5%, chance to evade cannot exceed 95%.
Evasion | Mechanics | Chance to Evade = 1 − Attacker's Accuracy ∗ 1.25 Attacker's Accuracy + ( Defender's Evasion × 1 5 ) 0.9 \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\text{Chance to Evade}}=1-{{\text{Attacker's Accuracy}}*1.25 \over {\text{Attacker's Accuracy}}+({\text{Defender's Evasion}}\times {\frac {1}{5}})^{0.9}} [2]
Evasion | Mechanics | There are two modifiers which bypass evasion: Cannot Evade enemy Attacks (from for example the Unwavering Stance keystone or Ezomyte Peak ), and attacks using Hits can't be evaded.
Evasion | Mechanics | Evasion also gives an implicit chance to not receive critical strikes from attacks. [3] If an incoming critical strike hit succeeds the initial hit/miss roll, a secondary check is performed to determine if it is a critical strike. If the first roll succeeds but the second roll fails, the non-crit damage is applied. Spell critical strikes ignore evasion.
Evasion | Mechanics | Evasion does not calculate the chance of each hit independently. Instead, it uses a deterministic "entropy" based system to ensure that enemies won't get long strings of hits or misses by chance. [3] To summarize, these are the calculation steps in each attack:
Evasion | Mechanics | As a result, if a player has a 1 in N chance to be hit, then the player will be hit exactly once for every N consecutive attacks. This eliminates all possibilities of lucky and/or unlucky streaks. It is still based on chance because of the entropy's value randomization in the first step. Note that if multiple mobs are attacking one character, all of the mobs' attacks share the same entropy value. [4] Also note that the chance to evade calculation on the character page is based on the average accuracy of a monster at the player's level.
Evasion | Interaction with Avoidance | Chance to Avoid X Damage is separate from evasion and chance to hit, and does not contribute to the calculation. As avoidance still is considered taking a hit, the evasion roll occurs prior to avoidance.
Evasion | Modifiers to chance to hit and chance to evade | Certain modifiers apply directly to the Chance to Hit and Chance to Evade stats, such as +(5-8)% chance to Evade Attack Hits while affected by Grace from Watcher's Eye. These modifiers are unaffected by modifiers to Accuracy or Evasion Rating, but will be scaled by modifiers to Chance to Hit/Chance to Evade.

Exerting | Description | Exerting is a mechanic that allows skills to enhance subsequent attacks performed by the character. It is primarily associated with Warcries , though not exclusive to them.
Exerting | Mechanics | Skills that exert other attacks cause the next attack(s) to be enhanced in certain ways, depending on the exerting skill. An exerting skill may be able to exert a number of attacks, and one attack can be exerted by multiple skills, if the type of attack is valid for each. The number of exerted attacks remaining is displayed on the Skill bar icons. Exerting has no duration. [1]
Exerting | Mechanics | Exerting applies to entire attacks, not to individual hits : exerting a skill like Rage Vortex will enhance all hits from that attack for its entire duration. [2]

Exerting | Mechanics | Note that attacks by Mirage Warriors count as exerted by General's Cry , including skills that could not be exerted by the player, like Blade Flurry.

Expedition | Description | Expedition is the league mechanic of Expedition league , released in version 3.15.0 which the player can first encounter in Act 6. This encounter is considered Extra Content and has a baseline greater than 8% chance to appear in any non-unique map area.
Expedition | General Mechanic | The player will encounter one of the four Expedition NPCs amidst heaps of dirt, skulls, various small flags and unearthed remnants. The player can place up to five explosives in the area marked by dirt heaps, which detonate one after the other with a short delay. Each remnant affected by explosives will apply its modifiers to the monsters and chests unearthed around it and those of each subsequent explosion. Each explosion will unearth monsters and treasures inside the blast area, which drop items and artifacts. Expedition chests and enemies sometimes drop special currency items that can be used to refresh the the items offered by Expedition NPCs. Runic monsters also have a chance to drop Expedition Logbooks.
Expedition | General Mechanic | Logbooks can be taken to Dannig , then you can select which area to go to to determine the area's modifiers and what type of artifact it contains. They open portals to larger Expedition areas with more remnants, flags and more placeable explosives. These areas also contain loot in caves hidden behind rock walls, that have to be affected by an explosive to become accessible. Logbook encounters can also spawn an Expedition boss, based on the faction.
Expedition | General Mechanic | After completing an encounter the player can trade their currency on site with the respective NPC or in town.
Expedition | General Mechanic | There are three kinds of markers which can be excavated with explosions:
Expedition | General Mechanic | Logbooks and refresh currencies can be stored in the Expedition Locker hideout decoration. Number of currently owned artifacts can also be seen there. Expedition affinity can be toggled on at the bottom of the interface, so any logbooks and refresh currency deposited in the stash will go in the locker instead.
Expedition | Trading | Trading currency found in unearthed chests introduces a second layer of complexity to the Expedition mechanic. The list below shows which member of the Kalguuran expedition the player can trade their currency with. Each NPC offers a different set of items:
Expedition | Expedition factions | Expeditions are related to one of the four Vendors e.g. if a player wants Exotic Coinage , they need to look for Black Scythe Mercenaries.
Expedition | Artifacts | Artifacts are not tradable.
Expedition | Items | Expedition chests and monsters drop Expedition currencies as well as Expedition Logbooks. Modifiers to increased item quantity of the area will affect the drop rate of both.
Experience | Description | Experience , commonly abbreviated to XP or EXP , is a game mechanic that allows characters to level up. When a character's current experience bar is full, they will level up, setting their current level's progress to 0%. Experience is primarily gained through killing monsters , though certain mechanics such as The Forbidden Sanctum , Trial of the Ancestors , and Betrayal encounters can also grant additional experience. Players can lose experience by dying, but cannot go below 0% experience or lose levels.
Experience | Experience table | The amount is the same for every character in every league. The number shows how much total experience is necessary to reach the level.
Experience | Death | Death occurs when the player's Life reaches 0 [1]. Loss of experience is incurred immediately upon death. The penalty is a percentage of the total required for the next level, depending on the area the player dies in, or its area level (e.g. in the Azurite Mine ):
Experience | Death | Losing experience in this way will not cause you to go under 0% experience or to lose a level.
Experience | Experience penalties | The player suffers a penalty to experience gained if the player is too far above or below the monster's level. There is a safe level range where no penalty is applied, which is equal to three plus one for every sixteen complete player levels: [2]
Experience | Experience penalties | SafeZone = ⌊ 3 + PlayerLevel 16 ⌋ \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\text{SafeZone}}=\left\lfloor 3+{\frac {\text{PlayerLevel}}{16}}\right\rfloor
Experience | Experience penalties | For example, a level 24 character has a safe zone of 4 levels. Any additional level difference in excess of this safe range is the effective level difference. So from monster level 20 to 28, there is an effective difference of 0; at monster levels 19 and 29, the effective difference is 1.
Experience | Experience penalties | EffectiveDifference = max ( | PlayerLevel − MonsterLevel | − SafeZone , 0 ) \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\text{EffectiveDifference}}=\max \left(|{\text{PlayerLevel}}-{\text{MonsterLevel}}|-{\text{SafeZone}},0\right)
Experience | Experience penalties | A monster at a certain level will give a certain amount of experience. If the player is outside the safe zone the following multiplier will be applied to the raw experience earned from the monster, with a minimum of 1% of the raw experience:
Experience | Experience penalties | For player levels below 95: XPMultiplier = max ( ( PlayerLevel + 5 PlayerLevel + 5 + EffectiveDifference 2.5 ) 1.5 , 0.01 ) \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\text{XPMultiplier}}=\max \left(\left({{\text{PlayerLevel}}+5 \over {\text{PlayerLevel}}+5+{\text{EffectiveDifference}}^{2.5}}\right)^{1.5},0.01\right)
Experience | Experience penalties | For player levels equal to or higher than 95: XPMultiplier = max ( ( PlayerLevel + 5 PlayerLevel + 5 + EffectiveDifference 2.5 ) 1.5 ∗ 1 1 + 0.1 ∗ ( PlayerLevel − 94 ) ∗ 1 3.1 XP Penalty , 0.01 ) \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\text{XPMultiplier}}=\max \left(\left({\frac {{\text{PlayerLevel}}+5}{{\text{PlayerLevel}}+5+{\text{EffectiveDifference}}^{2.5}}}\right)^{1.5}*{\frac {1}{1+0.1*({\text{PlayerLevel}}-94)}}*{\frac {1}{\text{3.1 XP Penalty}}},0.01\right)
Experience | Experience penalties | 3.1 XP Penalty is a new penalty for level 95 and above [3] listed in the following table:
Experience | Experience penalties | Continuing our example, a level 24 character receives 95% experience for level 19 monsters, 52.5% experience for level 17 monsters, and 20% experience for level 15 monsters.
Experience | Experience penalties | The plot below displays how the experience penalty varies with different zone and player levels. Notice that the safe zone with no experience penalty gets larger with higher player levels and that near max level it is impossible to play with no experience penalty.
Experience | Experience penalties | By following the safe zone recommendations for each player level a high experience gained per map ratio is guaranteed. However that does not necessarily mean it is the most efficient use of a players time. For example the difficulty in the safe zone might be too high leading to the map being cleared slowly and a low experience gained per hour even if the experience gained per map is high. Therefore to level efficiently a high experience gained per hour is necessary, not staying inside the safe zone of the experience penalty.
Experience | Experience penalties | Areas with monster level above 70 are considered to have a lower monster level for the purpose of experience penalty calculations. [4] This has no effect on the stats of the monsters in the area or the loot that those monsters drop.
Experience | Experience penalties | An analytically deduced formula for the preceding table is: EffectiveMonsterLevel = − 0.03 ∗ MonsterLevel 2 + 5.17 ∗ MonsterLevel − 144.9 \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\text{EffectiveMonsterLevel}}=-0.03*{\text{MonsterLevel}}^{2}+5.17*{\text{MonsterLevel}}-144.9
Experience | Experience penalties | Combining together the experience penalty for high level characters and the adjustment of monster level, here are some example sets of experience penalties, one for tier 8 (Effective monster level 74.10), one for tier 10 (Effective monster level 75.32), and one for tier 15 (Effective monster level 77.32).
Experience | Experience penalties | So a level 99 player will be earning 1.9% experience for clearing tier 8 content, 2.5% experience for clearing tier 10, and 4% experience for clearing tier 15. In practical terms, this means that if the player can clear a tier 8 more than twice as fast as a tier 15, they will be much better off clearing tier 8 content when looking at experience efficiency per hour (because 4.0 is a bit more than two times 1.9). And if they can clear tier 10 content at most 31.5% slower than tier 8 content, then they are better off clearing tier 10 content (because 2.5% is 31.5% more than 1.9%). Bear in mind that this changes with player level and with the density of monsters in a map as well.
Experience | Experience penalties | An additional consequence can be seen by the difference in XP multiplier across different levels. For example, tier 10 content at level 94 gives 9.6% experience, but at level 99 only gives 2.5% experience. This means that if a level 94 and 99 were to theoretically do the same tier 10 content (separately from each other), it would take the level 99 approximately 3.84 times longer doing the same content to gain the same absolute amount of experience. In other words, if a level 94 were to gain X million experience in tier 10 maps in one hour, then it would take the level 99 about 3 hours and 50 minutes to gain that same X million experience if they were going at the same pace.
Experience | Experience penalties | As an example using only tier 10 content as a guideline, the penalties for level 90 and above, expressed with the amount of time relative to leveling up from level 90 to 91 (using level 90->91 as a baseline), we can come up with a table showing what share of total time from level 90 to 100 a given level will take, as well as the cumulative progress towards level 100. Looking at the below chart, level 95->96 will take about 8.41% of the total time, and once you are complete with that level (in other words, base level 96), you will be 23.58% complete with progress towards level 100. Additionally, it will take about 6.576 times longer going from level 95 to 96 than it took to go from 90 to 91, as there is 1.46 times as much absolute XP to gain for that level, and the multiplier is 4.5 times lower at level 95 than at level 90, so 4.5 times less experience gained per unit time * 1.46 times as much experience to gain = 6.57 times longer to go from 95->96 than to go from 90->91.
Experience | Experience penalties | Note that changing the tier between 4 and 15 for the above chart does not change the percentage values very much, in each case, no matter which monster level the zone is, base level 98 will still be roughly 50% of the way from 90->100, and base level 99 will still be roughly 70% of the way. It works out this way because the XP multiplier only starts to bottom out at 1% when you're level 99 and running a tier 3 (effective monster level 70) zone; in higher level zones, the XP penalty formula decreases approximately linearly, and keeps roughly the same proportion between each level. This is where the efficiency aspect comes into play again. At level 99, if you can clear a tier 10 zone at most 2.5 times as slowly as a tier 3, you're better off running a tier 10 instead of a tier 3 (multiplier for level 99, tier 3 = 0.01, multiplier for level 99, tier 10 = 0.025). Similarly with Level 90 players, but it's more dramatic, as Level 90 tier 3 multiplier = 0.064, and Level 90 tier 10 multiplier = 0.306 [4.78 times as much]. So you'd need to clear a tier 3 at least 5 times as fast as a tier 10 on a level 90 character in order to be efficient.
Experience | Comparing experience gains at high levels | We can use the efficiency calculations from above to show how much experience a player of a given level must get per unit time in order to be achieving the same experience per unit time of another player level, taking into account experience penalties. If two characters are running tier 11 content, we can compare how much one is getting versus how much the other should be getting in order to keep pace with the other.
Experience | Figuring out how long it will take to get from one level to a different level | We can say that if we're going a specific speed at a given level in a given tier of content, then we can compute how fast you'll move to a different level.
Experience | Figuring out how long it will take to get from one level to a different level | To use this table, find your level in the left-hand column, and then the level you would like to reach on the top row. Where they intersect gives you a "Raw XP" value (in Millions), which you can divide by your XP/hour, to see how long it'll take to get from one level to the next. You can also subtract out the XP you've gained in your current level (in Millions) from the value, and divide, in order to get a better estimate.

Experience | Party play | In a party, a monster that would grant 1000 experience to a single character will instead grant PartySize * 1000 experience on kill, which then is split among the party members proportional to (PlayerLevel+10)^2.71. However, the experience values that each player would get are capped at the solo experience of the monster. This means that, compared to solo play, characters can get penalized for being lower level relative to the party, but not rewarded for being higher level. [5] [6] [7]
Experience | Party play | All other experience penalties and multipliers apply in addition to this party penalty.
Experience | Party play | The following formula captures this system, which caps out the multiplier at 1, while keeping the same effect for players who would be penalized. PartyPenalty x = min { 1 , PartySize ∗ ( PlayerLevel x + 10 ) 2.71 ∑ i = 1 n ( ( PlayerLevel i + 10 ) 2.71 ) } \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\text{PartyPenalty}}_{x}=\min\{1,{\text{PartySize}}*{\frac {({\text{PlayerLevel}}_{x}+10)^{2.71}}{\sum \limits _{i=1}^{n}{(({\text{PlayerLevel}}_{i}+10)^{2.71}})}}\}

Experience | Strategy | Simply avoiding dying and killing as many monsters as possible on the highest level zone you can comfortably clear lets you accumulate experience. League mechanics which add extra monsters like Breach , Beyond , Incursion , and Abyss , as well as Scarabs that add more or rarer monsters like Scarab of Monstrous Lineage and Domination Scarab of Evolution can help net you more XP/hour.
Experience | Strategy | For those wanting to level as fast and efficiently as possible, there are several specific methods of doing so. Most of these are run in a party in a rotation.
Experience | Strategy | Omen of Amelioration helps mitigate XP loss in case of an accidental death, but only once per zone.

Experience | Miscellaneous | Killing monsters that were raised from the dead by any means (revived by Necromancers , Soul Conduit Nemesis Mod , the reviving Strongbox affix) gives no additional experience. Player-summoned minions and monsters spawned by other monsters (ex: sirens ) also award no experience. Beyond demons , and monsters from Strongboxes do give experience, however.
Expiration rate | Description | The expiration rate of a temporary effect describes how fast or slow time progresses for that effect relative to real time.
Expiration rate | Description | Ordinarily, the expiration rate of a temporary effect is equivalent to real time – that is, one second of temporary effect duration lasts one actual second – however, there are modifiers that can increase or decrease it. Modifiers that cause a temporary effect to expire x% slower decrease the expiration rate of that effect, thereby making it last longer. Similarly, modifiers that cause it to expire x% faster (or expire x% more quickly ) increase its expiration rate, making it last a shorter period of time.
Expiration rate | Mechanics | Despite changing the total time that temporary effects last, it does not increase or decrease the duration of that temporary effect. For most characters this difference does not matter, because the main goal is an overall longer or shorter time for the game mechanic. The difference only matters for benefits and/or downsides that only affect expiration rate or duration. For example:
Expiration rate | Mechanics | Temporary effects that can possibly be affected by expiration rate include buffs , debuffs, curses, flask effects, and temporary auras. Temporary effects that are not affected by expiration rate include rage and Focus , which don't have a modifiable duration, but instead apply at fixed rates or for fixed intervals.
Expiration rate | Mechanics | Slower expiry rate is capped at 75% after combining all sources, or a 4x effective duration. [1]
Expiration rate | Formulas | The modifier expire x% faster has diminishing returns, while the modifier expire x% slower has increasing returns.
Expiration rate | Formulas | The expiration rate of an effect, where IncreasedExpirationRate and DecreasedExpirationRate are the sums of all expire #% faster and expire #% slower modifiers applicable.
Expiration rate | Formulas | ExpirationRate = 1 + IncreasedExpirationRate 100 − DecreasedExpirationRate 100 \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\text{ExpirationRate}}=1+{\frac {\text{IncreasedExpirationRate}}{100}}-{\frac {\text{DecreasedExpirationRate}}{100}}
Expiration rate | Formulas | From its base duration and expiration rate, we can calculate the effective duration of an effect.
Expiration rate | Formulas | EffectiveDuration = BaseDuration ExpirationRate \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\text{EffectiveDuration}}={\frac {\text{BaseDuration}}{\text{ExpirationRate}}}

Explode | Description | Explode effects cause a killed monster or corpse to release an area of effect explosion, dealing secondary damage to nearby enemies, based on the monster's maximum life.
Explode | Mechanics | Explosions deal secondary damage based on the maximum life of a corpse or killed monster, ignoring life modifiers from partying , Delve depth, and atlas keystones like Wellspring of Creation. [1] Their hits can be modified by global offensive stats (e.g. added damage, conversion , damage multipliers, critical strikes , area of effect , on-hit effects such as ailments and other debuffs ), as long as those stats are not specific for attacks or spells. Non-skill explosions do not receive stats from the skill that killed the enemy.
Explode | Mechanics | Non-skill explosions have a base critical strike chance of 0%. They may gain a chance to crit from flat additions such as +#% to Critical Strike Chance while affected by Hatred from a Watcher's Eye. Skill explosions use the skill's (non-weapon) critical strike chance, such as Detonate Dead 's base 6%.
Explode | Mechanics | If multiple different explosions trigger at once, they will all do their damage simultaneously, as multiple independent explosions. [2] Multiple stats that provide a chance to cause the same explosion will stack their chance instead. Explosions may cause further explosions if the conditions are met, such as a Herald of Ice explosion that freezes and kills another enemy.
Explode | Mechanics | Enemies that explode on kill do not leave corpses. Exploding an existing corpse consumes it.
Explode | Mechanics | Exploding enemy monsters on death can prevent some on-death effects, such as porcupine spikes and cold damage over time from spiders in Delve. It does not prevent on-death effects more separate from the monster, like volatiles from the Volatile Volatile Prefix Rare Monsters have Volatile Cores 5% increased Pack size 11% increased Rarity of Items found in this Area 13% increased Quantity of Items found in this Area 78% more Scarabs found in Area map modifier , the Crystalline Crystalline Intrinsic +40% to all Elemental Resistances (Hidden) Gain 40% of Physical Damage as Extra Damage of a random Element (Hidden) monster modifier , or tarred ground left by some zombie enemies.
Explode | Mechanics | Damage from explosions cannot be reflected.
Explode | Mechanics | While not explosions, comparable effects exist in Herald of Ash and Legacy of Fury , which inflict on-kill damage over time on nearby enemies, and Great Old One's Tentacles and Double Strike of Impaling , which cause impale debuffs on killed enemies to reflect damage in an area.
