Flat damage | Description | Flat damage refers to stats that add base damage. Base damage is calculated first. For more info about the entire damage calculation process see Receiving damage.
Flat damage | Identifying Flat Damage | All flat damage modifiers have a base stat number and damage type.
Flat damage | Identifying Flat Damage | Some modifiers apply limitations to the damage source.
Flat damage | Identifying Flat Damage | If there is no limitation this implies a Global modifier, which is sometimes called a generic modifier.
Flat damage | Identifying Flat Damage | Some modifiers have variable stats and others have 1 stat.
Flat damage | Identifying Flat Damage | Flat damage comes in 2 forms. Minimum damage and maximum damage.
Flat damage | Identifying Flat Damage | Anything that says adds x damage is considering minimum damage. Minimum damage will always apply to every hit.
Flat damage | Identifying Flat Damage | Anything that says adds x - y damage is adding a minimum and maximum damage range. The maximum damage represent the maximum range of damage possible.
Flat damage | Damage Types | Flat damage can come in all of the 5 damage types. See each page for more examples of each flat damage source.
Flat damage | Limitations | Flat damage is capable of affecting all hits, including those applied by attacks , spells , minions and secondary damage. It does not affect damage over time from any source, including minions.
Flat damage | Limitations | Global damage will apply to all hits, except for minions which scale their own damage. Affects that only apply to one source (like minions) explicitly state so in the modifier. There is no specific flat damage that only applies to secondary damage, but global damage will apply to secondary damage.
Flat damage | Damage Scaling | Average damage - To calculate your average flat damage add up your minimum and maximum damage and divide them by 2.
Flat damage | Damage Scaling | To calculate flat added attack damage, take the average or minimum damage and divide that by your other total flat sources total average or minimum and the answer is the amount of more damage that one source gave you.
Flat damage | Damage Scaling | Spell damage is the same calculations above, except non spell sources are multiplied by the damage multiplier on the spell gem. These calculations are different because the damage on the gem itself is not multiplied by the damage multiplier, which is different than attacks.
Flat damage | Damage Scaling | Secondary damage has the same calculations as spell damage. For example Herald of Ice.
Flat damage | Damage Scaling | Support gems - Flat damage from support gems can potentially do more or less damage than other options available. It is also possible for them to give the most damage at one point and not so at another. Non-gem sources that affect your flat damage and the level of the support gem can change the total damage granted by flat damage.
Flat damage | Damage Scaling | Items like Forbidden Shako and Replica Forbidden Shako can make it easier to get flat damage support gems to high levels without having many sources of plus levels to the skill gem.
Fleeing | Description | Fleeing is a status that causes enemies to attempt to run to a random point somewhere away from the player until they reach a certain point, are interrupted, or are unable to reach their selected point and give up. If a fleeing enemy becomes stunned , their fleeing behaviour will be interrupted. There is no fixed duration for fleeing. [1]
Fleeing | Mechanics | Magic monsters have a 50% chance to avoid fleeing for any reason, and rare and unique monsters are unaffected by fleeing (though chance to flee can still be inflicted).
Fleeing | Mechanics | Fleeing monsters do not use any offensive skills while they are actively trying to flee. Certain triggered skills may still occur while fleeing.
Fleeing | Mechanics | Certain types of monsters naturally flee when they are ignited. This includes apes , humanoids , and sea witches.
Fleeing | Modifiers | Corrupted weapons could have the legacy corrupted implicit modifier 5% Chance to Cause Monsters to Flee.
Flying | Description | Flying is an inherent property held by certain entities and cannot be acquired by the player.
Flying | Mechanics | Flying entities can freely move over gaps, ledges, and other non-traversable terrain, as well as small obstacles like rocks and prison bars which typically block movement. [1] Flying entities cannot go through solid walls, Frost Wall , or other extreme vertical terrain differences, however.
Flying | Mechanics | Flying entities ignore many ground effects. [2] However, they are still affected by Consecrated Ground and Desecrated Ground. Other arena-specific effects will vary on a case-by-case basis.
Flying | Mechanics | Flying entities do not block the movement of non-flying entities. [3]
Fragmented Memory | Description | Memories are found in the Synthesis leagues in Act and map zones.
Fragmented Memory | Mechanics | Each Act or map zone contains one fragmented memory, which Cavas or Zana will open. Entering a memory will spawn you next to one of the Memory Stabiliser. Interacting with a Stabiliser will open the zone and cause the memory to start decaying. Stepping too deep within the decay will forcibly eject you from the memory. It's also possible for the decay to spread into a Stabiliser, preventing the memory from being captured.
Fragmented Memory | Mechanics | The memory can be captured by interacting with all the Memory Stabilisers in it. A memory can have two to four Stabilisers. Afterwards, the memory will be captured and can be used in the Memory Nexus. The captured memory contains paths which determines how it can be connected. Its locations are based on which directions the Stabilisers were.
Fragmented Memory | Mechanics | Once the memory is captured, you can click the button on the bottom right to speed up the decaying process.
Fragmented Memory | Mechanics | Once you exit the memory, any items that dropped inside the memory will be transferred to where you opened the memory.
Fragmented Memory | Mechanics | Fractured items can drop in a memory.
Fragmented Memory | Cavas' Memory | After encountering The Elder for the first time and retrieving Memory Fragment I , the next fragmented memory zone is a special memory which belongs to Cavas. The zone contains waves of synthesized monsters. After completing this memory, Cavas will recover his memories and Zana will take over his role. This also enables bosses to spawn in the Memory Nexus.
Full life | Description | Full Life is a condition that applies when the character's current life is at 100%. Full Life works when under the influence of Chaos Inoculation.
Full life | Interactions | While taking damage over time , the full life condition can still be met if your net life recovery is greater than the net life loss, via stats such as regeneration , leech , or flasks. [1] [2] Note however that the player will still die from sufficiently much damage over time, even if their life recovery over time is greater than the life loss over time.
Gain on block | Description | Gain on block is a form of recovery that instantly restores an amount of life , mana or energy shield for each block from an enemy attack or spell.
Gain on block | Mechanics | When an player blocks a hit by an enemy, the player gains an amount of life/mana/energy shield equal to combined gain on block bonuses from all sources respectively. Unlike leech , life, mana, and energy shield gained this way are restored instantly.
Gain on block | Skill gems | Bone Offering provides a delayed Life Gain on block because it Grants Minions X% of Life Regenerated per Second if they have Blocked recently.
Gain on block | Unique items | Only items with explicit gain on block are listed here

Gain on block | Life gain on block | These passive skills grant additional life gained for each enemy attack blocked by a minion.
Gain on block | Energy Shield gain on block | These passive skills grant additional energy shield gained for each enemy spell blocked by the character.
Gain on hit | Description | Gain on hit is a form of recovery that instantly recovers an amount of life , mana or energy shield for each hit dealt by the character.
Gain on hit | Mechanics | Gain on hit effects instantly recover a static amount of resources. Different modifiers that apply to the same hit will stack additively. There is no cap on potential recovery, and each hit against each enemy can recover resources independently. Because it is instant, this type of recovery is unaffected by modifiers to recovery rate. [1]
Gain on hit | Mechanics | Life gain on hit is inherited by skills as an offensive stat, and can cause proxies to recover their own life, though this is normally only meaningful for totems.
Gain on hit | Mechanics | Similar to other on-hit effects, gain on hit effects do not apply to reflected damage.
Gain on hit | Unique items | Only items with explicit gain on hit are listed here

Gain on hit | Life gain on hit | These passive skills grant additional life gained for each enemy hit by the character's attacks.
Gain on hit | Mana gain on hit | These passive skills grant additional mana gained for each enemy hit by the character's attacks.
Gain on hit | Item modifiers | Item modifiers that grant resource on hit.
Gain on kill | Description | Life gain on kill , mana gain on kill , and energy shield gain on kill is a form of recovery that instantly restores an amount of life , mana , or energy shield respectively when the character kills an enemy.
Gain on kill | Description | When an enemy is killed by a character's attack, that character gains an amount of life equal to combined life gain on killing blow bonuses from passives and all other sources. This effect triggers once for each enemy killed. Unlike leech , recovery this way is applied instantly.
Gain on kill | Description | Effects which grant life, mana, or charges on kill do not grant these bonuses when kills are achieved through proxy sources of damage, i.e.; minions , traps , mines , or totems.
Gain on kill | Passive skills | There are passive skills that grant life or mana gain on hit bonuses.

Gain on kill | Mana gain on kill | These passive skills grant additional mana gained when the character kills an enemy.

Game mechanics | Description | Path of Exile can be intimidating for new players due to the fact that a certain level of understanding of game mechanics is demanded of players who wish to survive. In order to help facilitate planning and execution, this page contains information on the most important mechanics to understand and links to pages which explain specific mechanics in greater detail. It is intended to serve both as a guide to new players and as a primary reference for existing ones.
Game mechanics | Leagues | Before beginning path of exile players are given options for different leagues to choose from. Players can only interact with other players in the same league as them. Most items owned by players are restricted to the league they are found in, with some exceptions below.
Game mechanics | Leagues | Standard is the permanent, evergreen league with no modifiers. Path of Exile also releases temporary challenge leagues of the parent leagues that include new features to the game. These are like ladder resets, in that everybody joins the league with no characters and an empty stash. When temporary leagues end all characters and inventories and the stash will all move to standard.
Game mechanics | Leagues | Leagues also have three additional optional flags:
Game mechanics | Leagues | Characters with both Hardcore and Ruthless enabled are moved to the Void league on death, preventing them from being played at all.
Game mechanics | Leagues | Temporary leagues have the same options as standard. The temporary leagues with no modifiers tend to be the most popular leagues. Higher player population makes finding a party or rare items for trade easier.
Game mechanics | Classes | The main difference between the classes is their starting location on the passive skill tree and their Ascendancy class. Classes also start with different amounts of attributes and have different quest rewards.
Game mechanics | Ascendancy Classes | Each base class can choose from one of three Ascendancy classes (except for the Scion , who has only one) after completing the Lord's Labyrinth. Ascendancy classes offer powerful, specialized passive skills. You gain 2 Ascendancy skill points for each difficulty of the Labyrinth you complete, with 4 difficulties in all.
Game mechanics | Level Progression | All classes begin with the same base stats, and gain the same amount life , mana and evasion per level. Classes start with different accuracy stats but gain the same amount per level. The values all classes gain per level are:
Game mechanics | Private Stash | Your private stash allows you to store items and transfer them between characters. Stashes are shared between all your characters within a league - all of your Standard characters access one stash, while all of your Hardcore characters access a different stash. Items cannot be moved between leagues except by death to a character (From Hardcore or Challenge League Hardcore to Standard). Each account is initially limited to 4 stash tabs, but more can be bought through microtransactions.
Game mechanics | Chat Channels | There are two types of chat channels: Trade and Global Chat. These channels are League-specific. If you enter global chat in a Challenge league , then you will only be talking with people in that league only. Typing /global ## or /trade ## will put you into that number channel, provided it is not full.
Game mechanics | Chat Channels | Messages can be directed to different channels. Messages starting with
Game mechanics | Chat Channels | You can leave global or trade chat by unchecking the "Join Global Chat" or "Join Trade Chat" options on the chat window.
Game mechanics | Skills & Gems | Skill gems are the manner in which player characters are able to use and augment skills. Gems are placed in sockets by left-clicking it in the inventory to pick it up and then left-clicking it over the intended socket. Right clicking will remove the gem. Gems are either skills or supports, and skills come in several types whereof the two most common are Attacks and Spells.
Game mechanics | Skill gems | Skill gems creates the skill. They can come in various forms, such as attacking or casting a spell , summoning a minion or totem , throwing a trap or placing a mine , activating an aura or buff effect, and so on.
Game mechanics | Support gems | Support gems augments the skills, for example by increasing its power or adding more projectiles. The support gem needs to be linked to the gem to be active and the support needs to be able to support it. Reading the gem's tags is helpful in determining which support gems can support which skills. Common sense is also helpful - skills that don't do damage, such as Temporal Chains , won't benefit from Added Cold Damage Support nor would it add damage to an Aura. Note that skill properties may change depending on weapon - Elemental Hit , for example, is tagged with both Bow and Melee because it can be used with either, but Lesser Multiple Projectiles Support won't work when Elemental Hit is used with a sword.
Game mechanics | Damage Scaling and Effects | See also Damage Types. Understanding how damage scales is very important in Path of Exile. There are 5 main types of damage, which are Physical, Fire, Cold, Lightning, and Chaos. Fire, Cold, and Lightning are collectively known as Elemental Damage. Damage reduction from armour only affects physical damage.
Game mechanics | Dual wielding | Dual wielding provides a bonus to attack speed and block chance. The attack speed bonus is applied multiplicatively with other attack speed modifiers. The default attack and most other skills will alternate between hands for each skill use. Some skills attack with both weapons at once and deal two hits (e.g. Viper Strike ), some attack with both weapons and combine their damage (e.g. Cleave , Dual Strike , Viper Strike of the Mamba ), some alternate weapons within a single skill use ( Lacerate , though not Double Strike ). For skills that are weapon-restricted, both weapons must be compatible in order to use the skill.
Game mechanics | Combining damage properties | Path of Exile uses wording that is as literal as possible according to the classifications listed on this page so that consistent damage calculations can take place. For example, take Spectral Throw. It is a projectile attack that uses a melee weapon. This means that, for example, a passive node that grants 10% increased physical damage with Two-Handed Weapons will boost Spectral Throw 's physical damage when used with a two-handed melee weapon such as a staff, but a node that grants 15% increased melee physical damage will not boost Spectral Throw's physical damage, because Spectral Throw is a projectile attack, not a melee attack. This approach to properties is true of all mechanics in the game, but is most often a source of confusion for damage stacking.
Game mechanics | Damage conversion | Some skills and gear can convert one type of damage to another, resulting in a complex damage calculation. Damage conversion stacks additively, and is scaled down to fit 100% if total conversion exceeds 100%. Bonuses from different damages types are applied to the final product as though they were the same type - for example, if you had 100% cold to fire conversion 100 base cold damage 50% increased cold damage 50% increased fire damage Then you would have 50%+50% increased fire damage (see the following section), or 100% increased fire damage. This means your final damage is 200 fire damage.
Game mechanics | Modifier stacking | In general, integer modifiers are applied before percentages. Percentage modifiers using the words "% increased" or "% reduced" stack additively with one another, while "% more" and "% less" modifiers stack multiplicatively.
Game mechanics | Modifier stacking | When dealing with weapons, some modifiers that are listed on the weapon itself are applied first, before mods from other pieces of equipment, skills, and so on. This includes anything affecting physical damage, such as increased physical damage, added physical damage, quality etc., and also attack speed, critical strike chance, and accuracy. It does not include elemental damage mods. These can be called local modifiers - any modifier marked as "global," such as %increased Global Critical Strike Modifier, is not applied to the weapon first.
Game mechanics | Modifier stacking | Similarly, when dealing with armour, evasion, and energy shield on armour, any modifiers affecting those stats that are listed on the piece of armour are applied first. This includes quality and any other mods directly affecting armour, evasion, or energy shield amount. It does not include mods affecting the energy shield recharge delay or regeneration rate, only the amount of energy shield.
Game mechanics | Modifier stacking | Imagine I have 100 life, and two passive skills that each increase total life by 15%. The total bonus will be 30%, resulting in 130 life. Now imagine I am wearing boots that give +40 life, and have a passive skill that grants +20 life. The integer bonuses are applied first, giving me 160 life, then the percentage bonuses are applied to that subtotal, for a final total of 208 life.
Game mechanics | Modifier stacking | For example, let's look at a Samite Helmet with +69 armour, 92% increased armour, and 20% quality. This Horned Casque has a base armour rating of 240. Then the +69 is added to get 309 armour. Then the 92% bonus from the item and the 20% bonus from quality are added together to give a 112% armour increase, for a total of 655 armour.
Game mechanics | Modifier stacking | Another example calculation If you had a sword whose unmodified damage is 10-20, with the following modifiers:
Game mechanics | Modifier stacking | 50% increased physical damage on the weapon; 20% quality on the weapon; 5-10 added physical damage on the weapon; passive skills granting 30% increased sword damage; a skill that does 40% increased damage and 30% less damage;
Game mechanics | Modifier stacking | the calculation would look like this:
Game mechanics | Modifier stacking | Base damage: 10-20 Stage 1, on-weapon modifiers: (10-20 + 5-10) x (1 + 0.5 + 0.2) = 25.5-51 Stage 2, all other modifiers: (25.5-51) x (1 + 0.3 + 0.4) x 0.7 = 30-61
Game mechanics | Movement Speed | The base movement speed bonus of your character is 0%, or normal speed. If your movement speed bonus is at 0%, then it will not be shown on the "Defense" tab of the character screen. However, if it is anything else, such as -2%, it will be shown in the "Defense" tab.
Game mechanics | Movement Speed | Shields and body armours have hidden intrinsic movement speed penalties. Body armour based on armour or armour and energy shield cause 5% reduced movement speed. All other body armours cause 3% reduced movement speed. Shields cause 3% reduced movement speed. These are the nonmagical components; unique body armours such as Queen of the Forest can modify movement speed further.
Game mechanics | Currency | Instead of gold or other forms of money, Path of Exile uses what are known as "currency items". Currency items are displayed with light tan text colour in their item name. Currency can be consumed for a specific gameplay effect, such as crafting , or player-to-player trade.
Game mechanics | Currency | Items from NPC vendors cost some amount of currency (usually low-tier currency). When you trade with players, be prepared to barter or haggle unless a player has listed a "buyout", a set price for the item. Exchange rates between currency items are generally set by the players, as currency items can only be traded up to the next level of currency at a vendor and not traded down.
Game mechanics | Currency | General value of some basic currency:
Game mechanics | Currency | Mirror of Kalandra God-Tier: The rarest and highest value currency item in the game. It eclipses the networth of most of the playerbase.
Game mechanics | Currency | Divine Orb , Exalted Orb , Chaos Orb High-Tier: High value in the end-game. Commonly used for player trade and high-end crafting.
Game mechanics | Currency | Orb of Alteration , Orb of Alchemy , Regal Orb , Orb of Scouring , Orb of Regret , Chromatic Orb , Jeweller's Orb , Orb of Fusing , Gemcutter's Prism , Glassblower's Bauble , Cartographer's Chisel , Vaal Orb , Orb of Annulment , Sacred Orb Mid-Tier: Moderate value in large amounts. Common currency for crafting and other functions, not player trade.
Game mechanics | Currency | Scroll of Wisdom , Portal Scroll , Orb of Transmutation , Orb of Augmentation , Orb of Chance , Blacksmith's Whetstone , Armourer's Scrap , Blessed Orb Low-Tier: Currency that is rarely used for trading.
Game mechanics | Currency | Items on websites like official trade site and poe.ninja are widely listed with buyouts in terms of chaos orbs and divine orbs.
Game mechanics | Attribute requirements | Most gear has attribute requirements that must be met in order to equip it. These requirements come from the base item type and are unaffected by magical modifiers, quality, or number of sockets. If a gem has attribute requirements a character does not meet and the gem is socketed in an item then that character will be unable to use that item.
Game mechanics | Level requirements | Most items have a level requirement that must be met in order to equip them. There are two factors that affect level requirements:
Game mechanics | Drop rates | Drop tables are uniform across monsters of the same monster level. In other words, the pool of items that can potentially drop and the chance for a particular item to drop are not determined by the type of monster.
Game mechanics | Level difference currency penalty | There is a penalty to the chance of currency items (scrolls, orbs, etc.) dropping in areas with a monster level more than two levels lower than a character's level. Currency item Drops are not increased or decreased in this way when fighting in areas above your level. For the purposes of this penalty, your level is never considered to be higher than 68. Therefore, a level 75 character receives no penalty in a level 66 area.
Game mechanics | Level difference currency penalty | There are two modifiers that affect drop rates in the game, increased item rarity, and increased item quantity. There are three potential sources of these modifiers: - the player (skills, passives, gear etc.) - monsters (such as bosses and champions) - Party bonuses Modifiers from the player stack additively with each other, and are subject to diminishing returns. Modifiers from the party bonus and monsters stack additively with each other, and are not subject to diminishing returns. The total player bonus stacks multiplicatively with the total party & monster bonus.
Game mechanics | Item Rarity | Increased Item Rarity % modifiers (or IIR) increase the chances of an item being magic, rare, or unique. IIR increases with diminishing returns but they are only significant at very high IIR values. IIR has no effect on the number or type of currency items, scrolls, or gems that drop. When in a party, only the modifier from the character who lands the killing blow on an enemy is counted. If one of a character's minions lands the killing blow then the minion's IIR is added to the character's IIR and that sum is used.
Game mechanics | Item Rarity | Magic, rare, and unique monsters have an IIR modifier for drops.
Game mechanics | Item Quantity | Increased Item Quantity (or IIQ) increases the average number of items that drop from monsters and chests. It does not affect the type, quality, or rarity of item dropped, only the chance that something will drop. There is no cap on the usefulness of this modifier, as monsters can drop more than one item at a time. The base chance for an item to drop from a normal monster is 16%. This varies between monster types, and special monsters have higher drop chances.
Game mechanics | Item Quantity | When in a party, each player in the party after the first gives a +10% item quantity and +40% item rarity modifier on drops.
Game mechanics | Item Quantity | IIQ & IIR modifiers from support gems currently do not work with kills made by damage over time effects, such as the poison from poison arrow. Modifiers from your gear will affect those kills however.
Game mechanics | Quality | All weapons, armour, flasks, gems, and maps can randomly receive between +1% and +20% quality when dropped. This value can be increased by Blacksmith's Whetstones, Armourer's Scraps, Glassblower's Baubles, Gemcutter's Prisms, and Cartographer's Chisels, but is capped at 20%.
Game mechanics | Quality | The effect of quality depends on the item:
Game mechanics | Quality | On weapons , increased physical damage On armour , increased Armour rating, Evasion, and Energy Shield On life and mana flasks , increased life and mana recovery On utility flasks , increased duration On gems , the bonus is specific to each gem. Check the individual gem page for specifics On maps , increases the item quantity bonus from monsters in the map area
Game mechanics | Quality | There are a limited number of ways to increase quality beyond 20%.
Game mechanics | Modifiers on items | Modifiers are split up in to two main groups, prefixes and suffixes. A magic item can have only one prefix and one suffix, never two prefixes or two suffixes. Rare items can have up to six modifiers, it is unknown if there is a limit on how many of these can be prefixes/suffixes. A randomly generated rare item (from a drop or Orb of Alchemy) receives between four and six modifiers randomly, with the following odds: [1] 1/12 chance of 6 mods 4/12 chance of 5 mods 7/12 chance of 4 mods
Game mechanics | Modifiers on items | All modifiers have a level associated with them, and will only appear on items whose item level is greater than or equal to the modifier's level.
Game mechanics | Modifiers on items | Lists of available magical modifiers are available in the list of item modifiers section.
Game mechanics | Modifiers on items | The Culling Strike modifier (found on some unique items and Culling Strike Support ) causes monsters to die if you strike them down to 10% or less life.
Game mechanics | Sockets | There are four types of sockets :
Game mechanics | Sockets | Sockets appear randomly on most equipment. Higher level items can appear with more sockets than lower level items of the same type. The maximum amount of sockets that can appear on an item also varies by the type of item:
Game mechanics | Sockets | Items are more likely to receive sockets that match their attribute requirements. So an item requiring only dexterity is more likely to have green sockets than red or blue sockets. You can only put a blue (intelligence) gem in a blue socket, red gem in a red socket, etc. Sockets can be linked. The links are shown as gold bars between the sockets. Support gems affect any skill gems in sockets that they are linked to.
Game mechanics | Sockets | For example: This sword has 1 strength socket, 1 intelligence socket, and 2 dexterity sockets. Every socket is linked to every other socket. In this sword you could put:
Game mechanics | Sockets | So let's say you put in:
Game mechanics | Sockets | You would get a cleave skill that does extra cold damage, and raise zombie skill with zombies that do extra cold damage. You would not get zombies that have cleave, or raise a zombie every time you use cleave.
Game mechanics | Sockets | If two of the same support gem are linked to the same skill within the same socket group, they do not stack. Only the highest-level gem gives a bonus.
Game mechanics | Sockets | Additionally, two skill gems of the same type can be used in separate socket groups, resulting in more than one usable version of that skill. Skill Gems are only affected by support gems in the same socket group.
Game mechanics | Sockets | For example, imagine a piece of armour with 5 sockets. The first two sockets are linked in one group, and the remaining three sockets are linked in a separate group. If you put Cleave and Faster Attacks in the first group, and Cleave, Added Fire Damage, and Added Cold Damage in the second group, you would have two different versions of cleave available - one cleave skill that attacks faster, and another cleave that does bonus fire and cold damage.
Game mechanics | Sockets | Small letters appear over the skill icons for each support gem you have attached to that skill. This allows you to differentiate between the different versions if you have more than one of the same skill gem equipped.
Game mechanics | Item level | Each item has a level associated with it that is equal to the monster level of the area it dropped in. The monster level is shown on the map overlay (TAB key). Magic monsters (blue name) have +1 to their level, and will yield items with an item level one level higher than other monsters in the same area. Rare (yellow name) and unique (brown name) monsters have +2 to their level, and will yield items with an itemlevel two levels higher than other monsters in the same area. You can check an item's level by picking it up on the cursor and typing /itemlevel in the chat box. This item level determines which modifiers it can receive, and how many sockets it can receive.
Game mechanics | Parties | The maximum party size is 6 players.
Game mechanics | Effect on monsters | Monsters have increased life for each member inside a party.
Game mechanics | Effect on monsters | The original life amount is used for the purposes of determining the length of stuns and status ailments from elemental damage - this means monsters will not be harder to stun/ignite/etc. when fighting in a party.
Game mechanics | Effect on loot | Each player in a party after the first gives an increased item quantity modifier and increased item rarity modifier on drops. Increased Item Rarity & Quantity modifiers are only counted from the player who lands the killing blow.
Game mechanics | Effect on experience | Only party members that are nearby (roughly two screens) receive experience from a slain monster. If one member is in town or too far from the monster they get no XP. Monsters are still made harder by players elsewhere on the level but outside of XP range.
Game mechanics | Effect on flasks and killing blow modifiers | Only the character landing the killing blow gets bonuses from "(.) when you deal a killing blow" type of modifiers. Flasks does not apply to this.
Game mechanics | Instances | All areas in Path of Exile are instanced. When you enter an area, a new instance is created. Once you leave the area, the instance will remain in its current state for 15 minutes - if 15 minutes passes with no players entering the instance, it will be closed. This closes any portals you may have had to the area. Entering the same area again will create a new instance with a new randomly generated map. Areas without side areas attached (any area with two or less exits) has a shorter timer, and will only last 8 minutes while empty.
Game mechanics | Instances | Instances you create are private, and cannot be entered by other players unless they join your party. However, once a player has entered an instance, that instance remains associated with the player even if they leave the party. So it is possible to share an instance with non-party members in some circumstances. The exception to this is towns, which are always public, and cut-throat leagues, where all instances are public - meaning anyone can enter your instances at any time.
Game mechanics | Instances | Some areas have waypoints. Once activated (by clicking on the waypoint), waypoints allow you to travel instantly to any other waypoint you have activated.
Game mechanics | Instances | Ctrl-clicking on a waypoint destination in the waypoint menu, or an area transition such as a doorway, will bring up the instance management screen. This screen lists all available instances of the area you ctrl-clicked on, the players inside the instance, and the time remaining until they are closed. It also allows you to create new instances, and enter existing ones. Using the instance management screen you can have more than one instance of the same area open at a time, and choose which available instance you want to enter. This may be useful if one wants to respawn bosses, but note that instances are arranged so that bosses cannot be farmed without traveling a significant distance.
Game mechanics | Level difference experience penalty | Level affects the amount of experience you gain from killing enemies, based on the relative level of the player and monsters. A penalty is applied if you are too far above or below the monster level.
Game mechanics | Microtransactions | Microtransactions are in game digital goods purchased with real world money. Most effects are cosmetic.
Game mechanics | Microtransactions | Commons options (Does not include everything)
Ghost Shroud | Description | Ghost Shroud is the stack counter used by the Ghost Dance keystone.
Gold gambling | Description | Gold gambling , also referred to as the Black Market , is a type of vendor mechanic that can be accessed via various NPCs in towns or Faustus in a player's hideout or Kingsmarch. Players can spend Gold to obtain specific types of item class items, with a higher chance to obtain "well-rolled" or unique items.
Gold gambling | Mechanics | Items created through gold gambling are always at least magic rarity, and can result in unique items. For example, a random sample of 50 wands with a level 93 character resulted in a distribution of 12 magic wands, 45 rare wands, and 3 T5 unique wands.
Gold gambling | Mechanics | The generated item has an item level between the character's level and the character's level +3, up to a maximum range of i83-i86. This is the same regardless of which NPC/location is used to gamble.
Gold gambling | Mechanics | On magic or rare items, it uses a "well-rolled" system ( modifier tier rating ), causing random affixes to only roll from the top 50% of each mod group's eligible modifiers (e.g. at least T6 or higher +# to maximum Mana if 12 tiers possible), inclusive if an odd number of tiers eligible.
Gold gambling | Mechanics | Unlike Gwennen gambling , it cannot result in corrupted or influenced items.
Grand Heist | Description | Grand Heists are more elaborate Heists that require using Blueprints at The Rogue Harbour. The player must infiltrate a facility that contains multiple wings, retrieve the guarded items without raising alert, and escape with the contents alive.
Grand Heist | Description | Unlike regular Heists , Grand Heists require multiple Rogues to complete. The target item, inside a Curio Display , will be a selection of experimented base types , replica unique items , weapons or body armour with a Heist enchantment , Thief's Trinkets , or currency. You can only take one from of the selection before Lockdown begins.
Grand Heist | Description | Players cannot obtain artifacts that can be sold for Rogue's Markers from Curio Display, therefore Grand Heists are not a main source of Rogue's Marker. However, these artifacts can be found in the side rooms of the Grand Heist.
Grand Heist | Mechanics | If players get Divine Orbs or any items worth a lot of currency, they may simply exit the wing using the escape hatch, and then they may re-enter the wing and resume looting. This removes the Contraband status on all items in the players inventory, so that even if they die the items are not lost.
Grand Heist | Preparation | To start a Grand Heist, the player must take a Blueprint to the Planning Room in the Rogue's Harbour. There, players must assign rogues that will perform each job. After configuring the rogues and confirming the Blueprint, the plan is locked and you can't unlock more wings or rooms or change Rogue placements for that Blueprint. Players must then go to Adiyah, the Wayfinder to start the Grand Heist. Player must pay the fee of Rogue's Markers , and then Adiyah will open a portal to the location.
Grand Heist | Wings | Unlike a regular heist, a Grand Heist has multiple wings, and requires multiple jobs. A typical Grand Heist blueprint drops with only 1 wing and a few rooms unlocked.
Grand Heist | Wings | In order to unlock additional wings and rooms, players can use Whakano to reveal additional wings. Players can swap to Gianna or Niles within Whakano's interface (using the left/right arrows) to use them to unlock wings and rooms. The advantages to doing so are that Gianna provides a 10-30% discount (based on her highest job level) and Niles provides a 10% discount to unlocking wings and rooms.
Grand Heist | Wings | Each wing requires three different jobs to be filled. This allows you to bring up to three Rogues per wing, but one Rogue can fill multiple jobs if desired.
Grand Heist | Wings | Each wing contains its own valuable target item inside a Curio Display. Each wing has its own alert bar and its own lockdown process. After looting one wing and stealing the target item, players may return to Adiyah's portal to loot the next wing.
Grand Heist | Infiltration | When players enter the location, a map will display multiple entrances. Each entrance leads to one wing. Entering the wing will enter the heist location as usual and all mechanics are exactly the same as regular heists.
Grand Heist | Infiltration | All items picked up during the Heist are marked as Contraband. Contraband items cannot be used, equipped, or identified and are dropped on death.
Grand Heist | Infiltration | Players may open hidden rooms and chests using the rogues abilities as usual.
Grand Heist | Curio Displays | Unlike regular heists that contain an artifact that is sold for Rogue's Markers , Grand Heists contain valuable loot that players may keep for themselves. Many of these items cannot be obtained from any other sources in the game (such as replica uniques or experimented base type items.
Grand Heist | Curio Displays | Grand Heists contain 5 curio displays per wing, and players may select any one of them. Each curio display contains a different item. This allows players to select the most valuable or most useful item that they wish to have. Upon breaking the curio display of an item, lockdown begins immediately and players cannot take any of the other 4 items.
Grand Heist | Lockdown | Once the target item is taken or the Lockdown timer runs out, Lockdown begins. More enemies will spawn in the area and try to prevent your escape as usual.
Grand Heist | Lockdown | Unlike regular heists, Grand Heists allow players to unlock an "escape route" that is often very close to the Curio Display, making it easier for them to survive and escape with the final loot item. This escape route is also marked with on the minimap.
Grand Heist | Lockdown | After completing one wing, the entire process repeats for the other wings.
Grand Heist | Portal | Players may leave and re-enter Adiyah's portal multiple times in order to stash items, just like normal heists.
Grand Heist | Portal | The portal will close when all wings have been completed, either successfully or unsuccessfully. Even if players disconnect (logout) and login, they may return to the Rogue Harbour and the portal will remain active as long as the instance has not timed out. Note that the instance will time out if the player idles in the Rogue Harbour, unlike maps in your hideout. Players who need to AFK between wings should do so in the Grand Heist's crossroads area inside the instance.
Grand Heist | Death | If players die before lockdown has begun, all items marked with Contraband are dropped to the ground but Adiyah's portal remains up. Players may then return to the wing and pick up the loot and therefore nothing is lost.
Grand Heist | Death | If players die during lockdown, all items marked with Contraband are dropped to the ground. If there are other players in the same party, they may pick up the drops, but if the player is going solo then the loot is lost permanently. The wing will be blocked and players cannot enter the wing again. However, Adiyah's portal remains up and players may enter and loot other wings (if any).
Grand Heist | Rogues | Players may hire various rogues to assist them in heists and grand heists. Players may select which rogue performs which job and they will accordingly appear in the heist.
Grand Heist | Rogues | Each rogue has a specific set of perks that improve drops, allow players to open more reward chests (alert level reduction), or simply assist in combat.
Grand Heist | Locations | There are 4 different kinds of monsters that appear across the Grand Heist locations. The location is mentioned in the name of the Grand Heist blueprint, eg. Blueprint: Tunnels indicates that the Grand Heist will take place in the Tunnels location.
Grand Heist | Chest Rewards | Rewards are obtained directly by opening chests in Grand Heists.
Grand Heist | Curio Display Rewards | The following rewards only drop from Curio Displays in Grand Heists.
Grand Heist | Experimented base types | Experimented base types can be obtained from Curio Displays. They include weapons, shields and jewellery that have different implicit modifiers than ordinary equipment.
Grand Heist | Unique items | The following unique items can only be obtained from Curio Displays.
Grand Heist | Ruthless mode | In Ruthless mode , Heist Blueprints' reward chests only contain generic rewards (Weapon, Armour, Currency, Map). Upon entering the actual Grand Heist, the actual chests are obscured and only display the generic ? symbol; it is recommended to take a screenshot of the Blueprint reveal screen if you cannot remember the location of each chest. [1]
Ground effect | Description | A ground effect is the general term for a patch of terrain that has some consequence on characters or monsters positioned on it. Burning ground created by the Fire Trap skill is one common example of a ground effect.
Ground effect | List of ground effects | Fire damage over time:
Ground effect | List of ground effects | Cold damage over time:
Ground effect | List of ground effects | Lightning damage over time:
Ground effect | List of ground effects | Physical damage over time:
Ground effect | List of ground effects | Chaos damage over time:
Ground effect | List of ground effects | Movement speed debuffs:
Ground effect | List of ground effects | Other debuffs:
Ground effect | List of ground effects | Buffs:
Ground effect | List of ground effects | Related effects:
Ground effect | Mechanics | Detrimental ground effects do not affect allies of the character that created them, while those ground effects created by monsters or the environment will not affect other monsters. The inverse is true for beneficial ground effects. [1] Modifiers on items that care about ground effects affecting the player only apply to non-player ground effects.
Ground effect | Mechanics | Characters and monsters can be affected simultaneously by different types of overlapping ground effects. Those of the same type do not cumulatively stack their effects. For ground effects that inflict damage, only one of each type with the highest damage per second will cause damage at any given moment.
Ground effect | Mechanics | Flying monsters, including Raging Spirits and Watchers , are not affected by certain ground effects that lie close to the ground. Other ground effects, such as those that consist of vapor or smoke, can influence monsters above the ground as well. [2]
Harbinger | Description | Harbingers are a type of monsters that cannot be harmed directly. Harbingers summon enemies to fight the player while empowering them in different ways, and they can only be harmed by killing their minions. Harbingers can drop currency shards , for both ones seen in Wraeclast as well as their own exclusive currency.
Harbinger | Description | Harbingers do not spawn naturally in maps unlike most other forms of Extra Content. They can be encountered via the Ominous Arrival or Additional Harbinger Chance Atlas passive skills , using the Harbinger map device crafting option, in Kirac 's Atlas missions, in Harbinger nodes in the Azurite Mine , or by using a Harbinger Scarab.
Harbinger | Description | They were introduced to the game as a feature of the Harbinger league.
Harbinger | Abilities | Harbingers are invulnerable enemies that cannot be damaged directly and instead defeated by continuously defeating waves of summoned monsters. Harbingers can use a skill similar to Convocation regularly to teleport these monsters. Harbingers can also summon Obelisks which can attack players directly, create a Proximity Shield , or have buff or debuff aura effects.
Harbinger | Abilities | Harbingers can also use a variety of spells depending on their variant. These skills include recoloured versions of skills like Flame Dash or Ball Lightning , cast buffs or debuff skills, or cause effects on their summoned monsters such as creating a Righteous Fire -like degeneration aura around a monster.
Harbinger | Abilities | Some Harbingers can use aura skills or use certain Hexes or Marks as an aura.
Harbinger | Variants | This is not an exhaustive list:
Harbinger | Currency shards | Harbingers drop primarily currency shards. Shards from Harbingers are not affected by modifiers to Item Quantity - either from the player [1] or area modifiers [2] (tested by Prohibited Library ). Item quantity does apply in maps with the Items found in Areas are replaced by stacks of Currency Shards Kirac mission enchant, as it is considered an item conversion effect. Modifiers to item rarity do not affect currency shards in either case.
Harbinger | Currency shards | Maven's Chisel of Avarice 's "More Currency" stat does not appear to affect currency shard drops from Harbingers.
Harbinger | Currency shards | These items can directly drop from Harbingers:
Harbinger | Unique pieces | One of the following unique item pieces drops from the Harbinger Portal after players defeat the final King Harbinger in any variant of The Beachhead map. Some pieces can only be found from certain tier Beachheads due to area level; the Red tier Beachhead can drop any of these pieces. Combining these pieces in a certain configuration can create exclusive unique items.
Harbinger | Unique pieces | No results found
Harbinger | Harbinger scroll | The Harbinger Portal may drop one of the following Harbinger Scrolls after players defeat the final King Harbinger in Infused Beachhead. Using the scroll on the indicated unique item will upgrade it, improving the granted Summon Harbinger skill.

Harvest | Description | Harvest is a league mechanic where the player fights monsters in The Sacred Grove to obtain lifeforce , which is used for Harvest crafting.
Harvest | Description | This page discusses the current iteration of the Harvest mechanic - see the Harvest league page for a discussion of the mechanic as it was originally introduced.
Harvest | The Sacred Grove | Maps have a chance to contain a portal to the Sacred Grove. Each Sacred Grove instance contains 3-4 Lifeforce Dispersers, which are each attached to two plots of seeds which are collectively called a "Harvest". Each plot displays a list of monsters that will spawn from the patch, and the type of Lifeforce (colour) they will drop, as well as the tiers of the seeds.
Harvest | The Sacred Grove | Players can choose which patch to activate - when a patch is chosen, the other patch attached to the Lifeforce Disperser withers, and monsters spawn from the activated patch. These monsters drop Crystallised Lifeforce which can be used for crafting recipes at the Horticrafting Station.
Harvest | The Sacred Grove | Depending on the tiers of the seeds, greater amounts of Lifeforce can drop. They go from a dull gray for the lowest tier (T1), white (T2), light blue (T3), and then an orange-brown to denote the highest tier which has special loot (T4). The specific monsters encounterable are listed below. The seeds are ordered by tier from lowest to highest when read from top to bottom in the encounter.
Harvest | The Sacred Grove | The Sacred Grove is part of the map instance it is entered from, which means map modifiers apply within the Grove as well. Area quantity from map modifiers , quality , fragments , and Eldritch Altars will affect the amount of Lifeforce dropped by monsters, though with reduced (~50%) effectiveness. [1] [2] This is additive with modifiers that increase the quantity of Lifeforce dropped. (Player quantity modifiers have no effect.) [3]
Harvest | The Sacred Grove | Pack size linearly grants an equivalent chance to spawn an extra monster from each seed for seeds of tier 3 and below. Once a multiplier of 100% pack size is reached, at least two monsters are guaranteed to spawn; at 200%, at least three; etc. This is independent from other sources of extra monsters. [4]
Harvest | The Sacred Grove | The following table shows a summary of Harvest mechanics in Tier 16 maps. In lower tier maps, seed tier distribution will differ with a greater bias for low tier seeds, and a lower chance to upgrade seeds with Crop Rotation. Tier 4 seeds can still be encountered in as low as T1 maps and the average base lifeforce does not change between map tiers, however. This information is adapted from detailed analysis of Harvest mechanics on ForgottenArbiter's blog which is recommended for further reading.
Harvest | The Sacred Grove | If the chance for all three colours of plants are reduced by 100%, such as by stacking idols in Legacy of Phrecia , there is a failsafe mechanism that causes each Harvest to generate with a random colour; both plots in the Harvest will always have the same colour.
Harvest | Bosses | There is a small chance for a tier 4 seed patch to spawn, which contain a Boss monster. Their names have an orange-brown colour, like unique items. It is possible for more than one copy of a T4 seed to appear in a plot, and it is possible for the boss to get duplicated via Harvest passives.
Harvest | Bosses | Each boss can also sometimes drop their exclusive unique items: Plume of Pursuit , The Felbog Fang , and Bear's Girdle respectively.
Harvest | Bosses | These boss monsters have a chance to drop a Sacred Blossom , a map fragment which opens another instance of the Sacred Grove containing a boss fight with Oshabi, Avatar of the Grove. Oshabi is guaranteed to drop a Sacred Crystallised Lifeforce when defeated, which is used for high-end Harvest crafts.
Harvest | Unique items | The following items are exclusive to Harvest bosses:
Harvest crafting | Description | Harvest Crafting or Horticrafting refers to creating or improving items by utilizing harvested modifiers , or "crafts". It was introduced in the Harvest league and added to the core game in the Echoes of the Atlas expansion, and has undergone multiple updates since then. Players can explore maps to find entrances to the The Sacred Grove. Monsters in the Sacred Grove drop Crystallized Lifeforce which are used for Harvest crafting recipes using the Horticrafting Station.
Harvest crafting | Description | These crafts allow players to create greatly improved rare items, because they allow greater control over the modification process versus using orbs, or exchanging currency or fragment items for different ones.
Harvest crafting | Mechanics | The remove modifier portion of "Augment" harvest crafting options ignore the Cannot roll Attack/Caster Modifiers meta crafting modifiers. [1] [2] The added modifier from augment crafts do obey this craft. They do also obey Prefixes/Suffixes cannot be changed.
Harvest crafting | Modifier groups | To learn which tag a given modifier falls under, roll-over an item while pressing the Alt key. You will see the modifier tags above the modifier. Eg. "Adds # to # Cold Damage" falls under the groups of Attack, Cold, Elemental and Damage.
Harvest crafting | Modifier groups | A partial listing of modifiers that fall within the modifier tags are given as follows:
Heist | Description | Heists are missions that can be accessed using a Contract at The Rogue Harbour. The player must infiltrate the facility without raising alert, retrieve the guarded item, and escape with the contents alive.
Heist | Description | The target item will always be a single artifact that players may exchange with Faustus for Rogue's Markers , therefore Heist Contracts are an excellent means to generate Rogue's Markers.
Heist | Description | Grand Heists are larger more complex versions of Heists, and contain multiple wings and use multiple Rogues.
Heist | The Rogue Harbour | To enter The Rogue Harbour the first time, one Rogue's Marker is required. Right clicking this item will open a Portal to The Rogue Harbour. Afterwards, it can be freely accessed via the World Map or the chat command /heist.
Heist | Mechanics | Regular Heists are performed using Contracts. A contract can always be performed with a single Rogue , and requires a certain level of a certain job (eg. Lockpicking Level 5).
Heist | Preparation | To start a Heist, the player must take a Heist Contract to Adiyah, the Wayfinder. Before you can start the Heist, you must pay a fee of Rogue's Markers. The fee includes the Travel Fee, your Rogue 's Hiring Fee(s), and the Ring's Cut. Once it's paid, she will open a portal to the Heist location.
Heist | Preparation | Contracts, blueprints and markers can be stored in the Heist Locker , which is available in Rogue Harbour and as a free hideout decoration. Heist affinity can be toggled on at the bottom of the interface, so any Heist-specific items deposited in the stash will go in the locker instead.
Heist | Infiltration | Initially, only a few enemies will be on guard. There will also be patrols of enemy packs or a unique enemy roaming the area. The area contains small chests that contain items, as well as bigger guarded chests that contain items of specific reward types. Opening chests will raise the alert level, the amount which can be displayed by hovering over them.
Heist | Infiltration | All items picked up during the Heist are marked as Contraband. Contraband items cannot be used, equipped, or identified and are dropped on death. They will be unmarked as Contraband as soon as you reach the escape point. You do not need to complete the Heist in order to remove the Contraband mark. If players get Divine Orbs or any items worth a lot of currency, they may simply exit the heist location using the escape hatch, and then they may re-enter the location using the gate/pipe/trapdoor/door and resume looting. This removes the Contraband status on all items in the players inventory, so that even if they die the items are not lost.
Heist | Infiltration | While you can't open portals during the Heist or Grand Heist, you may freely leave and re-enter the Heist portal before the alert is raised. note you must enter the heist instance itself, not just the portal room, before you can leave without closing the portal.
Heist | Infiltration | The area will contain blocked paths, obstacles, and locked chests that will require your Rogue to clear away or open. Clicking the button above the item will command your Rogue to open/unlock it. Some tasks will require some time for them to perform, indicated by a progress meter. If they are damaged while performing the task, the progress meter will decrease.
Heist | Imminent Lockdown | When the Alert meter is maxed, it will start a counter before Lockdown. Once this happens, the player will have limited time to retrieve the target item before it is sealed away. The default time before lockdown is 22 seconds.
Heist | Imminent Lockdown | Opening chests during this phase will decrease the lockdown timer by 3 seconds.
Heist | Lockdown | Once the target item is taken or the Lockdown timer runs out, Lockdown begins. More enemies will spawn in the area and try to prevent your escape. When Lockdown occurs, some doors and obstacles previously open will be locked or rearmed, requiring your Rogue to remove it.
Heist | Lockdown | Any unopened chests will be locked during Lockdown. However, Tibbs and Niles 's perks will allow you to open one or two small/medium chest during Lockdown.
Heist | Lockdown | Once you reach the escape route, the Heist is successfully completed. The target item can be sold to Faustus, the Fence for Rogue's Markers.
Heist | Portal | Players may leave and re-enter Adiyah's portal multiple times in order to stash items.
Heist | Portal | The portal is only closed if players die during the "lockdown" mode. Even if players disconnect (logout) and login, they may return to the Rogue's Harbour and the portal will remain active, provided the location was not in "lockdown".
Heist | Death | If players die before lockdown has begun, all items marked with Contraband are dropped to the ground but Adiyah's portal remains up. Players may then return to the location and pick up the loot and therefore nothing is lost.
Heist | Death | If players die during lockdown, all items marked with Contraband are dropped to the ground. If there are other players in the same party, they may pick up the drops, but if the player is going solo then the loot is lost permanently. Adiyah's portal will also be closed.
Heist | Rogues | Players may hire various rogues to assist them in heists and grand heists. Players may select which rogue performs which job and they will accordingly appear in the heist.

Heist | Rogues | Note that the contracts must be at least level 50 for unlockable rogues to start appearing.
Heist | Rogues | Each rogue has a specific set of perks that improve drops, allow players to open more reward chests (alert level reduction), or simply assist in combat.
Heist | Locations | There are 4 different kinds of monsters that appear across the heist locations. The location is mentioned in the name of the heist contract, eg. Contract: Tunnels indicates that the heist will take place in the Tunnels location.
Heist | Rewards | Rewards are obtained directly by opening chests in heists and grand heists. This is possible in both Heist Contracts and Grand Heist Blueprints.
Heist | Rewards | Grand heists provide an additional large and possibly valuable reward within a Curio Display.
Heist | Unique contracts | The league introduced 5 unique contracts. Unique contracts will only drop after the client's quest storyline has been completed in the current league.

Heist | Lore | Heist was released in the Heist league , see that page for more details.
Heist Laboratory Mechanics | Description | Laboratory heists feature a specific faction of monsters that cannot be found in other areas, other than Prohibited Library heists and Foundry Map
Hit | Description | The term hit refers to any damage that isn't damage over time.
Hit | Mechanics | A hit applies a discrete amount of damage to a target instantaneously. The damage can be 0 due to mitigation or other effects, but can never be negative. [1] Damage dealt by hits always has one of 3 damage sources ( attack , spell or secondary ) and consists of any 5 damage types ( physical , fire , cold , lightning or chaos ).
Hit | Mechanics | Besides the amount of damage, its type and source, 'hit packages' also contain various mechanics and effects, such as:
Hit | Mechanics | It is possible for a single hit to involve multiple damage calculations, for example with dual wielding skills like Dual Strike or Viper Strike of the Mamba , the explosion of Explosive Arrow , or the wound mechanic of Vaal Flicker Strike. In this case, each damage calculation is independent, and the calculated totals are combined before damage is mitigated by the enemy. For the purpose of on-crit effects, a combined hit counts as a critical strike if at least one damage calculation dealt a critical strike. (This does not affect damage calculations, as those have already happened.) [2] [3] On-hit effects such as non-damaging ailments , Cruelty Support , or impale do not have independent calculations; these happen normally, when damage is applied by the combined hit. [4]
Hit | Mechanics | Because hits are a direct interaction between attacker and defender, they are able to query stats and conditions from both entities, allowing the existence of conditional modifiers such as against Chilled Enemies or from Blinded Enemies. Such modifiers are unable to affect non-ailment damage over time. [5] [6]
Hit | Mechanics | Some self-damage causes the player to hit themselves, which has modified interactions.
Hit | On/when hit effects | "On Hit" effects occur when the player deals a hit, "When Hit" effects occur when the player takes a hit.
Hit | On/when hit effects | On-hit effects occur after a hit's damage is calculated, except stun and damaging ailments , which happen during damage calculation. [7] This means effects like curses or other debuffs do not modify the damage of the hit that applies them. [8]
Hit | On/when hit effects | Blocking generally prevents the attacker's on-hit effects, but not the defender's when-hit effects. [9] This applies even when block does not prevent all damage, such as with Glancing Blows.
Hit | On/when hit effects | On-hit effects include, but are not limited to:
