Hit | Keystone passive skills | The following keystone passive skills are related to hit:
Hit | Masteries | The following Masteries are related to hit:
Hit | Ascendancy passive skills | There are Ascendancy passive skills that affect hit:
Hit combination | Description | Hit combination is a mechanic used by certain skills that allows them to combine the hit damage and ailment DPS of multiple damage calculations into one. It is typical of attacks that use both hands simultaneously while dual wielding , though not exclusive to them.
Hit combination | Mechanics | Skills that combine damage calculate their damage independently per weapon (e.g. Dual Strike ), per arrow ( Explosive Arrow 's explosion), or per wound ( Vaal Flicker Strike ). [1] The calculated values are then combined and applied as one, after mitigation and stun chance, but before the target rolls for block. See receiving damage for all steps of damage calculation.
Hit combination | Mechanics | This means each weapon/arrow/wound has its own:
Hit combination | Mechanics | Hit damage and ailment DPS values are combined before the target rolls for block. It is not possible to block a combined hit partially, except for Vaal Flicker Strike.
Hit combination | Interactions with hit-related effects | Effects that modify damage calculation, meaning hit damage, damaging ailment DPS, and stun, [8] apply to each damage calculation individually. Effects that occur after damage calculation apply only to the combined hit. For example, #% more Damage with Ignites you inflict with Hits for which the highest Damage Type is Fire checks each individual damage calculation, while Trinity Support 's highest Damage Type refers to damage taken from the combined hit instead.
Hit combination | Interactions with hit-related effects | Similarly, local damage and stun modifiers on weapons (e.g. Hits can't be Evaded , Attacks with this Weapon Penetrate #% Elemental Resistances , #% reduced Enemy Stun Threshold with this Weapon ) only affect the damage calculations of those weapons, while local weapon modifiers that apply after damage calculation affect the combined hit as a whole. For example, because leech occurs after damage is calculated and combined, Bloodseeker 's Life Leech from Hits with this Weapon is instant applies to all of a combined hit's damage, not just damage contributed by the Bloodseeker.
Hit combination | Interactions with hit-related effects | While hit combination is disadvantageous for effects like gain on hit , it can be advantageous for effects that scale with hit damage, such as Shock , Cruelty Support , or impale (which can be further magnified by e.g. The Impaler ), or for effects that interact favorably with a single high DPS ailment, such as Master Toxicist , Alchemist's Mark , Flame Surge , or Low Tolerance.
Hit combination | Interactions with hit-related effects | A combined hit stuns if any individual damage calculation successfully stunned. Similarly, for the purpose of effects that check for critical strikes, the combined hit is considered a critical strike if any component of it dealt a critical strike. This does not affect damage, as damage calculations have already happened. [9] [10] For example, Perfect Agony will already have prevented damaging ailments from weapons/arrows/wounds that failed to crit. [11]
Hit combination | Interactions with hit-related effects | When different skills or entities contribute to the same combined hit, which may be the case for Explosive Arrow , the combined hit is dealt by the attacker that caused it (i.e. the last arrow if the maximum number of stuck arrows was reached, otherwise the first). The hit will gain that attacker's on-hit effects and (non-damage) modifiers, such as ailment duration. [12]
Hit combination | Interactions with hit-related effects | Vaal Flicker Strike has unique behaviour in that each wound also counts as an immediate zero damage hit. These hits do not stun or apply on-hit effects that require damage, but can grant or apply other effects on hit, and will consume hits from existing impale debuffs. Each wounding hit can be blocked individually, preventing damage from that specific wound. Blocking the final combined hit prevents damaging ailments, even if unblocked wounding hits did calculate non-zero ailment DPS.
Hit combination | Relevant skills | Note that Viper Strike and Viper Strike of the Mamba do not combine damage due to their Each Weapon Hits separately.
Hunted Traitors | Description | Hunted Traitors are a category of non-native monsters that can appear inside a map that give greatly increased items and experience. Notably, they are considered hostile to both the player and regular enemies and will be engaged in combat with nearby enemies. [1]
Hunted Traitors | Description | Currently, Hunted Traitors can only be encountered in a map opened with a Scarab of Hunted Traitors.
Hybrid gem | Description | Hybrid gem is an unofficial term that refers to gems that have both a skill gem and support gem component, or in Infernal Cry 's case, a secondary skill.
Hybrid gem | Description | Hybrid gems do not include Lancing Steel , Shattering Steel of Ammunition or Splitting Steel of Ammunition , as the secondary skill Call of Steel cannot be supported by support gem linked to the Steel gems and is more akin to Detonate Mines granted by mine skills.
Identify | Description | Identifying reveals an Unidentified item's modifiers. Most items that drop from monsters or chests which can have randomized properties will drop/appear as an Unidentified item. An item can be identified by using a Scroll of Wisdom on the item or by using the "Identify Items" feature found at various NPCs.
Identify | Mechanics | Most items with a rarity higher than Normal drop unidentified. Non-normal strongboxes also usually appear unidentified. Vendor recipe outcomes, except "crafting" recipes that give a fixed mod, give unidentified items. Unidentified items cannot be equipped by the player or have other currency items applied to them. They also cannot be targeted with Animate Weapon or Animate Guardian. Item filters cannot read unidentified modifiers on items even if the modifiers are fixed.
Identify | Mechanics | Corrupted , Mirrored , and Unmodifiable items can be identified, but Contraband items (items found in Heist encounters) cannot be identified until the Contraband property is removed by exiting the area.
Identify | Mechanics | Items can drop already identified in certain cases, such as with other modifiers that cause items to drop identified. Certain items like most corrupted items and veiled items drop identified.
Identify | Identifying items | Unidentified items can be identified by using a Scroll of Wisdom on them. Additionally, all Act NPCs that sell currency and caster items, Helena in hideouts , and Rog in Kingsmarch have the "Identify Items" option available to them, which identifies all items in the player's inventory when pressed. The hotkey CTRL + ALT + LMB can be used to quickly use this function without opening the NPC menus. Nessa in Act 1 does not have this function until the player reaches The Cavern of Anger.
Identify | Maps | Unidentified maps can be opened in the Map Device , which adds a +30% item quantity bonus to non-unique maps. Modifiers on that map will still be hidden from the player even when in the map instance.
Identify | Selling | Identified magic , rare , unique items sell for different currency items than their unidentified variants. Unidentified magic and rare items give a set amount of Transmutation Shards when sold to vendors, while identified items give Alteration Shards and/or Alchemy Shards based on their modifiers. However, certain vendor recipes give more items when sold unidentified, such as the Chaos Orb recipe for a full set of equipment.
Identify | Selling | Players in trade leagues may sometimes wish to sell a unique item unidentified, particularly for items that can roll a wide range of modifiers that can't be rerolled, such as a Watcher's Eye or Impossible Escape. Some players will buy unidentified uniques to "gamble" on identifying a highly valuable modifier for a lower price.
Identify | Related unique items | The following unique items are related to the mechanics of identification:
Ignore | Description | Ignore is the ability to completely ignore certain effects, stats or game mechanics without directly affecting their values. Common mechanics that can be ignored on monsters include resistances , physical damage reduction , or the Hexproof keyword. Effects on the player that can be ignored include movement penalties from armour and attribute requirements.
Ignore | Mods | No results found
Ignore | Masteries | The following Masteries are related to Ignore:
Immortal Syndicate | Description | The Immortal Syndicate is a mysterious organization being investigated by Jun Ortoi. The player must neutralize the Syndicate members residing in the zone, then interrogate them for intelligence on their stronghold and leader, or bargain with them in different ways. Syndicate members can drop veiled items , and strongholds can contain various rewards depending on the position and rank of members, including scarabs.
Immortal Syndicate | Members | The Immortal Syndicate consists of the Syndicate Mastermind and a roster consisting of up to 14 of 17 other members, who are encountered in maps if the Immortal Syndicate has spawned on the map. Players will encounter members at random. They will appear on the minimap and may be guarding a Transport ( ), Fortification ( ), Research ( ) or portal to the player and attempt to assasinate them (Intervention).
Immortal Syndicate | Members | Gravicius will never appear on the very first Syndicate Board in new leagues. Rin only joins the Syndicate as a potential option after the player reaches Maps.
Immortal Syndicate | Investigation Board | Each known Syndicate member on the board will display the following: Rank, Task, and Syndicate Gear.
Immortal Syndicate | Investigation Board | Ranks are indicated by the number of stars on the top right, going up to 3 stars (Sergeant -> Lieutenant -> Captain). Higher-ranked members grant better rewards, hinted at by their tasks, but also equip more Syndicate Gear that make them more difficult. Executing a member raises their rank, while interrogating them lowers it. A member must be assigned to a division to have a rank and have their reward appear at the safehouse. If a member's rank falls to 0, they will become unassigned. Each division can have up to 5 members (including the leader), with a minimum of 2.
Immortal Syndicate | Investigation Board | The board also shows the relationship between Syndicate members. Trusted members (green lines) are more likely to assist each other in combat, while rivals (red lines) are more likely to attack or betray them instead.
Immortal Syndicate | Investigation Board | Each division has a leader. Leaders do not appear as primary targets and will only appear to help or hinder another member. If the leader is interrogated or their rank is lowered to 0, one of their subordinates in that division (or an unassigned member if no subordinates exist) with the highest rank will become the new leader.
Immortal Syndicate | Encounter | The Immortal Syndicate is divided into four divisions: Transportation, Fortification, Research, and Intervention. One random division can be encountered in an area in the campaign starting from Act 9 ; in maps , the player can encounter up to three (either Transportation or Fortification, and guaranteed Research and Intervention). If multiple events exist in an area, the active event must be completed to begin the next one.
Immortal Syndicate | Encounter | Once all members of an event have been defeated or successfully escaped, defeated members can be handled in one of three presented options. One of these options is always to release the member (middle button); this results in no change to the board state but still causes the member to provide default loot and experience. If multiple members are present, the options may change depending on their order of interaction and relationships with other members
Immortal Syndicate | Encounter | The other two options consist of "Interrogate" and one other option. The possible options are as follows:
Immortal Syndicate | Outcomes | The following outcomes are possible from Bargain:
Immortal Syndicate | Outcomes | The following outcomes are possible from Betray:
Immortal Syndicate | Syndicate gear | Syndicate members gain a random piece of Syndicate Gear (also referred to as Equipment) when they are Executed which grant them additional combat stats or skills. These are displayed on the Investigation Board interface.
Immortal Syndicate | Syndicate gear | The same Syndicate Gear cannot be attached to multiple members at the same time, and a member cannot have multiple gear of the same type. The maximum number of carried gear is three. Players cannot obtain these gear as they are not real items.
Immortal Syndicate | Syndicate gear | Syndicate Gear can be destroyed as a Betray or Bargain option.
Immortal Syndicate | Syndicate Safehouse | Once intelligence in a division reaches 100%, you can raid their safehouse. Talk to Jun in the hideout to open 6 portals to a safehouse. If the player does not raid the safehouse after reaching 100% intelligence, the intelligence will drop down to 90%. The safehouse's area level will be equal to the highest level Syndicate encounter you've completed for that specific division. Characters cannot open portals to a safehouse or enter a portal leading to one if they have not reached Highgate in Act 9.
Immortal Syndicate | Syndicate Safehouse | When raiding a Syndicate Safehouse, the Safehouse leader and all of his or her subordinates will defend it. Once they are defeated, the player can Execute the leader; all other members will flee. Afterwards, the 'living quarters' are unlocked. The 'living quarters' consist of up to 5 rooms that contain rewards or crafting benches that correspond to the members, their ranks, and the division of that safehouse. They can contain a Syndicate Crafting Bench that allows for a crafting spree with a pre-generated item or the player's own for a limited time, or a "Trapped chest" that provides a selection of items which only one item can be removed within a time limit. The notes on the Syndicate interface provide hints on what reward can be expected. These rewards are further described below.
Immortal Syndicate | Syndicate Safehouse | In addition to their respective rewards, Safehouse leaders have a chance to drop Veiled Chaos Orbs (~50% at Rank 3), certain types of Allflame embers (100% drop chance at Rank 3, weighted variants), and at area level 78+ (red tier maps ) also has a chance to drop a Syndicate Medallion (~12.5% at Rank 3), a map fragment required to access the Mastermind encounter. Additionally, safehouse leaders at area level 78+ have a chance to drop an exclusive veiled unique item (~5% at Rank 3); the specific unique item that can drop depends on the safehouse's division. [1]
Immortal Syndicate | Syndicate Safehouse | Upon executing the safehouse leader, the leader will lose all ranks and a random syndicate member that is not currently within a division (including any subordinates you just defeated) becomes the new leader of the division.
Immortal Syndicate | Detailed rewards by member/division | Trapped stashes rewarding equipment can be capped by space available (E.g. there is not enough space for more than 6x body armour in the trapped stash window).
Immortal Syndicate | League merge | When a league is merged with different Betrayal board states (e.g. a temporary league merge into permanent league ), the higher intelligence value of each division between the two leagues is kept. Other aspects of the Immortal Syndicate, including the members, their divisions, and their ranks, retain their state in the parent league.
Immortal Syndicate | Ruthless mode | There are many differences to safehouse loot with Ruthless mode enabled. Generally speaking, looting safehouses in Ruthless mode provides more ways to obtain pieces of equipment for specific slots, but is much less generous with currency items and crafting options.
Immunity | Description | Immunity is a stat that prevents and removes certain effects (e.g. debuffs or ailments ) or nullifies certain damage types. Immunity is typically worded as either Immune to X or Immunity to X.
Immunity | Mechanics | The most common forms of immunity prevent ailments , but items such as the Eye of Chayula can provide other immunities.
Immunity | Mechanics | Note that this should not be confused with Cannot be X ; although similar, and often also referred to as immunity, this stat is more akin to avoidance and does not remove any existing effects. [1]
Immunity | Mechanics | It should also not be confused with Unaffected by X or 100% effect reduction, which will cause the debuff icon to appear and affect the target, but have no actual effect. This is typically for situations where the debuff provides or enables a secondary beneficial effect.
Immunity | Damage immunity | Damage immunity is a form of mitigation. It mitigates damage after damage taken as , and damage mitigated by immunity counts as 'prevented' damage for e.g. Untiring or Divine Shield. Damage immunity will not prevent non-damage loss due to e.g. Dark Pact or Rathpith Globe.
Immunity | Damage immunity | The Cannot take Reflected Physical/Elemental Damage modifiers are similar to damage immunity, though they apply both before and after damage shifts.
Immunity | Monsters | Some bosses are immune to certain ailments or effects such as stun or knockback.
Immunity | Monsters | Some are immune to damage during certain phases of fights. Harbingers are immune to direct damage and are instead defeated by slaying their summoned monsters. Rare and Unique monsters are immune to fleeing.
Immunity | Modifiers | Flasks can grant temporary immunity to bleeding , curses , poison , ignite , chill , freeze , and shock with the following suffix mods. These mods also remove the effect. No results found
Immunity | Modifiers | The Essence of Delirium grants immunity to poison when applied to boots.
Immunity | Modifiers | Jewels can be corrupted to have You cannot be cursed with Silence , Corrupted Blood cannot be inflicted on you , You cannot be hindered , or You cannot be maimed.
Immunity | All elemental ailment immunity | No results found for the given query.
Influence | Description | Influence refers to monsters and items that have been empowered by powerful entities from the Atlas of Worlds. Influenced monsters can appear in maps that have had their influence drawn out by certain actions or modifiers, and may drop influenced items , special item bases that can roll modifiers not found on their normal counterparts.
Influence | Shaper/Elder | Maps can drop with a Shaper or Elder influence, adding monsters and hazards of their respective influence.
Influence | Shaper/Elder | Shaper Guardian maps are inherently Shaper-influenced. A map occupied by an Elder Guardian will also be Elder-influenced. Commander Kirac may offer a Shaper/Elder-influenced map without a Guardian as part of his mission or sold by him.
Influence | Conqueror | Maps that contain a Conquerors ' Citadel are influenced by the respective Conqueror. Conqueror-influenced maps contain packs of influenced monsters exclusive to that Conqueror, and map bosses gain a buff of the associated damage type.
Influence | Exarch/Eater | Once you obtain a Luminous Astrolabe or Flesh Compass , you can call upon the influence of the Searing Exarch or the Eater of Worlds to your map, respectively, from your map device. Exarch and Eater influences can be stacked with Shaper/Elder/Conqueror influences. Exarch/Eater-influenced monsters can spawn an eldritch altar on death, giving the player a choice of two modifiers to add the the map, and spawn more influenced monsters when activated.
Influence | Exarch/Eater | Exarch and Eater-influenced monsters can drop embers or ichors that add an eldritch implicit modifier to certain equipment types. Items with an eldritch implicit are not considered to be an influenced item, and an item cannot have an influence and eldritch implicit mods at the same time. They can also drop eldritch currency items with effects that change based on which of the two eldritch implicits have the higher tier.
Influence | Exarch/Eater | The Maven and Maven-witnessed bosses, despite being thematically similar, are not considered influenced, and have no respective monsters or items associated with the mechanic.
Influence | Originator | Players can obtain memory influenced maps that contain the Originator's influence in the Atlas. These maps contain Originator-influenced monsters that drop Memory Petals on death. These petals are used to activate special abilities within the map. These maps can roll modifiers normally found in Tier 17 maps and have a chance to drop items with Memory Strands. Tier 16 maps have a chance to drop as memory influenced maps randomly, and maps may occasionally contain a petal of roses that drop a memory influenced map relative to the current map's tier.
Influence | Originator | After finding a Memory Tear, Eagon will offer a chain of maps in the Threads of Consciousness that are influenced by the Originator.

Intensity | Description | Intensity is a counter for several in-game mechanics. Intensity is gained by using the skill that grants it and decays while moving.
Intensity | Description | Intensify Support improves area damage and decreases area of effect as you gain Intensity. Pinpoint Support improves projectile damage and decreases the number of fired projectiles as you gain Intensity. Crackling Lance scales beam width, branching angle and damage with Intensity.
Intensity | Mechanics | Without other items and passive skills, the maximum stack of Intensity is 3. An Intensity stack is lost once every 0.5 seconds while moving.
Intensity | Mechanics | Intensify and Pinpoint Support cannot support triggered skills, Vaal skills, instant skills, channelling skills, skills with a reservation or which create minions, or skills used by totems, traps or mines. Similarly, Crackling Lance will only gain Intensity when you "cast it", implying you do not gain Intensity if the skill is used by totems, traps or mines, or if it is triggered.
Intensity | Mechanics | When a gem is added to or removed from an item which currently has a skill with Intensity stacks socketed, those Intensity stacks are removed. The skill also stops gaining Intensity from (for example) the Spells which have gained Intensity Recently gain 1 Intensity every 0.5 seconds modifier on Apex Mode until intensity is gained again. This means there are no known ways to interact Intensity with totems, traps, mines or triggering.

Keyword | Description | Keywords are words or phrases with Path of Exile -specific mechanical significance. When appearing in modifier text, they are always capitalized. For words with everyday meanings, like "double", "triple", and " recently ", capitalized instances are keywords and follow strict in-game definitions, while non-capitalized instances refer to the everyday definition.
Keyword | Ailments | Ailments are a type of debuff associated and applied by one or more damage types. Ailments normally distinguish themselves from other debuffs by being applied by hits , which allows them to check conditions on the enemy, and vary their effect or duration based on damage instead of having a predetermined value from a skill or modifier.
Keyword | Ailments | Freeze , ignite , and shock are the default ailments of cold , fire , and lightning damage respectively. Critical strikes with these elements have a 100% chance of inflicting their respective ailments. Brittle , scorch , and sap are their respective alternate ailments.
Keyword | Ailments | Damaging Ailments : Damaging Ailments are ailments that deal damage over time. Bleeding , poison , and ignite are damaging ailments. The remaining ailments, chill , freeze , shock , scorch , brittle , and sap , are non-Damaging Ailment s.
Keyword | Bleeding | Bleeding is a damaging ailment inflicted by physical damage from attacks. Bleeding causes affected targets to take physical damage over time for a duration, based on 70% of the base physical damage of the skill per second. Bleeding deals triple the damage over time on moving targets. The base duration is 5 seconds.
Keyword | Bleeding | Bleeding can be Aggravated to cause it to deal damage as if the afflicted target is always moving, lasting for the bleed's remaining duration.
Keyword | Brittle | Brittle is a non-damaging ailment inflicted by cold damage. Brittle causes hits against affected targets to have up to +6% base critical strike chance against them, based on the cold damage of the hit. The base duration is 4 seconds. Brittle is cold damage's alternate ailment.
Keyword | Chill | Chill is a non-damaging ailment inflicted by cold damage. Chill slows the action speed of the affected target up to 30%, based on the cold damage of the hit. The base duration is 2 seconds. All hits of cold damage will attempt to inflict chill.
Keyword | Freeze | Freeze is a non-damaging ailment inflicted by cold damage. Frozen slows the action speed of the affected target, completely preventing the affected target from moving, attacking, or using any skills. The base minimum duration is 0.3 seconds and the base maximum duration is 3 seconds. Critical strikes dealt by cold damage have 100% chance to freeze.
Keyword | Ignite | Ignite is a damaging ailment inflicted by fire damage. Ignite causes the affected target to burn based on 90% of the base fire damage of the skill per second. The base duration is 4 seconds. Critical strikes dealt by fire damage have 100% chance to ignite.
Keyword | Poison | Poison is a damaging ailment inflicted by physical and chaos damage. Poison causes the affected target to take chaos damage over time for a duration, based on 30% of the base physical and chaos damage of the skill per second. Poison can stack and has no inherent limit. Each stack has an independent duration and will not be refreshed by inflicting additional stacks. The base duration is 2 seconds.
Keyword | Sap | Sap is a non-damaging ailment inflicted by lightning damage. Sap causes the affected target to deal up to 20% less damage, based on the lightning damage of the hit. The base duration is 4 seconds. Sap is the lightning damage's alternate ailment.
Keyword | Scorch | Scorch is a non-damaging ailment inflicted by fire damage. Scorch causes the affected target to have up to -30% lowered elemental resistances, based on the fire damage of the hit. The base duration is 4 seconds. Scorch is fire damage's alternate ailment.
Keyword | Shock | Shock is a non-damaging ailment inflicted by lightning damage. Shock causes the affected target to take up to 50% increased damage from all sources, based on the lightning damage of the hit. The base duration is 2 seconds. Critical strikes dealt by lightning damage have 100% chance to shock.
Keyword | Attributes | Attributes are dexterity , intelligence , and strength. Each attribute grants their own inherent bonuses and are used to satisfy equipment and gem attribute requirements.
Keyword | Attribute Requirements | Attribute Requirements are requirements on equipment and gems that define the amount of specific attributes that are required to equip a given item. Attributes can be modified globally with #% [increased/reduced] Attribute Requirements and modified locally with [+/-]# [Attribute] Requirement and #% [increased/reduced] [Attribute] Requirement.
Keyword | Dexterity | Dexterity is an attribute associated with cold damage , evasion , accuracy , and all equipment with dexterity requirements.
Keyword | Intelligence | Intelligence is an attribute associated with lightning damage , chaos damage , mana , energy shield , and all equipment with intelligence requirements.
Keyword | Strength | Strength is an attribute associated with fire damage , physical damage , armour , and all equipment with strength requirements.
Keyword | Buffs | Buffs are a type of effect that modifies a character or monster, usually in a neutral or positive way. When active, buffs appear with specific green borders in the UI on the upper-left hand corner of the screen. Buffs are either temporary and have durations , or are tied to specific modifiers.
Keyword | Adrenaline | Adrenaline is a non-stackable buff that grants 100% increased Damage , 25% increased Attack, Cast and Movement Speed , and 10% additional Physical Damage Reduction. You cannot gain Adrenaline while you have the Adrenaline buff.
Keyword | Alchemist's Genius | Alchemist's Genius is a non-stackable buff that grants 10% increased Effect of Flasks on you and 20% increased Flask Charges Gained.
Keyword | Chaotic Might | Chaotic Might is a non-stackable buff that grants Gain 30% of Physical Damage as Extra Chaos Damage.
Keyword | Conflux | Conflux is a family of non-stackable keyword [1] buffs that grant All of your damage [elemental ailment]s. Variants of conflux include Igniting Conflux ( ignite ), Chilling Conflux ( chill ), Shocking Conflux ( shock ), Elemental Conflux (shock, chill, & ignite), Scorching Conflux ( scorch ), Brittle Conflux ( brittle ), and Sapping Conflux ( sap ). Note that, despite being an elemental ailment, freeze has no associated type of conflux.
Keyword | Elusive | Elusive is a non-stackable buff that, at 100% effect, grants 30% increased Movement Speed and 15% chance to Avoid All Damage from Hits. Unlike other buffs, Elusive does not have an innate duration. Its effect decays over time at a rate of 20% per second and removes itself when it reaches 0% effect. You cannot gain Elusive while you have the Elusive buff.
Keyword | Fortification | Fortification is a stackable buff that grants 1% less Damage taken per Foritification. Foritification has a default maximum of 20 stacks and has a 6 second duration.
Keyword | Fortification | Hits may fortify , granting a variable number of fortification stacks, based on how much damage the hit would have dealt to the enemy before taking into account the enemy's damage reduction, relative to the enemy's ailment threshold. As there are no sources of fortify on hit that do not specify melee hits, it is practically impossible to fortify with a non- melee hit.
Keyword | Onslaught | Onslaught is a non-stackable buff that grants 20% increased Attack, Cast and Movement Speed. When applied by a Silver Flask , modifiers to flask effect will modify Onslaught's effect.
Keyword | Phasing | Phasing is a non-stackable buff that allows affected monsters and characters to move through enemies.
Keyword | Soul Eater | Soul Eater is a buff that causes affected characters and monsters to Eat a Soul when they kill an enemy, gaining an Eaten Soul. There is a maximum of 45 souls. Characters and monsters gain 5% increased attack speed and cast speed per soul, with monsters gaining an additional 2% less Damage Taken per soul. A soul is lost every 0.5 seconds if a soul has not been gained recently. The effect does not stack or refresh, and Soul Eater cannot be gained while an entity already has Soul Eater.
Keyword | Soul Eater | Soul Eater on monsters do not have a duration and will last indefinitely unless the monster has phase transitions. Soul Eater stacks are reset to zero if a monster becomes possessed by a Tormented Spirit.
Keyword | Tailwind | Tailwind is a non-stackable buff that grants 8% increased Action Speed.
Keyword | Unholy Might | Unholy Might is a non-stackable buff that grants 100% of Physical Damage Converted to Chaos Damage and 25% chance to inflict Withered for 2 seconds on Hit.
Keyword | Charges | Charges are a type of temporary effect similar to buffs. Charges are identified by silver borders around their icons in the UI and glowing orbs appearing around the owner of the charges. Endurance, frenzy, and power charges are the main types of charges; brutal, affliction, and absorption charges are their respective alternative charges.
Keyword | Minimum charges | Minimum charges are permanent charges. Skills and effects that remove or expend charges, like bypassing the cooldown of Flicker Strike or using Discharge will not affect minimum charges.
Keyword | Absorption Charges | Absorption Charges are a type of charge associated with intelligence. It is the alternate charge to power charges. All player characters have the following modifiers:
Keyword | Affliction Charges | Affliction Charges are a type of charge associated with dexterity. It is the alternate charge to frenzy charges. All player characters have the following modifiers:
Keyword | Brutal Charges | Brutal Charges are a type of charge associated with strength. It is the alternate charge to endurance charges. All player characters have the following modifiers:
Keyword | Endurance Charges | Endurance Charges are a type of charge associated with strength. Endurance charges are red. All player characters have the following modifiers:
Keyword | Frenzy Charges | Frenzy Charges are a type of charge associated with dexterity. Frenzy charges are green. All player characters have the following modifiers:
Keyword | Power Charges | Power Charges are a type of charge associated with intelligence. Power charges are blue. All player characters have the following modifiers:
Keyword | Cosmetics | Cosmetics may be granted by associated item modifiers.
Keyword | Curses | Curses are a category of debuff classified into two categories: Hexes and Marks.
Keyword | Curse limit | By default, one curse can be active at a time on a target. While a curse is active, applying a different curse on the same target will expire the oldest curse. Different targets can have different curses applied by the same player, without the curses being lifted from the others. You can apply an additional Curse can increase this limit.
Keyword | Hexes | Hexes are a type of curse characterized by being able to be applied to multiple targets.
Keyword | Marks | Marks are a type of curse characterized by only applying to single targets. Marks will not expire through duration.
Keyword | Marks | Each character can only place a mark on one target at any time. This limit is shared between all mark skills. If you applied a mark on an enemy and then apply any mark skill again, the previous mark will expire. Moving a great distance away from the marked target will also expire the mark.
Keyword | Damage sources | All damage originates from one of four sources.
Keyword | Attack | Attacks are a category of skills characterized by the attacker trying to hit their target with their weapon , while unarmed , or with projectiles fired directly from their weapon ( bows and wands ). If the damage does not involve an attacker trying to hit with any of the previous methods, it is an attack. Attacks have a chance to be evaded , determined by the defender's evasion rating and the attacker's accuracy. Unlike spells, attacks will always try to deal damage.
Keyword | Spell | Spells are the set of all skills that are not attacks ; they do not involve the attacker trying to hit their target with their weapon , while unarmed , or with projectiles fired directly from their weapon ( bows and wands ). Unlike attacks, many spells do not deal damage. Spell damage cannot miss.
Keyword | Secondary | Secondary damage is a category of damage characterized by being difficult to scale due to being neither attack nor spell damage. Explosions , damage dealt by heralds , and self-damage dealt through items like Heartbound Loop and Scold's Bridle are examples of secondary damage.
Keyword | Damage over Time | Damage over Time is damage inflicted continuously over a period of time. Unlike damage from all other sources, damage over time cannot hit. All damage over time effects are a kind of debuff.
Keyword | Damage over Time | Damage over Time Multiplier multiplies the amount of damage dealt by damage over time.
Keyword | Damage types | All damage belongs to one of five types: cold, lightning, fire damage, physical, and chaos damage. Cold, lightning, and fire damage are classified as elemental damage.
Keyword | Damage types | Physical damage
Keyword | Damage types | Lightning damage
Keyword | Damage types | Cold damage
Keyword | Damage types | Fire damage
Keyword | Damage types | Chaos damage
Keyword | Debuffs | Debuffs are a type of effect that modifies a character or monster , usually in a negative. When active, debuffs appear with specific red borders in the UI on the upper-left hand corner of the screen. Debuffs are either temporary and have durations , or are tied to specific modifiers. For each adjective keyword describing the state of having a given debuff, there is an associated verb keyword that describes the action of applying it, conforming to standard rules of English.
Keyword | Blinded | Blinded is a keyword debuff that causes the affected target to have 20% less Accuracy , 20% less Evasion , and reduces the target's light radius to the minimum value.
Keyword | Corrupted Blood | Corrupted Blood is a stackable debuff that deals physical damage over time. Corrupted Blood can stack up to ten times. The damage dealt is a flat value, highly variable depending on its source. Inflicting Corrupted Blood onto a target will refresh the duration of all existing stacks.
Keyword | Covered in Ash | Covered in Ash is a keyword debuff that causes the affected target to have 20% increased Fire Damage Taken and 20% less Movement Speed. Covered by Ash applied by Infernal Cry has variable values of #% increased Fire Damage Taken.
Keyword | Covered in Frost | Covered in Frost is a keyword debuff that causes the affected target to have 20% increased Cold Damage Taken and 50% Critical Strike Chance.
Keyword | Crushed | Crushed is a keyword debuff that causes the affected target to have -15% additional Physical Damage Reduction.
Keyword | Debilitated | Debilitated is a keyword debuff that causes the affected target to have Deal 10% less Damage and 20% less Movement Speed.
Keyword | Exposure | Exposure is a family of keyword debuffs that includes Lightning Exposure , Cold Exposure , and Fire Exposure. Targets that have Exposure of a given element will have -% to the respective resistance. If unspecified, Exposure's default value if unspecified is 10% if applied by a character , and 25% if applied by a monster. However, when specified by its source, its value may be highly variable.
Keyword | Extinguish | Extinguished is a keyword debuff that prevents the afflicted from applying elemental ailments.
Keyword | Hinder | Hindered is a keyword debuff that causes the affected target to have #% reduced Movement Speed. Hinder's default value is 30% reduced Movement Speed. However, many sources of Hinder specific custom values. Multiple hinders do not stack. Hinder is applied by spells , just like maim is by attacks. Since hinder and maim are different debuffs, an enemy can be affected by both simultaneously.
Keyword | Intimidate | Intimidated is a keyword debuff that causes the affected target to have 10% increased Attack Damage taken.
Keyword | Maimed | Maimed is a keyword [1] debuff that causes the affected target to have 30% reduced Movement Speed. Multiple maims do not stack. Maim is applied by attacks , just like hinder is by spells. Since maim and hinder are different debuffs, an enemy can be affected by both simultaneously.
Keyword | Malediction | Malediction is a keyword debuff that causes the affected target to have 10% increased Damage taken and 10% reduced Damage dealt.
Keyword | Taunted | Taunted is a keyword debuff that causes the affected target have Deal 10% less Damage to any targets that did not apply the taunt. If a monster is affected, they will prioritize targeting the source of the taunt over any other targets.
Keyword | Unnerved | Unnerved is a keyword debuff that causes the affected target to have 10% increased Spell Damage taken.
Keyword | Withered | Withered is a stackable keyword debuff that causes the affected target to have 6% increased Chaos Damage taken. Withered can stack up to 15 times on a single target.
Keyword | Defences | Defences , usually referred to as Global Defences , is a keyword that collectively refers to armour , energy shield , evasion rating , and ward. It may also refer to the base defences granted by a specific piece of equipment , in the case of modifiers like #% increased Defences from equipped Shield.
Keyword | Armour | Armour is a form of defence that mitigates physical damage from hits. When a defender is hit by physical damage, their armour is checked against the incoming physical damage and the armour accordingly provides a certain percentage of physical damage reduction. A given percentage of physical damage reduction granted will require exponentially greater quantities of armour against a linearly increasing amount of damage dealt. Armour is most effective against relatively small hits and least effective against relatively large hits.
Keyword | Energy shield | Energy shield is a form of defence that acts as an additional hit pool which damage is taken from before life. Energy shield will recharge naturally after the defender has not taken any damage for 2 seconds.
Keyword | Evasion rating | Evasion rating is a form of defence that grants a chance to prevent incoming attacks from hitting the defender. When an attacker tries to hit a defender, the attacker's accuracy is checked against the defender's evasion rating. The greater the attacker's accuracy and the lesser the defender's evasion rating, the greater the chance to hit becomes.
Keyword | Evasion rating | Evade refers to your overall chance to evade an attack. Effects which grant an flat amount of chance to evade is added after calculating evasion rating against accuracy.
Keyword | Ward | Ward is a form of defence that reduces the damage taken from an incoming hit equal to the current value of ward. When ward defends damage, all ward is depleted; ward regenerates 4 seconds after being depleted.
Keyword | Gems | Gems are a type of item divided into two categories: skill gems and support gems. Equipped skill gems grant unique skills to the character. Support gems do not grant skills; instead, they augment the effects and abilities of compatible skills and skill gems.
Keyword | Skill gems | Skill gems , also known as Active Skill Gems , are a type of gem that, when equipped in an item socket , grant unique skills to the character. Only player characters can use skill gems.
Keyword | Support gems | Support gems are a type of gem that augment the effects and abilities of compatible skills and skill gems. To support a skill gem, a support gem must be socketed into an item socket connected by a socket link to the socket in which the skill gem is socketed. When socketed into items with modifiers that grant skills, like Death's Oath 's Trigger Level 20 Death Aura when Equipped or The Dancing Dervish 's Triggers Level 15 Manifest Dancing Dervishes on Rampage , support gems will support the given skills regardless of links. The effects of support gems may additionally be granted by modifiers like Socketed Gems are Supported by Level # [Support Gem Name].
Keyword | Ground effects | Ground effects are patches of terrain that grant certain effects to characters or monsters while they are standing on them. When you are standing on a beneficial ground effect, its effects will appear as a buff on the UI, while detrimental ground effects will
Keyword | Brittle ground | Brittle ground is a detrimental ground effect that inflicts brittle. Unless otherwise specified, it has a base brittle value of 2%.
Keyword | Burning ground | Burning ground is a detrimental ground effect. Burning ground deals burning damage ( fire damage over time ). The values of damage dealt by differing sources of burning ground are highly variable.
Keyword | Caustic ground | Caustic ground is a detrimental ground effect. Desecrated ground deals chaos damage over time. The values of damage dealt by differing sources of caustic1 ground are highly variable.
Keyword | Consecrated ground | Consecrated ground is a beneficial ground effect. Consecrated ground grants the following effects:
Keyword | Chilled ground | Chilled ground is a detrimental ground effect that inflicts chilled. Unless otherwise specified, it has a base chill value of 10%.
Keyword | Desecrated ground | Desecrated ground is a detrimental ground effect. Desecrated ground deals chaos damage over time. The values of damage dealt by differing sources of desecrated ground are highly variable.
Keyword | Profane ground | Profane ground is a detrimental ground effect. Profane ground inflicts the following:
Keyword | Sapped ground | Sapped ground is a detrimental ground effect that inflicts sapped. Unless otherwise specified, it has a base sapped value of 6%.
Keyword | Scorched ground | Scorched ground is a detrimental ground effect that inflicts scorched. Unless otherwise specified, it has a base scorch value of 10%.
Keyword | Shocked ground | Shocked ground is a detrimental ground effect that inflicts shocked. Unless otherwise specified, it has a base shock value of 15%.
Keyword | Tarred ground | Tarred ground is a detrimental ground effect that inflicts 60% reduced Movement Speed.
Keyword | Hit | Hits are effects that deal distinct amounts of damage to a target instantaneously. The damage can be mitigated down to 0, but can never be negative. Damage dealt by hits always originates from one of 3 damage sources ( attack , spell or secondary , but note that damage over time never hits.) and is composed of any 5 of the damage types ( physical , lightning , cold , fire or chaos ).
Keyword | Accuracy | Accuracy is a mechanic that determines an attack 's chance to hit. When an attacker tries to hit a defender with an attack, the attacker's accuracy is checked against the defender's evasion rating. The higher the attacker's accuracy, and the lower the defender's evasion rating, the higher the chance to hit becomes.
Keyword | Accuracy | +# to Accuracy Rating on a one-handed weapons only affects the local accuracy of that weapon , (relevant while dual wielding ), while Global Accuracy Rating refers to the accuracy of all weapons.
Keyword | Avoidance | Avoidance is a defensive mechanic that prevents incoming hit damage, stuns , or ailments. The damage will still count as a hit, even if damage taken is 0. Damage avoidance from hits is capped at 75%.
Keyword | Block | Block is a defensive mechanic that prevents incoming attack damage. Block is capped by default at 75%.
Keyword | Block | Spell block is mechanically identical to block , with the exception that it applies to spell damage instead of attack damage.
Keyword | Critical strikes | Critical strikes are hits affected by critical strike multiplier. When a skill is used or triggered , a value between 0 and 99.99 is rolled, determining the critical strike chance required by hits to become critical strikes during the crit check. Each hit's critical strike chance is calculated independently. This value is then checked against the crit roll; if the crit chance exceeds the crit roll, the hit will become a critical strike.
Keyword | Critical strikes | Attack skills that pass the crit check must also roll its chance to hit/evade check again (see accuracy/evasion) in order to successfully crit. Failing this second hit chance check does not cause the attack to be evaded; instead, it downgrades the crit to a non-crit. This roll does not affect your entropy value.
Keyword | Culling Strike | Culling Strike is a keyword modifier that causes affected hits to instantly kill enemies with 10% of their maximum life remaining or less.
Keyword | Dodge | Dodge is a defensive mechanic that grants a chance to prevent all effects of an incoming hit of the specified damage source. Unlike evasion , dodge chance is not affected by accuracy and is also not affected by entropy. Currently, the only source of dodge comes from Acrobatics.
Keyword | Double damage and triple damage | Double damage and triple damage are keywords, following strict in-game definitions instead of their everyday meanings.
Keyword | Savage Hit | Savage Hit is a keyword [1] that defines a hit that removes at least 15% of the target's maximum life. Damage to energy shield , mana and ward are not counted toward the savage hit threshold.
Keyword | Suppression | Spell suppression is a defensive mechanic that reduces incoming spell damage. Chance to suppress spell damage can reach up to 100% chance. The default amount of damage suppressed is 50% (halving the damage).
Keyword | Stun | Stun is a mechanic that involves the immobilization of a character or monster after they have taken damage from a hit. The higher the damage taken was relative to the target's maximum life , the longer the stun duration. Melee damage has a +25% bonus to stun chance and non- physical damage has a -25% penalty to stun chance.
Keyword | Keystones | The names of all keystone passive skills on the passive skill tree are keywords and their respective modifiers function identically to their passive tree counterparts. For example, Grelwood Shank 's modifier Point Blank grants the same bonuses as allocating Point Blank. Multiple instances of the same keystone do not stack.
Keyword | Keystones | Some keystone-like modifiers are exclusive to keyword modifiers and cannot be found on the main passive skill tree. Some of these effects appear as monsters modifiers.
Keyword | Battlemage | Battlemage is a keyword [2] that grants Gain Added Spell Damage equal to the Damage of Your Main Hand Weapon.
Keyword | Everlasting Sacrifice | Everlasting Sacrifice grants When you reach full Energy Shield, Sacrifice all Energy Shield to gain +5% to all Maximum Resistances for 4 seconds.
Keyword | Far Shot | Far Shot is a keyword [3] that grants Projectile Attack Hits deal 20% less Damage to targets at the start of their movement, dealing up to 60% more Damage to targets as the projectile travels farther.
Keyword | Shepherd of Souls | Shepherd of Souls grants When you use a Vaal Skill, other Vaal skills gain 50% of the consumed Souls. Deal 30% less Damage with Non-Vaal Skills.
Keyword | Hexproof | Hexproof is a keyword [4] that grants Unaffected by Hexes. Curses negated by Hexproof will have their floating Curse icons above the entity replaced by lock symbols. Hexproof monsters with these lock symbols are still considered cursed even if the curses have no effect.
Keyword | Unwavering | Unwavering is a keyword related to the monster modifier Cannot be Stunned (Hidden) MonsterImplicitCannotBeStunned1 Intrinsic Cannot be Stunned (Hidden) that signifies that the monster cannot be stunned.
Keyword | Transfiguration of Body | Transfiguration of Body is a keyword that grants Increases and Reductions to Maximum Life also apply to Attack Damage at 30% of their value.
Keyword | Transfiguration of Mind | Transfiguration of Mind is a keyword that grants Increases and Reductions to Maximum Mana also apply to Damage at 30% of their value.
Keyword | Transfiguration of Soul | Transfiguration of Soul is a keyword that grants Increases and Reductions to Maximum Energy Shield also apply to Spell Damage at 30% of their value.
Keyword | Lucky | Lucky is a keyword that causes a mechanic to roll twice and use the highest value of the two. For mechanics which only have a pass/fail state, the roll succeeds if at least one of the two rolls is a success.
Keyword | Unlucky | Unlucky causes a mechanic to roll twice and use the lowest value of the two. For mechanics which only have a pass/fail state, the roll fails if at least one of the two rolls fails.
Keyword | Projectiles | Projectiles are entities which are produced by a spell or ranged attack which travel independently of their creator until they collide with an enemy or obstacle or reach their travel distance limit of 150 Units.
Keyword | Projectiles | Projectiles cannot "shotgun"; a single target may not be hit by multiple projectiles formed in the same instance by the same source. Barrage effects and area of effect damage stemming from those projectiles may effectively bypass this limitation.
Keyword | Projectiles | When a projectile hits an enemy, one of the following behaviours may apply. Only a single effect can apply per hit enemy and are applied in the following order:
Keyword | Split | The projectile splits , breaking into (X) auto-targeting projectiles. The auto-targeting radius limitations are similar to chain.
Keyword | Split | Split projectiles are considered the same projectile after splitting and therefore will not target the same target twice.
Keyword | Pierce | The projectile pierces , passing through the enemy after hitting it and continues along its previous trajectory. Once a projectile has exhausted its pierce count, one of the other effects listed in this section may apply.
Keyword | Fork | The projectile forks , breaking off into two identical projectiles which each travel at a 60-degree angle from the projectile's original path.
Keyword | Chain | The projectile chains , choosing a target within a certain radius, and travelling in the direction of that target. A target cannot be hit twice by the same projectile. If a skill produces multiple projectiles at once and chains, none of the projectiles may chain to an enemy which has already been struck by a projectile from the same attack or cast. If there are no valid targets in range of the original enemy, it will target an enemy but not hit, instead passing through.
Keyword | Return | The projectile returns , changing direction and moving in the direction of its point of origin. Targets can be hit once on the way out and once on the way back; however, the specific target they return from is only hit once.
Keyword | Proxies | Proxy is a term that refers to entities created by a character that may inherit certain skills from its character and offensive modifiers affecting its character while still remaining distinct from the character. Totems , traps , mines , and mirages are examples of proxies. Minions are not proxies. Character-specific defensive modifiers, like +# to Maximum Life , character-related modifiers like #% increased Movement Speed , and effects that specify "you" like Winterweave 's The effect of Chill on you is reversed will not apply to proxies. Only damagable proxies may apply Taunted.
Keyword | Proxies | Examples of proxies include totems , traps , mines , and mirages. Minions are not considered proxies.
Keyword | Totem | Totems are a type of immobile proxy created by skills that create a monolith-shaped entity that uses the character's skills. They may also appear as a monster type. Totems will continue to use its skill for as long as it is active, pursuant to modifiers to cast speed , attack speed , and action speed where appropriate.
Keyword | Totem | Player-created totems are targetable, damageable, and only last for a certain duration. Skills used by totems inherit the player's offensive stats.
Keyword | Traps | Traps are a type of immobile proxy created by skills that throw proximity-triggered devices on the ground that, when activated, produce various, generally damage-dealing, effects. After releasing its effect once, the trap will disappear.
Keyword | Traps | Traps are targetable, damageable, and will expire after a certain duration if not triggered.
Keyword | Mines | Mines are a type of immobile proxy created by skills that throw devices on the ground that, when remotely detonated, produce various, generally damage-dealing, effects. Undetonated mines will reserve life or mana until detonated with a skill like Detonate Mines. After releasing its effect once, the trap will disappear.
Keyword | Mines | Mines are targetable, damageable, and will expire after a certain duration if not triggered.
Keyword | Reservation | Reservation is a mechanic that involves the use of resources like life or mana to pay for an ongoing effect. Rather than paying the cost upfront as with other skills, a percentage of said resource is set aside as unusable for as long as the effect is active.
Keyword | Reservation Efficiency | Reservation Efficiency modifies the percentage of resources reserved by reservation effects. It can be modified with #% [increased/reduced] [resource] Reservation Efficiency.
Keyword | Resources | Resources is a term under which life and mana are categorized. [a]
Keyword | Life | Life is a core mechanic of Path of Exile - all monsters and characters have life. A character's life's is shown in the bottom left-hand corner of the UI, as a red globe filled proportionally to the character's remaining life. When their life reaches 0, characters and monsters die. Life is fully restored upon entering a town. Light radius is based on current life.
Keyword | Life | Characters and monsters are considered to be on low life while their current life is equal to 50% of their maximum life or lower.
Keyword | Life | Low mana is a condition that applies when the character's mana falls below 50% of their maximum mana. However, it does not apply in conjunction with Blood Magic.
Keyword | Life | Characters and monsters are considered to be on full life while their current life is equal to 100% of their maximum life.
Keyword | Mana | Mana is a core mechanic of Path of Exile - all monsters and characters have mana. Mana is normally used as a cost for skills and reservation effects.
Keyword | Recently | Recently is a keyword [1] that defines the period of the past 4 seconds.
Keyword | Rarity | Rarity categorizes all monsters , Vaal Side Areas , strongboxes , and most items. They may be normal , magic , rare , or unique. Normal, magic, and rare items of the same basetype are defined by the number of explicit modifiers they can roll from a shared modpool, while unique variants of that basetype appear with set modifiers unique to that variant.
Keyword | Normal | Normal items are items that have no explicit modifiers. Normal items are identified by their white item box.
Keyword | Magic | Magic items are items that can roll a maximum of one prefix and one suffix. Magic items are identified by their blue item box.
Keyword | Rare | Rare items are items that can roll a maximum of three prefixes and three suffixes, with the exception of rare jewels , which can only roll two prefixes and two suffixes. Rare items are identified by their yellow item box.
Keyword | Unique | Unique items are items that cannot roll modifiers from the shared modpool from their basetype, and instead are generated with a special set of modifiers specific to that unique variant. Unique items are identified by their orange/brown item box.
Keyword | Reflect | Reflect causes sources of damage or status effect to be applied back to the entity that applied it. The damage source of reflected damage will match the source of damage (Ex. reflected attack damage is also considered an attack). Sources of damage reflection that scales with the damage value of the source are calculated based on damage taken after mitigation.
Keyword | Hex Reflection | Hex Reflection causes hexes inflicted upon the hexed to be reflected back to the hexer.
Keyword | Recovery | Recovery refers to any mechanic that involves the gaining of life , energy shield , or mana , including leech , regeneration , and recoup. Some forms of recovery, like Flesh and Spirit 's Recover 20% of Life on Rampage do not fall into any of these categories and are classified as generic recovery.
Keyword | Energy Shield Recharge | Energy Shield recharge triggers when a character or monster with missing energy shield hasn't taken damage in the 2 seconds. Their energy shield will begin recovering at a rate of 33.3% per second, until either they take damage or energy shield is filled, upon which the recharge will stop and the 2 second timer will begin.
Keyword | Energy Shield Recharge | Modifiers to the start of energy shield recharge like #% faster start of Energy Shield Recharge will modify the 2 second delay that occurs before recharge begins.
Keyword | Energy Shield Recharge | The rate at which energy shield recovers can be modified by modifiers like #% [increased/reduced/more/less] Energy Shield Recharge Rate.
Keyword | Leech | Leech is a form of recovery that restores an amount of life , mana , or energy shield over time, relative to the damage inflicted on an enemy. Leech is based on the damage taken by the enemy, not the amount of life removed. Unless otherwise specified below, "life" is interchangeable for "mana" and "energy shield".
Keyword | Leech | Maximum Recovery per Leech
Keyword | Leech | Total Recovery per second from Leech
Keyword | Leech | Maximum total Recovery per second from Leech
Keyword | Leech | When the resource that leech is recovering is filled, those leech instances will be removed and you are no longer considered leeching. Modifiers like Life Leech effects are not removed when Unreserved Life is Filled , commonly known as "Overleech", will cause those instances to continue to attempt to recover life even if there is no more life to recover.
Keyword | Leech | #% of Leech is Instant allows the a percentage of the recovery from leech to be applied instantly, instead of over time. For this reason, instant leech is not modified by modifiers like #% increased Life Recovery Rate , as there is no "Rate" to modify.
Keyword | Regeneration | Regeneration is a form of recovery that restores an amount of life , mana , or energy shield over time. Rage may also be regenerated, but is not recovery. Regenerate #% of [life/mana/energy shield] per second will grant flat regeneration. Regeneration is calculate per minute, not per second.
Keyword | Regeneration | #% [increased/reduced] [life/mana/energy shield] Regeneration Rate directly modifies the rate at which regeneration occurs.
Keyword | Recoup | Recoup is a form of recovery that replaces #% of Damage taken gained as [life/mana/energy shield over 4 seconds when Hit with Recoup #% of Damage taken as [life/mana/energy shield]. While recoup effects usually occur over a period of 4 seconds, modifiers like the Life Recoup Effects instead occur over 3 seconds from the relevant Recovery Mastery and Nine Lives may modify this duration.
Keyword | Resistance | Resistances reduce the amount of incoming damage by their value. Defeating Kitava in both Act 5 and Act 10 incurs -30% penalties to all resistances, adding up to -60%. " Elemental Resistances " refer to cold, fire, and lightning resistances.
Keyword | Resistance | Negative resistances are hard capped at -200%. The effects of x% reduced Resistance(s) is capped at 100%. There are four types of resistances:
Keyword | Maximum resistances | All characters have the following modifiers:
Keyword | Maximum resistances | Maximum resistances can be increased or reduced to hard caps of 90% and -200% respectively.
Keyword | Penetration | Penetration may apply to resistances. When a hit penetrates a percentage of the defender's resistance, the taken damage is calculated with that percentage subtracted from the appropriate resistance.
Kill | Description | Kill is a keyword that refers to causing death of an enemy. Killing blow is a keyword that refers to kills from hits.
Kill | Mechanics | Kills on a specific character can be checked using the /kills command. Kills are tracked up to approximately 16 million, after which it states, "You have killed an uncountable number of monsters." [1]
Kill | Awarding credit for kills | When a target is killed, the kill is credited to the entity that dealt the killing blow, or if the target died to damage over time , to the entity that inflicted the target's oldest damaging debuff. [2]
Kill | Awarding credit for kills | Kills by minions or proxies are normally credited to the minion or proxy, and will not trigger the player's on-kill effects, though exceptions exist:
Kill | Corpses | Most enemies leave corpses on death. Totems , shattered enemies, and enemies that are destroyed (e.g. Pyre , Kitava's Feast ) don't leave corpses.
Kill | Corpses | Corpses can be utilized in several ways, for example:
Kill | Corpses | Corpses can be targeted by holding the A key by default, but only if the player has a skill that can target corpses.

Knockback | Description | Knockback is an on- hit effect that slightly pushes targets away from the attacker. Unlike a stun , a knockback does not interrupt the target's actions. [1]
Knockback | Mechanics | Knockback has a minimum knockback distance of 0.4 metres. Knockback occurs at a rate of 3.75 metres/second [2]. The movement from knockback is not affected by action speed or movement speed modifiers.
Knockback | Mechanics | Knockback direction is skill dependent but is generally away from the thing (not necessarily the player) doing the hit. Projectiles knockback targets in the direction the projectile is travelling meaning returning projectiles could knockback enemies back towards the attacker on the way back. However, some area projectile based skills like Ball Lightning / Rolling Magma knockback enemies away from the centre of the projectile as they travel. [3]
Knockback | Mechanics | Being knocked back counts as moving, and the target will suffer the increased damage over time from bleed while being knocked back.

Knockback | Related quality stats | There are no skill gems that have stats from quality related to knockback.

Knockback | Related quality stats | The following support gems have stats from quality related to knockback :
