League mechanics | Description | League Mechanics are a set of challenge league features which were reworked and permanently added to the game after their respective league finished. Each represent a powerful way to obtain crafting material, item drops, or augment items. They are named after the league in which they first appeared and are sometimes referenced by that name in game.
League mechanics | Description | Most are considered Extra Content and their chance to be encountered in maps can be positively modified. Many can be modified or eliminated entirely with Atlas tree passives.
League mechanics | Abyss | Abysses are interactable objects which spawns cracks and pits that spawn monsters. The Abyss cracks trail randomly along the area, and on the final pit it spawns an Abyssal Trove, containing rewards. Occasionally, they may instead spawn a Stygian Spire or an entrance to the Abyssal Depths , which contains a boss. Abysses can close up if the player takes too long to kill the monsters. Abysses are marked on the minimap with a green icon.
League mechanics | Affliction (The Viridian Wildwood) | A high-level area may spawn a portal at the start that leads to the Viridian Wildwood , a forest covered in perpetual darkness. Sacred Wisps will uncover the darkness as you move, but you can only uncover a limited amount of darkness before you must return. You can collect three types of Wisps that are dispersed into the main zone once you leave the Wildwood, empowering random enemies by increasing their power and item drops. You may also find various random encounters inside the Wildwood.
League mechanics | Affliction (The Viridian Wildwood) | In Affliction league , the Wildwood could contain an Azmeri Wanderer NPC that grants access to a Wildwood ascendancy class , granting access to unique abilities.
League mechanics | Ambush (Strongboxes) | Strongboxes are a special type of loot container. When opened, a strongbox will release groups of monsters to surround and attack the character. Strongboxes come with affixes that affect its drops and hazards and can be modified with currency items.
League mechanics | Anarchy (Rogue Exiles) | Rogue Exiles are unique monsters with player skins and use players skills. On death, exiles drop a large amount of items, including one for each equipment slot.
League mechanics | Bestiary (The Menagerie) | Beasts are marked on the minimap with a yellow icon or red icon and can be hunted with Einhar Frey. Captured beasts can be used for beastcrafting in The Menagerie for crafting effects.
League mechanics | Bestiary (The Menagerie) | In Bestiary league , the player would have to capture the beasts by themselves using nets.
League mechanics | Betrayal (Immortal Syndicate) | The Immortal Syndicate can appear and has three encounters per area. Syndicate members are marked on the minimap and may be guarding a transport , fortification or research. They may also appear out of portals and attempt to assassinate the player.
League mechanics | Betrayal (Immortal Syndicate) | Defeating the syndicate members will provide intelligence in the investigation which is coordinated with Jun Ortoi. Once intelligence in a faction reaches 100%, the player can raid their safehouse for significant rewards based on the leader and rank of the safehouse members. At high levels, safehouse leaders can drop a map fragment used to challenge the Syndicate Mastermind.
League mechanics | Beyond | When an area has a Beyond encounter enabled, enemies have a chance to spawn a small red orb on death. If there are enough other red orbs around each other, they will spawn a pack of hostile Beyond demons. Occasionally, a Beyond boss may spawn instead. Once a Beyond boss spawns, no more Beyond monsters can be spawned in that area.
League mechanics | Blight | Blights are tower defence-like encounters that can spawn from Fungal Growths in any map area, which will always be accompanied by Sister Cassia. The player must defend the pump while building towers until all monsters are slain.
League mechanics | Blight | Blight encounters are also found in Blighted maps and Blight-ravaged maps that have all the monsters removed, save for a single special Blight encounter.
League mechanics | Breach | Breaches come in two forms: Unstable Breaches and Breach Hives.
League mechanics | Breach | Unstable Breaches appear as grasping hands when approached create an expanding circle that summons Hiveborn monsters. Unstable Breaches collapse after a given time, which can be extended by killing Breach monsters. If enough Breach monsters have been slain, the Breach become stabilized, summoning more Breach monsters.
League mechanics | Breach | Breach Hives are surrounded by organic walls and flaming burrows that destroy nearby walls when touched. Reach the core to summon Ailith , and the player must defend her against waves of enemies while she prepares to destroy the Hive. Endgame Breaches may contain an entrance to a Hive Fortress that contains an extended defence mission.
League mechanics | Breach | When a Breach encounter is complete, the player gains Hiveblood that can be spent on the Genesis Tree to open a Wombgift and collect its rewards, which include Foulborn currency and Foulborn unique items.
League mechanics | Delirium | A Mirror of Delirium is a glittering black gateway which spawn within a close distance from the zone entrance. Once a player passes through it, it spawns a gray fogs that spreads outwards throughout the map, beginning the Delirium encounter.
League mechanics | Delirium | Delirium is a zone-wide effect that spawns new enemies and empowers existing ones, and increases in intensity as you venture further out. As the player kill enemies inside the mist, a reward bar on the bottom left will start filling up. The fog dissipates outwards over time, and the Delirium encounter ends if you're outside of the fog long enough or when ended early.
League mechanics | Delirium | Delirium orbs can be used to add a permanent Delirium effect to a map.
League mechanics | Delve (Azurite Mine) | Voltaxic Sulphite appears on the minimap as a golden yellow mineral and can be mined with Niko, Master of the Depths. It provides fuel to explore the Azurite Mine which is one of the Endgame activities.
League mechanics | Domination (Shrines) | Shrines can appear randomly in most areas, granting significant bonuses to nearby monsters or casts spells at nearby players, and are often guarded by monsters. Players can activate the shrine to temporarily gain its bonuses.
League mechanics | Essence | An essence can be obtained by killing monsters trapped in essence crystals. Activating the centre essence crystal three times will break the crystals, freeing the trapped monsters. Essences are used for crafting.
League mechanics | Expedition | The player will encounter one of the four Expedition NPCs. The player can place explosives in the area to unearth monsters and chests. Explosions can be used to unearth Remanants which add a difficulty modifier and rewards to any subsequent monsters or items unearthed.
League mechanics | Expedition | An Expedition logbook can drop and be taken to Dannig , who can open portals to larger Expedition areas with more remnants, flags and placeable explosives.
League mechanics | Harvest | A portal leading to the The Sacred Grove may spawn in areas. There, you can find multiple patches of plants connected to each other in pairs. You can activate one of these patches to begin harvesting it by defeating the monsters that spawn from it. These monsters drop Lifeforce , which are used for various Harvest crafting options via the Horticrafting Station.
League mechanics | Harvest | In Harvest league , the player is in charge of growing the plants by planting seeds within the Sacred Grove then slaying the monsters that emerge from them after they grow over time and placing machinery to store and dispense Lifeforce to grow higher tier plants.
League mechanics | Heist (The Rogue Harbour) | A Smuggler's Cache is a type of loot container that contain contracts , Rogue's Markers , and a quest contract. These can be used in The Rogue Harbour which is one of the endgame activities.
League mechanics | Incursion (Temple of Atzoatl) | A Temporal incursion is a short-duration visit to a temple room. Defeating one of two Vaal Architect in the incursion or using a Stone of Passage will customize and upgrade The Temple of Atzoatl. After all incursions are finished, a map of the Temple may be opened.
League mechanics | Legion | Legions are ancient armies frozen in the midst of battle. They can be encountered by touching a Timeless Monolith , which spawns the Legions and gives the player a window of time in which they can be "killed". Once the timer ends, "killed" mobs are broken out and can fought for rewards.
League mechanics | Legion | Emblems obtained from the monolith encounters can be used in the map device to open a special Legion encounter, which rewards Timeless jewels.
League mechanics | Rampage | Rampage is a "kill-streak" mechanic that grants bonuses as you continue killing enemies within a short period of time.
League mechanics | Rampage | Rampage can only be accessed via certain unique items and modifiers.
League mechanics | Ritual | Multiple Ritual altars can spawn in areas. Once the enemies around the altar are slain, interacting with a Ritual altar begins a Ritual encounter. The altar traps the player within its area and spawns enemies killed near the altar until all enemies are slain. Each subsequent Ritual encounter in the same area will spawn all the monsters that were spawned by previous altars.
League mechanics | Ritual | Each enemy slain during a Ritual encounter grants Favour. Favour is used to purchase items offered by the Ritual altars and does not carry over outside the zone. Items can also be deferred instead, paying a part of its cost to have it reappear in future Ritual encounters.
League mechanics | Sanctum | Forbidden Tomes have a chance to drop randomly in areas. You can use them to enter the Forbidden Sanctum , a roguelike-inspired dungeon where you must travel deep into the Sanctum while avoiding enemies and traps that damage your Resolve. The players can acquire boons and afflictions along the way that make the run easier or harder, as well as collect Relics that can be slotted to give yourself a bonus for future Sanctum runs. It is one of Path of Exile's endgame activities.
League mechanics | Sanctum | In the Forbidden Sanctum, you can acquire currency items immediately, at the end of the floor, or at the end of the dungeon. Certain unique Relics allow you to gain exclusive unique items by completing a Sanctum run with it.
League mechanics | Sentinel | Sentinels are constructs that when deployed empower enemies in exchange for increasing their item drops. A sentinel has a chance to spawn at the beginning of high-tier maps.
League mechanics | Sentinel | In Sentinel league , Sentinels could be equipped and deployed by the player and enhanced using the Sentinel Controller skill tree, but each Sentinel could only be used a limited number of times. New Sentinels could be crafted using the Power Core by combining two Sentinels.
League mechanics | Settlers (Kingsmarch) | Upon reaching the endgame, players can visit the town of Kingsmarch. There, you can spend Gold to hire workers and assign them to passively farm crops, mine or smelt ores, or disenchant items for Thaumaturgic Dust. These items can be sent out as shipments to other regions in exchange for rewards. All Kingsmarch worker activities are done in real time as long as there is enough gold in the Treasury to pay their wages. The speed of each task and the chance of a shipment returning with reduced rewards depends on worker levels.
League mechanics | Settlers (Kingsmarch) | Ore deposits spawn in zones. Clicking an ore deposit will begin an encounter, and once the encounter is complete, the ores will be sent to Kingsmarch for processing.
League mechanics | Settlers (Kingsmarch) | Shipments can provide tattoos and runegrafts as rewards, depending on the port the shipment was sent to. The Recombinator crafting bench costs gold and Thaumaturgic Dust to use. You can also hire Atlas Runners to run your maps using the Kalguuran Map Device.
League mechanics | Tempest | Areas containing Tempests will randomly spawn coloured circles of winds that empower or hinder both allies and enemies inside its radius after a delay. Enemies empowered by a Tempest often drop more items.
League mechanics | Tempest | Currently, Tempests cannot be encountered normally, but can be made to spawn through various means, such as Scarab of Radiant Storms or in The Temple of Atzoatl when the temple has the room Tempest Generator or its upgraded variants.
League mechanics | Tempest | In Tempest league , zones would contain a random Tempest. Act zones would cycle between Tempests in real time. A larger variety of Tempests were also available.
League mechanics | Torment (Tormented Spirits) | A Tormented Spirit is a green spirit which flee when encountered and imbue any normal or magic monsters with dangerous powers or possess a rare or unique monsters to empower it. Monsters touched or possessed by a Tormented Spirit have improved item drops.
League mechanics | Ultimatum | The Trialmaster can appear to offer an Ultimatum encounter. To begin, you must choose a difficulty modifier to add to the encounter. You must them complete up to 10 waves (by default) of the objective without leaving the zone, failing the objective, or dying. For each wave you complete, you earn a reward. You may either end the encounter and take all your earned rewards, or continue to the next wave by adding another modifier. If you fail the encounter, all earned rewards will be lost.
League mechanics | Ultimatum | Ultimatum encounters may reward an Inscribed Ultimatum that opens up an arena where you wager its requisite item to gain a reward if you can complete an extra-long Ultimatum wave.
League mechanics | Warbands | Warbands are four factions of special monsters. Warbands can drop exclusive unique items or magic items with an exclusive modifier.
League mechanics | Warbands | Currently, Warbands can only be found in certain maps as map bosses, or in specific nodes in the Azurite Mine. There are no Atlas passive skill directly associated with Warbands.
League mechanics | Warbands | In Warbands league , random packs of a certain Warband could occupy various zones. Act zones would cycle between Warbands in real time.
League mechanics | Archnemesis | In Archnemesis league , players can customise a Rare monster's mods by applying Archnemesis modifiers to petrified monsters, found throughout every area. Each Archnemesis modifier applied to a monster carries over to subsequent petrified monsters in the area.
League mechanics | Archnemesis | The mechanic was not added to the core game after Archnemesis league, but the new monster modifiers replaced old systems and were reworked several times after.
League mechanics | Bloodlines | Bloodlines is a special type of monster modifier that can appear on Magic monsters.
League mechanics | Bloodlines | In Version 3.18.0 , many Bloodlines modifiers were removed or merged into Archnemesis modifiers. Archnemesis modifiers were replaced with a simpler modifier system in Version 3.20.0.
League mechanics | Breach (Breach league) | Breaches are timed monster-spawning portals identified by a red hand-like construct within a purple circle. Walking into the hand will activate the breach, expending its area gradually then collapsing after a certain period of time. Breach monsters drop splinters used to form a Breachstone , which opens up an area containing one large Breach that leads to a boss.
League mechanics | Breach (Breach league) | This form of Breach was replaced with the Breach from Keepers league in Version 3.28.0.
League mechanics | Crucible | The Crucible Forge allows players to unlock and level up Crucible passive trees on weapon and shields. Experience towards the Crucible passive tree is gained by killing Crucible monsters. The Forge of the Titans contains a forge that lets you sacrifice an item to combine its Crucible tree with another.
League mechanics | Crucible | The mechanic was not added to the core game after Crucible league.
League mechanics | Harbinger | A Harbinger is a blue glowing monster named with strange runes. They can only be harmed by killing their minions and mainly drop currency shards.
League mechanics | Harbinger | Harbingers were removed from the game in Version 3.28.0.
League mechanics | Invasion | Invasion Bosses are unique monsters that can appear in zones and "invade" it.
League mechanics | Invasion | Invasion bosses were phased out of the game over time. It was last offered as a map device crafting option in Version 3.3.0. Additionally, many Vaal side area bosses are based on Invasion bosses.
League mechanics | Kalandra (Lake of Kalandra) | Interacting with a Mirrored Tablet displays a map represented by grids. The player is given a choice to modify or add a tile to the tablet. Once all empty grids on the tablet have been filled, you can enter the Lake of Kalandra to loot it for rewards, with loot scaling as you move further away from the entrance.
League mechanics | Kalandra (Lake of Kalandra) | The Lake of Kalandra can contain a Reflecting Mist. The Reflection gives you a choice between two Mirrored rings or amulets to take, which have multiplied positive or negative values. The modifier values inverted on their counterparts. Rarely, you can be given the option to reflect your own ring/amulet to create two items with the same effect.
League mechanics | Kalandra (Lake of Kalandra) | The Lake of Kalandra was not added to the core game, but in Version 3.25.0 , tier 16+ map monster packs can occasionally spawn a Reflecting Mist, with a chance to drop an itemised version of itself.
League mechanics | Legacy (Leaguestones) | Leaguestones can be slotted to add one of 17 previous league mechanic to the next zone you enter a limited number of times, up to three at a time.
League mechanics | Legacy (Leaguestones) | Leaguestones were only available during Legacy league.
League mechanics | Mercenaries | Players can encounter a Trarthan Mercenary in areas. There are three options available for each mercenary: hire them for a gold fee, take one of their items, or exile them and temporarily prevent mercenaries of the same attribute alignment from appearing. All three options require the player to defeat them in a duel. Defeating a mercenary raises Renown, and dying to a mercenary or choosing to not fight them lowers it. Higher Renown results in more difficult but more rewarding mercenaries are and increases the chance of an Infamous Mercenary from spawning.
League mechanics | Mercenaries | Players can have a hired mercenary accompany them. These mercenaries act like allied party members who assist in combat and can be equipped with your own items. If a mercenary dies, they will not lose their items, but you will need to pay a gold fee to revive them.
League mechanics | Mercenaries | Mercenaries can sometimes hold Trarthan gems , which the player can take as a reward. Infamous Mercenaries can also have exclusive unique items or an equipment with an exclusive Infamous modifier on them.
League mechanics | Mercenaries | Mercenaries did not go in to the core game after Version 3.26.0. Trarthan gems are now obtainable from Gem reward chests in Heists.
League mechanics | Necropolis | The Lantern of Arimor allows players to preview monsters that are present in an upcoming zone, as well as random modifiers attached to them. Players can choose what monsters will be affected by the modifiers by swapping them around or use an Ember of the Allflame to transform them into a different monster. Monsters can drop corpses that are used for crafting in the Necropolis.
League mechanics | Necropolis | The mechanic was not added to the core game after Necropolis league.
League mechanics | Nemesis | Nemesis is a special type of monster modifier that can appear on Rare monsters.
League mechanics | Nemesis | In Version 3.18.0 , many Nemesis modifiers were removed or merged into Archnemesis modifiers. Archnemesis modifiers were replaced with a simpler modifier system in Version 3.20.0.
League mechanics | Metamorph | Monster organ sample may drop from monsters marked on the mini-map with a circular green icon. These can be combined to create a powerful Metamorph boss monster. A sufficiently powered Metamorph can drop itemised organ samples that can be taken to Tane's Laboratory to create an even more powerful Metamorph.
League mechanics | Metamorph | Metamorph was removed from the game in Version 3.23.0.
League mechanics | Perandus | Perandus chests are guarded by monsters and magical effects that can only opened after enough of its guardians have been slain. They contain Perandus Coins that can be traded to Cadiro Perandus , who will offer a random unique items for coins.
League mechanics | Perandus | Perandus chests did not spawn normally, but could be made to spawn with a map device craft or Perandus Scarabs.
League mechanics | Perandus | Perandus mechanics were removed from the game in Version 3.16.0.
League mechanics | Prophecy | A Silver Coin can be used to receive a Prophecy from Navali. Each Prophecy will triggers its effect when you fulfill the condition it meets. Some Prophecies let you upgrade a unique items into a Fated item.
League mechanics | Prophecy | Prophecies were removed from the game in Version 3.17.0.
League mechanics | Scourge | In Scourge league , players receive the Blood Crucible , which is filled with the blood of slain monsters. The device can be activated to transports the character into a parallel reality. This version of Wraeclast is inhabited by demons known as The Scourge. When the Blood Crucible's blood runs out, or if the player chooses to go back, the character is instantly shifted back to normal reality.
League mechanics | Scourge | Equipment can be placed into the Blood Crucible. After killing enough Scourge Demons, the item can be transformed (Scourged). It becomes corrupted and gains two Scourge modifiers , which are in addition to the regular implicit and explicit mods. The Blood Crucible could be upgraded to improve Scourge outcomes.
League mechanics | Scourge | Blood Crucible mechanics were not added to the core game after Scourge league, but Scourge monsters replaced old Beyond demons later.
League mechanics | Synthesis | Synthesis league mechanics included the Memory Nexus and Fragmented Memories. The player must stabilize Memories found in zones as the area slowly fades away to capture it. Captured memories are used to create paths in the Memory Nexus that you can enter and loot for rewards, increasing as you chain more memories together. The Synthesiser can be used to combine three fractured items into a synthesised item with implicits based on the components' modifiers.
League mechanics | Synthesis | The mechanic was not added to the core game after Synthesis league, but synthesised and fractured items can be found or crafted from other various mechanics, and unique Synthesis maps containing bosses from Synthesis league can be found in the endgame.
League mechanics | Talisman | In Talisman league , a monster can be claimed a Talisman , causing it to be empowered with various abilities. The monster will drop the Talisman on death, but other monsters can claim it before you can. The Stone Circle can be used to sacrifice five of the same tier talismans to summon a monster holding a talisman of a higher tier. If five tier 3 talismans were sacrificed, it opens a portal to a boss fight against Rigwald, the Wolven King.
League mechanics | Talisman | These mechanics were not added to the core game (though the Delve node Ritual Grounds contains monsters empowered by Talismans), but Talismans could be acquired from various mechanics. Unique talismans are part of the core drop pool.
League mechanics | Trial of the Ancestors | The Trial of the Ancestors is a tournament against fallen Karui chieftains and their tribes in the afterlife. The players is tasked to assemble a team of warriors, gear them with equipment or field items, then lead them to victory by destroying the enemy team's totems and earn rewards with each victory.
League mechanics | Trial of the Ancestors | The mechanic was not added to the core game after Ancestor league.
Leech | Description | Leech recovers an amount of life , mana , or energy shield over time, relative to the damage inflicted on an enemy. Leech is based on the damage taken by the enemy, not the amount of life removed. [1] [2]
Leech | Mechanics | All leech mechanics act the same way for life, mana, and energy shield. Examples in this article use life, but if the character has equal statistics for a different resource (mana or energy shield), they will apply in the same way.
Leech | Mechanics | Whenever a character with some source of leech hits a monster, a leech instance is created. Hitting multiple enemies with a single use of a skill creates that many leech instances.
Leech | Mechanics | Life Leech instances have the following properties by default: [4]
Leech | Mechanics | Leech grants recovery to the entity that hits the target. If a minion or totem with leech hits an enemy, leech will grant recovery to that minion or totem, not the character. Skills used by totems and other proxies create leech instances with recovery caps based on the player's maximum life, not their own. [6] While recovery is irrelevant for most proxies because they're immortal, untargetable, or have 1 life, it may be relevant for uniques like Machina Mitts or The Retch.
Leech | Modifiers | Leech can be modified significantly through passives, support gems, and equipment. Modifiers affecting life leech are damage Leeched as Life , Maximum Recovery per Life Leech , total Recovery per second from Life Leech and Maximum total Life Recovery per second from Leech.
Leech | Modifiers | There are a few notable ways to affect leech:
Leech | Leech duration | The duration of a life leech instance is defined by the maximum recovery per life leech, divided by the leech rate of 2% of maximum life per second. By default, the maximum amount of life leeched per instance is 10% of a character's maximum Life, resulting in a maximum duration of 5 seconds.
Leech | Leech duration | No stat currently exists to modify the base rate of a leech instance. The maximum recovery may be modified through Maximum Recovery per Life Leech , which in turn modifies maximum duration. For example, a 100% increase from Brutal Fervour will result in a maximum recovery per life leech of 20%, recovered at a rate of 2% per second for 10 seconds.
Leech | Leech duration | Partial instant leech will reduce the total over time recovery, not the rate. For example, when 10% of leech is instant, and the leech instance recovers 1% instantly and 9% over time, its duration will be 4.5 seconds.
Leech | Leech duration | Modifiers to total Recovery per second from Life Leech amplify recovery from leech, not the base rate of the leech instance. Multiplying recovery does not 'empty' a leech instance faster. [7]
Leech | Leech duration | Additionally all instances of life leech are discarded as soon as the character reaches full unreserved life. This discarding can be prevented by overleech mechanics, for example by "Life Leech effects are not removed when Unreserved Life is Filled" effects like Immortal Ambition or Offering to the Serpent (Synthesised). Petrified Blood also enable overleech as it ignores leech above low life without removing it. The leech duration is not modified by those effects, they just prevent premature end of the leech.
Leech | Leech duration | Examples: 1. A character with none of the leech modifiers changed has 1.000 maximum life, with 1% of damage leeched, and hits 1 enemy 1 time for 4.000 damage. The leech is 40. It leeches 20 life per second for 2 seconds leeching a total of 40 life. 2. A character with none of the leech modifiers changed has 1.000 maximum life, with 1% of damage leeched, and hits 1 enemy 1 time for 40.000 damage. The leech is 400, reduced to the maximum of 100 total per life leech (instance). The character recovers 20 life per second for 5 seconds leeching a total of 100 life. 3. A character with none of the leech modifiers changed has 1.000 maximum life, with 1% of damage leeched, and hits 5 enemies 5 times each for 40.000 damage. The leech of each instance is 400, reduced to the maximum of 100 total per life leech (instance), with 25 leech instances. The character wants to recovers 2500 life per second, but is limited to 200 life per second from the Maximum Total Life Recovery Per Second from Leech. Each instance has a duration of 5 seconds, because it reached the Maximum Recovery per Life Leech. Each individual leech instance ends 5 seconds after the initial hit. The total recovered health depends on the time spread of the hits, due to all maximums being reached.
Leech | Combined Recovery Rate | The total life leech recovery rate is the sum of all recovery rates from all life leech instances.
Leech | Combined Recovery Rate | This combined rate is subject to the total leech rate cap, which is by default 20% of the character's maximum health.
Leech | Combined Recovery Rate | Reaching this maximum rate requires a number of leech instances equal the total maximum rate cap divided by the leech rate of each instance.
Leech | Combined Recovery Rate | For a default character, this is 10 instances, provided that each hit deals enough damage to reach the maximum amount that can be leeched per instance.
Leech | Instant leech | Effects that cause some or all of leech to be instant will still be capped by maximum recovery per leech. For partial instant leech, the duration of non-instant leech will be equal relative to its remain duration after instant leech.
Leech | Instant leech | For example, using life leech with the 10% of Leech is Instant mod and no other modifiers to maximum leech, a single hit that leeches life for the maximum amount will recover 1% of your life instantly and the remaining 9% over 90% of the leech duration (4.5 seconds by default).
Leech | Instant leech | Instant leech is not affected by modifiers to (leech) recovery rate, since its rate is instant.
Leech | Types of leech | Several types of leech apply exclusively to certain skill types. Some leech types only work for attacks , others only works with elemental damage or all sources of physical damage. Any such specializations are defined in the modifier.
Leech | Types of leech | Generally the leech modifiers follow this template:
Leech | Types of leech | #% of X Y Damage Z Leeched as Life/Mana
Leech | Types of leech | Where X can be:
Leech | Types of leech | Y can be:
Leech | Types of leech | and Z can be:
Leech | Types of leech | Note that if X , Y or Z are not specified it means that it applies to all those types.

Legion | Description | Legions are ancient armies frozen in the midst of battle. They can be encountered by touching a Timeless Monolith , which breaks out the Legions and gives the player a window of time to defeat them. This encounter is considered Extra Content and has a baseline 8% chance to appear in any non-unique map area.
Legion | Overview | Players can find a Legion by interacting with a Timeless Monolith. Monoliths have a base greater than 8% chance to spawn in a map.
Legion | Overview | Monoliths can also be found via other sources:
Legion | Overview | Interacting with the Monolith will reveal a battle between two Legion factions that are in stasis. A timer will start once the Monolith is activated. During this phase, the enemies can be "killed", breaking them out of stasis and allowing them to be fought when the timer ends for rewards. The timer can range from 14 to 20 seconds (or more with Atlas passives), with a longer timer in lower-level zones. Once the timer runs out, all the enemies that were broken out of stasis will remain and start attacking. Enemies that didn't get broken out will disappear.
Legion | Overview | Schism : Alternatively, taking the Timeless Conflict keystone will disable the Legion timer. Instead, breaking out monsters and chests from stasis will contribute progress towards a Schism, as shown by a progress bar. Once the progress bar is full, the Schism will occur and the Legion encounter will begin. Breaking out monsters and chests with rewards or more powerful monsters will contribute more progress towards the Schism. [1]
Legion | Overview | Some Legion enemies have a symbol above their heads, indicating an additional reward type they will drop. Chests and War Hoards can also spawn, which can be destroyed and opened after the timer runs out. Destroying a Chest or War Hoard will free all nearby enemies without symbols in a radius around it. The general of each Legion can occasionally spawn, always spawning in the far rear of the formation. If a general spawns, the monolith will display a wave of purple on the bottom in the direction of the general.
Legion | Overview | Generally, rarer, more rewarding spawns will spawn further away from the monolith. Therefore, it's advised to move deep into a formation as quickly as possible if you are looking for rare spawns.
Legion | Mechanics | Rarity : Legion Sergeants are rare monsters whereas Legion Generals are unique monsters.
Legion | Items | There are two types of currency associated with monoliths; each are specific to the legion.
Legion | Splinters | Legion enemies and chests can drop Splinters of their Legion. 100 Splinters of the same type can be combined into an Emblem.
Legion | Emblems | Emblems are obtained from combining Splinters. They can be put into a map device in order to open a portal to the Domain of Timeless Conflict. You must use at least two Emblems of different Legions to open a portal to the Domain. A fifth slot for the Map Device can be unlocked by completing a tier 17 map or Maven's Invitation: The Atlas , allowing all 5 Emblems to be used (commonly called a 5 way). Unrelenting Emblems occasionally drop as a reward from the Domain of Timeless Conflict when all five factions are present.
Legion | Emblems | The following unique timeless jewels drop exclusively in the Domain of Timeless Conflict.
Legion | Legions | There are a total of five different legions. The Eternal Empire, Karui, and Vaal are the most common, with the Templar Legion being rarer, and the Maraketh Legion being the rarest.
Life | Description | Life (also called Health or Hit Points) is the health source of a character or monster. For the player it is shown as a red orb in the lower left of the screen and will decrease when receiving damage. Characters die when they reach 0 life and must be resurrected in town or checkpoint. Players can recover life by using flasks , gaining life regeneration from passive skills and equipment, or leeching life from enemies, among other mechanics. Life is fully restored upon entering a town or hideout (except in Ruthless mode , which requires you to interact with certain NPCs). Light radius is based on current life.
Life | Description | Every class starts out with 50 life and has the following stats:
Life | Calculation | Total maximum life can be calculated with the following formula:
Life | Calculation | Life total = ( 38 + Level Character × Life per level + Strength 2 + ∑ i = 1 a added Life ) × ( 1 + ∑ j = 1 b increased Life j − ∑ k = 1 c reduced Life k ) × ∏ l = 1 d ( 1 + more Life l ) × ∏ m = 1 e ( 1 − less Life m ) \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\begin{aligned}{\text{Life}}_{\text{total}}=&\left(38+{\text{Level}}_{\text{Character}}\times {\text{Life per level}}+{\frac {\text{Strength}}{2}}+\sum _{i=1}^{a}{\text{added Life}}\right)\times \\&\left(1+\sum _{j=1}^{b}{\text{increased Life}}_{j}-\sum _{k=1}^{c}{\text{reduced Life}}_{k}\right)\times \\&\prod _{l=1}^{d}(1+{\text{more Life}}_{l})\times \prod _{m=1}^{e}(1-{\text{less Life}}_{m})\end{aligned}}
Life | Calculation | Flat life bonuses are added directly to base life ( +x to maximum Life ). Percent-based modifiers apply to flat life bonuses, as well as base life and life from strength ( +x% increased maximum Life ). See modifiers.
Life | Calculation | More life multipliers like those found on Dissolution of the Flesh or Life Mastery are applied last.
Life | Life cap | The highest possible maximum life value (or life cap) is 2,147,483,647 or 2 31 - 1; this number is typically only reached by monsters through "infinite" scaling mechanics like deep Delve. Ailment threshold can still continue to increase after hitting the life cap.
Life | Life cap | Maximum life cannot be reduced below 1. For example, equipping rings and amulets which have been reflected to have negative life values cannot place the character below a life total of 1.
Life | Life scaling | Certain unique items grant special additional scaling for life based on other attributes:
Life | Mechanics scaled by life | Certain unique items , skills , and ascendancies scale based on maximum life.

Life | Support Gems | Support Gems with effects that scale maximum player life:

Life | Spending life | Like mana and energy shield with Eldritch Battery , life may be spent in the following ways:
Life | Spending life | Strictly speaking, life "spent" must specifically be a cost. It is not the same as sacrificing life (like with Dark Pact ), reserving it, taking self-damage (e.g. Forbidden Rite or Righteous Fire ), or losing life (e.g. The Burden of Shadows ). Notably, as stated above, modifiers to skill costs do not affect these.
Life | Life transforming jewels | These unique jewels transform life from passive skills into another base statistic.
Life | Unique Items | While the +x to maximum Life modifier is quite common on unique items, the x% increased maximum Life modifier is less common and can only appear on unique items. Certain unique items also grant +x to maximum Life in exceptional quantities or on weapons.

Light Level | Description | From observations made there are 3 main light levels.
Light Level | Description | High : No light radius based on Life.
Light Level | Description | Medium : Small discernible change on the edge of your light radius , does not affect visibility much. This can come in different shades.
Light Level | Description | Low : Outlying areas are dark enough that recognizing shapes is possible but difficult
Light radius | Description | Light radius is a stat which affects the maximum radius you can see clearly in low Light Level areas. Your light radius is further reduced by your current percentage of maximum life. This makes it very difficult to see in dark areas when on Low Life. An Energy Shield Mastery and Incandescent Heart changes your light radius to be based off your proportion of Energy Shield instead of life, aiding visibility for low life builds.

Lingering blade | Description | Lingering blades are created by certain skills and can be detonated with Blade Blast or animated with Animate Weapon. Lingering Blades remain on the ground for a duration and can be used by specific skills. If Animated, they count as Daggers, and have the stats equivalent to a Glass Shank.

List of vendor recipes in Ruthless mode | Unique items | The following vendor recipes are used to craft unique items. A vendor recipe is also the only way to obtain most of the unique items on this list, apart from trading with other players.
List of vendor recipes in Ruthless mode | Unique items | A unique item can have its modifiers rerolled by vendoring it along with two more of the same unique item. The result is comparable to using a Divine Orb and a Blessed Orb.
List of vendor recipes in Ruthless mode | Sockets | These recipes require single items with certain patterns of sockets. These can sometimes be found at vendors and can be immediately resold for a profit.
List of vendor recipes in Ruthless mode | Direct Purchases from Vendors | Most orbs are purchasable from vendors, and can thus be ranked like coins in normal currency. There are several progression tables below showing who sells what and what their equivalent value is in measurable orbs. Instead of using the sell window, players must click "Purchase Items" when talking to a vendor. These are not technically recipes, but are included here for convenience.

List of vendor recipes in Ruthless mode | Single Item with Mods | These recipes result from selling a single item when no other recipes are valid. An identified Fractured modifier will vendor for quadruple its default price.
List of vendor recipes in Ruthless mode | Scroll Fragment | This is the "default" recipe. If an item does not have a more powerful recipe, it defaults to producing a Scroll Fragment. 5 Scroll Fragments automatically combine to form a Scroll of Wisdom.
List of vendor recipes in Ruthless mode | Transmutation Shard | Transmutation Shard s come from identified items depending on their affixes. 20 Transmutation Shards automatically combine to form an Orb of Transmutation. Most affixes sell for Transmutation Shards.
List of vendor recipes in Ruthless mode | Alchemy Shard | Certain rarer affixes may yield Alchemy Shard s instead of Transmutation Shards. 20 Alchemy Shards automatically combine to form an Orb of Alchemy.

List of vendor recipes in Ruthless mode | Quality Items | When done for multiple instances of the recipe at once, each individual combination must add up to 40%. For example: 6 items of 19%, 13%, 15%, 9%, 17% and 7% quality would add up to 80%, but would not actually grant 2 of the resulting quality items, only 1. This is because the 2 individual combinations do not add up to 40 each.

Loss | Description | Loss is a catch-all term for negative changes to resources, primarily life , mana , and energy shield. It can be considered the opposite of recovery.
Loss | Mechanics | Loss is fundamentally not limited to specific mechanics. It is not necessarily caused by damage , and damage does not necessarily cause loss (e.g. Ward , Dissolution of the Flesh ).
Loss | Mechanics | Loss from non-damage sources does not hit , cannot be modified by defensive stats, and does not interrupt recharge. [1]
Loss | Mechanics | While certain loss mechanics will always leave players with a minimum of 1 life (e.g. sacrificing, tinctures with Bloodsoaked Blade), loss does not need to originate from damage to kill the player.
Loss | Mechanics | Loss determines whether a hit is savage. [2]
Loss | Mechanics | Over-time loss is tracked partially. It's possible to lose 1 life over a duration. [3]
Loss | Interactions with recovery | Recovery and loss are normally distinct modifications. [4] When the same event causes both loss and recovery, they are not totalled and applied together; they modify your resources individually, in an order appropriate for the effects involved. (Except Gluttony of Elements.) [5] Modifiers that prevent or disable recovery do not affect loss.
Loss | Interactions with recovery | When over-time loss and over-time recovery occur together, loss is always handled second. [6]
Low life | Description | Low life is a condition that applies when life is at 50% or lower. Linking mana-reserving skills (such as auras ) to Arrogance Support which converts them into Life-reserving skills is one of the easiest way to maintain the low life condition.
Low life | Description | Players that use low life will typically either use energy shields to protect their health or Petrified Blood if they're not using energy shields. "LL" is commonly used to describe this type of build, which stands for "Low Life".
Low life | Description | The only way to achieve Low Life while Chaos Inoculation is allocated is with Coward's Legacy , as a maximum life of 1 counts as being on full life.
Low life | Description | The low life state unlocks several interesting aspects for a character, but can be difficult to maintain efficiently.

Low life | Trivia | Since version 0.9.6 , the player light changes to noticeably reddish over the 33% - 37% range [ confirmation needed because of 3.14 change ] to make it easier to judge when the condition applies.
Low Mana | Description | Low Mana is a condition that applies when the player's mana pool falls below 50%. However, it does not apply if the maximum mana is set to 0 due to Blood Magic. [1]
Luck | Description | Luck is a mechanic that rolls an outcome or a number in a range more than once, with Lucky rolls applying the best result of two rolls, Unlucky rolls applying the worst result of two rolls, and Unexciting rolls applying the "middle result" of three rolls.
Luck | Description | Modifiers that specify Damage or when Damaging and luck refer specifically to damage ranges after any increased/more modifiers (or "tooltip damage range"), not to the base damage of the weapon/skill. These stats do not affect other mechanics like chance to hit/ accuracy or critical strike chance. [1] Additionally, these stats only apply to hit damage, and have no effect on the damage roll of damage over time from damaging ailments , which roll entirely independently of the hit damage's roll. [2]
Luck | Description | Lucky and Unlucky modifiers affecting the same stat or mechanic will cancel each other out. [3] Sources of Unexciting modifiers usually cancel out both Lucky and Unlucky modifiers.
Luck | Effectiveness | With percentage rolls, such as critical strike chance , lucky/unlucky rolls will be up to a 100% more/less modifier, changing linearly towards 0% as critical chance increases. As for damage rolls , the average damage from the roll will be at up to 33% more or less, when the minimum damage is close to zero, but will have a much weaker effect when the minimum damage is closer to the maximum.
Luck | Binary Rolls | More specifically, the lucky critical strike chance can be calculated from the following formula:
Luck | Binary Rolls | C r i t C h a n c e L u c k y = 2 × C r i t C h a n c e D e f a u l t − C r i t C h a n c e D e f a u l t 2 \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}CritChance_{Lucky}=2\times CritChance_{Default}-{CritChance_{Default}}^{2}
Luck | Binary Rolls | For example, the lucky critical strike chance for an default critical strike chance of 40% could be calculated as follows:
Luck | Binary Rolls | C r i t C h a n c e L u c k y = 2 × 40 % − 40 % 2 = 64 % \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}CritChance_{Lucky}=2\times 40\%-40\%^{2}=64\%
Luck | Binary Rolls | It should be noted that these calculations neglect the effect of accuracy on critical strikes.
Luck | Damage in a Range | Given an integer roll between min and max , the normal expected value is m i n + m a x 2 \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\frac {min+max}{2}}.
Luck | Damage in a Range | A lucky roll has expected value m i n 3 + 2 ∗ m a x 3 + m a x − m i n 6 ∗ ( 1 + m a x − m i n ) \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\frac {min}{3}}+{\frac {2*max}{3}}+{\frac {max-min}{6*(1+max-min)}}.
Luck | Damage in a Range | Note that the last term in this is always between 0 and 1/6 and therefore is negligible (it is a byproduct of the fact our uniform variable only takes values over the integers.) This simplifies the formula to m i n + 2 ∗ m a x 3 \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\frac {min+2*max}{3}}.
Luck | Damage in a Range | The average damage is effectively nudged closer toward the max damage, and further from the minimum damage. The damage boost, on average, is a sixth of the difference between minimum and maximum damage.
Luck | Damage in a Range | Example 1: You shoot a level 20 Fireball. The maximum damage is 1643, and minimum damage is 1095, for an average of 1369. The difference between minimum and maximum is 548. If the damage is lucky, you get an average 548/6=91.3 extra damage, for a new average damage of 1369+91.3=1460.3 damage. This is a 6.6% damage boost.
Luck | Damage in a Range | Example 2: You cast a level 20 Spark. The maximum damage is 1198, and minimum damage is 63, for an average of 630.5. The difference between minimum and maximum is 1135. If the damage is lucky, you get an average 1135/6=189.2 extra damage, for a new average damage of 189.2+630.5=819.6 damage. This is a 30% damage boost.
Luck | Damage in a Range | How much does lucky improve our expected value - if our minimum damage is 0 then we get a 33% more multiplier. As the minimum damage increases our percentage increase decreases.

Mana | Description | Mana is a resource utilized by player characters. It is most commonly used to pay for cost of most skills. For the player it is shown as a blue orb in the lower right of the screen and will decrease when used. Players can recover mana by using flasks , gaining mana regeneration from passive skills and equipment, or leeching mana from enemies, among other mechanics. Mana is fully restored upon entering a town or hideout (except in Ruthless mode , which requires you to interact with certain NPCs).
Mana | Description | Every class starts with 40 mana and has the following stats:
Mana | Mechanics | Every two points of Intelligence grants +1 mana. [1]
Mana | Mechanics | Blood Magic sets your maximum mana to 0. The when on Low Mana and when on Full Mana modifiers are not triggered with 0/0 mana. [2]
Mana | Calculation | Total maximum mana can be calculated with the following formula:
Mana | Calculation | Mana total = ( 34 + Level Character × Mana per level + Intelligence 2 + ∑ i = 1 a added Mana ) × ( 1 + ∑ j = 1 b increased Mana j − ∑ k = 1 c reduced Mana k ) × ∏ l = 1 d ( 1 + more Mana l ) × ∏ m = 1 e ( 1 − less Mana m ) \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\begin{aligned}{\text{Mana}}_{\text{total}}=&\left(34+{\text{Level}}_{\text{Character}}\times {\text{Mana per level}}+{\frac {\text{Intelligence}}{2}}+\sum _{i=1}^{a}{\text{added Mana}}\right)\times \\&\left(1+\sum _{j=1}^{b}{\text{increased Mana}}_{j}-\sum _{k=1}^{c}{\text{reduced Mana}}_{k}\right)\times \\&\prod _{l=1}^{d}(1+{\text{more Mana}}_{l})\times \prod _{m=1}^{e}(1-{\text{less Mana}}_{m})\end{aligned}}
Mana | Calculation | Flat mana bonuses are added directly to the base mana ( +X to maximum Mana ). Percent-based modifiers apply to flat mana bonuses, as well as base mana and mana from Intelligence ( +X% increased maximum Mana ). See modifiers.
Mana | Mana Scaling | Intelligence grants +1 Mana per 2 Intelligence.

Mana before Life | Description | Mana before Life is a game mechanic that allows mana to be used to take damage, increasing effective health.
Mana before Life | Mechanics | When taking damage , a percentage of damage that would be dealt to the defender's life is deducted from mana instead. If the character has insufficient current mana to fully take the damage to mana, then the remainder of the damage will be taken to life instead. This effect occurs after almost all other forms of avoidance and mitigation.
Mana before Life | Mechanics | Damage taken to energy shield has no interaction with this stat [1]. However, with Eldritch Battery , the damage taken from mana before life will be taken from energy shield first instead. Chaos damage will still bypass energy shield this way.
Mana before Life | Mechanics | Although taking mana before life does increase effective health, it does not cause mana to affect the player's thresholds for ailments or stun. [2]
Mana before Life | Mechanics | Having sufficient mana recovery is required to prevent rapid hits or damage over time from continually draining mana, preventing skill usage.
Mana before Life | Mechanics | This effect is capped at 100%. Having more than 100% of damage taken from Mana before Life will not cause you to lose more Mana than you were to take to Life.
Mana before Life | Mana/Life ratio | For mana to not run out before life , the unreserved mana should be at least 67% of unreserved life, granted that 40% of damage is taken from mana before life. Other ratios can be found using the following formula. Note that this only applies to a single hit and does not take into account other forms of recovery or damage prevention.
Mana before Life | Related legacy modifiers | These modifiers can only be obtained in permanent leagues as a legacy modifier.
Mana before Life | Unique items | The legacy unique That Which Was Taken can also roll with a modifier that grants 3% of Damage is taken from Mana before Life.
Map Device | Infobox | Hideout Item. Creates an object in your hideout. 2 Variations
Map Device | Description | The Map Device is a world object that allows the player to access certain areas by placing items such as maps , map fragments , or other map-related items inside it. The Map Device starts with four slots, and up to two additional slots can be unlocked.
Map Device | Accessing the Map Device | The first interactable Map Device the player encounters is located in The Chamber of Sins Level 1 in Act 7 to use Maligaro's Map quest item to enter Maligaro's Sanctum. This Map Device cannot activate any other map.
Map Device | Accessing the Map Device | In the Epilogue , players will gain access to a fully functional map device in the Karui Shores. After completing the mission A Call to Arms , the player will also receive a personal Map Device decoration which can be placed in your hideout and used instead. This personal Map Device can then be used by any character that has completed Act 10.
Map Device | Mechanics | In order to activate the device, maps , one or more map fragments , and/or miscellaneous map items need to be placed inside the Map Receptacle. Generally, only one item is required, but for certain map fragments the player may be required to arrange the fragments in a certain order (typically as keys to an endgame boss).
Map Device | Mechanics | It is also possible to place other map-related items alongside a map for bonuses:
Map Device | Mechanics | The map device interface also allows players to view and use their accumulated Kirac master missions. It also comes with a collapsible 4x5 mini-inventory or "rucksack" that can store maps, map fragments, and currency items. This inventory is shared with the map device interface for Kirac ( Maven's Invitations ) and Eagon ( memory threads ) to allow for quick crafting.
Map Device | Mechanics | By default, the map device has 4 items slots usable to open and modify areas. Two additional slots can be unlocked for a total of 6 slots. To unlock the additional slots, the player must do the following, in any order:
Map Device | Mechanics | The map device can also add one of several different map crafting options to map areas, including a boost to item quantity up to 8% as you complete maps (the default), guaranteed previous challenge league encounters for the price of a couple Chaos Orb s (also known as Kirac mods, unlocked as your complete maps), or rarely other mechanics such as Monstrous Treasure through the use of certain Atlas passive skills.
Map Device | Mechanics | The player will also unlock various upgrades to the map device as they progress through the endgame, such as enabling Maven , Exarch , or Eater beacons that permit Maven-witnessing a map boss or adding Exarch or Eater influence to your maps, or unlocking additional Atlas Passive Skill Tree presets to quickly switch between up to 3 different Atlas tree layouts.
Map Device | Mechanics | Six portals to a map or endgame area are opened when the Map Device is activated. A portal is consumed each time you enter the area, and the number of portal uses are shared within a party.
Map Device | List of map crafting options | Various map crafting options are unlocked as the player increases their Atlas map bonus completion. These map crafts, like the Atlas passive tree , applies only to your non-unique maps. The first use of each craft (except Fortune Favours the Brave) is free, and additional free uses may be obtained via the Atlas notable Shaping the Mountains.
Map Device | List of map crafting options | The standard map crafting options grant increased item quantity or add a specific league mechanic to the map. The item quantity and available crafting options increase with Atlas completion. Scarabs found in maps with these crafts also have a 50% increased chance to be for that league content.
Map Device | List of map crafting options | Certain map crafting options for mechanics that are limited to 1 in a map (e.g. Expedition) cause an error [1] if attempting to add another source of the encounter (like an Expedition Scarab ), whereas other options like Breach will apply the craft and consume Breach Scarabs.
Map Device | List of map crafting options | Fortune Favours the Brave selects a random map crafting option. Unlike choosing a specific option, Fortune Favours the Brave cannot block an outcome from happening; for example, it is possible to open a map with an Expedition Scarab and randomly roll Expedition, wasting the use of Fortune Favours the Brave. [2]
