Map Device | List of map crafting options | Special map crafting options can be obtained via Shaping the Skies or from It That Fled in a Research safehouse :
Map Device | List of map crafting options | These map crafting options can be obtained by placing a Scarab of Bisection into your map device.
Map Device | List of map crafting options | These map crafting options can be obtained by placing a Horned Scarab of Awakening into your map device.
Map Device | Other map-like items | These items can be used on a Map Device to open an instance to an area. They are classified as Map Fragments by item class.
Map Device | Other map-like items | These fragments require a complete set to open portals to a boss:
Map Device | Other map-like items | Five copies of these fragment can be used to open portals to a zone containing an Uber Pinnacle Boss, provided you have already defeated the regular version of the boss:
Map Device | Other map-like items | These items can be used on a Map Device to open an instance to an area. They are classified as Misc Map Items by item class.
Map Device | Other map-like items | Expedition Logbook s cannot be opened using the map device, and instead must be opened through Dannig.
Map Device | Lore | Players encountered two Map Devices in throughout the Act 1 to 10. The Ancient Reverie Device in The Chamber of Sins Level 1 , which was repaired before Act 7 and allowed the player character to use Maligaro's Map during Act 7. The device cannot be used again afterwards [3]. The player also encountered another nonfunctional map device in the Eternal Laboratory subarea of The Solaris Temple Level 2. That map device (known as the Reverie Device) was made by Malachai , and is canonically a copy of the device in the Chamber of Sins. The Reverie Device was previously functional until version 3.0 in the Merciless difficulty of The Solaris Temple Level 2.
Map Device | Lore | A third device was located in The Templar Laboratory which was made by Valdo Caeserius , though this area is no longer accessible due to the change of endgame timelines. This map device exploded during the epilogue of the Conquerors of the Atlas expansion. The map device in The Templar Laboratory was functional from version 3.0 until 3.9. This map device is also used in Path of Exile Mobile , 20 years before the first game. A fourth device exists inside of The Shaper's Realm.
Map Device | Lore | In previous expansions Conquerors of the Atlas and Echoes of the Atlas (version 3.9 to 3.16), player restored a fifth map device from spare parts in the Vault of Venarius as part of the Picking Up the Pieces quest; it is implied that these were remnants of the map device Venarius used to encounter the Elder. In the same patches, a sixth device can be seen during Sirus boss fight, which is located on the Cathedral Rooftop (in the Atlas of Worlds, not the The Cathedral Rooftop in Oriath ). This map device connects to the one in the Templar Laboratory (now restored), allowing the player to chase down Sirus. The Sirus encounter is not part of the current storyline, and the boss encounter is considered an interactable "memory" that generated by the power of the Atlas.
Map Device | Lore | In the current expansion, Siege of the Atlas , Commander Kirac explains that the Citizen Vanguard has secured at least 3 functional map devices set up in the bunker at the Karui Shores. More decorations similar to the personal Map Device can be seen in the Kirac's Vault subarea of the Karui Shores. Portals from the map device in either Karui Shores or hideout are shared, preventing the ability to open two different map instances at once. It is unknown if the map devices in the Karui Shores are new map devices, or recovered from Wraeclast and Oriath.
Map Device | Lore | When opening a map that contains a Smuggler's Cache as part of Kirac's master mission, he claims that the "criminals" may possess their own map device.
Map Device | Lore | During Synthesis league , the Memory Nexus and boss memory fragments also contained a decoration that resembled a map device (now purchasable as the Synthesis Map Device MTX ). However, due to Synthesis not going core, it is unclear whether these are real map devices or if they still currently exist.
Map Device | Lore | In Settlers league , the player is able to construct Kalguuran Map Devices and hire Atlas Runners to run their maps. They are constructed by Isla , using her experience on map devices she gained 20 years ago , and modified with Kalguuran runes.
Memory thread | Description | Threads of Consciousness , also known as memory threads or simply "threads", are a strange thread-like substance found near tears in reality caused by distorted memories called "memory tears". Eagon Caeserius is able to link to these memory threads to open portals to dreamscapes of Zana 's memories, introduced in the quest Threads of the Originator.
Memory thread | Description | Tears are marked on the map with an icon:
Memory thread | Mechanics | Players can find a bundle of iridescent threads near a memory tear in the first tier 14+ map opened. Interacting with it allows Eagon to extract the location of a Memory Thread in the Atlas of Worlds , creating a gauntlet of typically 3 adjacent maps on the Atlas (starting on the map you found the Memory Thread in) plus an exclusive Tier 16 memory guardian map not normally found on the Atlas ( Courtyard of Wasting Map , Chambers of Impurity Map , Theatre of Lies Map ), containing a memory guardian. Players can interact with Eagon in their hideout to craft these maps; they are also affected by your Atlas tree , scarabs , and other map fragments , and map crafting options from your map device. Eldritch Beacons cannot be activated on these maps during the initial quest. The areas will be opened in sequence each time you interact with Eagon in your hideout if you successfully complete the previous map.
Memory thread | Mechanics | All of the maps in a Memory Thread are considered memory influenced maps. Their random modifiers roll from regular map modifiers as well as Tier 17 map modifiers. Within these maps, monsters may be imbued with Memory Petals, granting them enhancements. Defeating these enemies grants Memory Petals to you which can be spent to activate between one to two random Memory Petal Skills. A third Skill can be granted in areas affected by the Memory Altar modifier +(20-40)% chance for Area to contain an additional Memory Petal Skill. The petals for each ability have individual counters. Petals can also be obtained from moving near clusters of petals scattered around the map.
Memory thread | Mechanics | Additionally, equipment found in these maps may sometimes have Memory Strands that enhance crafting outcomes.
Memory thread | Mechanics | Defeating each map boss in the Thread spawns a Memory Altar, providing two different modifier choices. The picked modifier will be applied to the remaining maps in the Thread, stacking up as you get further in. These effects can range from affecting Memory Petal acquisition, Memory Strands found on items, various map mechanics or map crafting options , or other miscellaneous bonuses.
Memory thread | Post-quest | After completing the Threads of the Originator quest and defeating all three Incarnation pinnacle bosses for the first time, the mechanics of Memory Threads change slightly:
Memory thread | Cursed | If a player fails to complete a memory thread map (either by using up all portals or letting the instance expire, or by manually opening the map again before it is completed), the map can be attempted again; however, it will remove all currently acquired Memory Altar modifiers from this map and subsequent maps, and adds the unremovable enchantment Area is Cursed. This modifier significantly penalizes item drops (IIQ) and player experience , and restricts certain content from appearing. It also significantly reduces the number of memory petals obtained and prevents Exarch or Eater influence monsters and altars from appearing. However, it can be useful as an infinite source of maps to rush for specific rewards not impacted by the drop penalty, such as graftblood from Breach encounters.
Memory thread | Cursed | It is unrelated to curses.
Metamod | Description | A meta-crafting modifier , commonly referred to as a metamod , is an item modifier that changes the way in which various crafting methods apply to an item.
Metamod | Overview | There are five metamods that can be applied to items:
Metamod | Overview | The following legacy metamod is only available on existing items in permanent leagues.
Metamod | Overview | These modifiers can be unlocked as crafts from specific end-game unique maps. See Crafting Bench § Crafting modifiers for details. All of the above metamods except multimod can also be added via Beastcrafting using a Wild Bristle Matron.
Metamod | Overview | Metamods do not grant stats or bonuses, but rather affect other mods, and may override regular crafting rules. [1] For example, Prefixes Cannot Be Changed will prevent an Orb of Annulment from removing a desirable prefix modifier. It will not, however, prevent adding a new modifier, such as through an Exalted Orb or Chaos Orb , as it only applies to existing modifiers. Note that some currencies and crafting methods cannot be used on items with metamods, such as essences [2] , or ignore metamods, such as Awakener's Orb s.
Metamod | Rules and Exceptions | Some of the currencies and crafting options available will ignore different metamods. Likewise, currencies such as Orb of Alchemy must be used on a normal item, which invariably may not have a crafted modifier on them. The tables below show which options will respect or ignore metamods.
Mirage | Description | Mirages are a league mechanic introduced in Mirage league. Throughout Wraeclast, players can encounter a gateway to the Astral Realm, containing a mirage of a limited part of the current area holding a tortured captive Djinn that must be released.
Mirage | Mechanics | Areas can contain a single Mirage. Entering it will take the player to an imperfect copy of the surrounding area around the Mirage called a "Mirage Area"; this area is not determined by distance but rather the total walkable terrain, adjusting around walls or obstacles. [1]
Mirage | Mechanics | Mirage Areas are part of the same instance as the original area and are affected by all area modifiers. Mirages will duplicate most league mechanics that spawned in the original area, though not perfectly, which can result in changes to certain mechanics or rewards, described further below. In areas that contain Mirages, league mechanic content that can be copied by the mirage will generally tend to spawn close to the mirage if possible.
Mirage | Mechanics | Mirage Areas also contains several Afarud monster packs that can drop Djinn coin currencies or Afarud uniques.
Mirage | Mechanics | Additionally, before entering, Varashta can augment the Mirage, granting a choice between one of three Wishes that can modify the mirage's rewards or monsters or grant powerful buffs. Each Wish is associated with one of three Djinn (Ruzhan, Navira, and Kelari), which will determine which type of Djinn coin can drop in the area.
Mirage | Wishes | Wish for Glyph can be combined with Perandus Signet to have up to a 9% chance to drop an extra Scroll of Wisdom on kill with The Unseen Hand.
Mirage (proxy) | Description | A mirage is an invulnerable, untargetable clone of the player (or a monster) that uses specific skills. It is a type of proxy , and scales with the player's offensive stats, but does not attribute hits or kills to the player. Mirages may persist for a duration, or disappear as soon as their animation are completed.
Mirage (proxy) | Description | Mirages cannot be targeted and cannot apply Taunt.
Modifier | Description | Modifiers generally change various aspects of the entity they are affecting. Most commonly modifiers apply stats , however they can also apply buffs or grant skills and can often be found on items , monsters , strongboxes or areas.
Modifier | Description | A modifier should be seen as an instance of change applied to an entity. A basic modifier does nothing on its own, it is given the effect by the associated stats (and their values), buffs and skills.
Modifier | Mechanics overview | A modifier applies statistics , a buff or grants a skill to an entity. Modifiers are specific to items , monsters , strongboxes or areas.
Modifier | Mechanics overview | Since not all statistics have a visible text, it is possible that some effects are granted by the modifier but are not visible to the player. On the wiki, some of these effects have a custom text specific to the wiki and are noted with (HIDDEN) in the description. In particular area and monster effects may be hidden from the player.
Modifier | Mechanics overview | Modifiers can either be innately applied (as "implicit" modifier) to entities, be granted under specific conditions or randomly generated.
Modifier | Mechanics overview | Some specific circumstances like the rarity of a monster, being touched or possessed by a Tormented Spirit , etc can also apply modifiers innately without them being randomly generated.
Modifier | Mechanics overview | Modifier generation is gated by specific conditions that govern if and how likely a modifier is going to appear:
Modifier | Mechanics overview | The values of stats include a minimum and maximum value, which is most commonly used on items - the actual value of the stat in the cases where minimum and maximum are not the same will be randomized within with equal chances, so for example a Stat with a minimum value of 1 and a maximum value of 3, can either be 1, 2 or 3 at 1/3 chance for each value.
Modifier | Mechanics overview | If a buff is specified, Modifiers also include a value for the buff, but unlike for Stats it is not randomized and fixed.
Modifier | Mechanics overview | If a skill is specified, the specified skill (at the specified level) will be granted to the relevant entity. The modifier does not include values for the skill other then the level as they're defined by the skill itself. Often this is found on items, where they grant skills, such as The Whispering Ice unique item.
Modifier | Local and global | Modifiers can be categorized as "local" or "global" modifiers.
Modifier | Local | The concept of "local" modifiers has broadened since its original technical definition [2]. This can be seen by the use of (local) in the trade site for modifiers that failed to meet the original criteria of just base stat modifications, like #% chance to Poison on Hit.
Modifier | Local | Currently, local modifiers can be identified by fulfilling any of the following requirements:
Modifier | Local | Item Properties : Item properties encompass all default properties of an item, including its base stats, attribute and level requirements, and sockets and links. Base stats can be found at the top of the item's tooltip. For example, #% increased Attack Speed and Adds # to # Physical Damage on a weapon will modify the "Attacks per Second" and "Physical Damage" stat on the weapon itself. Certain stats may not be immediately obvious, as most base items have that stat's default value at 0. For example, Adds # to # Fire Damage on a Solarine Bow directly adds to the weapon's base damage, of which Fire Damage is usually 0 for weapons. Default base stats are displayed in white , while modified base stats are displayed in blue (with the exception of fire / cold / lightning / chaos damage on weapons, which are colour-coded based on their damage type and have a base stat of 0).
Modifier | Local | Hand-specific : Modifiers that include " with this Weapon " or " Main/Off Hand " should be considered local, despite being conditional, as they only apply to attacks using that specific hand/weapon. These types of modifiers are technically global modifiers that apply locally to one or both hand(s), and therefore cannot be scaled by other local increases [3].
Modifier | Local | Weapon Hit Effect : Stats on weapons that apply on an attack hit with a generic (modifier-less) weapon (e.g. #% Chance to Poison on Hit , #% Chance to Maim , #% of Physical Attack Damage Leeched as Life ) are considered local. Flat modifiers to accuracy or chance to hit on weapons are also considered local, as chance to hit is hand-specific and determined on hit. While Poison and Bleeding chance are local, Ignite chance is always global, as generic weapons do not have base fire damage and therefore cannot ignite.
Modifier | Global | Global modifiers encompass all other modifiers that are not local. All conditional stats are global except for the main/off-hand stats listed above [4]. Global stats never modify an item's base stats and instead apply to the character's stats, and therefore cannot interact directly with other local modifiers. For example, the damage from Adds # to # Physical Damage on a weapon is scaled by #% increased Physical Damage and quality on a weapon, but Adds # to # Physical Damage to Attacks from the ring is not (as rings do not have base damage) and added separately in addition to the weapon's base damage before calculating any other global increased/more modifiers. Modifiers that state "Global" are always global.
Modifier | Global | In general, conditional modifiers should always be considered global.
Modifier | Global | Hybrid modifiers (modifiers with more than one line per stat) treat each line independently. A hybrid modifier can have both local and global parts, such as of Tacati - 30% chance to Poison on Hit , (26-30)% increased Chaos Damage (Suffix).
Modifier | Terminology | In general modifiers are referred to as such, however there are many special cases of modifiers that correspond to specific sets and Modifiers#Conditions :
Modifier | Implicit modifiers | Implicit modifiers always spawn on entities before the addition or change of additional modifiers (for example by changing the rarity ).
Modifier | Implicit modifiers | On monsters , implicit modifiers can be very commonly found. For example, some monsters are granted damage conversion which converts their inherent damage to that of another element. However, on unique monsters and bosses implicits are most notable - for example most bosses are granted a boost to their item rarity and item quantity as well as other bonuses such as on Atziri.
Modifier | Implicit modifiers | On items , visible implicit modifiers are most commonly found on:
Modifier | Implicit modifiers | Shields and body armour also commonly have a hidden movement speed penalty modifier.
Modifier | Implicit modifiers | Unlike the implicit modifiers on monsters, the implicit modifiers on equipment can be by altered in various ways:
Modifier | Implicit modifiers | Certain unique items also have special interactions with implicits:
Modifier | Enchantments | Enchantments are additional modifiers that can be added to items through specific means. Enchantments have their own mod slot on items and do not use the implicit mod slot. [5] Most items can have up to one enchantment at a time. Any level of rarity , even unique items , can be enchanted. Mirrored cannot receive an enchantment. [6] They are always fixed values, so Blessed Orbs have no effect on them. [7] Applying an enchantment on an already enchanted item replaces the old enchantment with the new one. Enchantments can be removed from a non-corrupted item using the Crafting Bench recipe; this cannot be done with maps and jewels. Corruption does not remove the enchantments of an item.
Modifier | Scourge mods | If an item becomes Scourged using the Blood Crucible , it gains two Scourge modifiers, one positive and one negative. Scourge mods are separate from implicit mods and enchantments. Blood Crucible upgrades can cause an item to gain additional Scourge mods. This mechanic has not been added to the core game and can only be found on legacy items in permanent leagues.
Modifier | Explicit modifiers | Explicit modifiers are generally dynamically generated by changing the rarity of the entity or by other modification.
Modifier | Explicit modifiers | The number of affixes given by rarity depends on the rarity class:
Modifier | Explicit modifiers | Monsters have different means of receiving modifiers:
Modifier | Explicit modifiers | On items, modifiers can be changed by spending currency :
Modifier | Explicit modifiers | Certain sources can drop items with special explicit modifiers not found on standard items:
Modifier | Explicit modifiers | Areas may receive modifiers depending on how they were created unlike items, monsters or strongboxes:
Modifier | Conditions | Modifiers usually include conditions which are used to determine how they appear. These are generally used to govern the creation of explicit modifiers on entities.
Modifier | Domain | The domain of a modifier specifies what kind of game object it applies to. The domains are primarily reverse engineered, as detailed information has been removed from the game files.
Modifier | Generation type | The mod generation determines "how" the mod will be created on an item. The generation types are primarily reverse engineered, as detailed information has been removed from the game files.
Modifier | Mod Level | The required level of the relevant entity. For example, this can be the required item level or a monster level.
Modifier | Mod Level | However, there are cases where this is not respected: in particular this is the case for any mods that are directly given to other entities, such as implicit mods including enchantments or monsters with innate mods.
Modifier | Mod Level | The mod level is also a factor in calculating the level requirement of items ; raising the level requirement up to 80% requirement of the mod (with the requirement rounded down to the nearest whole integer). In particular this is the case for mods on unique items and for enchantments
Modifier | Mod Level | For example, Seven-League Step normally has a level requirement of 1, however after adding a legacy 0.5% of Damage Leeched as Life if you've Killed Recently enchantment from the Labyrinth its level requirement increases to ⌈ 66 × 0.8 ⌉ = 52 \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}\left\lceil {66\times 0.8}\right\rceil =52.
Modifier | Group/family | Each modifier belongs to one or more groups (or families). These restrict which modifiers may appear on an object together. [1] Only one modifier from any given group may appear on an object; in other words, all modifiers belonging to a group are mutually exclusive with one another.
Modifier | Group/family | This is often used used to influence the crafting of items, where players will add a mod from an undesired group of modifiers to block it. This means the undesired mods in that group will not be added when crafting currency is used. Together with the item level requirements, this creates the "tiered" system of modifiers.
Modifier | Tags | Mods use the internal Tag system to determine on which entities they can appear and how likely they are to appear on entities. Tags are classified as spawn weight tag and mod tag:
Modifier | Spawn weight tag | Spawn weight tag primarily functions like this:
Modifier | Spawn weight tag | So, for example:
Modifier | Mod tag | Mods can be found tagged with mod tags. A non-exhaustive list can be found below. Some mods do not have any tags. These tags can interact with Catalysts , Fossils , Harvest crafting, and Heist enchantments.
Modifier | Mod tag | In the table below, the tags on the top row have associated Harvest crafts. As a result, they also have associated tag colours. The tags on the bottom row have neither.
Modifier | Mod tag | The metamods of Spellcraft - Cannot roll Attack Modifiers (Suffix) and of Weaponcraft - Cannot roll Caster Modifiers (Suffix) can interact with Harvest crafting, Exalted Orbs , Orbs of Annulment , and the beastcrafting recipes "Add a Suffix, Remove a Random Prefix" ( Farric Lynx Alpha ) and "Add a Prefix, Remove a Random Suffix" ( Farric Wolf Alpha ).
Modifier | Mod tag | For example, when an Exalted Orb is used on an item with the of Spellcraft of Spellcraft Suffix Cannot roll Attack Modifiers , the Exalted Orb cannot add modifiers with the "Attack" tag. Similarly, when an Orb of Annulment is used on an item with the of Weaponcraft of Weaponcraft Suffix Cannot roll Caster Modifiers modifier, it will not remove any modifiers with the "Caster" tag.
Modifier | Mod tag | Some crafting methods ignore or cannot be used with metamods. Awakener's Orb s [8] ignore them. Essences [9] and resonators socketed with fossils may not be used on items with metamods.
Modifier | Mod tag | Quality applied to jewellery , such as rings , belts , and amulets , can only be applied with Catalysts. Each type of Catalyst will apply a different type of quality which increases magnitudes of modifiers with the tags associated with the quality type.
Modifier | Mod tag | For example, when a Fertile Catalyst is applied to jewellery , it will apply a quality that increases the magnitude of modifiers with the Life or Mana tags, up to 20%. A modifier normally granting "+79 to Maximum Life" on the item will be enhanced to instead grant "+94 to Maximum Life", and a modifier normally granting "Non-Channelling Skills have -7 to Total Mana Cost" will be enhanced to instead grant "Non-Channelling Skills have -8 to Total Mana Cost". Modifiers enhanced this way will round down decimal values.
Modifier | Mod tag | Fossils multiply the weights of modifiers that match the type of the fossil, For example, Metallic Fossil s will multiply the weight of modifiers with the Lightning tag by 1000%, and the modifiers with Physical tags by 0%. Effectively, this will result in modifiers with the lightning tag to appear 10x more oftenwhen the item is rolled, and modifiers with the physical tag never rolling.
Modifier | Mod tag | Many heist -exclusive enchantments can modify the magnitudes of modifiers of certain tags, both positively and negatively. These enchantments can be acquired either through the use of a Tailoring Orb on a body armour , use of a Tempering Orb on a weapon , or found already rolled as an item in a Curio Display at the end of a Blueprint wing. (All Grand Heist layouts with "Enchanted Rare Body Armour" and "Enchanted Rare Weapon" as a reward type).
Modifier | Mod tag | For example, the enchantment 8% increased Explicit Life Modifier magnitudes will enhance a modifier that normally grants "+100 to Maximum Life" to granting "+108 to Maximum Life". Some Heist enchantments come with downsides. The hybrid modifier 10% increased Explicit Life Modifier magnitudes + 25% reduced Explicit Speed Modifier magnitudes will increase the magnitudes of modifiers with the Physical tags by 10%, but reduce the magnitudes of modifiers with the Speed tag, such as 19% increased Attack Speed by 25%.
Modifier | Mod tag | Many Harvest crafting methods interact with modifier tags.
Modifier | Mod tag | The craft "Reforge a Rare item with random modifiers, including a (tag) modifier" will completely reforge the modifiers of a Rare item, similar to a Chaos Orb , while guaranteeing a modifier with the specified tag. If there are no valid tags in the mod pool to roll for the selected item , the craft cannot be used. The add/remove crafts work as expected.
Modifier | Mod tag | The craft "Change a modifier that grants (Element) Resistance into a similar-tier modifier that grants (Different Element) Resistance" will swap a resistance modifier of a certain element into that of another one.
Modifier | Modifier Tier Rating | Modifier Tier Rating is a mechanic first introduced in Necropolis league 's gravecrafting that is able to prevent low tier modifiers from rolling. The exact mechanics are not fully known, however there are two popular models that may explain how this system works.
Modifier | Redistribution model | The more popular explanation is that it can block low tier modifiers without directly affecting the relative weight of mod types during mod generation. Unlike fossils , which act like a multiplier to the weights of certain modifier types (e.g. 10x weight for Fire modifiers), modifier tier rating prevents a percentage of eligible mod tiers within each mod type, exclusive, rounded up to the nearest whole number [10] :
Modifier | Redistribution model | M T R % = 1 − ( 100 / ( x + 100 ) ) \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{MTR\%}=1-(100/(x+100)) where x \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}x = total added Modifier Tier Rating.
Modifier | Redistribution model | With +50 to Modifier Tier Rating, it will prevent the lowest 34% of mod tiers from rolling. With +100, the lowest 50%, and +200, the lowest 67%, and so on. The weights of the blocked modifiers are redistributed to the tiers of modifiers of the same mod type [11] , such that the relative weights within a mod type remain the same, and the relative weights for each mod type against the total pool of prefixes/suffixes remain the same. Modifiers with only a single (eligible) tier are unaffected by modifier tier rating.
Modifier | Redistribution model | For example, assume a modifier type (e.g. the prefix #% increased Fire Damage ) has three tiers that can roll at the item's item level , with Tiers 3/2/1 having weights of 1000/600/200 respectively. With a modifier tier rating of +100, preventing the lowest 50% tier modifiers from rolling, exclusive, this prevents Tier 3 from rolling and redistributes the weight of 1000 to the other eligible tiers. The weights of Tiers 3/2/1 are now 0/1350/450 respectively. Tier 2 is still 3x more likely to roll than Tier 1, and chance of rolling any increased Fire Damage prefix versus any other prefix modifier type is still the same with a total weight of 1800.
Modifier | Redistribution model | In simpler terms, this system forces modifiers to roll with higher tiers without affecting the chance to roll a specific type of modifier. It will can be used to more easily obtain lower weight modifiers with multiple tiers (e.g. Merciless Merciless Prefix (170-179)% increased Physical Damage ) but does not make very rare single tier modifiers (e.g. Magister's Magister's Prefix +1 to Level of all Spell Skill Gems ) any more likely to roll.
Modifier | Refactored weight model | It has been noted that Model 1, though generally accepted, does not match certain data sets [12] , particularly in cases where the weights of different tier modifiers differ (e.g. #% increased Physical Damage has a weight of 1000 for T8-6, but higher tiers have consecutively lower weights, down to a weight of 25 for T1.
Modifier | Refactored weight model | To account for this, an alternative model uses the same formula to determine the number of modifiers to block:
Modifier | Refactored weight model | M T R % = 1 − ( 100 / ( x + 100 ) ) \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{MTR\%}=1-(100/(x+100)) where x \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}x = total added Modifier Tier Rating.
Modifier | Refactored weight model | However, instead of distributing the weight of the blocked tiers, the weights of the remaining tiers are multiplied based on the number of total and remaining tiers instead [13] :
Modifier | Refactored weight model | n e w w e i g h t = o l d w e i g h t ∗ o r i g i n a l t i e r s r e m a i n i n g t i e r s \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{newweight}={oldweight}*{\frac {originaltiers}{remainingtiers}}
Modifier | Refactored weight model | For example, with increased Physical Damage has 8 tiers. T2 has a weight of 50, and T1 has a weight of 25. T8 to T1 has a total weight of 3775. By blocking 6 tiers, T2 has a new weight of 200, and T1 has a new weight of 100, for a total weight of 300.
Modifier | Refactored weight model | In this model, the total weight of each mod type *is* affected, thus resulting in differences in the chance to roll each modifier type as modifier tier rating increases.

Movement speed | Description | Movement speed (often referred to as MS ) is a defensive stat that determines how fast an entity can move by running.
Movement speed | Mechanics | Base movement speed is 3.7 meters per second, [1] and can be modified in various ways, such as passives , equipment , flasks , or (de)buffs. It has no minimum or maximum.
Movement speed | Mechanics | Body armours and shields apply an innate movement speed reduction while equipped. The exact penalty differs depending on the base type of the item; this is usually -3% movement speed, except for pure strength or hybrid strength/intelligence body armours which have a -5% movement speed penalty.
Movement speed | Mechanics | On enemies, normal rarity enemies can have their movement speed reduced to 0%, rendering them immobile. Magic and higher rarity enemies have a minimum movement speed value. [2]
Movement speed | Mechanics | Action speed affects the speed of all animations, including moving, but does not directly modify the movement speed stat. It instead acts as a separate multiplier.
Movement speed | Suffix | NOTE: The Quicksilver Flask gained as a quest reward from finishing Mercy Mission quest in Act 1 cannot roll "of Adrenaline" suffix because its item level is too low.
Movement speed | Unique Items | There are several unique items that affect movement speed.

Mysterious Barrels | Description | Mysterious barrels are special barrels that add extra loot and monsters to maps. They could be added to maps with Mysterious Scarabs and certain sextant mods, but these have been removed.
Mysterious Barrels | Mechanics | There are several varieties of barrels that can spawn:
Mysterious Darkshrine | Description | Mysterious Darkshrines can be found in the Lord's Labyrinth. When activated, a shrine will impart a beneficial effect. There are four darkshrines in each run. They are found by pulling switches on the walls, or in some case: pulling the switches on the sculpture in front of the hidden door. The switches will always appear on the upper left or upper right part of the walls. The minimap will show the passageway and the hidden rooms, but it won't appear in the game itself.
Mysterious Darkshrine | Izaro's voice-over | Activating a Mysterious Darkshrine plays a randomly selected voice-over line, spoken by Izaro. Depending on the player's game settings, a text transcript of the voice-over may be displayed in the chat log. These voice-overs should not be confused with the text that appears in the chat log to describe the effect of the activated shrine. There are three possible voice-over lines:
Mysterious Darkshrine | List of shrine effects | There are a limited number of shrine effects, all beneficial. Which effect a Mysterious Darkshrine will impart is determined by the layout of the Labyrinth. "Be Twice Blessed" is the only effect which can occur more than once, but will provide no additional bonus for multiple effects. [ citation needed ]
Net | Description | Nets were items used to capture beasts in the Bestiary leagues. Obtaining nets is not possible anymore. Existing nets remain in the permanent leagues , but don't have a use.
Net | Mechanics | Players can throw a net at any catchable beasts using a hotkey (Default: V). It will use the currently equipped net. Right clicking a net in your inventory will change the equipped net.
Net | Mechanics | When throwing a net at a beast, it will go into a capturing state and becomes momentarily stunned. The beast has a significant amount of damage reduction while being captured and cannot be killed in this state.
Net | Mechanics | If successfully captured, Einhar will appear and take the beast to the Menagerie. The lower the beast's life the more likely it is to get captured. If capturing fails, the beast is freed, recovers some life and becomes Enraged. You may try again after the Enrage effect wears off.
Net | Nets | The list below displays the different nets used to capture weak or strong beasts.
Observer Totem | Description | The Observer Totem is a totem that appears only in Heist contracts that require a rogue with the Perception ability. This totem can raise the Alert Level of the heist, and always appears in groups. A player who mishandles an Observer Totem group can rapidly push the heist into Imminent Lockdown and cause the heist to fail before reaching the target.
Observer Totem | Description | Observer Totems are typically found in groups of five, in a single room or in a length of hallway. Their appearance varies depending on the location of the contract.
Observer Totem | Description | Observer Totem mechanics were changed in Version 3.12.3 , in a way that makes the totems much more manageable.
Observer Totem | Inactive phase | Observer Totems start out inactive. An inactive Observer Totem is unlit and invulnerable. If a player comes too close to the inactive totem, or if another Observer Totem nearby activates, the totem will enter its active phase.
Observer Totem | Active phase | In the active phase, the totem displays a flashing light. The totem is now vulnerable to attacks. But every few seconds, the totem's light will flare more brightly. Very shortly thereafter, the totem will emit a red circular pulse. If any character is touched by this pulse, the Alert Level will instantly increase by approximately 15-20%. Minions , totems , traps , and mines touched by the pulse will not raise the Alert Level.
Observer Totem | Active phase | During the heist's Lockdown phase, all Observer Totems will activate. However, the totems are harmless at this point, since the Alert Level is already at maximum.
Observer Totem | Active phase | Characters attacking an Observer Totem in melee will often be hit by one alert pulse before destroying the totem, and potentially may be hit by alert pulses from other nearby totems as well.
Observer Totem | Active phase | A solo character can often just quickly move through the area before any Observer Totems have a chance to pulse. Parties can do the same if they stay close together and move in unison.
Oil | Description | An oil is a currency item that can be acquired from Blight encounters. Using them on certain items gives these items an anointment , which can modify them in various ways.
Oil | Mechanics | Oils can be applied by the player via Cassia , to blighted maps , rings , amulets or blight unique items in order to add an enchantment modifier to the item that have different effects based on the item type:
Oil | Standard oils | There are 13 standard oils that form a tiered progression in terms of rarity and value.
Oil | Special purpose oils | Three other oils have additional drop requirements and special uses.
Oil | List of Anointable uniques | These specific unique can also be anointed , even if they are not an amulet or ring. They gain the same passive skills that those oils would apply to an amulet. These items can drop from completing Blighted maps or Blight-ravaged maps, with the exception of Stranglegasp , which only drops in Blight-ravaged maps, and Replica Stampede , which is only available as a reward from Grand Heists.
Oil | List of Anointable uniques | Cowl of the Cryophile, Cowl of the Thermophile, and Cowl of the Ceraunophile can have up to two anointments, while Stranglegrasp can have up to four anointments.
Oil | List of Anointable uniques | If a corruption results in turning these into a Rare item, they will retain their anointments. With a Tainted Mythic Orb , it is possible to turn them into a different unique item of the same base item that normally cannot have anointments, or in the case of Stranglegasp, cannot have more than two anointments. Applying a new anointment to non-Blight uniques will cause them to lose any extra anointments beyond the default for their equipment type.

Omniscience | Description | Omniscience is a pseudo-attribute, similar to Devotion found from Militant Faith. Currently, Omniscience can only be gained while Crystallised Omniscience is equipped.
Omniscience | Lore | Omniscience is mentioned in the dialogue of The Envoy , regarding the boss that The Searing Exarch served, the Cleansing Fire. Crystallised Omniscience is one of the loot of The Searing Exarch.
Overkill damage | Description | The term overkill damage refers to a killing blow 's damage in excess of the target's remaining life. [1] [2]
Overkill damage | Damage | Overkill damage is calculated by subtracting the target's remaining health from the amount of damage done. For example, if a target has 10 life and 10 energy shield , and an attacker deals a hit of 100 damage, the target dies and the overkill damage is 80. If overkill damage is not greater than 0, it is ignored.
Overkill damage | Damage | The term does not apply to damage over time because a hit is required; damage over time can never overkill. [3]
Overkill damage | Interactions with culling strike | Overkill and culling can fundamentally never interact. [2] If a hit doesn't kill a target itself but triggers culling strike or Headsman that kills, damage from them doesn't count towards overkill damage and it stay negative, and, accordingly, overkill effects will not trigger.
Overkill damage | Related skills | The following skills utilize the overkill mechanic:
Overwhelm (game mechanic) | Description | Overwhelm is a retired keyword that applies to hits that deal physical damage , causing the hit to ignore a set value of the target's physical damage reduction. [1]
Overwhelm (game mechanic) | Mechanics | Overwhelm works similarly to resistance penetration , subtracting the specified amount from the target's effective physical damage reduction against the hit. However, Overwhelm cannot reduce physical damage reduction into the negatives. [2]

Path of Exile Royale | Description | Path of Exile Royale was a Game Mode added for April Fool's Day 2018. The game mode pits up to 100 players in a last-man-standing match on a large island. It was re-introduced to the game in version 3.14.3b. It was available on every weekend throughout the Expedition league except on launch weekend. It was extended into the Scourge league but not extended further.
Path of Exile Royale | Mechanics | Joining a Royale match works like joining a race - Royale can be found on the character selection screen, in the Events list (under the list of characters). A round of Path of Exile: Royale requires a fresh, separate character, which can be created as usual. There is no need to make a new character for each round though — once a character is created, it can be selected again to join more games, though they'll be reset to level 1 and lose all their items each time.
Path of Exile Royale | Mechanics | Entering the game as the character will put you in a new Royale mode queue. The character will be put on the shores of Royale Island where the players wait for the game to fill. During the waiting period, no one is able to move. Once there are 50 players, there will be 30 additional seconds for players to join (up to maximum of 100) before the game starts. After the round starts, players are allowed to move freely.
Path of Exile Royale | Mechanics | The game mode takes place in a large island, with players placed on the edges of the map. Traveling inward, more monsters and items can be found. There is a safe zone that periodically shrinks towards the center every 2 minutes. The danger zone is marked with a red border and the next danger zone is marked with a blue border. An arrow under the character will point towards the safe zone if it is within the green zone. Players within the danger zone will take damage over time which increases over time.
Path of Exile Royale | Mechanics | Items can be looted from killed monsters, players, or collected from loot chests. Various containers exist in the map:
Path of Exile Royale | Mechanics | Players will drop their corpse which can be looted on death, containing all their items they were carrying. Any gems they had socketed will be unsocketed. Notably, item filters are disabled in Royale.
Path of Exile Royale | Mechanics | There are also flask stations which completely refill all flasks when touched. After they've been used, their power is drained for a few seconds, after which they can be used again.
Path of Exile Royale | Mechanics | On death, you can choose to Spectate, turning into an invisible ghost that can freely roam the map.
Path of Exile Royale | Mechanics | The winner of PoE Royale receives a Rhoa Feast hideout decoration. Additional wins will upgrade the decoration.
Path of Exile Royale | Gameplay changes | Compared to the normal game, players start with more life, less mana but more mana regeneration, higher stun and ailment thresholds, more balanced base attributes, and faster experience gain. The area has the mods 40% increased Experience gain, Area has increased monster variety, Found Items drop Identified in Area.
Path of Exile Royale | Gameplay changes | A separate skill tree exists for Royale mode, which is shared among all classes. Players gain 2 skill points on level up. There is no need to confirm skill point allocations, and skill points cannot be refunded.
Path of Exile Royale | Gameplay changes | Every player starts with a 3-link R-G-B one-handed sword, one-handed mace, and bow in their inventory, as well as 2 Small Life Flask s and a Small Mana Flask.
Path of Exile Royale | Gameplay changes | Several skill gems and unique items were rebalanced for low levels and added to the game mode.
Path of Exile Royale | Gameplay changes | Health flasks effects are interrupted if the user receives a hit from another player.
Path of Exile Royale | Gems | There are currently around 50 skill gems and 15 support gems available in Royale. They have been chosen from all of the gems in the regular game and, if necessary, scaled down for use in low-level play. For example, it is possible to find a skill at level 1 that requires level 28 in regular Path of Exile. The skills available are exclusively damage and/or movement related.
Portal | Description | A portal is an entity that allows instant travel to and from the town in the Act where it is created (or the previous town if the current town is unvisited) and between a map and a hideout. The standard blue portal appearance can be changed by purchasing a Portal Effect.
Portal | Description | Each area can only have one portal active at once. It can be moved with Portal Scrolls or the Portal gem.
Portal | Portals in Acts | Player-created portals can be used to travel to town unlimited times by any party members. However, it will disappear once the creator uses it from the town-side. Other party members can use the town-side portal unlimited times. Towns will show portals of other party members who are currently in the same Act of the campaign.
Portal | Portals in Acts | Portals will automatically disappear after the instance they are linked to has expired. The expiration time for instances is 8 minutes for normal instances and 15 minutes for "hub" instances (instances that lead to more than one instance, eg. Mud Flats which leads to Fetid Pool and Submerged Passage). A portal will not expire as long as the instance it is linked to is prevented from expiring (eg. a player stays in it).
Portal | Portals in Acts | When joining another players instance in a party (by clicking the Portal icon on their party portrait), players will spawn at the portal if one exists.
Portal | Portals created by a Map Device | Portals work differently when created by a Map Device and the corresponding portal inside the map. See Map Device for more information.

Prevented damage | Description | Prevented damage is a value in hit damage calculation used by certain mechanics.
Prevented damage | Mechanics | Prevented damage is the difference between a hit's calculated damage before the defender's mitigation, and the final damage taken , if that difference is positive. Taking more damage than the amount calculated before mitigation will not count as "negative" prevented damage. [1]
Prevented damage | Mechanics | Damage is prevented by various damage mitigation mechanics. These include:
Prevented damage | Mechanics | Resistance also prevents damage, though no mechanic currently interacts with prevented non-physical damage.
Prevented damage | Mechanics | Mechanics that occur before or after damage mitigation do not count as preventing damage. This includes mechanics that prevent the hit (e.g. evasion , dodge ), preempt the damage (e.g. Proximity Shield , Divine Shrine ), or change how damage is applied (e.g. Ward , Steelskin , Petrified Blood , The Jinxed Juju , Dissolution of the Flesh ). [3] [4] Taking damage as another type also does not prevent damage; shifting physical damage to fire (and then resisting it) does not count as preventing any physical damage. [5]
Prevented damage | Mechanics | While reflected damage normally does not interact with on-hit or when-hit effects, mitigating it does count toward prevented damage, whether by reduced Reflected Damage taken modifiers [6] or more general mitigation such as armour. Note that Cannot take Reflected Physical/Elemental Damage applies at two stages, and only counts as preventing damage in the damage mitigation step, not when it preempts damage before the damage taken as step.
Projectile | Description | Projectiles are entities that travel independently of their creator until they collide with an enemy or obstacle, or reach their travel distance limit of 15 metres. [1] Skill gems that create projectiles usually have the Projectile or Bow gem tag.
Projectile | Speed and duration | All projectiles have a speed, which can be altered by Projectile Speed modifiers. Reduced projectile speed has a maximum of 99% [2] [3] , but there is no limit for increased projectile speed.
Projectile | Speed and duration | All projectiles also have a duration (which can be infinite). In most cases, this duration is not mentioned on the skill itself and cannot be modified. Some skills, such as Spark , do have an explicit duration which can be modified.
Projectile | Speed and duration | The speed and duration will determine the distance a projectile will travel, up to its maximum range (at most 15 metres). [4] Increasing the Projectile Speed of limited-duration projectiles will allow them to travel a further distance before they expire. For example, Freezing Pulse creates projectiles that initially deal full damage but deal less damage progressively throughout its total distance (" by the time they dissipate "). Increasing the Projectile Speed of Freezing Pulse will cause the projectiles to hit the target sooner in its total distance, and therefore deal more damage than a slower-moving Freezing Pulse that travelled the same distance to the target.
Projectile | Speed and duration | However, note that projectile speed does not affect the distance at which specific projectile effects occur. For example:
Projectile | Speed and duration | Certain skills that have area effects, such as Rolling Magma , Eye of Winter and Soulrend or that can repeatedly hit the target with each projectile, such as Spark and Spectral Helix can be made to deal increased single-target damage by reducing their projectile speed to its minimum value.
Projectile | Ground and airborne projectiles | Most projectiles travel through the air. However, some travel along the ground.
Projectile | Ground and airborne projectiles | Airborne projectiles can be aimed up and down cliffs and other height transitions and can impact the ground or ceiling. This can sometimes cause the projectile to miss a target's vertical hitbox when dealing with a steep angle, as they may fly over the heads of enemies or harmlessly impact the ground at the enemy's feet. [ citation needed ] Airborne projectiles will pass through most low obstacles such as small chests and rocks.
Projectile | Ground and airborne projectiles | Projectiles that travel along the ground are subject to the same restrictions as a walking player. This means they cannot be fired up or down cliffs or ledges, and will instead collide with the edge. Skills that create ground projectiles include Spark and Lightning Strike.
Projectile | Projectile Behaviours | When a projectile successfully collides with an enemy or obstacle, the projectile either ends, or continues with one of the projectile behaviours described below. If an attack projectile misses a target (due to insufficient accuracy ) it will continue through the target without colliding.
Projectile | Projectile Behaviours | Whenever a projectile collides, it will attempt each of its remaining behaviors, [5] prioritized in this order: Split , Pierce , Fork , Chain , Return. Only a single behaviour can occur per collision. For example, a projectile with a remaining Chain and Return will Chain if a target exists to Chain to, but it will Return immediately against a single enemy. A projectile with Pierce and Chain will Pierce enemies, but can Chain from terrain with % chance to be able to Chain when colliding with terrain (as terrain cannot be pierced).
Projectile | Projectile Behaviours | On collision, the projectile splits into ( X ) number of auto-targeting projectiles. The auto-targeting radius limitations are similar to chain: ~6 metres. A projectile can only split once.
Projectile | Projectile Behaviours | Split projectiles are considered the same projectile after splitting and therefore will not target the same monster twice. For most skills, split will not increase the number of hits against a single target, but exceptions are possible when a secondary part of the skill has a different target list (e.g. Tornado Shot ) or does not need to directly collide to deal damage (e.g. Splitting Steel ).
Projectile | Projectile Behaviours | Sources of split include:
Projectile | Projectile Behaviours | The projectile passes through the enemy after hitting it and continues along its previous trajectory. It is possible to disable " Projectiles Pierce all Targets " behaviour on skills via Snakepit , allowing a projectile to Fork/Chain/Return instead.
Projectile | Projectile Behaviours | The projectile splits into two identical projectiles which each travel at a 60-degree angle from the projectile's original path. This angle can be modified via passive skills. Certain items and passives can also add additional projectiles to a fork. Similar to Split, the two projectiles are considered continuations of the original projectile.
Projectile | Projectile Behaviours | Kinetic Bolt has a unique behaviour which causes it to change directions in a zig-zag motion, and additional forks will cause it to change direction additional times instead. Hitting an enemy does not cause it to disappear.
Projectile | Projectile Behaviours | Sources of fork include:
Projectile | Projectile Behaviours | Chain is a behaviour of both projectiles and certain skills that have chaining targeting, such as Arc. Regular projectiles have a targeting range of approximately 6 metres. Unlike other projectile behaviours, chain requires an enemy within range to occur.
Projectile | Projectile Behaviours | A chaining projectile chooses a target within a certain radius, and travels in the direction of that target. If a skill produces multiple projectiles at once and chains, none of the projectiles may collide with an enemy that has already been struck. If there are no valid targets in range of the original enemy, chain may aim at an enemy that was already hit, but the projectile will pass through without colliding.
Projectile | Projectile Behaviours | Rolling Magma has a unique behaviour which causes it to bounce in the same direction several times, and additional chains cause it to bounce additional times instead. Hitting an enemy does not cause it to disappear.
Projectile | Projectile Behaviours | Sources of chain that apply to projectiles include:
Projectile | Projectile Behaviours | The projectile returns in the direction of its creator. Unlike other behaviours, returns allows one additional collision (per simultaneous set) against targets that were already hit. [6] If a projectile returns directly from an enemy, that enemy cannot be hit by other returning projectiles in the same set. [7] A projectile can normally only return once.
Projectile | Projectile Behaviours | Return has the lowest priority among projectile behaviours. [8]
Projectile | Projectile Behaviours | Sources of returning projectiles include:
Projectile | 'Shotgunning' | The game normally prevents 'shotgunning'. When multiple projectiles are created simultaneously, only one of those projectiles can collide with the same target. Projectiles after the first will pass through without colliding. This prevents standing inside an enemy and hitting the same enemy 9 times from a single Split Arrow attack. Similarly, it prevents multiple collisions from Forked or Split projectiles (that Return). [9]
Projectile | 'Shotgunning' | Shotgun prevention only interacts with collisions , not all hits.
Projectile | Non-collision hits | Certain skills have a "ground-targeted" aim, firing projectiles at the ground near the player's cursor. These skills can directly collide with enemies (normally once), and hit enemies without colliding, by dealing area damage when projectiles explode or stop existing. Their damage is often balanced to account for this mechanic. For example:
Projectile | Non-collision hits | There is also a variation of ground-targeted projectiles which can never collide with enemies. For example:
Projectile | Non-collision hits | Normally, there is no limit on the number of times a projectile skill can hit a single enemy through area effects. However, Unearth and Rolling Magma have non-standard behaviour.
Projectile | On-collision effects | Some projectiles explode or have an area component on every collision, while other projectiles only explode when the projectile is destroyed by exhausting all projectile behaviours or hitting an obstacle. Explosions are generally projectile area damage, while non-exploding hits are only projectile damage.

Proxy | Description | A proxy (also referred to as "remote skill") is a term that refers to entities that use the character 's skills. Because skills inherit the player's offensive stats, a proxy is able to copy the player offensively, while remaining a separate entity for other purposes, such as reflect. Totems , traps , mines , and mirages are examples of proxies. Minions are not proxies, as they use their own skills, with their own stats.
Proxy | Examples of proxies | The following types of skills are considered proxies:
Proxy | Mechanics | Proxies use skills borrowed from the character , which contain the character's offensive modifiers, including on-hit effects and modifiers that apply or modify debuffs. While they are not 'you', many stats worded as 'you' or 'your' will apply to the player's skills even when used by proxies. [1] Proxies that cannot be targeted or expire immediately after a hit cannot taunt.
Proxy | Mechanics | Skill : With the exception of Flamewood Support , proxies can only access one of the player's skills. This means they cannot trigger skills granted by support gems like Impending Doom Support , by passives like Tawhoa's Chosen , or apply a Hex from a skill socketed in Mark of Submission.
Proxy | Mechanics | When a Vaal skill is modified to create proxies (by e.g. Spell Totem Support or Trap Support ), each proxy requires one skill-use worth of souls to create, and each will have enough souls to use its skill once. Proxies cannot gain or recover souls for themselves, and therefore cannot reuse a Vaal skill even if a trap/mine becomes able to trigger/detonate an additional time. [2] Some proxies cannot be created by Vaal skills at all, such as Reflection mirages.
Proxy | Mechanics | Stats : Proxies do not inherit the player's stats globally, only their skill. [3] They do not inherit the player's defensive stats, movement speed , or action speed. Even if proxies are given their own offensive stats, those stats would not apply to the skill they use; the player's skill has the player's stats. [4] [5] For example, a totem that somehow gains the Onslaught buff will not attack any faster. It will attack faster when the player is buffed.
Proxy | Mechanics | In the rare case a proxy deals damage outside its borrowed skill, like Hinekora, Death's Fury 's on-totem-kill explosion, that damage will not scale with the player's stats. [6] In this case, the damage will only scale with the proxy's own global stats and stats added to the hit through debuffs on the enemy, like Flammability 's Hits against Cursed Enemies have +#% chance to Ignite. (Not to be confused with Totems Explode on Death effects, which is direct damage dealt by the player.)
Proxy | Mechanics | Hits : As separate objects, proxies' hits are their own. On-hit effects like Life gained per Enemy Hit or Take 100 Fire Damage when you Ignite an Enemy will apply to the proxy. While most on-hit effects are inherited by the skill proxies use, proxies cannot be used for effects that specifically track the player, like Heralds and Corrupting Fever. [7]
Proxy | Mechanics | Kills: Proxies can be credited with kills. They do not have the player's on-kill effects unless those effects are inherited by the borrowed skill, such as Icefang Orbit 's Poisoned Enemies you Kill with Hits Shatter or killing blow explosions like the Devastator passive or Quecholli. [8]
Proxy | Mechanics | Note: most damage over time from proxies will credit the player with kills to prevent the possibility of kills going to deleted objects. [9] Exceptions exist, such as Searing Bond , Siphoning Trap , or The Retch. Kills can also be taken from proxies by affecting enemies with Gravebind.
Proxy | Mechanics | Minions : When proxies summon minions, those minions are the player's, not the proxy's, [10] and will still benefit from all of the player's minion-related stats. They do not scale with proxy stats (e.g. trap damage). Minions themselves are not proxies, though the Profane Proxy ring has a similar mechanic, granting Summon Skitterbots the player's Hex skill as a curse aura. [11]
Quality | Description | Quality improves the signature stat of an item such as the physical damage on weapons and base defence rating on armours or adds additional bonuses to gems.
Quality | Mechanics | Any item that drops with randomly generated quality can drop with up to 30% quality. This chance is weighted, with the majority of items having 0% quality, and quality above 20% being progressively more rare. Certain monster reward modifiers can also cause all non-gem items that can have quality to have 1%-30% quality. Any normal rarity or unidentified item with at least 1% quality will have a temporary Superior affix.
Quality | Mechanics | Quality can be applied via currency to most equipment ( quivers being the exception), as well as gems , maps , and strongboxes. Each item type has a currency item associated with it that increases its quality. Quality does not affect the requirements for using an item or the mana cost of skills.
Quality | Mechanics | Increasing the quality on weapons and armours also makes crafting sockets and links with Jeweller's Orbs and Orbs of Fusing easier. Each 1% quality improves the result by 1%. This makes obtaining many sockets and links 20% more likely on 20% quality items and even likelier on 30% quality items.
Quality | Mechanics | Increasing quality via currency is generally capped at 20%. However, there are certain methods that can increase quality beyond that, including:
Quality | Amount | The amount of quality given by a quality-increasing currency item depends on the equipment's item level. The higher the item level, the less quality each currency item will give.
Quality | Amount | For most items, the amount of quality added by currency items follows this formula:
Quality | Amount | Below is a table showing the probabilities for different levels of items and their amount of quality that will be added by the currency:
Quality | Amount | For maps , the quality added by Maven Chisels (and Cartographer's Chisel ) is always 20%.
Quality | Amount | For gems , the quality added by Gemcutter's Prism is always 1%.
Quality | Amount | Quality currencies always add 1% quality to unique items, regardless of its item level.
Quality | Effect on items | Quality on equipment is multiplicative to its local stats. For example, 20% quality on a weapon is equivalent to it having 20% more Physical Damage. In another example, a piece of gear that naturally gives 100 Armour that has the mods +50 to Armour and 90% increased Armour and 20% quality would give ( 100 + 50 ) ∗ ( ( 100 + 90 ) / 100 ) ∗ ( ( 100 + 20 ) / 100 ) = 342 {\textstyle \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}(100+50)*((100+90)/100)*((100+20)/100)=342} Armour.
Quality | Effect on items | The table below displays what currency items can be used on each category of items to alter its quality and their bonuses:
Quality | Effect on items | Certain Harvest crafting crafts can apply enchantments on weapons and body armours that could change the effect of quality on that item instead of the default quality (weapon physical damage or body armour defences). This does not affect other aspects of quality such as the chance to have a certain number of sockets or links.
Quality | Skill gems | Both skill gems and support gems may have quality. Every skill is affected by quality differently, but it frequently improves the damage dealt with the skill or provides small improvements like increased Area of Effect. Even those that do have their damage improved will see different improvement rates for a given amount of quality.
Quality | Skill gems | The quality of skill gems may be improved with a Gemcutter's Prism. These upgrades always improve a skill's quality by 1%. Alternatively, a level 20 non- awakened support gem and a Gemcutter's Prism can be vendored (sold to a NPC) for a level 1 gem with 20% quality.
Quality | Skill gems | The effect of quality scales with the base quality effect, however, only whole numbers will be granted (and thus the effect will always be rounded down); for example 3% quality on a gem with 0.5% effect will only grant 1% effect and not 1.5% effect. Effects with some degree of fractions are rounded to their natural bases (i.e. seconds will be rounded to milliseconds, etc.).
Quality | Skill gems | It is possible to get a gem's quality above 20%. Corrupting a gem can increase its quality by up to 23%. Enhance Support and certain gear modifiers can also improve gem quality.

Rage | Description | Rage is a counter utilized by certain attack skills and Ascendancy classes. Characters with Rage deal more attack damage — this affects the hit damage with attacks, but not ailments from the attack such as Bleeding. This increases in magnitude with the amount of Rage accumulated. Rage rapidly depletes if you haven't gained Rage or taken a hit for 2 seconds.
Rage | Mechanics | The maximum Rage a character can have by default is 30, but can be increased by items and passives. A character loses 10 Rage every second after not having gained Rage or been hit in the past 2 seconds. Inherent Rage loss is #% slower/faster modifiers affect the amount of Rage lost per second. Sources which grant Rage over time such as Chainbreaker and Kaom's Spirit do not reset the timer for inherent Rage loss.
Rage | Mechanics | Characters gain the following effects for each point of Rage:
Rage | Mechanics | Effects which state "Every Rage also grants", such as Kaom's Primacy and Crave the Slaughter , will scale with Rage effect.
Rage | Mechanics | Rage is not classified as a buff , therefore increased buff effects will not apply to the effects of having Rage. [1]
Rage | Mechanics | All sources of Rage gain on hit are combined into one source. There is a shared cooldown preventing you from generating Rage on Hit from more than one hit every 0.5 seconds.
Rage | Mechanics | Minions cannot gain Rage.
Rage | Active skill gems | The following active skill gems are related to rage:
