Rampage | Description | Rampage is a kill streak mechanic that provides rewards for killing increasing numbers of enemies without stopping. The rampage effect is only available for characters equipping certain items.
Rampage | Mechanics | The rampage counter keeps a running total of consecutive kills, including kills by proxies and minions. When the character or a nearby party member fails to get a kill within five seconds of the previous kill, the rampage counter will reset to zero. When the counter reaches certain milestones, the character enters a new rampage tier and a special, beneficial effect is triggered.
Rampage | Mechanics | In addition to the tier effects, the character gains the following stats :
Rampage | Mechanics | The maximum rampage count is 1000. Kills after this number is reached will not increase the rampage count any more, but will renew the countdown.
Rampage | Mechanics | You do not gain Rampage stacks if you have an active Rampage killstreak but no longer have any source of Rampage on your character.
Rampage | Mechanics | Animate Guardian can't gain rampage, even if it meets the requirements of the relevant part of the equipment.
Rampage | Mechanics | The Writhing Jar , Vaal Breach etc. can be used to sustain Rampage while there are no nearby enemies to kill, or if the only enemies are invulnerable, such as during certain boss immunity phases.
Rampage | Rampage tiers | There are 13 rampage tiers. The number of kills required per tier remains the same throughout the parts.
Rampage | Unique Items | The table below lists unique items that are related to rampage:
Range | Description | The range of a skill or effect is the maximum Distance it can influence anything from its point of origin.
Range | Mechanics | Melee attacks have a relatively short range determined by adding weapon range to the radius of a character's hitbox (which is 2), though it can be greatly extended by utilizing certain passives and items. Maximum travel distance for projectiles is 15 metres [1] for each instance of movement [2] , although many projectiles in the game dissipate before reaching it, which limits their effective range. Effects such as fork, chain, or split, would count as new instances of movement, allowing projectiles to travel further than 15 total metres.
Range | Mechanics | Range of melee attacks can be improved with various passive skills and items. Range bonuses provided by passive tree, jewels and non-weapon equipment are global, meaning they will apply to both weapons if dual-wielding. However, range bonuses on weapons, including corrupted implicits, crafted bonuses or ones on uniques like Wideswing or Atziri's Disfavour are local and will extend the range only for the weapon they are located on, with the notable exception of Prismatic Eclipse , which offers a global bonus.
Range | Dual Wielding | When dual-wielding weapons with different range, the range used is dependent on the skill. [3]
Range | Attack Range and Area of Effect Radius | Attack skills that create an AoE anchored on your character, like Cleave , Sweep or Ground Slam are completely unaffected by attack range. Cyclone receives increased area of effect from additional Melee Strike Range and additional Weapon Range (none from base Weapon Range). Radius of skills that create an area of effect on the point of impact, like Molten Strike or single target skills supported by Melee Splash Support is also unaffected by attack range, however it does allow you to attack from a greater distance, pushing the AoE further from you, potentially affecting more enemies.
Range | Weapon range | Weapons have the following base ranges:
Range | Related unique items | See also Strike § Related unique items for unique that alter melee strike range
Rarity | Description | All monsters, strongboxes and most of the items come in one of four different rarities. The common rarity is normal , followed by magic , rare and unique. Higher rarity means things are higher valued but occur less frequently in the game.
Rarity | Item rarity | Many types of dropped items roll a random rarity with normal items being the most common and unique items the least common. The specific order of operations is as follows:
Rarity | Item rarity | Magic , rare , and unique items found by the player are initially unidentified and a Scroll of Wisdom must be used to discover their properties.
Rarity | Item rarity | The number of sockets that can be found on an item is not affected by rarity; this instead relies on its item level.
Rarity | Rarities | Normal items (also called base items) are the "default" state of items without any explicit modifiers / affixes. Some specific base types have implicit modifiers.
Rarity | Rarities | A normal item can be upgraded into a magic item using an Orb of Transmutation , or a rare item using an Orb of Alchemy. Using an Orb of Chance can upgrade a normal item into a magic , rare , or even unique item of the same base type.
Rarity | Rarities | Magic items have the same base statistics as a normal item of the same type, but have magical modifiers on them given by affixes , up to one prefix and one suffix. The types of modifiers that can be found or added to an item depend on its item level , the base type and any additional flags on the item (such as shaped or elder ).
Rarity | Rarities | A magic item with only either a prefix or suffix property can have a second property of the missing type added to it by using an Orb of Augmentation. The affixes can be rerolled with an Orb of Alteration.
Rarity | Rarities | A magic item can be upgraded into a rare item using a Regal Orb. It will retain its current affixes and one new affix will be added.
Rarity | Rarities | When Cloak of Tawm'r Isley is equipped, it grants player dropped magic item identified.
Rarity | Rarities | Rare items function the same as magic items, except they have at most six affixes – up to three prefixes and up to three suffixes. Found rare items or items made rare with an Orb of Chance or an Orb of Alchemy will always have at least 4 affixes, but it is possible to get a rare item with only 2 or 3 by using a Regal Orb or Orb of Annulment. A rare item with less than 6 affixes can gain an additional mod with an Exalted Orb or a crafted mod using a Crafting Bench. Chaos Orbs completely reroll a rare item's affixes, again giving between 4 and 6 mods.
Rarity | Rarities | Rare items are given a randomly generated name.
Rarity | Rarities | Flasks , Tinctures , and Relics cannot be of rare rarity.
Rarity | Rarities | Jewels , Abyss Jewels , and Rogue's equipments can only have up to 4 explicit modifiers; however, the Corrupted Gaze Atlas Passive Skill can cause Abyss Jewels to drop corrupted with up to six explicit mods. Maps can have 8 mods as a result of corruption.
Rarity | Rarities | Unique items have the same base stats as a normal item of the same type, but have specific names, unique artwork and set lists of modifiers instead of affixes. While the three preceding rarities are strictly better than the one before (e.g. rare items are always more powerful than magic items), this is not the case with unique items. They usually provide different and particular modifiers (sometimes thematically grouped) that can't be found on other items. Therefore they are considered to be more build-defining, granting effects that can be built around, but generally grant less pure stats than rare items.
Rarity | Increased Item Rarity | Players can boost their chances of finding higher rarity items with Increased Rarity of Items Found. This does not affect items without rarity, such as currency. Combining item rarity modifiers with item quantity modifiers is sometimes called Magic Find (MF), referring to the equivalent stats in Diablo.
Rarity | Increased Item Rarity | Rarity modifiers can apply to four multiplicative factors:
Rarity | Increased Item Rarity | Player rarity modifiers do not affect items dropped from chests. [4]
Rarity | Increased Item Rarity | Monster reward modifiers that convert loot into another type may be scaled by rarity modifiers, though scarab conversions do not appear to be. [5]
Rarity | Increased Item Rarity | When in a party, only the stats from the player credited with the kill are applied - multiple characters attacking a monster will not stack their item rarity bonuses. If a minion gets a kill, the summoner's IIR is used, in addition to IIR from Item Rarity Support. IIR on gear worn by minions (through Necromantic Aegis or Animate Guardian ) is never used. [6]
Rarity | Monster rarity | The rarity of a monster grants various multipliers to its base stats. Among the stats affected are life , damage , granted experience and flask charges, item quantity and rarity, and a reduced chance to flee. [7]
Rarity | Monster rarity | Rarity also causes monsters to drop items with a higher item level. Magic mobs drop items one level higher than the area, while rare and unique enemies drop items two levels higher.
Rarity | Magic monster modifiers | Increased statistics, and given one monster modifier. They appear in smaller groups. Magic monsters may also have Torment and/or Delirium modifiers.
Rarity | Magic monster modifiers | All magic monsters receive the following mods:
Rarity | Magic monster modifiers | Additionally magic monsters receive a life multiplier based on their level:
Rarity | Rare monster modifiers | Greatly increased statistics, and given two to four monster modifiers. They spawn by themselves, but multiple rares may still be close together. Rare monsters may also have Torment , Essence , Bestiary , and/or Delirium modifiers.
Rarity | Rare monster modifiers | All rare monsters receive the following mods:
Rarity | Rare monster modifiers | Additionally rare monsters receive a life multiplier based on their level:
Rarity | Unique monster modifiers | Unique Monsters that appear in certain areas, including bosses. Some unique monsters like Tormented Spirits and Rogue Exiles can spawn in most areas as well.
Rarity | Unique monster modifiers | All unique monsters receive the following mods:
Receiving damage | Description | The following is an overview of most steps involved in damage calculations. Receiving damage involves several steps to determine whether the damage hits , how much damage is dealt by the attacker, how much of that damage is prevented by the defender's mitigation, and what resources (e.g. life , energy shield ) are ultimately lost as a result.
Receiving damage | Order of operations | The list below displays the order of operations when an attacker attempts to damage a defender:
Receiving damage | Damage over time | Damage over Time generally follows the same principle, however this damage source doesn't hit , which means that it ignores evasion, armour , ward , and other mechanics limited to hits. Damage over time occurs at the start of each server frame, before potential hit damage, though after over-time recovery. [24]
Receiving damage | Damage over time | While damaging ailments are applied by hits, they have a separate base DPS calculation, starting from the flat damage of a hit. Hit-specific offensive modifiers will not apply to this calculation, nor will the defender's mitigation. This prevents debuffs like ignite from scaling twice with stats like #% increased Fire damage , or being reduced twice by fire resistance. Mitigation applies after the hit, over time, when damage is actually taken. (This includes immunities: physical immunity does not remove base damage for poison inflicted by a hit of mixed physical and chaos.)
Recoup | Description | Recoup is a keyword mechanic that recovers an amount of life , mana , or energy shield over time, based on the damage taken from a hit.
Recoup | Mechanics | The amount recoup recovers is based on a percentage of hit damage taken, calculated after mitigation such as resistance , though before mechanics that change how damage is applied (e.g. Ward , Steelskin , Petrified Blood , The Jinxed Juju , Dissolution of the Flesh ). [1] Recoup stacks; each instance is independent. [2]
Recoup | Mechanics | Recouping normally occurs over 4 seconds, meaning a value of 40% of Damage taken Recouped as Life recovers 10% of the damage taken per second. This duration may be modified through stats such as the Life Recoup Effects instead occur over 3 seconds Recovery Mastery passive, granting the same total recovery over an altered duration. Like other over-time recovery effects, modifiers to the player's overall recovery rate will scale recoup's recovery without lowering its duration.
Recoup | Mechanics | Recoup instances are not removed when the relevant resource is filled. They are unaffected by effect expiration modifiers such as Temporal Chains.
Recoup | Passive skills | Passive skills related to Recoup:
Recoup | Passive skills | Passive Mastery effects related to Recoup:
Recoup | Passive skills | Ascendancy skills related to Recoup:

Recoup | Mods | crafting bench veil mod:
Recoup | Jewels | Abyss Jewels can have 2-3% of damage taken recouped as mana as a prefix. Harvest (until version 3.19 which removes the craft) can give jewels 1% implicit recouped mana. During heist league the heist can drop jewel with the enchantment implicit that the same as the harvest implicit. This gives a theoretical maximum of 5% per Abyss jewel (and 2% per classic jewel, timeless jewel and cluster jewel by stacking the two implicits) in permanent leagues. Multiple jewels can stack these modifiers additively.
Recoup | Elevated | The following modifiers can only be obtained by using a Orb of Dominance on an influenced Body Armour which have at least two influenced mods, including an existing T1 damage taken as mod. Note that the orb remove one random influenced mod in the process and upgrade another influence mod. Moreover, all the damage taken as explicit mods are in the same mod group thus using the orb on legacy item that have two damage taken as mods, may remove the mod but not adding the new elevated mod.

Recovery | Description | Recovery refers to all positive changes to the current values of resources, most commonly life , mana , or energy shield. It is a catch-all term, not limited to specific mechanics. [1] [2] [3] The opposite of recovery is loss.
Recovery | Forms of recovery | There are many possible sources of recovery, for example: [4]
Recovery | Forms of recovery | While recovery from specific mechanics can be modified in general (e.g. #increased Life Recovery from Flasks ), modifiers that apply to a character are typically limited to over-time recovery by modifying Recovery rate , such as the of Smothering of Smothering Suffix 16% increased Quantity of Items found in this Area 9% increased Rarity of Items found in this Area 6% increased Pack size Players have 20% less Recovery Rate of Life and Energy Shield map modifier.
Recovery | Forms of recovery | Because modifiers to recovery rate do not apply to individual mechanics, but instead to the total value after all over-time recovery mechanics have been pooled together, they are multiplicative with more specific rate modifiers like #% increased Life Regeneration Rate. [5] They are also unaffected by caps on maximum recovery for specific mechanics, like leech.
Recovery | Forms of recovery | Note that modifiers to an entity's Recovery Rate modify over-time recovery (the amount gained) without lowering the duration of recovery effects. According to a GGG developer, this modifier was initially intended to be increased recovery per second , [ citation needed ] but was changed to the simpler (but technically wrong) Recovery rate. Recovery rate modifiers on Flasks and Flask Recovery Rate modifiers (e.g. Belly of the Beast , Herbalism ) do cause flask effects to recover the same total amount over a shorter period of time, however.
Recovery | Forms of recovery | When recovery and loss occur at the same time, over time, recovery is calculated first. [6] Instant recovery and loss generally have an order depending on the involved effects, except Gluttony of Elements.
Recovery | Recovery cap | While instant recovery is limited by the recoverable maximum, over-time recovery is limited by the same maximum in every 33ms server frame. This effectively 'caps' meaningful over-time recovery to 30 times the recoverable maximum per second. This is unaffected by over-time loss / damage ; over-time recovery and over-time loss are independent events. [7] [8]

Reflecting Mist (interactable object) | Description | A Reflecting Mist (or Reflective Mist ) is a type of interactable mechanic first introduced in the Kalandra league. It has a chance to appear in tier 16 and 17 maps.
Reflecting Mist (interactable object) | Description | Upon killing a specific monster pack in an area where a Reflecting Mist will appear, it will appear as a misty mirror on a column of basalt. Once it appears, an icon will display on the minimap. Interacting with it will result in one of two outcomes: displaying a menu which generate a pair of Reflected items, or dropping a Reflecting Mist currency item.
Reflecting Mist (interactable object) | Reflected item | The Mist offers a choice between two Reflected mirrored Rare rings or amulets with unusual modifiers. Some are scaled-up versions of existing modifiers, while others are strong negative versions of the same modifier. The rings provide inverse stats to each other; a negative mod on one ring is positive on the other. Only one ring can be chosen. The modifier multiplier magnitude is randomly chosen between 1.4x to 2.5x in 0.1 increments and applies to all modifiers with scaleable values. The modifiers are heavily skewed against a fully negative/positive result.
Reflecting Mist (interactable object) | Reflected item | For a list of modifiers that are not simply negative values of their regular versions, see List of inverted modifiers.
Reflecting Mist (interactable object) | Reflected item | Sometimes, it may offer a ring base-type originally exclusive to the Lake of Kalandra which grant alternate effects based on which ring slot they are equipped into:
Reflecting Mist (interactable object) | Reflected item | These rings come Rare and Mirrored. They can be vendored 5-to-1 at any vendor to obtain a craftable, non-mirrored version.
Reflecting Mist (interactable object) | Reflecting Mist currency | The Mist drops a currency item also called a Reflecting Mist , allowing the player to choose a Rare ring or amulet to reflect. See the item page for specific details.

Repeat | Description | Repeating is a potential behaviour of skills. When you use a skill that repeats, you pay one cost and consume one cooldown , but play the animation (and thus cause the effects of the skill) an additional time for each repeat. [1]
Repeat | Mechanics | Skills that repeat will cause the player to perform multiple skill animations, counting as a single skill use. [2] Accordingly, repeats share the same critical strike roll, are usually performed with the same weapon when attacking while dual wielding , [3] [4] and modifiers like when you Attack / when you Cast a Spell occur only once. Repeating is not inherently faster than using a skill a second time, though most sources of repeat do provide speed bonuses.
Repeat | Mechanics | Most skills do not repeat by default, but can be made to repeat using support gems (e.g. Spell Echo Support , Multistrike Support ), passives ( Fatal Flourish ), or buffs ( Echoing Shrine ). Stats and items may interact specifically with repeats, such as Plume of Pursuit.
Repeat | Mechanics | Note that although similar, Unleash Support and Awakened Unleash Support cause effects to "reoccur", which is not a repeat mechanic.
Repeat | Mechanics | The following types of skills or portions of skills never repeat:
Repeat | Mechanics | Skills that repeat cannot be exerted.
Repeat | Skill-specific interactions | Some mechanics are limited per use of a skill, such as gaining charges from Power Charge On Critical Support and Flicker Strike , or gaining Trauma from Boneshatter. Repeating does not circumvent these limits, as repeats are still the same skill use.
Repeat | Skill-specific interactions | Vaal skills can repeat if 2+ charges are available, consumes charges per repeat. Vaal skills with only 1 charge available do not repeat.
Repeat | Skill-specific interactions | Support gems linked to minion skills will cause both the summoning skill and skills used by its minions to repeat, if applicable.
Repeat | Skill-specific interactions | Most movement skills like Flame Dash , Whirling Blades , Dash , and Leap Slam repeat in the same direction as the initial skill use. Shield Charge also repeats in the same direction, but only the hit final AOE slam portion, not the movement itself. Note travel skills cannot be supported by Multistrike Support.
Repeat | Attacks | Ruthless Blows from Ruthless Support occur on every third attack (skill use), rather than on every third repeat. This means that when supported by Multistrike Support , the 7th, 8th, and 9th hit will be Ruthless, not the 3rd, 6th, and 9th. [5]
Repeat | Related base stats | The following skill gems have stats related to repeat :
Repeat | Related quality stats | The following skill gems have stats from quality related to repeat :
Repeat | Related base stats | The following support gems have stats related to repeat :
Repeat | Related quality stats | The following support gems have stats from quality related to repeat :
Repeat | Related quality stats | There are no support gems that have stats from quality related to repeat.

Reservation | Description | Reservation is a method of using a resource, typically mana or life , to pay for auras , herald skills, buffs, mine skills, or any skill with an ongoing effect. Some items may also reserve resources. Rather than paying the cost once as with normal skills, a portion of the resource is set aside as unusable for as long as the skill is active. Reserving a resource does not affect its maximum, so percentage modifiers such as Regenerate 1% of Maximum Life are unaffected when you reserve life, for example.
Reservation | Description | Reserved resource values from Skills are multiplied by support gem cost & reservation multipliers as usual. The Blood Magic Keystone and Arrogance Support will cause skills that usually reserve Mana to reserve Life instead.
Reservation | Reservation Efficiency | Reservation Efficiency (RE) is a modifier that can modify the reservation of one or several Skill reservations. The total of all Increased Reservation Efficiency modifiers whether from passives , jewels , or items , is summed before being applied. It uses the following formula:
Reservation | Reservation Efficiency | Resource Reserved = Base Reserve % 100 % + Total Reserve Efficiency % \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\text{Resource Reserved}}={\dfrac {{\text{Base Reserve }}\%}{100\%+{\text{Total Reserve Efficiency }}\%}}
Reservation | Reservation Efficiency | Reservation multipliers such as that granted by Enlighten Support are multiplicative with reductions from Reservation Efficiency. Modifiers to cost , such as Inspiration Support and Elreon's mod will not have any effect on reservation.
Reservation | Reservation Efficiency | A reduced reservation efficiency of 100% or higher would cause skills to have infinite reservation, making the player unable to use any reservation skills.
Reservation | Reservation Efficiency | Blessing skills can remove an aura's reservation, with some caveats.
Reservation | Reservation Efficiency | Reservation Efficiency does not affect reservation effects that do not come from a skill, such as Midnight Bargain and Blood Price

Resistance | Description | Resistance modifies the amount of damage taken from elemental ( fire , cold , or lightning ) or chaos damage. It can be changed with equipment, passives, buffs/debuffs, and other modifiers.
Resistance | Description | Resistances work separately from damage reduction and are not treated as such.
Resistance | Mechanics | Resistance reduces or increases the amount of damage taken from certain damage types , whether it is a hit or damage over time. It is calculated after damage avoidance and before damage reduction effects.
Resistance | Mechanics | All entities have resistance values. Player resistances can be viewed in the Defence tab in the Character panel (default hotkey C ). An estimate of enemy resistances are indicated by icons beneath their life bars.
Resistance | Mechanics | Modifiers which affect "elemental resistance" apply to fire, cold, and lightning resistances equally. Sources of elemental resistance will not apply to chaos resistance, but sources that affect "all resistances" will apply to elemental and chaos resistances. Physical resistance does not exist.
Resistance | Mechanics | Resistances have a default maximum of 75%. Having resistances above the maximum will not provide any further reduction to damage, though some mechanics will consider excess resistance values (See Uncapped resistances and Overcapped resistances ). Maximum resistance can be increased with sources of +#% to Maximum [Type] Resistance(s) , up to a hard limit of 90%.
Resistance | Mechanics | Negative resistances are hard capped at -200%. [1] The effects of x% reduced Resistance(s) is capped at 100%.
Resistance | Damage mitigation | Resistances mitigates the incoming damage according to
Resistance | Damage mitigation | dmg red = ( 1 − Resistance ) ∗ dmg \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\begin{aligned}{\text{dmg}}_{\text{red}}&=(1-{\text{Resistance}})*{\text{dmg}}\end{aligned}}
Resistance | Damage mitigation | where dmg red is the damage after reduction, Res is the character's resistance and dmg is the initial damage.
Resistance | Damage mitigation | The damage ratio between a character with -60% resistance and a character with 75% resistance that are hit with same amount of damage is
Resistance | Damage mitigation | 1 − ( − 0.6 ) 1 − 0.75 = 6.4 \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\begin{aligned}{{1-(-0.6)} \over {1-0.75}}&=6.4\end{aligned}}
Resistance | Resistance reduction | Resistances can be reduced through various debuffs or modifiers. Curses and exposure are the primary methods of reducing resistances. Resistances can go below 0%, and have a hard cap of -200%.
Resistance | Resistance reduction | A permanent penalty to all resistances (including Chaos Resistance) is applied to player characters depending on their progression in the story. It is not possible to avoid this penalty before entering the Epilogue and maps.
Resistance | Resistance inversion | Effects that treat resistances as inverted will multiply the target's capped resistances by -1. The higher the enemy's resistance value, the more benefit inversion will provide. Conversely, this modifier against an enemy with negative resistances will cause it to be treated as if it had positive resistances. Inverted resistances are still subject to maximum/minimum resistance caps.
Resistance | Resistance penetration | Only hits can penetrate resistances. Penetration is applied as damage is dealt, after other resistance calculations. Penetration applies to capped resistance value, so an enemy with 75% capped resistances against a hit with 30% penetration will take damage as if they had 45% resistances. [2]
Resistance | Resistance penetration | Negative resistances are capped at -200%, but penetration can exceed this value as it does not directly modify the target's resistances.
Resistance | Resistance penetration | "Reverse penetration", typically in the format of Your Hits treat X Resistance as #% higher than actual value , is additive with penetration values.
Resistance | Ignore resistances | Stats that grant the ability to ignore resistances prevent resistances from being calculated in the damage formula but do not affect the enemy's actual resistance stats. Mathematically, ignored resistances can be treated as always 0% and discards any further resistance increases or reductions, inversions, or penetration. This modifier can result in a damage loss if the ignored resistance was already negative.
Resistance | Uncapped resistances | In-game alt text: Uncapped Resistance is the value Resistance would have if ignoring Maximum Resistance
Resistance | Uncapped resistances | The sum of all resistance stats from equipment, passives, etc. is considered "uncapped resistances". This value does include the -30%/-60% penalty from completing Act 5/10. Only resistances up to the maximum resistance value provide damage mitigation; the uncapped values are only used for calculating other effects that ignore your maximum resistance caps like The Wise Oak.
Resistance | Uncapped resistances | Resistance reductions such as curses and exposure directly affect uncapped resistance values.
Resistance | Overcapped resistances | In-game alt text: Overcapped Resistance is the amount by which Uncapped Resistance is higher than Maximum Resistance
Resistance | Overcapped resistances | Overcapped resistances are your total resistances that exceed your maximum resistance value. Only resistances up to a player's maximum resistances will provide damage mitigation but overcapped resistances serve as a buffer against resistance reduction such as curses and exposure before they can reduce your resistances below your maximum resistances. It can be calculated by subtracting the uncapped resistances (on the left) from the maximum resistances (on the right) in the player's character stats menu. Overcapped values are also used for calculating other modifiers such as The Formless Flame.
Resistance | Increased/Reduced resistances | Modifiers that increase or reduce resistances by a percentage, e.g. X% Reduced Elemental Resistances are multiplicative against your uncapped resistances. Note that this mod is distinctly different from mods like -X% to Elemental Resistances [3]. There is a cap at 100% reduced Resistances (permanently setting your resistance to 0 and causing it to be unable to be modified further other than penetration [4]. As reduced resistance modifiers cause your resistances to become less negative or less positive, they are detrimental for builds that use Doryani's Prototype or stack additional maximum resistances as they increase the investment required to reach the desired caps. This modifier is additive with other sources of X% increased or reduced Elemental Resistances. [5]
Resistance | Increased/Reduced resistances | The modifier X% Less Elemental Resistances works similarly but is multiplicative with itself and other sources, not additive. [6]
Resistance | Increased/Reduced resistances | To calculate the required resistances, use the formula y = ab (x - 60) where y = the maximum cap of the resist, a = sum of all % Increased/Reduced Resist modifiers as decimal, b = % More/Less Resist modifiers as decimal, and x being the required actual resistances on gear, auras, etc. The -60 refers to the resistance penalty from Acts.
Resistance | Increased/Reduced resistances | For example, a build with 75% maximum resistance, 70% Reduced Resistances , and 55% Less Resistances would be calculated: 75 = 0.3 * 0.45 (x - 60); x = +477% resistances is required to hit 75% of that resist (from -60%).
Resistance | Maximum resistances | Each resistance has the following default cap:
Resistance | Maximum resistances | Maximum resistances can be increased or reduced to hard caps of 90% or -200% respectively. Exceeding these values will not provide additional benefits/downsides, but do provide a buffer against further modification (for example, a character with +20% maximum resistances from items will effectively go from 75% to 90% max res, and can ignore up to 5% max res reduction from debuffs and/or map modifiers before the max res value is reduced below 90%).
Resistance | Maximum resistances | There are various ways to alter the maximum resistances:

Resistance penetration | Description | Resistance penetration is a stat for hit damage that lowers the target's effective resistance to specific damage types for the purpose of damage calculations. The target's actual resistance value itself is untouched. [1]
Resistance penetration | Mechanics | When a target takes a hit with resistance penetration, that target's effective resistance is lowered for determining the amount of damage dealt by the hit. Resistance penetration does not modify the target's resistance or maximum resistance stats , only the hit's damage calculation.
Resistance penetration | Mechanics | The target's effective resistance to damage type t \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}t is
Resistance penetration | Mechanics | where r t \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}r_{t} is the target's resistance to damage type t \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}t , m t \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}m_{t} is the target's maximum resistance to damage type t \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}t , and p t \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}p_{t} is the resistance penetration of the hit for damage type t \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}t.
Resistance penetration | Mechanics | Just like resistance stats, effective resistance can be a negative number. There is no minimum limit on effective resistance imposed by the game mechanics. [2] It is not affected by the -200% cap on actual resistances. [3]
Resistance penetration | Mechanics | Due to the fact that resistance penetration is a property of hits, it cannot apply to damage over time. [4]
Resistance penetration | Mechanics | Penetration functions against a specific resistance, not for a specific damage type. For example, chaos penetration would do nothing for Hexblast 's chaos damage if that chaos damage is resisted by fire resistance. Fire penetration would apply. [5]
Resistance penetration | Mechanics | Penetration with a negative value is worded Your Hits treat X Resistance as #% higher than actual value and raises the target's effective resistance instead. It is additive with regular penetration, and affected by the same mechanics, such as Abhorrent Interrogation 's Your Hits cannot Penetrate. [6]
Resistance penetration | Efficacy of resistance penetration versus resistances | It can be shown that resistance penetration is more effective in terms of damage dealt against targets with higher resistances.
Resistance penetration | Efficacy of resistance penetration versus resistances | The percentage increase to damage type t \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}t as a result of resistance penetration is
Ritual | Description | Rituals are encounters that spawn from Ritual Altars. After activating the Altar, players must defeat the enemies enclosed within the Ritual Circle, gaining Tribute in the process. Players can then spend the earned Tribute to purchase various types of rewards including pre-identified rare items. Tribute gained is tied to the area and does not carry over to Ritual Altars found in other areas.
Ritual | Description | This encounter is considered Extra Content and has a baseline greater than 8% chance to appear in any non-unique map area.
Ritual | Mechanics | Ritual Altars can be randomly encountered while playing through the campaign (guaranteed first encounter in The Northern Forest in Act 2 ) and have a baseline greater than 8% chance to randomly spawn in any end-game map. The amount of Altars that appear in each instance is either three or four. All of the Altars in an instance are part of the same set: same type , spawn pool and reward pool. Rituals will typically also spawn additional packs of monsters from the Viridian Wildwood.
Ritual | Mechanics | Small, moving blood pools will appear under killed enemies that count towards the ritual when activated. Luring monsters into a ritual circle will not add them to the encounter (except the map bosses); they must have already been tied to that ritual when the map was opened. Monsters spawned by shrines , Delirium , Legion , Niko encounters, Tormented Spirits , Rogue Exiles , and Hunted Traitors can be revived by a ritual if they spawn near an altar. Other monsters from league mechanics cannot be revived.
Ritual | Mechanics | The amount of tribute earned from killing the monsters during the encounter depends on the monster's rarity, and how many times it has appeared in a ritual in the current map:
Ritual | Mechanics | It is important to note that the rarities of monsters spawned at a ritual altar is not always equivalent to the rarities of monsters that were killed for that ritual. (i.e. even if you kill exclusively normal monsters before activating the ritual altar, the ritual encounter itself will still be able to spawn magic or rare monsters. Likewise, the monster modifiers of slain magic or rare monsters are not preserved when revived in a ritual.)
Ritual | Mechanics | Summoned minions (e.g. Undead minions spawned by Necromancers or adds spawned by map bosses) do not get added to the monster pool, and minions summoned during an encounter provide no tribute when killed.
Ritual | Mechanics | Players can use the Ritual Rewards button to view the number of rituals in the area, number of completed rituals and the reward pool.
Ritual | Rewards | After completing a ritual, players can click the Altar to display the Favours interface that allows players to select their own rewards, in exchange for Tribute points. Tribute points do not carry over between zones; if you can't afford an item, you can Defer the item to pay part of its cost (with fees) and have it appear again later.
Ritual | Rewards | Tip: It makes sense to complete all altars before deciding what to spend tribute on. If you do this then you will have maximum knowledge before making your choices - you will know how many points you have and all visible options.
Ritual | Ritual-exclusive rewards | Default Ritual rewards include:
Ritual | Generic rewards | Special Reward Rituals (ones that resemble the Gore Portal Effect microtransaction) cause the entire window to only contain Divination Cards , Currency , or Unique items. Rerolling in this scenario will always return a Special Reward window.
Ritual | Deferring rewards | Deferring allows players to mark rare rewards that they cannot presently afford with the Tribute they have, and those same items will re-appear in a later ritual.
Ritual | Deferring rewards | It is recommended to keep at least 2000 tribute after rerolling a window to be able to ensure the most expensive rewards can be deferred, which is approximately 20,000 tribute at original cost.
Ritual | Ritual variations | Ritual Altars spawn in various types, listed below. Each type has different modifiers, giving a different set of buffs to enemies and environment effects.
Ritual | Ritual variations | Altars which use the Gore Portal Effect model, are surrounded by a fence, and change the hue of the environment when active are considered "Ritual Altars with Special Rewards", or a "Special Ritual". These rituals have rewards all of the same type per reward window refresh, either all Unique items, currency , or divination cards except the Vaal Ritual , which alters the rewards in a different way.
Ritual | Ritual variations | The Nameless Ritual can appear in Tier 14+ Maps [3] and is also considered a Special Ritual. Unlike the other Special Rituals, however, it has a unique, taller version of a regular altar, and the King in the Mists 's voicelines are played when interacting with these rituals. Additionally, its rewards are exclusively a guaranteed An Audience With The King and various Ritual-exclusive rewards such as Ritual Splinters, Ritual base types, and Corpse items. It has an estimated 1.5%-2% baseline chance to appear. [4]
Runic | Description | Runic monsters are encountered in Expedition. They spawn from the large skulls on spikes and have the Runic tag. In addition to being more difficult than regular monsters, they are affected by the modifiers of remnants which have been triggered before they spawned. Runic monsters also have Ward.
Runic | Description | One unique runic monster is a shield mob which will be directionally immune to damage when their shield is up. They can be damaged either by attacking from behind or moving close to the monster which will cause it to drop its shield.
Ruthless mode | Description | Ruthless mode, also known as Hard Mode , is a character creation flag that significantly increases the difficulty and changes the playstyle of the game by opting-in to extreme item scarcity and various other changes.
Ruthless mode | Description | Named after the historical Ruthless difficulty from Closed Beta , it employs item scarcity and shifts of relative item values to simulate the Path of Exile experience in the early days (without the desync). This mode is meant to be intentionally brutally difficult, where reaching higher acts is an achievement, and traditionally weak items are felt as valuable. For example, a player may have difficulty equipping a full set of items by Act 4. Most items found will be normal rarity, and crafting currency will be extremely rare.
Ruthless mode | Description | This mode was designed as a pet project of Chris Wilson and other senior developers over 18 months. Features of Ruthless mode will have little to no impact on the core gameplay of the rest of the game. It is intended as a testing ground for radical changes and experiments. A change in Ruthless does not indicate that the change will also be made in the regular game. [1]
Ruthless mode | Description | Ruthless Mode can also be enabled alongside other difficulty enhancing game modes like Solo Self-Found or Hardcore , for extra challenge. (Non-Ruthless leagues are colloquially called ' Bench '.)
Ruthless mode | Description | Ruthless mode is best for those that want to experiment or relive a longer and slower Path of Exile that closely resembles its older iterations and game design principles.
Ruthless mode | Overview | Ruthless can be selected by ticking a checkbox in the character selection screen. This mode is available for selection at any time after creating an initial character on an account. A Ruthless character can only be created on initial character creation. Unlike SSF , Ruthless characters cannot be migrated into a non-Ruthless league , and Hardcore characters get deleted on death in ruthless.
Ruthless mode | Overview | Ruthless characters will play in a separate League with their own ladder.
Ruthless mode | Brief comparison of changes | Compared to the Base Game , the following are the main TL;DR differences to expect in terms of added, removed or reworked game mechanics. [2]
Ruthless mode | Brief list of added or buffed content in Ruthless | Full detailed list of changes can be seen below.

Ruthless mode | League content changes | This almost guarantees that when extra content appears on your map, it has a high probability to be Alva, with a small chance of the other 3 masters appearing.

Ruthless mode | Master Changes | Masters have received several changes in their reward systems:
Ruthless mode | Master Changes | Beastcrafting rewards have been completely reworked; they provide crafts for Talismans , flask enchantments , etc. Bestiary Orb now costs 1x Orb of Chance from Einhar instead of 1x Chaos Orb. Ruthless bestiary recipes can be seen on on poedb.tw.
Ruthless mode | Master Changes | Fractured walls in the Azurite Mine are now more likely to contain deposits of Azurite and Resonators rather than reward chests. Nodes that contain <damage type> items provide fossils instead of rare items. Chaotic Resonators have been replaced by their equivalent Alchemical Resonators.
Ruthless mode | Master Changes | Incursion modifier items cannot be obtained. Tier 3 Room special chests (e.g. " Contains a Valuable item ") can contain sacrifice fragments. The area level for the Temple of Atzoatl in Ruthless is the average level of all your Incursions.
Ruthless mode | Master Changes | Members of the Immortal Syndicate no longer drop non-unique veiled items. The rewards for each member in safehouses have been reworked. The area level for Betrayal Safehouses is now the average level of areas Betrayal progress was made in. This does not apply to the Mastermind's Lair.
Ruthless mode | Master Changes | Kirac Missions' highest map tiers are equal to or lower than the highest tier map you have completed, within the tier bracket (1-5, 6-10, 11-16). After a certain amount of progress into the Atlas, his map vendor options will generally only provide maps of lower tiers than the highest tier you have completed. Additionally, Orb of Unmaking now costs 1x Orb of Chance from Kirac instead of 2x Orb of Regret , and Cartographer's Chisel no longer get offered for purchase.

Sacrifice Set | Description | The Sacrifice Set represents a complete set of four map fragments: Sacrifice at Dusk , Sacrifice at Dawn , Sacrifice at Noon and Sacrifice at Midnight. When each is placed in the map device in the correct configuration, these fragments will open portals to the Atziri encounter in the Apex of Sacrifice.
Sacrifice Set | Description | The drop rates of 4 fragments themselves are not equal. Extra fragments can be used along with a map to add quantity to the map drop. A single fragment can also be used to open 6 portals to a random vaal side areas.
Sacrifice Set | Trade | The Sacrifice Set cannot be obtained as a standalone item. However, items listed for trade in premium stash tabs can be priced in whole sets. As specified by the official trade website , the following code can be used to list items for trade, priced at n complete sets:
Sacrifice Set | Trade | ~price n sacrifice-set
Sacrifice Set | Trivia | The visual design of the Sacrifice Set likely references the Aztec sun stone. The Vaal are generally modelled after the Aztec.
Scourge | Description | Scourge encounters were a game mechanic introduced in the Scourge leagues. After the challenge leagues ended, Scourge wasn't integrated in the core game. Instead, it was later merged into Beyond.
Scourge | Overview | In the Scourge leagues, players encountered The Last to Die , who offered the character the Blood Crucible. The Blood Crucible fills with the blood of slain monsters. Once it reaches a threshold, the device can be activated, which transports the character into a parallel reality. This version of Wraeclast is inhabited by demons known as The Scourge. When the Blood Crucible's blood runs out, or if the player chooses to go back, the character is instantly shifted back to normal reality.
Scourge | Overview | Equipment can be placed into the Blood Crucible. After killing enough Scourge Demons, the item can be transformed (Scourged). It becomes corrupted and gains two Scourge modifiers , which are in addition to the regular implicit and explicit mods. The Scourge modifiers will consist of one beneficial and one detrimental mod. A Scourged item can be put into the Blood Crucible a second time and third time, each increasing the power of the Scourged modifiers. The Blood Crucible works on already corrupted items.
Scourge | Overview | Maps can also be placed into the Blood Crucible after certain upgrades.
Scourge | Nightmare | Nightmare refers to the realm of the Beyond demons. Modifiers affecting "Monsters in Nightmare" refer to any monster while within the Scourge realm; this wording also refers to any monsters in a map affected by Niko's Memory of Chasms or its associated Kirac mission.
Scourge | Bosses | Three Unique boss enemies can spawn in the Nightmare realm. The boss encountered depends on the type of enemies in that map. When encountered, the Blood Gauge pauses for 5 seconds during the spawning animation, and every time the boss lost 5% of its life (refreshes each time; the time does not accumulate). By default, only up to one boss can spawn in a map, but a specific Scourged map modifier can allow spawning multiple of the same boss in that map. Defeating Scourge bosses will cause several Tainted currencies and Scourged items to drop, including Scourged Unique items with two positive and two negative modifiers. Defeating a Scourge boss also has a chance to drop a Viscera Cauldron , which granted a third equipment slot for the Crucible.
Scourge | Scourge rewards | Scourge demons can drop Tainted currency. These items can modify corrupted items, which usually can't be altered with currency.
Scourge | Scourge rewards | Note that although Tainted Blessing is introduced in the same patch, but it is a core drop.
Self-damage | Description | Self-damage refers to damage the player deals to themselves through certain skills or items, generally without requiring an enemy or hazard. Unlike effects that cause pure loss , self-damage can be mitigated. Self-damage that isn't over time hits , and may inflict ailments , be recouped , or contribute to Cast when Damage Taken Support.
Self-damage | Reflected damage | Note: reflected damage does not trigger on/when hit effects. It can contribute to prevented damage and damage taken for effects like Cast when Damage Taken Support.
Sentinel | Description | Sentinels are a type of interactable mechanic first introduced in the Sentinel league and occasionally appear in high-tier maps.
Sentinel | Mechanics | Sentinels have a chance to appear in tier 16 and 17 maps. A Sentinel with random modifiers will spawn near the starting portal. Players can interact with it to repair it, granting the ability to deploy it in that area by clicking on the button or using the corresponding hotkey.
Sentinel | Mechanics | When a Sentinel is deployed, it will follow the player around for a duration, firing beams at nearby monsters to empower them. Monsters recover to full life when gaining Empowerment. Empowerment increases damage dealt and reduces damage taken by the monster, but also increases the experience, item rarity, and item quantity of the monster when killed. Empowering an enemy also has a chance for it to gain an additional reward, displayed by an icon over them.
Sentinel | Mechanics | The Sentinel will disappear once it has empowered a set number of enemies, is dismissed manually, when the Sentinel's duration expires, or if the player dies or leaves the instance.
Sentinel | Types of Sentinels | There are three types of Sentinels:
Sentinel | Types of Sentinels | Red Stalker Sentinels fire beams periodically to empower enemies.
Sentinel | Types of Sentinels | Blue Pandemonium Sentinels fire a beam only once, chaining to multiple enemies. Unlike the other types, they deplete after firing their beam once, even if it didn't get to empower the maximum number of enemies.
Sentinel | Types of Sentinels | Yellow Apex Sentinels fire a beam to empower enemies, but only target Rare and Unique monsters.
Sentinel | List of Sentinels | Sentinels can have different base types, which determine their duration, number of monsters it can empower, and the strength of the empowerment. (The amount of charges it has is no longer relevant.)
Sentinel | List of Unique Sentinels | Unique sentinels were only available in Sentinel league and cannot be found in the game currently.
Sentinel | In Sentinel league | In Sentinel league , Sentinels could be found as items dropped by enemies and from Sentinel Caches. The first Sentinel Cache you open with your character will drop a Sentinel Controller , giving you access to the Sentinel Controller, which is used to upgrade your Sentinels, and adding Sentinel equipment slots. You can equip one of each type of Sentinel.
Sentinel | In Sentinel league | Sentinels drop as unidentified and are Unmodifiable. Sentinels also have a limited number of times they can be deployed. There is no way to add charges to a Sentinel.
Sentinel | In Sentinel league | Sentinels can be deployed most types of zones except unique maps.
Sentinel | Sentinel Controller | The Sentinel Controller interface, unlocked after using the Sentinel Controller , allows you to allocate passive bonuses to Sentinels by making connections between Runic Nodes by placing Filaments. Most Runic Nodes require only one Filament; larger Runic Nodes require two Filaments, and Sentinel Slots require three Filaments. The number of Filaments required also represents the number of power units used. Killing enemies empowered by Sentinels grant experience towards unlocking additional power units, starting at 4 up to a maximum of 30 power units at max experience. Filaments can be placed and removed freely without any cost. The Sentinel Controller configuration can be changed anywhere, but the changes will not apply until you enter a new instance and will not affect your Sentinels in the current instance.
Sentinel | Power Core | A Power Core allows you to combine two Sentinels (regardless of charges left) to create a new, fully charged Sentinel. The Sentinel will receive a combination of mods from both components, with a chance for unpredictable changes. Certain Sentinel base types can only be created with Power Cores. There are four different types of Power Cores: Power Core , Transforming Power Core , Augmenting Power Core , Amplifying Power Core.
Shatter | Description | Monsters who are killed by hits while frozen shatter , leaving no corpse behind. Unique bosses cannot shatter. The on-death effects of many monsters will not occur if they are shattered, such as that of the Porcupine Goliath.
Shatter | Mechanics | Non-unique enemies that are killed while frozen shatter into pieces. They will still leave loot, but most other on-death effects are prevented, including:
Shatter | Mechanics | These on-death effects are not suppressed:
Shatter | Mechanics | Kills from damage over time will not shatter enemies. Only hits can cause shatter. [1] Culling strike is recommended for damage over time builds that are able to freeze enemies to be able to shatter enemies.
Shrine | Description | Shrines are special objects that apply an effect to nearby monsters or cast spells at nearby players. Interacting them allows the player to temporarily steal their power for themselves. This mechanic is also referred to as Domination.
Shrine | Description | Shrines are considered a form of Extra Content.
Shrine | Mechanics | Shrines can appear randomly in most areas. Shrines are often surrounded by a pack of monsters guarding it. Initially, shrines will only buff enemies and damage players. When touched, the shrine's effect is removed and given to the player for 45 seconds (20 seconds for Divine Shrines) in the form of a status effect. Shrine effects will either buff the player (but not their allies ) or cast spells that damage enemies. A player can be affected by multiple different shrine effects.
Shrine | Mechanics | Shrine effect duration and buff effect can be modified with certain items and passives.
Shrine | Mechanics | Certain effects from shrines, namely effect that deal with on death effects, are symmetrical. For example, enemies near an Apparition Shrine have a chance to drop influenced items on death, as do monsters killed by the player while they have the Apparition Shrine buff effect on them.
Shrine | Mechanics | There are two kinds of shrines: Buff (green border) and Spell (blue border); Buff shrines grants buffs to affected monsters, players, the player's nearby party members. Spell shrines cast spells around themselves or affected players, but do not originate from the player and thus are unaffected by their mods. All buff shrine effects are affected by buff duration and effect modifiers.
Shrine | Mechanics | Right-clicking on the status icon will remove the shrine effect.
Shrine | Lesser shrines | Lesser shrines do not spawn naturally and are generated by the Create Lesser Shrine skill from The Gull. Unlike regular shrines, they have no ongoing effects before being touched and disappear after 10 seconds, which can be modified with duration modifiers. Touching a lesser shrine grants a buff to the player for 20 seconds. Lesser Shrine buffs are also affected by Shrine buff effect and duration modifiers.
Shrine | Cycling shrine buffs | Sources of the mod Gain a random shrine buff every 10 seconds ( Harmony of Purpose , Runesmithing staff enchantment) select a random shrine buff from the above list every 10 seconds. The shrine buff is removed if the source granting it is removed. The base duration of each buff is 10 seconds. Increasing the duration through applicable modifiers allows several shrine buffs acquired this way to be active simultaneously. Note that some of the shrine buffs might not apply in all areas, such as low-level campaign areas.
Shrine | Cycling shrine buffs | If this grants the effects of a Freezing, Lightning, or Skeletal Shrine, it will grant their Greater versions instead.
Shrine | Cycling shrine buffs | In maps, small-sample testing [1] suggests the following rough tentative distribution of weights for the different buffs:
Shrine | List of special Shrines | These shrines only appear from certain effects that spawn them and cannot be chosen by modifiers that grant random shrine buffs (except Greater shrine buffs).
Shrine | Lesser | These shrines are produced by the Create Lesser Shrine skill, available from The Gull. Alternatively, Blunderbore also grants two of these Lesser Shrines.
Shrine | Greater | Greater shrine effects are not granted by shrines and can only appear from effects that grant random shrine buffs (i.e. cycling shrine buffs, The Golden Charlatan )), replacing their regular counterparts.
Shrine | Scarab | This shrine can appear in maps with an Domination Scarab of Evolution applied to it.
Shrine | Scarab | These shrines can appear in maps with an Domination Scarab of Apparitions applied to it. The shrines themselves are guarded by apparitions of the respective Elderslayers or God-touched monsters.
Shrine | Atlas | Allocating the All That Glitters Atlas passive node provides a 10% chance for each shrine in your maps to instead be a Covetous Shrine.

Smuggler | Description | Smuggler is a faction in the world of Wraeclast. This faction has its own tilesets Smuggler's Den and Underbelly , which are the locations of a heist or grand heist.
Smuggler | Lore | The name "Smuggler" is routinely mentioned in the Azurite Mine node Smuggler's Stash , which spawns up to 6 rogue exiles as node bosses, as well as in the name of Tormented Smuggler , a type of tormented spirit.
Smuggler | Lore | The smugglers became a full faction of its own in the Heist league , which has its own monster types and tilesets: Smuggler's Den and Underbelly. In maps, players can also find Smuggler's Cache , which drops Contracts and Blueprints. The dropped Contracts and Blueprints are not limited to Smuggler's Den and Underbelly tilesets, however.
Smuggler | Lore | Commander Kirac refers to this faction as "criminal" when debriefing for Heist atlas missions :
Smuggler | Lore | Contract: The Slaver King uses Smuggler's Den tilesets. However, it's unknown if Friedrich Tarollo is one of the leaders of the smugglers. In the lore of Contract: The Slaver King unique quest contract, Tarollo is a slave trader.
Smuggler | Lore | Underbelly tileset does not have its own unique heist contract.
Snapshot | Description | Snapshotting is a term that describes creating effects or states with values based on your current stats, that do not update if your stats change later. It is mostly removed in the modern game, outside bugs or debuffs. [1]
Snapshot | Mechanics | When something is snapshotted, it will not change its values based on stat changes that occur later. For example:
Snapshot | Mechanics that snapshot | Some effects apply to entire uses of a skill, such as critical strike rolls, exerting with warcries or Ambush , Ruthless Blows from Ruthless Support , Intensity stacks, or Master Distiller. These are not related to changing stats, and should not be considered snapshotting.
Solo Self-Found | Description | Solo Self-Found (SSF) is a character creation flag that marks a character to be unable to interact with other characters, which disables features like trading or partying. [1]
Solo Self-Found | Overview | Solo Self-Found can be selected by ticking a checkbox in the character selection screen. A SSF character can only be created on initial character creation, but the SSF flag can be removed from a character at any time by migrating it into the corresponding trade league.
Solo Self-Found | Overview | SSF characters will play in a separate league with their own ladder. Together with the flag, this results in the following restrictions:
Solo Self-Found | Overview | If the character is no longer SSF, it will be transferred to the non-SSF parent league permanently and the highest level reached within the ladder will be retained, however any further progress will not be accounted for.
Solo Self-Found | Overview | It is also possible to migrate all characters and league progress to the non-SSF parent league.
Solo Self-Found | Strategy | Since it is not possible to trade or interact with other players, it is of utmost importance that a SSF character (especially the first in a league) is able to clear all act bosses on its own and is able to survive without specific items.
Solo Self-Found | History | Solo self-found historically existed in an unofficial form based on honour. Characters intended to be SSF would usually have the letters "SSF" somewhere in the name, and unofficial player run ladder websites could be used to enter and track players. [2] Official SSF restrictions and ladders were added in version 2.6.0.
Spell suppression | Description | Spell Suppression is a type of mitigation associated with dexterity. By default, it provides a chance to lower the damage of hits and ailments inflicted by spells by 40%.
Spell suppression | Mechanics | Characters do not have any base chance to suppress spells. It can be obtained from various sources, typically associated with dexterity or evasion: for example from passive skills in the Shadow/Ranger areas of the passive tree, rolled randomly on evasion armour, and directly from dexterity with the Magebane keystone.
Spell suppression | Mechanics | Spell suppression rolls its chance per spell hit. It can be stacked to 100%, guaranteeing suppression. The spell damage prevented is normally 40%, which can be raised by Prevent +#% of Suppressed Spell Damage. The same multiplier applies to the DPS of damaging ailments, relevantly Ignite and Poison , as Bleeding cannot be applied by spells. Secondary damage caused by spells is also mitigated by spell suppression. [1]
Spell suppression | Mechanics | Spell suppression occurs toward the end of mitigation, after resistances and damage reduction , but before stun and block. [2] [3]

Split (item property) | Description | Splitting items refers to the use of the Fenumal Plagued Arachnid beast, Fractured Fossil , or x% chance to create a Split Copy corpse modifier in the Necropolis to create a split copy of an item. This adds the split property to both copies, preventing them from being split again.
Split (item property) | Restrictions | Synthesised , fractured , and influenced items cannot be split. This restriction prevents bases with valuable synthesised implicit modifiers or fractured modifiers from being duplicated.
Split (item property) | Restrictions | Items with an enchantment also cannot be split. This prevents any non-legacy cluster jewels from being split, as they always have an enchantment.
Split (item property) | Restrictions | The beastcrafting version of the split craft using the Fenumal Plagued Arachnid also cannot split items with catalyst quality. This can be done with Fractured Fossil s, despite the error message saying otherwise when attempting to Fracture Fossil an enchanted item, and retains the original quality type and amount on both copies. [1]
Split (item property) | Restrictions | Note that these restrictions do not apply the other way around. For example, it is not possible to split a fractured item, but it is possible to fracture a split item.
Split (item property) | Split items | Items with the split property can be crafted on normally (unlike mirrored and corrupted items), except that they cannot be further split, and the split property cannot be removed via imprint.
Split (item property) | Split items | To be specific, items with the split property:
Split (item property) | Split items | If the split item has an implicit modifier, both split copies will keep the implicits. However, in the case of Eldritch implicit modifiers , one of the split copy will only have the Eater implicit and the other will only have the Exarch implicit.
Split (item property) | Split items | If the item that has been split has a Crucible Passive Skill Tree , both copies of the item will have the same trees and retain the same amount of experience as the original item.
Split (item property) | Split items | Both split items will have the same amount of Memory Strands as the original item.
Stat | Description | Stats modify a single statistic of the game. Stats can apply to most aspects of the game, such as the player's character , items , monsters , skills or an area. Common sources of stats include modifiers , passive skills , buffs and skills.
Stat | Overview | Each stat has an internal ID (for example maximum_life_+% ) and a number of settings associated with it. Stats themselves do not have a value, their values are given by other sources such as modifiers or skills. The values are always integers [1] and round downs to the nearest integer if the stat value is modified [2].
Stat | Overview | The ID and the values are used for translating the stat into a more human readable format, as such, stats may often appear in descriptions differently then they are used in game. This means they may omit information (i.e. values) or change their text and numbers to be more readable. For example the stat maximum_life_+% will appear as x% increased maximum Life for positive values and x% reduced maximum Life for negative values on things that affect the player's character, but will appear as Extra Life and Reduced Life on monsters respectively.
Stat | Overview | It is also possible that the description of a stat is omitted entirely and not visible to the player, however stats will still be effective. Very often this is the case for monster modifiers such as hidden item quantity or rarity boosts. This is also the case for stats that have a value of exactly 0.
Stat | Sources | An incomplete list of sources:
Stat | Interaction | Stats will stack with themselves additively, so two or more stats with the same ID will simply be added up. [3]
Stat | Interaction | However, there is a distinction between Global and Local stats: [4]
Stat | Interaction | Stats with different IDs may also interact with each other, however there is no dead set rule on how different stats interact with each other. Often the interaction can be derived from the description of the stats.
Stat | Rule of thumb based on descriptions | The visible description generally hints at a few rules for the interaction. However be wary there may be edge cases where it behaves differently.
Stat | Rule of thumb based on descriptions | What this means in plain English is that you add the various "increased"/"reduced" effects together into a single multiplier, and multiply the base stat by the result, whereas you multiply the base stat by each "more"/"less" effect in turn.
Stat | Rule of thumb based on descriptions | The total stat value can be calculated as the sum of any added stat, multiplied by the sum of all increases and reductions to stat, multiplied by all more and less stat modifiers.
Stat | Rule of thumb based on descriptions | stat t o t a l = ∑ i = 1 a added stat i × ( 1 + ∑ j = 1 b increased stat j − ∑ k = 1 c reduced stat k ) × ∏ l = 1 d ( 1 + more stat l ) × ∏ m = 1 e ( 1 − less stat m ) \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\begin{aligned}{\text{stat}}_{total}=&\sum _{i=1}^{a}{\text{added stat}}_{i}\times \\&\left(1+\sum _{j=1}^{b}{\text{increased stat}}_{j}-\sum _{k=1}^{c}{\text{reduced stat}}_{k}\right)\times \\&\prod _{l=1}^{d}(1+{\text{more stat}}_{l})\times \prod _{m=1}^{e}(1-{\text{less stat}}_{m})\end{aligned}}

Stat | Rule of thumb based on descriptions | Often a stat has a set of types determining to which statistics it applies. Types can be subtypes or supertypes of other Types. Supertypes affect their subtypes but not vice versa. Many types correspond to Gem Tags ; however, this relationship is not strict. For example, Molten Strike has the Melee tag, but its projectiles do not do melee damage, and Explosive Arrow has the Attack tag, but the charge detonation does not do Attack damage.

Stone Altar | Description | In the Talisman leagues , Stone Altars could be found throughout Wraeclast. At these altars, the player could sacrifice sets of five different talismans of the same tier to summon a monster possessed by a higher-tier Talisman. The rarity of the output Talisman was selected at random from the five input ones (i.e. if the player puts three magic, one unique and one normal talisman into the stone altar, the resulting talisman will have 60% chance to be magic, 20% chance to be unique and 20% chance to be normal).
Stone Altar | Description | If the player used five third-tier Talismans at a stone altar, it summoned a portal to an area where Rigwald, the Wolven King could be fought.
Stone Altar | Description | After the Talisman league ended, Stone Altars were not added to the core game. Currently they are not implemented but may make a return in the future. [1]
Stone Altar | Spawn Locations | They had a 100% chance to spawn in the Western Forest , the Hedge Maze , and the Dried Lake. The Ledge had a 100% chance to spawn one in Cruel and Merciless. The Imperial Gardens had a 60% chance. The Dread Thicket was 50%. Kaom's Dream and Stronghold had a 35% chance. The Belly of the Beast areas had a 20% chance in Normal, up to 30% in Merciless. All non-unique maps had a 35% chance to spawn a stone altar as well. Stone altars could spawn also in other areas, but not too often.
Stone Altar | Item level | The item level of talismans obtained from stone altars was an average of the five talismans used, where the the lowest-level talisman was counted once, the highest-level talisman was counted three times, and the middle three talismans were counted twice. The summoned monsters are the same level as the resultant talisman that the player should get from using the altar. That means using high-level talismans in a low-level area on a low-level character is ill-advised.
Stone Altar | Item level | The level of the stone altar's area mattered only if the talismans used resulted in a talisman lower than the level of the area. In this case, the monsters summoned from the stone altar will match the level of the area, rather than the level of the talisman. This does not cause them to drop higher level Talismans than they otherwise would have. [2]
Stone Altar | Monsters | When a stone altar was activated with tier 1 or 2 talismans, groups of monsters would appear from among the following:
Stone Altar | Monsters | For tier 1 talismans, one of these monsters would be possessed by the tier 2 talisman. For tier 2 talismans, a random unique monster would be holding the tier 3 talisman:

Stun | Mechanics | Hits have a chance to stun based on their damage compared to the target's maximum life. The base duration of the stun animation is 350ms.

Synthesiser | Description | The Synthesiser was a device used to create synthesised items from fractured items. It has since been removed from the game and is currently not available anymore.
Synthesiser | Mechanics | The Synthesiser could be found in the Memory Nexus. To use the Synthesiser, players had to place three rare fractured items of the same item class. The inventory size of each item did not matter, but the item class had to match. For example, one-handed maces and sceptres were considered two different item classes. It was also possible to substitute a unique fractured item that dropped from Venarius or any of the other four Synthesis bosses instead of one of these rare items.
Synthesiser | Mechanics | The Synthesiser would then create a new synthesised item with one to three synthesised implicit modifiers based on all of the modifiers on the three base items, not just the fractured modifiers.
Synthesiser | Mechanics | Synthesised implicits could be targeted:
Synthesiser | Fate of the game mechanics | After the Synthesis leagues ended, most of its content was not added to the core game. As a result the Synthesiser and the Memory Nexus was made unavailable. Fractured and Synthesized items will not be added until 3.11 Harvest league , only through harvest crafting on pre-made bases. As well as random drops in side of Heist Contracts and Blueprints in 3.12 Heist league.
Tag | Description | Tags are internally used by the game to describe certain properties/aspects of entities. These are then usually used later to govern certain rules about those entities, such as which modifiers can spawn on which items.
Tag | Overview | Most entities, like monsters, areas, mods and items come with their own list of tags. The tags are used to describe some properties of those entities, for example currency items are usually tagged with default, currency
Tag | Overview | Modifiers: Modifiers have tags which can be used to manipulate or determine crafting outcomes (e.g. fossils , harvest crafting ), or the modifiers can be the targets of other bonuses (e.g. catalysts , heist enchantments ). Spawn tags determine the eligibility of modifiers to roll on specific base types of items.
Tag | Overview | Areas: Areas may have tags which determine the layout or features of an area, or may be a descriptive tag which may also be correlated to certain divination card drop locations.
Tag | Overview | Monsters: Monster tags may also determine the drop sources of certain divination cards, or may be used to categorize certain monsters.
Taunt | Description | Taunt is a debuff that makes an affected enemy unable to consider any object as a potential target, except the source of the debuff. It also causes enemies to deal 10% less damage to other entities. [2] [3] (Note: this effect does not appear to be currently working. [4] ) It lasts for 3 seconds. Taunt can be applied by players, minions, monsters, or proxies that are targetable (e.g. totems , but not traps , mines , or mirages ). Taunt immediately expires when the character (or proxy) that applied it dies or expires.
Taunt | Description | When multiple sources are taunting the same enemy, the first taunt applied determines the aggro. The targeted source can maintain aggro indefinitely as long as it maintains its taunt on the target. [3]
Taunt | Description | All targets can be taunted unless made immune through a modifier; however, taunt will not cause The Shaper , The Elder , Shaper Guardians , Elder Guardians , or various other unique bosses to retarget towards the source of the taunt. [5]
