Tempest | Description | Tempests are a game mechanic that causes environmental hazards to appear randomly in an affected area. Each tempest hazard appears as a swirling vortex of energy that discharges after several seconds to apply certain buffs to both player characters and monsters within it.
Tempest | Encounters | Tempests are considered Extra Content , but do not have a base chance to spawn in areas. They can only be accessed via specific means.
The Lake of Kalandra | Description | The Lake of Kalandra is an area introduced during Kalandra League and occasionally made accessible during certain events. Players can interact with Mirrored Tablets to create paths from Reflection tiles in the Lake to generate increasingly difficult and rewarding encounters.
The Lake of Kalandra | Mirrored Tablet | Every area and map in Kalandra League contains a Mirrored Tablet altar used for constructing your Lake of Kalandra. Each Tablet allows you to place 1-2 Reflections (tiles) on the Lake, and completely filling it allows you to run it and reap the rewards you've worked for.
The Lake of Kalandra | Mirrored Tablet | Completed Mirrored Tablets from Act zones must be opened in the Acts, via the Mirrored Tablet columns. Map-tier Mirrored Tablets are itemized and can be opened via the Map Device.
The Lake of Kalandra | Mirrored Tablet | The size of the Lake in the Mirrored Tablet depends on the area level that the Tablet was first generated in. It begins as a 2x2 grid in Act 1, up to 4x4 by Act 10, and up to randomly 4x5 or 5x5 in T16 maps.
The Lake of Kalandra | Mirrored Tablet | Reflection tiles may appear with 2-4 notches on their borders; these indicate a higher tier encounter and generally have harder content and greater rewards.
The Lake of Kalandra | Mirrored Tablet | Tiles also scale in difficulty based on their Manhattan distance (the shortest route from the entrance to the given reflection). Difficulty scales monster damage and damage reduction, as well as rewards. Rewards from chests appear to scale linearly up to Difficulty 5, then taper off from Difficulty 6 onwards.
The Lake of Kalandra | Mirrored Tablet | Area level of the lake is calculated similarly to The Temple of Atzoatl , and will be equal to the average level of zones a player activated altars in plus 10 levels, but no higher than the highest level zone an altar was activated in, and no higher than level 75 if any altar was opened in a campaign zone. [1]
The Lake of Kalandra | Monster Reflections | Tiles contain packs of monsters with one Unique named "Effigy of X", based on existing Unique Monsters from Acts or Invasion bosses. Defeating around 95% of the tile's monsters spawns a Submerged Chest with random rewards that scales with difficulty.
The Lake of Kalandra | Monster Reflections | Monster Reflection reward types include generic (currency, maps, gear), quality currency , armour , weapons , and jewellery.
The Lake of Kalandra | League Reflections | Tiles contain various encounters from other Challenge Leagues, including Extra Content and Masters. The encounter's respective rewards scale with difficulty.
The Lake of Kalandra | League Reflections | Each level of Difficulty increases the number of Artifacts dropped. The Unique Boss always drops a stack of Reroll Currency.
The Lake of Kalandra | League Reflections | Be careful of Tormented Spirits applying Silence.
The Lake of Kalandra | League Reflections | Each level of Difficulty increases the quantity of items dropped from Strongboxes. Does not affect items dropped by monsters in the Strongboxes. T3 Strongbox tile tends to spawn Diviner's, Operative's, and Cartographer's Strongboxes.
The Lake of Kalandra | League Reflections | Each level of Difficulty increases the base duration of Shrine buffs on players.
The Lake of Kalandra | League Reflections | Each level of Difficulty increases the chance for Essence Monoliths to contain additional Essences.
The Lake of Kalandra | League Reflections | Each level of Difficulty increases the quantity of Breach Splinters in Breach Hands. Does not affect Breach Splinters dropped from monsters.
The Lake of Kalandra | League Reflections | Each level of Difficulty increases the quantity of Timeless Splinters dropped.
The Lake of Kalandra | League Reflections | Each level of Difficulty increases the quantity of Currency Shards dropped from Harbingers.
The Lake of Kalandra | League Reflections | Each level of Difficulty increases the quantity of Sulphite obtained from Voltaxic Sulphite deposits. The T3 node grants a decent amount of Azurite.
The Lake of Kalandra | League Reflections | Each level of Difficulty increases the quantity of Tainted Currency dropped. The tile contains many rats that have a chance to spawn a Beyond Portal, up until a Beyond Boss is generated. Does not guarantee a Beyond Boss.
The Lake of Kalandra | League Reflections | Adds a Mirror of Delirium which temporarily covers the Lake in Delirium fog. Does not appear to scale with Difficulty.
The Lake of Kalandra | League Reflections | Each level of Difficulty increases the experience granted by monsters in this tile. Similar to Untainted Paradise.
The Lake of Kalandra | League Reflections | Spawns a Fisherman NPC and contains an interactable Tackle Box which contains a fishing -related Unique item.
The Lake of Kalandra | League Reflections | Each level of Difficulty increases the magnitude of modifiers Reflected by the Ethereal Reflecting Mist.
The Lake of Kalandra | Boss Reflections | Boss reflections are higher tier versions of Monster Reflections that spawns one or more Unique Bosses, including Rogue Exiles and Map Bosses. Can spawn Map Bosses of maps that are not currently on the Atlas.
The Lake of Kalandra | Boss Reflections | Boss reflection reward types include gems , currency , divination cards. maps , scarabs , and Unique items.
The Lake of Kalandra | Legacy Reflections | The following reflection types have been removed in the most recent iteration of the Lake of Kalandra, mainly because the mechanic has been removed from the game.
The Lake of Kalandra | Legacy Reflections | Each level of Difficulty increases the chance to double dropped rewards and Catalysts. Cannot drop an itemized Organ.
The Lake of Kalandra | Special Tiles | These tiles can occasionally appear alongside Reflection choices. These can alter your current Mirrored Tablet and can be used to fine-tune your Reflections' placement and difficulty. These choices can be Exiled, though it is generally a poor idea to do so as they are less common than regular Reflections and are useful to have. Swapping a Reflection with another nearby Reflection can be used similarly to a "skip".
The Lake of Kalandra | Reflection Abilities | These abilities can be used a set number of times per Tablet once unlocked. Additional uses of these abilities can be unlocked by completing certain encounters at the required difficulty. It is highly recommended to unlock the Reroll and Exile options completely as soon as possible. Exiling three of the Fire, Cold, Lightning, or Physical Monster Reflections makes it much more likely to have a chance to receive one of the Encounter Reflections or Boss Reflections as one of your three options.
The Lake of Kalandra | Reflecting Mist | Sometimes, Kalandra may appear in the Lake of Kalandra, and create a Reflecting Mist upon completing an encounter of Difficulty 4 or higher, offering you a choice between two Reflected mirrored rare rings or amulets with unusual mods. Some are scaled-up versions of existing modifiers, while others are strong negative versions of the same modifier. The rings provide inverse stats; a negative mod on one ring is positive on the other. The magnitude of the modifiers is dependent on the difficulty of the completed encounter ranging from 2.0x at Difficulty 4 to 3.3x at Difficulty 17 (0.1 increments) and applies to all modifiers with scaleable values. You may only pick one of these items to take.
The Lake of Kalandra | Reflecting Mist | Sometimes, it may offer a ring basetype exclusive to the Lake of Kalandra and likewise contains alternate effects based on which ring slot they are equipped into:
The Lake of Kalandra | Reflecting Mist | These rings come Rare and Mirrored , and contain the higher magnitude modifiers of Reflected rings. They can be vendored 5-to-1 at any vendor to obtain a craftable, non-mirrored version.
The Lake of Kalandra | Reflecting Mist | Kalandra's Touch [2] used to be a possible rare outcome, replacing one of the rings in the Reflecting Mist; however, after it became a core drop item in version 3.20.0 , it is unknown whether it is still a possible outcome in current iterations of the Lake of Kalandra.
The Lake of Kalandra | Reflecting Mist | The modifiers are scaled by a coefficient based on the difficulty the mist spawns in. They do not spawn in difficulty less than 4.
The Lake of Kalandra | Reflecting Mist | Rarely, an "evil" version of Kalandra will appear shrouded in teal-coloured mist, mirroring Unique enemies in the tile and granting an additional Reflecting Mist. These mirrored enemies will also drop mirrored items. This will be denoted with the following voicelines:
The Lake of Kalandra | Reflecting Mist | Kalandra: You are meddling in forces beyond your understanding! Kalandra: Show me what you are truly made of.
The Lake of Kalandra | Reflecting Mist | Kalandra may also occasionally give an additional Reflecting Mist without doubling the boss.
The Lake of Kalandra | Ethereal Reflecting Mist | Rarely, you may be offered a Reflection of Kalandra encounter, which allows you to Reflect your own ring or amulet and distort it in a similar process. The magnitude of the modifiers depends on the difficulty of the encounter. Again, you may only keep one of the resultant items.
The Lake of Kalandra | Ethereal Reflecting Mist | The Blast from the Past Event introduced the possibility to be able to reflect jewellery with Recombinator -only modifiers to increase their magnitude, specifically:
The Lake of Kalandra | Ethereal Reflecting Mist | The increased effect of modifiers from reflecting jewellery scales with Difficulty.
The Lake of Kalandra | Lore | Some encounters contain Ancient Etchings which provide lore surrounding Kalandra and the lake, including describing some rules surrounding the lake.
The Lake of Kalandra | Trivia | The Lake of Kalandra appears to be inspired by the Giant's Causeway in Ireland and other basalt formations.
The Pantheon | Description | The Pantheon is a system of divine powers that players can activate to grant various defensive passive buffs, introduced in The Fall of Oriath expansion. These powers grant various defensive or utility bonuses and become available when players defeat certain gods in Acts 6 through 10.
The Pantheon | Description | There are twelve gods that each grant a power; four major gods and eight minor gods. A player can only have one major and one minor power activated at a time. The bonuses can be freely swapped with no extra cost, as long as the player is in a town or hideout.
The Pantheon | Description | Upgrading a god's power requires consuming a Divine Vessel and a map with a boss that can upgrade a pantheon power. Once completed, activating a pantheon power will also activate all unlocked upgrade effects associated with that god's power.
The Pantheon | Description | The Pantheon is not available in Ruthless mode.
The Pantheon | Upgrading | Every major and minor god can be upgraded. All Major gods have 3 upgrades and Minor gods have 1 upgrade. This means, in total, you can get up to 4 simultaneous buffs from a Major god, and 2 simultaneous buffs from a Minor god.
The Pantheon | Upgrading | Upgrades to the Pantheon are shared between all characters in the same league, but their effects are disabled until the character has completed the quest An End to Hunger (completing the campaign ).
The Pantheon | Upgrading | In order to upgrade a god power, players need to:
The Pantheon | Upgrading | There must be space in the map device for the Captured Soul or it will be deleted. This is typically not a problem unless the player adds more items to the map device's slots before completing the opened map.
The Pantheon | Downgrading | To "downgrade" (remove) a Pantheon Power upgrade for a single character , follow the same procedure as upgrading; it acts as a toggle.
The Pantheon | Strategy | If the player is struggling on an encounter, particularly in Maps , swapping a Pantheon power can provide a quick boost to survivability. For example, when facing Shock , swapping to Garukhan 's power might help.
The Pantheon | Maps | For maps specifically, you can hold onto maps with less desirable modifiers such as Burning Ground , swap to Abberath run all of them, then swap back to your usual power.
The Pantheon | Resistances | If you're unable to max your Resistances with your equipment, you can swap to souls that provide mitigation to those damage types until you are able to upgrade.
The Pantheon | Dialogue | Dialogue with Sin promptly after killing the deities. (Not in town)

The Pantheon | Ryslatha (Act 6) | Sin: Release this land to the will of its true children.

Tormented spirit | Description | Tormented Spirits are a special type of monster. Once spotted, these apparitions of dead criminals flee from the player with their ill-gotten gains. When a tormented spirit touch another monster, it imbues them a with buff that increases their danger, but also their reward. When a tormented spirit touches a Rare or Unique monster, it possesses it and makes them even more powerful, but also makes them more rewarding. [1] This mechanic is also referred to as Torment.
Tormented spirit | Description | Tormented spirits are considered a form of Extra Content.
Tormented spirit | Mechanics | Tormented spirits are Unique monsters that can be randomly found throughout acts and maps. Tormented spirits are unable to attack directly. Once a player gets within range, it will attempt to flee from the player while also attempting to pass through other monsters along the way, stopping every few seconds.
Tormented spirit | Mechanics | Any Normal and Magic monsters that the spirit passes through receive a " Touch " modifier based on the spirit type. If the tormented spirit touches a Rare or Unique monster, it will go inside that monster and possess it, despawning itself and giving the monster a " Grip " modifier. Tormented spirits cannot affect other tormented spirits. If a tormented spirit stays alive long enough without possessing anything it will eventually despawn itself, leaving no items. Certain effects can cause monsters to spawn in with a Touch or Grip modifier already applied.
Tormented spirit | Mechanics | Monsters that have been touched or possessed by a tormented spirit receive increased damage and attack, cast, and movement speed, along with any special effects given by that specific tormented spirit, as well as 25% increased item quantity and item rarity for a Touch modifier, and 50% increased item rarity for a Grip modifier. If a tormented spirit is killed, it is guaranteed to drop one rare item. If a rare monster is possessed, at least two rare items are guaranteed to drop, and if a unique monster is possessed, at least three rare items are guaranteed to drop. [2]
Tormented spirit | Mechanics | Tormented spirits spawn in with a hidden 90% less damage taken modifier that tapers off to 0% over 15 seconds after they become active. For each monster they touch, they take 5% increased damage. Each tormented spirit can touch up a maximum of 50 enemies.
Tormented spirit | Mechanics | Fairgraves' Tricorne allows the player to receive a Touch modifier if they touch a tormented spirit. The Speaker of the Dead keystone allows tormented spirits to possess the player, granting you its Grip modifier and allowing you to touch up to 40 monsters.
Tormented spirit | Torment modifiers | Note: information is based on inferences from metadata and may not be 100% accurate.
Tormented spirit | Unusual | These Tormented Spirits can only appear in maps affected by a Torment Scarab of Peculiarity. Every monster Possessed by an usual variant will drop an item specific to the tormented spirit. (map, scarab or unique item) The Betrayer and Heretic Touched monsters also have a chance to drop a specific item (scarab or map depending on the spirit). The chance is supposedly 10%, following the metadata which may not be accurate. The scarabs dropped this way doesn't seem to be affected by modifiers on the atlas tree, as notable nodes such as Loved by the Sun doesn't prevent abyss scarabs to drop.
Toughness | Description | Toughness is a property of monsters that multiplicatively affects the damage they take. Increased toughness causes monsters to take less damage while reduced toughness causes them to take more damage.
Toughness | Calculation | The damage taken by the monster based on their toughness is calculated as follows, rounded to the nearest whole number:
Toughness | Calculation | Failed to parse (SVG (MathML can be enabled via browser plugin): Invalid response ("Math extension cannot connect to Restbase.") from server "https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/":): \color[RGB]{163,141,109} \text {Relative Damage Taken} = 1 - \dfrac {100\%} {100\% + \text{Total Increased Toughness }\%}
Toughness | Calculation | (6567-19899)% increased Toughness is the maximum possible value for Toughness that permits the monster to take damage. At 19900% increased Toughness or above, the monster has 100% less damage taken, effectively granting damage immunity.
Trapped Stash | Description | A Trapped Stash is an interactable object found in Immortal Syndicate safehouses containing certain Syndicate members.
Trapped Stash | Description | After interacting with the trapped stash, the player is shown a small collection of items such as unique items or currency stacks depending on the member associated with the room and safehouse type. The player has eight seconds to take one item after which the trapped stash closes and cannot be interacted with again. If multiple trapped stashes are present, the timer must fully expire before another trapped stash can be opened, even if the player already took an item.
Trial of the Ancestors | Description | The Trial of the Ancestors is a league mechanic found in Ancestor league. The player participates in the tournament against fallen Karui chieftains and their tribes overseen by Hinekora , Mother of Death.
Trial of the Ancestors | Entry | To access the Halls of the Dead , the player must use a Silver Coin from town or hideout , or enter using the waypoint. The player needs to click the Well of Passing to cross over into the afterlife. Silver Coins are also used as the entry fee to participate in each round of the tournament. Trial of the Ancestors can be accessed as soon as the player has access to Lioneye's Watch in Act 1.
Trial of the Ancestors | The Tournament | The tournament is held until the last team is standing. A team is eliminated when they lose twice in a tournament.
Trial of the Ancestors | The Tournament | The player can select opponents based on sponsors or rewards. Sponsors grant favour towards their tribe if you win the round, which can be used to buy warriors, field items, and equipment. Rewards can vary from currency, items, tattoos, and unique items. Favour is used to purchase warriors and equipment. You can sell your warriors or equipment to another tribe to gain their favour. You get an additional 50 favour from sponsors per tournament round. In addition, each round you always gain 250 favour from Navali, or 500 if you lost the round.
Trial of the Ancestors | The Tournament | You will also gain ranking as you participate in the tournament. Ranking determines the trial's monster level, damage and damage reduction, as well as the item level, rarity, and/or stack size of rewards. Losing a tournament lowers rank by a small amount, whereas winning a tournament increases rank by a larger amount.
Trial of the Ancestors | The Tournament | If you win the tournament, Hinekora will offer you a choice between a few exclusive items. Additionally, there are some rewards that initially can only appear in the final round of the tournament, although they can show up earlier at higher ranks.
Trial of the Ancestors | The Tournament | Your favour and your warriors and equipment are reset between tournaments. Winning a tournament always grants 3 to 4 random warriors when you start the next tournament. Losing in the tournament will instead only grant a chance for random warriors.
Trial of the Ancestors | The Trial | Fight alongside your selected warriors to defeat the enemy chieftain and warriors, and banish their totems to prevent them from repawning. Players have to channel near a totem to banish it and cannot deal damage to it directly. Being hit while banishing a totem interrupts actions and prevents all actions for a duration.
Trial of the Ancestors | The Trial | Defeated warriors revive at their ancestral totem after a delay which increases each time they die. Dying during a trial does not count as a death (no experience loss or sending Hardcore character to Standard will occur). All enemies immediately respawn if an enemy totem is banished by the player; this does not occur if a warrior banishes it instead. Banishing all enemy totems wins the match.
Trial of the Ancestors | The Trial | Both teams can select up to 16 Warriors or Field Items to assist the player or enemy chieftain in battle. Up to 4 Warriors can be assigned to each role.
Trial of the Ancestors | The Trial | Flankers should be prioritized, followed by escorts and defence. The player should prioritize killing enemies while warriors focus on totems.
Trial of the Ancestors | Opponents | You can select an opponent to battle each round. Each chieftain grants different rewards per round. Each warrior from that tribe has an innate effect based on their tribe.
Trial of the Ancestors | Opponents | All enemies are unaffected by taunt , cannot be repeatedly knocked back (up to 5 times every 5 seconds) or forced to flee , and cannot have movement speed slowed beyond 50% base movement speed. Warriors are also immune to conversion via Conversion Trap.
Trial of the Ancestors | Warriors | Players begin a tournament with an Honoured Warrior, an Honoured Sage, and a Tuatara in their initial roster. Up to 4 tribe-specific warriors can also randomly join your initial roster for the next tournament; this is guaranteed if you win a tournament and has a chance to occur if you lose a tournament.
Trial of the Ancestors | Warriors | Additional warriors can be purchased from the respective tribe's chieftain using favour. Each tribe's cheapest warrior is always available for purchase after the first round, while higher-tier warriors may be offered for purchase in later rounds. Higher-tier warriors are not always guaranteed to show up in a tournament.
Trial of the Ancestors | Equipment | One piece of equipment can be equipped onto each warrior, granting certain buffs themed around each tribe. Equipped equipment is retained between rounds, but is destroyed at the end of a tournament.
Trial of the Ancestors | Field item | Field items can be placed before a match in any of the 16 Warrior positions. Idols can be used in combat once; unused idols can be used in the next match. Used field items and field items unused by the end of the tournament are destroyed.
Trial of the Ancestors | Rewards | Rewards are obtained after winning a round or tournament by heading towards Navali and Hinekora at the northernmost point of the arena. An Ancestral War Chest appears after a short delay.
Trial of the Ancestors | Rewards | Rarer rewards like Makanga Tattoos, Loyalty Tattoos, and tribe uniques are more likely to appear later in a match, typically as the final match in a tournament. Player rank will also increase the appearance rate of rarer rewards.
Trial of the Ancestors | Round rewards | Round rewards can be obtained by defeating opponents that offer their exclusive rewards. Each round reward is tied to a specific tribe.
Trial of the Ancestors | Round rewards | Loyalty tattoos are a type of tattoo that grants a triggered skill that summons the spirit of a tribe's chieftain as a minion. These minions also provide a buff while active. Only 1 Loyalty tattoo can be applied at one time.
Trial of the Ancestors | Round rewards | Makanga tattoos have very powerful effects, but they require adjacent nodes to be allocated in a certain way for them to do anything. They have a chance to appear as a reward in the final round of the tournament.
Trial of the Ancestors | Fated rewards | Fated rewards can be obtained from Hinekora after successfully winning a tournament. Players are provided a choice between two chests containing an honoured tattoo and an omen. At higher ranks, she may offer an exclusive unique item or her signature currency instead.
Trial of the Ancestors | Fated rewards | Hinekora can also rarely offer special tattoos with unique effects.
Trial of the Ancestors | ToTA-specific builds | High-level Trials scale to levels of damage and damage reduction beyond normal scaling in most of the rest of the game, similar to deep delve. Because of this, players may opt to create specific characters or utilise certain strategies to effectively farm this mechanic and solely focus on crowd control strategies (e.g. Void Sphere , movement speed and action speed slows) and damage avoidance. See this guide for a more detailed overview.
Trial of the Ancestors | Act 4 strategy | Certain strategies exist where players will create and level up characters purely in Trial of the Ancestors after stopping at the Crystal Veins in Act 4. This prevents Kaom and Utula from appearing in the Halls as chieftains, limiting the roster of 10 possible tribes to 8 instead. This has some pros and cons:
Triple damage | Description | Triple damage is an effect that causes a hit to deal triple its damage. Triple damage overrides and does not stack with double damage.

Ultimatum | Description | The Trials of Chaos , also known as Ultimatum , is a league mechanic introduced with the Ultimatum leagues. It was added to the core game in Version 3.23.0.
Ultimatum | Mechanics | The Trialmaster and an altar can be found in The Vaal City and The Temple of Decay Level 1 in Act 7. It has an 8% chance to spawn in maps. The altar displays a reward, the objective, and three modifiers to choose from. The player must select a modifier before beginning the trial.
Ultimatum | Mechanics | There are four possible objectives:
Ultimatum | Mechanics | After successfully completing a round, the encounter is frozen in time, and the player is offered two choices: end the trial and receive the accumulated rewards, or aim for more rewards and start the next round by selecting a new modifier to add.
Ultimatum | Mechanics | If the player's character dies, stays outside of the circle for too long, or receives 7 stacks of Ruin , the Ultimatum is failed and all rewards will be removed. The Altar being destroyed in "Protect the Altar" encounters also is considered a fail state.
Ultimatum | Mechanics | Each trial has 10 rounds. In Tier 14+ maps (area level 81+), upon starting the final round, there is a chance (~3% [1] ) you will get teleported into the Trial of Ordeals' arena and face the Trialmaster as a boss. Ultimatum Scarab of Dueling guarantees the Trialmaster boss will appear regardless of map tier, as long as Gruelling Gauntlet is not allocated. Allocating the Gruelling Gauntlet keystone or using the Imbued Ultimatum map device craft with an Horned Scarab of Awakening increases the maximum rounds to 13, with the former disabling the ability to face the Trialmaster or control the modifiers.
Ultimatum | Mechanics | Modifiers to pack size and Ultimatum Encounters in your Maps spawn #% increased number of Monsters will increase the number of monsters spawned in each wave during a round, but the cooldown of each wave also appears to increase proportionally such that the average monster kill rate is the same in optimal conditions, such that there is no overall difference in the speed at which "defeat waves of enemies" and "protect the altar" objectives are completed.
Ultimatum | Partying | When facing a Trial of Chaos with other players, each player will be offered their own individual set of rewards [2]. When an individual player fails the trial, they will lose their rewards but the trial will continue with the remaining players.
Ultimatum | Partying | In between waves, the players will vote on which modifier to add to the next wave. The one with the most votes gets added. In case of ties, a mod is randomly chosen between them. Players have a limited time to vote, but the timer is paused if at least one party member is not present in the zone.
Ultimatum | Rewards | Ultimatum Encounters offer cumulative rewards. Upon successfully completing or terminating an Ultimatum encounter, each round's rewards are dropped at the altar's location. Failing an Ultimatum encounter forfeits all accumulated rewards in that instance.
Ultimatum | Rewards | Rewards include corrupted (including double corrupted) rare items and maps , corrupted unique items, divination cards , currency , catalysts , and Inscribed Ultimatum s. Rewards appear at or after certain waves:
Ultimatum | Rewards | The above wave counts are appropriately affected via Stand Your Ground or Ultimatum Scarab of Bribing 's stats that cause rewards to be granted as though completing additional round(s) (e.g. Catalysts will instead appear on Wave 3/7). This also causes the upgraded rewards to appear earlier, therefore having more chances at this reward tier per Ultimatum encounter.
Ultimatum | Rewards | Map item quantity does not scale rewards with the exception of catalysts.
Ultimatum | Rewards | Temptation Step , Gamblesprint , and Relic of the Pact can exclusively be obtained randomly as Ultimatum round rewards.
Ultimatum | Rewards | Additionally, the maximum Inscribed Ultimatum difficulty that can appear is limited by the area level of the Ultimatum encounter:
Ultimatum | The Trialmaster | The Trialmaster also has his own set of exclusive drops, including Tainted Catalyst s and several unique items:
Ultimatum | The Trialmaster | Defeating the Trialmaster also grants the character the opportunity to obtain or change into the Chaos Bloodline Ascendancy class.
Ultimatum | Inscribed Ultimatum | Inscribed Ultimatum can be obtained as rewards for completing Ultimatum rounds, or randomly as an area drop in maps that contain Ultimatum encounters. Inscribed Ultimatums come in four varieties:
Ultimatum | Inscribed Ultimatum | Each Inscribed Ultimatum lists a random Ultimatum encounter type and list of modifiers for that challenge. Inscribed Ultimatums can used in a map device to access the Utzaal Arena , which only contains an altar. The required item must be placed on the altar to start the trial.
Ultimatum | Inscribed Ultimatum | Unlike a regular Ultimatum encounter, which takes place in a circular area, Inscribed Ultimatum encounters take place within the entire arena and consists of a single wave that lasts significantly longer. ‎
Ultimatum | Modifiers | ‎
Ultimatum | Strategy | Builds that can consistently succeed in full clearing Ultimatums typically have solutions for most or all Ultimatum modifiers, reducing the chance for bad luck:
Ultimatum | Strategy | If opting to take Ruin modifiers, avoid using blue-coloured skills or microtransactions , as it can reduce visual clarity of Ruin-inflicting enemy skills.
Vendor recipe system | Description | The vendor recipe system allows the player to sell items to any town vendor in exchange for a multitude of currency items and equipment. Each recipe requires semi-specific items or combinations of items be put into the sell window at the same time, and the outcome will change based on any recipes that have been matched. Unless noted otherwise, each item may only be involved in a single recipe at a time.
Vendor recipe system | Description | Items (and their costs) sold by vendors as part of their normal inventory are covered on the vendor page.
Vendor recipe system | Equipment | Unless otherwise stated, the item level and rarity of the item produced are both equal to the lowest item level and rarity among all items required for the recipe.
Vendor recipe system | Basic crafting | The following vendor recipes involve crafting of existing items ( see also: crafting ) to add or upgrade a specific modifier.
Vendor recipe system | Basic crafting | Beyond that, these recipes are split into two categories: one the creates a new item with a guaranteed modifier, and one that adds a modifier to the existing item.
Vendor recipe system | Basic crafting | Some recipes are specific to a certain rarity of target item: if the ingredients do not match the recipe, consider using a currency orb first such as the Orb of Transmutation to make the item into Magic rarity.
Vendor recipe system | Basic crafting | All recipes of this type create a new base item (with randomized base defences).
Vendor recipe system | Basic crafting | Fractured items and corrupted items cannot be used as base items for these recipes.
Vendor recipe system | Basic crafting | All recipes of this type add a modifier to an existing item or alters the item without affecting its other stats.
Vendor recipe system | Basic crafting | Fractured items and corrupted items items cannot be used as base items for these recipes.
Vendor recipe system | Flasks | Vendor recipes related to creating and upgrading flasks :
Vendor recipe system | Unique items | The following vendor recipes are used to craft unique items. A vendor recipe is also the only way to obtain most of the unique items on this list, apart from trading with other players.
Vendor recipe system | Unique items | Using all same-influenced items as input will create an influenced output.
Vendor recipe system | Unique items | A unique item can have its modifiers rerolled by vendoring it along with two more of the same unique item. The result is comparable to using a Divine Orb and a Blessed Orb.
Vendor recipe system | Sockets | These recipes require single items with certain patterns of sockets. These can sometimes be found at vendors and can be immediately resold for a profit.
Vendor recipe system | Single Item with Mods | These recipes result from selling a single item when no other recipes are valid.
Vendor recipe system | Scroll Fragment | This is the "default" recipe. If an item does not have a more powerful recipe, it defaults to producing a Scroll Fragment. 5 Scroll Fragments automatically combine to form a Scroll of Wisdom.
Vendor recipe system | Transmutation Shard | Transmutation Shard s come from unidentified items. 20 Transmutation Shards automatically combine to form an Orb of Transmutation.
Vendor recipe system | Alteration Shard | Alteration Shard s come from identified items depending on their affixes. 20 Alteration Shards automatically combine to form an Orb of Alteration. Most affixes sell for Alteration Shards.
Vendor recipe system | Alchemy Shard | Certain rarer affixes may yield Alchemy Shard s instead of Alteration Shards. 20 Alchemy Shards automatically combine to form an Orb of Alchemy.
Vendor recipe system | Orb of Augmentation | An identified rare item with six affixes can be traded for an Orb of Augmentation. Note that magic items may only have a maximum of two affixes.
Vendor recipe system | Quality Items | These recipes produce currency items that improve the quality of their category of items. To produce the currency requires either one of the following:
Vendor recipe system | Quality Items | When done for multiple instances of the recipe at once, each individual combination must add up to 40%. For example: 6 items of 19%, 13%, 15%, 9%, 17% and 7% quality would add up to 80%, but would not actually grant 2 of the resulting quality items, only 1. This is because the 2 individual combinations do not add up to 40 each.
Vendor recipe system | Multiple Rare Items | These recipes require multiple items, mostly rares.
Vendor recipe system | X of a Kind | These recipes require multiple identified rare items with the same name.
Vendor recipe system | Straight Flush | These recipes require multiple items of the same base item type (e.g. Recurve Bow ), one from each rarity specified. Items that cannot increase in quality, such as jewellery and belts, will never yield Orbs of Alchemy with this recipe.

Vendor recipe system | Downgrade | These recipes partially reverse the main progression at a sharp penalty.
Vendor recipe system | No Known Recipes | These items have no known recipes, though many can be purchased directly.

Ward | Description | Ward is a defence capable of taking damage from hits before life or energy shield. It can only be found on item bases and uniques related to Expedition and Kingsmarch.
Ward | Mechanics | Ward is not a pool that can be depleted partially; it is either unbroken or broken. Ward does not break when a hit is prevented (e.g. evasion , spell dodge ), when a hit's damage is fully mitigated (e.g. immunity , avoidance , block ), or when damage is fully taken from another resource first (e.g. an Aegis buff).
Ward | Mechanics | Hit damage that would reach energy shield , life , or mana is first taken by your Ward and breaks Ward for a duration. Any damage left over is taken by your energy shield, life, or mana. [1]
Ward | Mechanics | Broken Ward is restored after a set delay, normally 2 seconds, which is modified by #% faster/slower Restoration of Ward modifiers. Taking hits while Ward is broken has no effect on the delay.
Ward | Mechanics | No type of hit damage bypasses Ward. But ward does not take damage or break due to damage over time.
Ward | Mechanics | Ward can still break while using Dissolution of the Flesh : Ward breaks to take damage, necessarily before Life that would be lost by taking Damage can be determined.
Ward | Mechanics | As a type of defence, Ward can be scaled by % increased (Global) Defences from e.g. Skin of the Loyal , the Chayula's Chayula's Prefix 50% increased Global Defences prefix on Grasping Mail , or Summon Stone Golem. [1]
Weapon swap | Description | Weapon swap is a mechanic that allows characters to switch between two different sets of weapons , shields , quivers or unarmed attacks.
Weapon swap | Skill gem effects | Many skill gems have effects that last only as long as the gem is socketed in the player's active equipment. Thus, for any skill gems that are swapped out of the active weapon set, any effects that are tied to the skill gem will also be removed.
Weapon swap | Skill gem effects | However, generic effects that are not tied to a specific skill gem will typically persist even after the skill gem's removal.
Weapon swap | Skill gem effects | Note: these mechanics are not strictly about weapon swap; they also apply when manually unsocketing a skill gem.
Weight | Description | Weight is a game mechanic based on the concept of weighted probability that is a central part of many other systems found in Path of Exile , including how item drop rate, modifier roll chance, and in Ruthless mode , Extra Content spawn rate.
Weight | Overview | Weight systems are used when the chance for an outcome is dependent on the ratio between other outcomes. These systems work by assigning a number (weight) to each rollable outcome, and the weight is compared to the sum of all outcomes' weights to create a ratio. For example, if a modifier with a weight of 1000, and a total weight of 40,000, that modifier has a 2.5% chance to roll (1000/40,000).
Weight | Overview | The weight system also can apply to systems without data-mineable weights, such as the chance to encounter a master in a map. In these cases, an arbitrary relative weight can be assigned to all outcomes for the purpose of calculating ratios and how modifiers affect them.
Weight | Overview | Examples of systems that use weights:
Weight | Modifying weights | When multiplying weights, the total weight must always be increased or decreased the same amount as the individual weights. This causes the written multiplier to be different from the actual change.
Weight | Modifying weights | All similar modifiers with "increased" or "reduced" must be added together before applying the multiplier.
